when you say she's a programmer , she did do some , but the real thing is to have said the future is going to be much , much more than this .	當你說她是程式設計師時 , 她做了一些事 , 但真正要說的是 , 未來會比這個還要多 。
now , a hundred years later , this guy comes along , alan turing , and in 1936 , and invents the computer all over again .	一百年後 , 這個傢伙出現了 , 艾倫•圖靈 , 1936年 , 發明了電腦 。
now , of course , babbage's machine was entirely mechanical .	當然 , babbage的機器完全是機械的 。
turing's machine was entirely theoretical .	圖靈的機器完全是理論的 。
both of these guys were coming from a mathematical perspective , but turing told us something very important .	兩者都來自數學觀點 , 但圖靈告訴我們一件非常重要的事 。
he laid down the mathematical foundations for computer science , and said , " it doesn't matter how you make a computer . "	他為電腦科學奠定了數學基礎 , 並說: 「 不管你怎麼製造電腦 。 」
it doesn't matter if your computer's mechanical , like babbage's was , or electronic , like computers are today , or perhaps in the future , cells , or , again , mechanical again , once we get into nanotechnology .	不管你的電腦是不是機械 , 像是babbage , 或電子 , 像現今的電腦 , 或未來 , 細胞 , 還是在機械式上 , 一旦我們進入奈米科技 。
we could go back to babbage's machine and just make it tiny . all those things are computers .	我們可以回到babbage的機器 , 把它做得很小 。 所有東西都是電腦 。
there is in a sense a computing essence .	在某種意義上 , 電腦是存在的 。
this is called the church–turing thesis .	這叫做教堂正在進行分析 。
and so suddenly , you get this link where you say this thing babbage had built really was a computer .	突然間 , 你就有了這個連結 , 你說這個東西babbage建了一台電腦 。
in fact , it was capable of doing everything we do today with computers , only really slowly .	事實上 , 它能夠用電腦來做我們現今所做的每件事 , 只有很慢 。
to give you an idea of how slowly , it had about 1k of memory .	為了讓各位知道 , 它的記憶有多慢 。
it used punch cards , which were being fed in , and it ran about 10 , 000 times slower the first zx81 .	它用打孔卡 , 被送進去 , 它跑了大約一萬倍 , 第一個zx81 。
it did have a ram pack .	它的確有拉姆包 。
you could add on a lot of extra memory if you wanted to .	如果你想要的話 , 你可以加入很多額外的記憶 。
so , where does that bring us today ?	所以 , 今天會帶我們到哪裡 ?
so there are plans .	這裡有計畫 。
over in swindon , the science museum archives , there are hundreds of plans and thousands of pages of notes written by charles babbage about this analytical engine .	在瑞典 , 科學博物館的檔案庫中有數以千計的計劃和數以千計的筆記 , 由查爾斯•巴比奇所寫的 。
one of those is a set of plans that we call plan 28 , and that is also the name of a charity that i started with doron swade , who was the curator of computing at the science museum , and also the person who drove the project to build a difference engine , and our plan is to build it .	其中一個是我們稱之為 「 規劃28 」 的一系列計畫 , 這也是我從多倫斯•瑞德開始的慈善機構 , 他是科學博物館的計算器 , 也是開工專案建造出差別引擎的人 , 我們的計畫就是建造它 。
here in south kensington , we will build the analytical engine .	在南肯辛頓 , 我們會建造分析引擎 。
the project has a number of parts to it .	這個專案有很多部件 。
one was the scanning of babbage's archive .	其中一個是babbage的檔案 。
that's been done . the second is now the study of all of those plans to determine what to build .	這已經完成了 。 第二個是這些計畫的研究 , 來決定要建造什麼 。
the third part is a computer simulation of that machine , and the last part is to physically build it at the science museum .	第三個部分是電腦模擬這個機器 , 最後一部分是在科學博物館建造它 。
when it's built , you'll finally be able to understand how a computer works , because rather than having a tiny chip in front of you , you've got to look at this humongous thing and say , " ah , i see the memory operating , i see the cpu operating , i hear it operating . i probably smell it operating . "	當它被建造出來時 , 你終於能夠了解電腦是如何運作的 , 因為在你面前的小晶片 , 你必須去看這個謙遜的東西 , 說: 「 啊 , 我看到記憶運作 , 我看到cpu運作 , 我聽見它運作 。 我可能聞過它正在運作 。 」
but in between that we're going to do a simulation .	但在這兩者之間 , 我們要做一個模擬 。
babbage himself wrote , he said , as soon as the analytical engine exists , it will surely guide the future course of science .	babbage自己寫信 , 他說 , 當分析引擎存在時 , 它肯定會引導未來的科學課程 。
of course , he never built it , because he was always fiddling with new plans , but when it did get built , of course , in the 1940s , everything changed .	當然 , 他從來沒有打造它 , 因為他總是在找新的計畫 , 但在1940年代 , 當然 , 一切都改變了 。
now , i'll just give you a little taste of what it looks like in motion with a video which shows just one part of the cpu mechanism working .	現在 , 我來給各位一些味道 , 用影片呈現出cpu機制運作的一部分 。
so this is just three sets of cogs , and it's going to add . this is the adding mechanism in action , so you imagine this gigantic machine .	這只是三組齒輪 , 它會加入 。 這是加強機制的動作 , 所以你想像一下這個巨大的機器 。
so , give me five years .	所以 , 給我五年 。
before the 2030s happen , we'll have it .	在2030年以前 , 我們將會有它 。
thank you very much .	謝謝大家 。
in this imagefilled talk , yann arthusbertrand displays his three most recent projects on humanity and our habitat stunning aerial photographs in his series " the earth from above , " personal interviews from around the globe featured in his web project " 6 billion others , " and his soontobereleased movie , " home , " which documents human impact on the environment through breathtaking video .	在這個影像的演說中 , 雅南•伯特蘭展示了他三個近期的項目 , 關於人性和我們的棲息地 , 在他的系列 「 地球上 」 的個人訪談 , 來自世界各地的個人訪談 , 在他的網路專案中 , 「 六十億人 」 , 以及他的 「 月亮的電影 」 , 《家 」 , 記錄了人類對環境的影響 。
art , climate change , environment , film , future , humanity , media , photography	藝術、氣候變遷、環境、電影、未來、人性、媒體、攝影、攝影 。
yann arthusbertrand captures fragile earth in wideangle	雅南.伯特蘭曾捕捉到很脆弱的地球 , 位在廣大的角度 , 形成了很脆弱的地球 。
i have a big impact on the planet to travel here by plane .	我對地球有很大的影響力 , 靠飛機來到這裡 。
i emitted , in the atmosphere , nine tons of co2 ; that is the weight of two elephants .	我在大氣中排放了九噸的二氧化碳 , 這是兩隻大象的重量 。
i came here to speak about ecology , and i emitted as much co2 as a frenchman in one year .	我來到這裡 , 談到生態學 , 一年內我排放的二氧化碳就和法國人一樣多 。
so what do i have to do ?	所以 , 我該怎麼做 ?
i have to kill a frenchman when i come back at home ?	當我回到家時 , 我必須殺死法國人嗎 ?
i have to do my carbon offset in another way , like i do every time .	我得要用另一種方式來抵銷碳 , 就像我每次都這樣做 。
in fact my work is to show our impact on our planet .	事實上 , 我的工作就是向我們展示我們對地球的影響 。
i'm going to show you some examples of the last pictures i've done in the last year .	我要給你們看一些我過去一年所拍攝的照片 。
alberta sand oil , a lot of pollution .	亞伯達石油 , 很多污染 。
you know the problem ; we don't want to believe what we know .	你知道問題 ; 我們不想相信我們所知道的 。
in alberta people work nonstop , 24 hours by seven to extract as much oil as they can .	在阿爾伯達人工作時 , 24小時 , 7個小時 , 盡可能地提取石油 。
we know about the end of oil .	我們知道石油的終點 。
oil sand is not a longterm solution .	石油沙不是長期的解決方案 。
but we use three times more oil than we find every year .	但我們每年用的石油比我們發現的還要多三倍 。
we don't want to believe what we know .	我們不想相信我們所知道的 。
coral reef in new caledonia .	新卡里尼亞的珊瑚礁 。
100 percent of the coral may be wiped out before 2050 because of global warming .	珊瑚的百分之百可能在2050之前就被消滅 , 因為全球暖化 。
and you know how coral are very sensitive to temperature , and are very important for the biodiversity of the sea .	你知道珊瑚對溫度非常敏感 , 對海洋的生物多樣性很重要 。
north pole . i've done this picture last summer .	北極 , 我去年夏天拍了這張照片 。
it was impossible to do this picture 15 years ago .	15年前不可能拍攝這張照片 。
now there is a new way open between atlantic and pacific .	現在 , 大西洋和太平洋之間有一種新的開放方式 。
the thickness of the arctic decreased more than 40 percent since 1960 .	從1960年起 , 北極的厚度減少了超過40% 。
there is a new face of kilimanjaro without ice .	在沒有冰的情況下 , kilimanjaro有新的面孔 。
it lost 80 percent of its ice .	它失去了80%的冰 。
according to scientists , in 100 years all the mountain glacier will be gone .	根據科學家 , 一百年來 , 所有山上的冰河都會消失 。
glaciers are very important for the life on earth .	冰河對地球上生命是很重要的 。
like al gore told you , two billion people live on the water from the glacier of himalaya .	像高爾說過你 , 有二十億人住在喜馬拉雅冰河的水上 。
return of fish men .	回歸魚的男人 。
one fifth of human kind depend on fish to live .	五分之一的人類依賴魚生存 。
today now 70 percent of the fish stock are overexploited .	現今 , 70%的魚儲存被過度利用 。
according to fao , if we don't change our system of fishing the main sea resources will be gone in 2050 .	根據fao的說法 , 如果我們不改變我們在2050年捕撈主要海資源的系統 。
we don't want to believe what we know .	我們不想相信我們所知道的 。
the beautiful picture , by [unclear] in africa .	非洲的美麗照片 。
one human of six have not enough to eat in the world .	六個人中就有一個人不夠吃東西 。
one billion people have not enough to eat .	十億人不夠吃 。
in africa , corn is one of the main foods in many places .	在非洲 , 玉米在許多地方都是主要的食物之一 。
here in america , 90 percent of the corn cultivated is used to feed animals or to do oil .	在美國 , 百分之九十的玉米培養被用來餵養動物 , 或做石油 。
palm tree plantation in borneo .	植物在婆羅的棕櫚樹 。

and i feel humbled by their strength .	我對他們的力量感到謙卑 。

at the moment , my family is very poor , my life here in shenzhen is just about showing myself that i can earn more and to let my parents stay and have something to live on .	目前 , 我的家人非常貧窮 , 我住在深圳這裡的人生 , 只是為了讓自己知道我能賺更多 , 讓我的父母留下來 , 有些東西可以活下來 。

now i am going to speak to you about my movie .	現在我要跟各位談我的電影 。

the name of the movie is " home " " maison . "	電影的名字是 「 家 」 , 「 馬尼森 」 。

video: this earth is four and a half billion years old .	影片:地球已經四十五億年了 。
these plants , several hundred million years old .	這些植物 , 數億年的歷史 。
and we humans have been walking upright for only 200 thousand years .	我們人類已經走向直徑了20萬年 。
we've managed to adapt , and have conquered the whole planet .	我們成功適應了 , 征服了整個星球 。
for generations , we've been raising our children , not unlike millions of other species living beside us .	數世代以來 , 我們一直在養育我們的孩子 , 而不是其他數百萬種物種 , 生活在我們身邊 。
for the past 30 years i've been closely watching the earth and its dwellers from high up in the sky .	過去30年來 , 我很仔細地看著地球和它的居民從天空上升起 。
our life is tied to the wellbeing of our planet .	我們的生命與地球的幸福有關 。
we depend on water , forests , deserts , oceans .	我們依賴水、森林、沙漠、海洋 。
fishing , breeding , farming are still the world's foremost human occupations .	魚類、繁殖、農業 , 仍然是世界上最先進的人類職業 。
and what binds us together is far greater than what divides us .	把我們結合在一起 , 遠比我們分裂的更大 。
we all share the same need for the earth's gifts the same wish to rise above ourselves , and become better .	我們都一樣對地球的禮物有同樣的需求 , 希望在我們自己上升 , 變得更好 。
and yet we carry on raising walls to keep us apart .	然而 , 我們仍繼續提高牆壁 , 讓我們無法分開 。
today our greatest battle is to protect the natural offerings of our planet .	現今 , 我們最大的戰役是保護地球的天然資源 。
in less than 50 years we've altered it more thoroughly than in the entire history of mankind .	不到50年 , 我們徹底地改變它 , 比人類的整個歷史還要徹底 。
half of the world's forests have vanished .	世界上一半的森林都消失了 。
water resources are running low .	水資源在下降 。
intensive farming is depleting soils .	密集農業正在耗盡土壤 。
our energy sources are not sustainable .	我們的能量來源不是永續的 。
the climate is changing .	氣候正在改變 。
we are endangering ourselves .	我們正在危害自己 。
we're only trying to improve our lives .	我們只想改善我們的生活 。
but the wealth gaps are growing wider .	但財富差距越來越大 。
we haven't yet understood that we're going at a much faster pace than the planet can sustain .	我們尚未了解 , 我們要達到的速度比地球能維持的速度還要快 。
we know that solutions are available today .	我們知道 , 現今的解決方案是可用的 。
we all have the power to change this trend for the better .	我們都有改變這個趨勢的力量 。
so what are we waiting for ?	所以 , 我們在等什麼 ?

in this accessible talk from tedxboston , richard resnick shows how cheap and fast genome sequencing is about to turn health care upside down .	在這場tedxboston的演講中 , 理查.resnick展示了如何便宜且快速的基因組定序將會把健康照護顛倒 。
dna , biotech , health care , science , technology	dna、生物科技、健康照護、科學、科技、科技、科技、科技、科技、dna、生物科技、
richard resnick: welcome to the genomic revolution	理查.雷尼克:歡迎來到基因革命 。
ladies and gentlemen , i present to you the human genome .	各位先生女士 , 我向你們展示人類基因組 。
chromosome one , top left .	染色體 , 左上方 。
bottom right are the sex chromosomes .	右下角是性染色體 。
women have two copies of that big x chromosome ; men have the x and , of course , that small copy of the y .	女性有兩個x染色體的複製品 ; 男性有x , 當然 , 還有y的小複製品 。
sorry boys , but it's just a tiny little thing that makes you different .	抱歉男孩 , 但這只是一件小事 , 讓你有所不同 。
so if you zoom in on this genome , then what you see , of course , is this double helix structure the code of life spelled out with these four biochemical letters , or we call them bases , right: a , c , g and t .	所以如果你放大這個基因組 , 你可以看到 , 這雙螺旋結構是生命的編碼 , 用這四個生物化學字母拼出來 , 或我們稱它們為鹼基 , 右邊是:a、g、t 。
how many are there in the human genome ? three billion .	在人類基因組中有多少 ? 30億 。
is that a big number ?	這是個大數字嗎 ?
well , everybody can throw around big numbers .	嗯 , 每個人都可以投擲大量的數字 。
but in fact , if i were to place one base on each pixel of this 1280 by 800 resolution screen , we would need 3 , 000 screens to take a look at the genome .	但事實上 , 如果我把這1280像素的每一個像素點放到800個解析度螢幕上 , 我們需要3000個螢幕來觀察基因組 。
so it's really quite big .	所以它真的很大 。
and perhaps because of its size , a group of people all , by the way , with y chromosomes decided they would want to sequence it .	也許是因為它的大小 , 一群人 , 順道一提 , y染色體決定他們會想要定序 。
and so 15 years , actually , and about four billion dollars later , the genome was sequenced and published .	15年後 , 實際上 , 大約40億美金後 , 基因組被定序並發表 。
in 2003 , the final version was published , and they keep working on it .	2003年 , 最後的版本被發表了 , 他們繼續研究它 。
that was all done on a machine that looks like this .	這一切都在機器上完成 , 看起來像這樣 。
it costs about a dollar for each base a very slow way of doing it .	每一塊一塊錢 , 每一塊錢的成本都很緩慢 。
well folks , i'm here to tell you that the world has completely changed and none of you know about it .	嗯 , 我來這裡要告訴各位 , 世界已經完全改變 , 沒有人知道這個世界 。
so now what we do is we take a genome , we make maybe 50 copies of it , we cut all those copies up into little 50base reads , and then we sequence them , massively parallel .	所以現在我們要做的是把基因組做成50個複製 , 我們把所有複製品切成50個鹼基閱讀 , 然後我們將它們定序 , 相當平行 。
and then we bring that into software , and we reassemble it and we tell you what the story is .	然後我們將這個軟體放入軟體中 , 我們重新組合 , 告訴你這個故事是什麼 。
and so just to give you a picture of what this looks like , the human genome project: 3 gigabases , right .	所以 , 給各位看這張圖片 , 人類基因組計畫:3gbabes , 對 。
one run on one of these machines: 200 gigabases in a week .	一個在其中一台機器上跑:一週內有200gbas 。
and that 200 is going to change to 600 this summer , and there's no sign of this pace slowing .	今年夏天將有600個改變 , 沒有這種減速的跡象 。
so the price of a base , to sequence a base , has fallen 100 million times .	所以基地的價格下降了一億倍 。
that's the equivalent of you filling up your car with gas in 1998 , waiting until 2011 , and now you can drive to jupiter and back twice .	等同於1998年填滿你的車輛 , 等到2011年 , 現在你可以開車到木星再回來兩次 。
world population , pc placements , the archive of all the medical literature , moore's law , the old way of sequencing , and here's all the new stuff .	世界人口、pc地點、醫療文獻、摩爾定律、舊方式定序 , 所有新東西 。
guys , this is a log scale ; you don't typically see lines that go up like that .	各位 , 這是個邏輯尺度 ; 你通常不會看到像這樣的線條 。
so the worldwide capacity to sequence human genomes is something like 50 , 000 to 100 , 000 human genomes this year .	人類基因組測序的能力是今年五萬到十萬個人類基因組 。
and we know this based on the machines that are being placed .	我們知道這個基於被放置的機器 。
this is expected to double , triple or maybe quadruple year over year for the foreseeable future .	這是預期的兩倍、三倍或四倍的未來 。
in fact , there's one lab in particular that represents 20 percent of all that capacity .	事實上 , 特別有一間實驗室代表所有能力的20% 。
it's called the beijing genomics institute .	叫做北京基因學研究所 。
the chinese are absolutely winning this race to the new moon , by the way .	中國人絕對贏了這個新月球 , 順便一提 。
what does this mean for medicine ?	這對醫學意味著什麼 ?
so a woman is age 37 .	一個女人37歲 。
she presents with stage 2 estrogen receptorpositive breast cancer .	她帶著2個雌激素接受器官的乳癌 。
she is treated with surgery , chemotherapy and radiation .	她接受手術、化療和輻射治療 。
two years later , she comes back with stage three c ovarian cancer .	兩年後 , 她帶著第三個卵巢癌 。
unfortunately , treated again with surgery and chemotherapy .	不幸的是 , 再次接受手術和化療治療 。
she comes back three years later at age 42 with more ovarian cancer , more chemotherapy .	三年後 , 她回到了42歲 , 患有更多卵巢癌 , 更多的化療 。
six months later , she comes back with acute myeloid leukemia .	六個月後 , 她帶著急性白血病回來 。
she goes into respiratory failure and dies eight days later .	她走進呼吸道失敗的8天後死去 。
so first , the way in which this woman was treated , in as little as 10 years , will look like bloodletting .	首先 , 這位女士在十年內被治療的方式 , 看起來會像血液循環一樣 。
and it's because of people like my colleague , rick wilson , at the genome institute at washington university , who decided to take a look at this woman postmortem .	由於像我同事rickwilson這樣的人在華盛頓大學的基因組研究所他決定看這位女子
and he sequenced , he took skin cells , healthy skin , and cancerous bone marrow , and he sequenced the whole genomes of both of them in a couple of weeks , no big deal .	他的基因序列 , 將皮膚細胞、健康的皮膚和癌症骨髓定序 , 幾週內 , 兩者的基因組 , 沒有什麼大不了的 。
and then he compared those two genomes in software , and what he found , among other things , was a deletion , a 2 , 000base deletion across three billion bases in a particular gene called tp53 .	接著 , 他比較了軟體中這兩種基因組 , 他發現 , 其它東西之一 , 是廢棄物 , 兩千多個鹼基 , 在一個叫做tp53的基因中 , 一個叫做tp53的基因 。
if you have this deleterious mutation in this gene , you're 90 percent likely to get cancer in your life .	如果你在這個基因中有這種惡性突變 , 你的生命中有90%的可能性會罹患癌症 。
so unfortunately , this doesn't help this woman , but it does have severe , profound if you will , implications to her family .	不幸的是 , 這並不能幫助這位女士 , 但這確實有嚴重、深刻的意義 , 影響她的家人 。
i mean , if they have the same mutation , and they get this genetic test , and they understand it , then they can go and get regular screens , and they can catch cancer early and potentially live a significantly longer life .	我的意思是 , 如果它們有相同的突變 , 它們會得到這個基因測試 , 它們會了解它 , 那麼它們會去取得常規的螢幕 , 它們可以早期發現癌症 , 且有可能活得更久 。
let me introduce you now to the beery twins , diagnosed with cerebral palsy at the age of two .	讓我向你們介紹beery雙胞胎 , 在2歲時 , 被診斷出腦性麻痺症 。
their mom is a very brave woman who didn't believe that the symptoms weren't matching up , and through some heroic efforts and a lot of internet searching , she was able to convince the medical community that , in fact , they had something else .	他們的母親是一位非常勇敢的女人 , 她不相信症狀不會跟上 , 透過一些英雄的努力和許多網路搜尋 , 她能夠說服醫學界 , 事實上 , 他們還有別的東西 。
what they had was doparesponsive dystonia .	他們有的是反對的失調症 。
and so they were given ldopa , and their symptoms did improve , but they weren't totally asymptomatic .	所以他們得到了ldopa , 他們的症狀也改善了 , 但他們並沒有完全的症狀 。
turns out the gentleman in this picture is a guy named joe beery , who was lucky enough to be the cio of a company called life technologies .	原來這張照片裡的先生是joebeery的傢伙 , 他很幸運成為一家叫做 「 生命科技 」 的公司 。
they're one of the two companies that makes these massive whole genome sequencing tools .	它們是兩家公司 , 製造出大量基因組定序的工具之一 。
and so what he did was he got his kids sequenced .	他做的是讓他的孩子做定序 。
and what they found was a series of mutations in a gene called spr , which is responsible for producing serotonin , among other things .	他們發現的是一系列的突變 , 一種叫做spr的基因 , 它負責生產血清素 , 其它東西 。
so on top of ldopa , they gave these kids a serotonin precursor drug , and they're effectively normal now .	所以在烏托邦的頂端 , 他們給這些孩子一個血清素前吸毒 , 現在他們很正常 。
guys , this would never have happened without whole genome sequencing .	各位 , 沒有完整的基因序列 , 這絕對不會發生 。

the year after it's $100 , give or take a year .	一百美金 , 給或花一年後 。

so here's little nick likes batman and squirt guns .	這有點像蝙蝠俠和松鼠槍 。
and it turns out nick shows up at the children's hospital with this distended belly like a famine victim .	結果發現尼克出現在兒童醫院 , 帶著這種偏離的肚子 , 就像是饑荒受害者 。
and it's not that he's not eating , it's that when he eats , his intestine basically opens up and feces spill out into his gut .	不是他沒有吃飯 , 而是當他吃飯時 , 他的腸子基本上會打開 , 餵食從他的腸子中吐出來 。
so a hundred surgeries later , he looks at his mom and says , " mom , please pray for me . i'm in so much pain . "	一百個手術後 , 他看著他的媽媽 , 說: 「 媽 , 請為我禱告 。 我非常痛苦 。 」

so the theory is that he's having some immunological reaction to what's going on to the food essentially , and that's a natural reaction , which causes some programmed cell death .	理論是 , 他對食物本質上發生的免疫反應有一些免疫反應 , 這是一種自然反應 , 造成了一些程式化的細胞死亡 。

we're sending his marrow across the country to save the life of a child with leukemia .	我們把他的骨髓送到全國 , 以拯救白血病孩童的生命 。
so actually how do we harvest this bone marrow ?	所以 , 我們要如何收集這些骨髓 ?
well we have a whole o . r . team , general anesthesia , nurses , and another doctor across from me .	我們有一整個o.r.團隊 , 普通麻醉、護士 , 還有另一位醫師 。
bob's on the table , and we take this sort of small needle , you know , not too big .	鮑勃站在桌上 , 我們拿著這個小針 , 你知道的 , 不是太大 。
and the way we do this is we basically place this through the soft tissue , and kind of punch it into the hard bone , into the tuchus that's a technical term and aspirate about 10 mls of bone marrow out , each time , with a syringe .	基本上 , 我們用柔軟的組織將它放到硬骨上 , 進入到管子裡 , 一個技術上的術語 , 每次用針筒挖出10磅的骨髓 。
and hand it off to the nurse . she squirts it into a tin .	把它交給護士 。 她把護士放進一個薄片裡 。
hands it back to me . and we do that again and again .	把它們交給我 。 我們一而再再而三地這樣做 。
about 200 times usually .	通常是兩百次 。
and by the end of this my arm is sore , i've got a callus on my hand , let alone bob , whose rear end looks something more like this , like swiss cheese .	到了我的手臂結束後 , 我手上有一支打招呼 , 更不用說鮑勃 , 他的屁股看起來像這樣 , 像瑞士起士 。
so i'm thinking , you know , this procedure hasn't changed in about 40 years .	我在想 , 這個程序在40年內沒有改變 。
and there is probably a better way to do this .	這樣做可能還有更好的方法 。
so i thought of a minimally invasive approach , and a new device that we call the marrow miner .	所以我想到一個最低侵入性的方法 , 我們稱之為骨髓礦物 。
and the marrow miner , the way it works is shown here .	而骨髓礦物 , 它的運作方式在這裡 。
our standard seethrough patient .	我們的標準可見病人 。
instead of entering the bone dozens of times , we enter just once , into the front of the hip or the back of the hip .	與其進入骨頭數十次 , 我們進入了一次 , 進入髖骨或髖骨的前面 。
and we have a flexible , powered catheter with a special wire loop tip that stays inside the crunchy part of the marrow and follows the contours of the hip , as it moves around .	我們有一個彈性、強力的導管 , 帶著一個特殊的電線循環 , 留在骨髓中 , 跟著骨髓的輪廓 , 繞著骨髓移動 。
so it enables you to very rapidly aspirate , or suck out , rich bone marrow very quickly through one hole .	所以它讓你可以很快速地得到靈感 , 或吸取豐富的骨髓 , 很快地通過一個洞 。
we can do multiple passes through that same entry .	我們可以通過相同的入口進行多次傳遞 。
and , so , very quickly , bob can just get one puncture , local anesthesia , and do this harvest as an outpatient .	所以 , 很快地 , 鮑勃只能用一針針針刺 , 當地的麻醉 , 把收穫做成耐心 。
so i did a few prototypes . i got a small little grant at stanford .	所以我做了一些原型 。 我在史丹佛得到了一個小小的補助 。
and played around with this a little bit .	再玩一下 。
and our team members developed this technology .	我們的團隊成員開發了這項技術 。
and eventually we got two large animals , and pig studies .	最後我們得到了兩個大型動物 , 豬研究 。
and we found , to our surprise , that we not only got bone marrow out , but we got 10 times the stem cell activity in the marrow from the marrow miner , compared to the normal device .	我們發現 , 令人驚訝的是 , 我們不只拿出骨髓 , 我們還收到了10倍的幹細胞活動 , 從骨髓礦物質的10倍 , 相較於正常的裝置 。
this device was just fda approved in the last year .	這個裝置在去年才被核准 。
here is a live patient . you can see it following the flexible curves around .	這裡是現場的病人 , 你可以看到它跟著彈性的曲線 。
there will be two passes here , in the same patient , from the same hole .	同一個病人 , 在同一個洞裡 , 會有兩個過來 。
this was done under local anesthesia , as an outpatient .	這是在本地麻醉的情況下進行的 。
and we got , again , about three to six times more stem cells than the standard approach done on the same patient .	同樣的 , 我們得到的幹細胞 , 比同一個病人用的標準來得多3到6倍 。
so why should you care ? bone marrow is a very rich source of adult stem cells .	你為什麼要在乎 ? 骨髓是成人幹細胞非常豐富的來源 。
you all know about embryonic stem cells .	你們都知道胚胎幹細胞 。
they've got great potential but haven't yet entered clinical trials .	他們有很大的潛力 , 但尚未進入臨床試驗 。
adult stem cells are throughout our body , including the bloodforming stem cells in our bone marrow , which we've been using as a form of stemcell therapy for over 40 years .	成人幹細胞遍佈我們的身體 , 包括骨髓中的血液循環幹細胞 , 我們已經用它作為幹細胞治療的形式 , 已經超過40年了 。
in the last decade there's been an explosion of use of bone marrow stem cells to treat the patient's other diseases such as heart disease , vascular disease , orthopedics , tissue engineering , even in neurology to treat parkinson's and diabetes .	在過去的十年中 , 用骨髓幹細胞來治療病人的其他疾病 , 例如心臟病、血管疾病、血管疾病、組織工程 , 甚至神經科醫師來治療帕金森氏症和糖尿病 。
we've just come out , we're commercializing , this year , generation 2 . 0 of the marrow miner .	我們才剛出櫃 , 今年 , 我們在商業化 , 2.0的骨髓礦物 。
the hope is that this gets more stem cells out , which translates to better outcomes .	希望這能讓更多幹細胞發揮作用 , 轉譯成更好的結果 。
it may encourage more people to sign up to be potential livesaving bone marrow donors .	它可能會鼓勵更多人登記 , 成為潛在生命的骨髓捐贈者 。
it may even enable you to bank your own marrow stem cells , when you're younger and healthier , to use in the future should you need it .	它甚至可能讓你能夠銀行你自己的骨髓幹細胞 , 當你更年輕、更健康時 , 用在未來你應該需要它 。
and ultimately and here's a picture of our bone marrow transplant survivors , who come together for a reunion each year at stanford .	最終 , 這張照片是我們骨髓移植的倖存者 , 他們每年都在史丹佛聚會 。
hopefully this technology will let us have more of these survivors in the future .	希望這項技術能讓我們在未來有更多的倖存者 。
physicist and surfer garrett lisi presents a controversial new model of the universe that just maybe answers all the big questions . if nothing else , it's the most beautiful 8dimensional model of elementary particles and forces you've ever seen .	物理學家和衝浪者葛瑞特•萊西在宇宙中展現了一種爭議性的新模式 , 可能只能回答所有大問題 。 如果沒有其他的 , 它是最美麗的 「 基本粒子 」 模型 , 和 「 力 」 。
physics , science , technology	物理、科學、科技、技術、
garrett lisi on his theory of everything	格雷特•萊西在他的理論上 , 所有事物的理論都有 。
whoa , dude . check out those killer equations . sweet .	哇 ! 老兄 。 看看那些殺手方程式 。
actually , for the next 18 minutes i'm going to do the best i can to describe the beauty of particle physics without equations .	事實上 , 接下來的18分鐘 , 我要盡我所能描述粒子物理的美麗 , 不用方程式來描述 。
it turns out there's a lot we can learn from coral .	結果發現 , 我們可以從珊瑚身上學到很多 。
coral is a very beautiful and unusual animal .	珊瑚是一種非常美麗且特別的動物 。
each coral head consists of thousand of individual polyps .	每個珊瑚的頭部都是一千個個個體的聚合物 。
these polyps are continually budding and branching into genetically identical neighbors .	這些聚合物不斷地推動並分成基因相同的鄰居 。
if we imagine this to be a hyperintelligent coral , we can single out an individual and ask him a reasonable question .	如果我們想像這是一個超級智慧的珊瑚 , 我們能單獨的分離 , 並問他一個合理的問題 。
we can ask how exactly he got to be in this particular location compared to his neighbors if it was just chance , or destiny , or what ?	我們可以問他在這個特定的位置與鄰居相比 , 如果只是機會 , 或命運 , 又怎樣 ?
now , after admonishing us for turning the temperature up too high , he would tell us that our question was completely stupid .	在我們要求將溫度變高之後 , 他會告訴我們 , 我們的問題是完全愚蠢的 。
these corals can be quite kind of mean , you see , and i have surfing scars to prove that .	這些珊瑚的意思是 , 你看 , 我有衝浪的疤痕來證明它 。
but this polyp would continue and tell us that his neighbors were quite clearly identical copies of him .	但這隻多利普會繼續告訴我們 , 他的鄰居很明顯是他相同的複本 。
that he was in all these other locations as well , but experiencing them as separate individuals .	他也處在其他地方 , 但身為獨立的個體 。
for a coral , branching into different copies is the most natural thing in the world .	對珊瑚而言 , 分成不同的複製品是世界上最自然的東西 。
unlike us , a hyperintelligent coral would be uniquely prepared to understand quantum mechanics .	和我們不同 , 超級聰明的珊瑚會是獨一無二的準備 , 來了解量子力學 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics very accurately describes how our universe works .	量子力學的數學非常準確地描述我們的宇宙是如何運作的 。
and it tells us our reality is continually branching into different possibilities , just like a coral .	它告訴我們 , 我們的現實是不斷分成不同的可能性 , 就像珊瑚一樣 。
it's a weird thing for us humans to wrap our minds around , since we only ever get to experience one possibility .	對我們人類來說這是一件奇怪的事 , 因為我們只能體驗一個可能性 。
this quantum weirdness was first described by erwin schrödinger and his cat .	這個量子奇怪的最初是由erwinschordinger和他的貓所描述 。
the cat likes this version better .	貓喜歡這個版本 。
in this setup , schrödinger is in a box with a radioactive sample that , by the laws of quantum mechanics , branches into a state in which it is radiated and a state in which it is not .	在這個裝置中 , 薛丁格在一個裝有放射性樣本的盒子裡 , 由量子力學定律 , 分支成一種狀態 , 它是被輻射及狀態的狀態 。
in the branch in which the sample radiates , it sets off a trigger that releases poison and schrödinger is dead .	在該樣本放射線的分支中 , 它會產生一種觸發 , 釋放毒藥和薛丁格死了 。
but in the other branch of reality , he remains alive .	但在現實的另一個分支中 , 他仍然活著 。
these realities are experienced separately by each individual .	這些現實都被每個人獨立的體驗 。
as far as either can tell , the other one doesn't exist .	無論如何 , 另一種都不存在 。
this seems weird to us , because each of us only experiences an individual existence , and we don't get to see other branches .	這對我們來說很奇怪 , 因為我們每個人都只會經歷個人存在 , 而我們卻無法看到其他分支 。
it's as if each of us , like schrödinger here , are a kind of coral branching into different possibilities .	彷彿我們每一個人 , 像薛丁格一樣 , 都是一種珊瑚分支 , 變成不同的可能性 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics tells us this is how the world works at tiny scales .	量子力學的數學告訴我們 , 世界如何在微小的尺度上運作 。
it can be summed up in a single sentence: everything that can happen , does .	它可以在單一句話中總結:所有可能發生的一切 。
but this does not mean everything happens .	但這並不表示每件事都會發生 。
the rest of physics is about describing what can happen and what can't .	物理的其他部分是描述可能發生什麼事 , 以及什麼是不可行的 。
what physics tells us is that everything comes down to geometry and the interactions of elementary particles .	物理告訴我們 , 一切都歸功於幾何學和基本粒子的互動 。
and things can happen only if these interactions are perfectly balanced .	只有在這些互動完全平衡的情況下 , 情況才會發生 。
now i'll go ahead and describe how we know about these particles , what they are and how this balance works .	現在我要向前描述我們對這些粒子的認識 , 它們是如何運作的 , 以及這個平衡如何運作 。
in this machine , a beam of protons and antiprotons are accelerated to near the speed of light and brought together in a collision , producing a burst of pure energy .	在這個機器中 , 一道質子和反物質的一道接近光速 , 並在碰撞中產生出純能量 。
this energy is immediately converted into a spray of subatomic particles , with detectors and computers used to figure out their properties .	這種能量馬上被轉換成亞原子粒子噴灑 , 用以前的偵測器和電腦來找出它們的特性 。
this enormous machine the large hadron collider at cern in geneva has a circumference of 17 miles and , when it's operating , draws five times as much power as the city of monterey .	這台巨大的機器 , 日內瓦的大型強子對撞機有17英里的圓圈 , 當它在運作時 , 它的電力和蒙特雷市的電力差不多五倍 。
we can't predict specifically what particles will be produced in any individual collision .	我們不能明確地預測哪些粒子會在任何個別碰撞中產生 。
quantum mechanics tells us all possibilities are realized .	量子力學告訴我們所有可能性 。
but physics does tell us what particles can be produced .	但物理學確實告訴我們哪些粒子能產生什麼 。
these particles must have just as much mass and energy as is carried in by the proton and antiproton .	這些粒子必須有相同的質量和能量 , 就像質子和反粒子一樣 。
any particles more massive than this energy limit aren't produced , and remain invisible to us .	任何比這個能量限制更大的粒子都無法產出 , 且對我們來說保持隱形 。
this is why this new particle accelerator is so exciting .	這就是為什麼這個新粒子加速器這麼令人興奮 。
it's going to push this energy limit seven times beyond what's ever been done before , so we're going to get to see some new particles very soon .	它會把能源限制在過去七倍之外 , 所以我們很快就會看到一些新粒子 。
but before talking about what we might see , let me describe the particles we already know of .	但在談談我們可能看到的之前 , 讓我描述一下我們已經知道的粒子 。
there's a whole zoo of subatomic particles .	有一大堆亞原子粒子 。
most of us are familiar with electrons .	我們大部分人都熟悉電子 。
a lot of people in this room make a good living pushing them around .	在這間房間裡 , 很多人會做一個好的活力推動他們 。
but the electron also has a neutral partner called the neutrino , with no electric charge and a very tiny mass .	但電子也有中性伴侶 , 叫做中子 , 沒有電荷和一個非常小的質量 。
in contrast , the upanddown quarks have very large masses , and combine in threes to make the protons and neutrons inside atoms .	相較之下 , 上方的夸克有很大的質量 , 三者結合 , 讓質子和中子在原子裡面 。
all of these matter particles come in left and righthanded varieties , and have antiparticle partners that carry opposite charges .	所有這些物質粒子都出現在左右 , 各式各樣的反粒子 , 帶著相反載荷的反粒子 。
these familiar particles also have less familiar second and third generations , which have the same charges as the first but have much higher masses .	這些熟悉的粒子也比較不熟悉的第二代和第三代 , 和第一代相同的載荷 , 但質量較高 。
these matter particles all interact with the various force particles .	這些物質粒子都與不同的力粒子互動 。
the electromagnetic force interacts with electrically charged matter via particles called photons .	電磁力會透過稱為光子的粒子 , 與電導電物質互動 。
there is also a very weak force called , rather unimaginatively , the weak force , that interacts only with lefthanded matter .	還有一種非常微弱的力量 , 叫做 「 虛弱的力量 」 , 只和左撇子有所互動 。
the strong force acts between quarks which carry a different kind of charge , called color charge , and come in three different varieties: red , green and blue .	夸克之間的強力作用 , 帶著不同的載荷 , 叫做顏色載荷 , 三種不同的品種:紅、綠和藍 。
you can blame murray gellmann for these names they're his fault .	你可以怪murraygellmann , 他們是他的錯 。
finally , there's the force of gravity , which interacts with matter via its mass and spin .	最後 , 重力的力量是透過質量和旋轉的物質相互作用的 。
the most important thing to understand here is that there's a different kind of charge associated with each of these forces .	最重要的是 , 每一股力量都有不同的載荷 。
these four different forces interact with matter according to the corresponding charges that each particle has .	這四種不同的力量相互作用 , 根據每個粒子都有的相對載荷 。
a particle that hasn't been seen yet , but we're pretty sure exists , is the higgs particle , which gives masses to all these other particles .	目前還沒見過的粒子 , 但我們非常確定存在 , 是希格斯粒子 , 它給了所有其他粒子的質量 。
the main purpose of the large hadron collider is to see this higgs particle , and we're almost certain it will .	大型強子對撞機的主要目的是看到希格斯粒子 , 我們幾乎確定它會 。
but the greatest mystery is what else we might see .	但最大的謎團是我們還能看到的 。
and i'm going to show you one beautiful possibility towards the end of this talk .	我要給你們看一段美麗的可能性 , 讓你們看看這場演說的尾聲 。
now , if we count up all these different particles using their various spins and charges , there are 226 .	現在 , 如果我們用不同的旋轉和載荷計算所有不同的粒子 , 會有226個 。
that's a lot of particles to keep track of .	要追蹤很多粒子 。
and it seems strange that nature would have so many elementary particles .	大自然會有這麼多的基本粒子 。
but if we plot them out according to their charges , some beautiful patterns emerge .	但如果我們根據他們的指控來繪製它們 , 有些美麗的圖案就會浮現出來 。
the most familiar charge is electric charge .	最熟悉的電荷就是電荷 。
electrons have an electric charge , a negative one , and quarks have electric charges in thirds .	電子有電荷 , 負電荷 , 夸克有三分之一的電荷 。
so when two up quarks and a down quark are combined to make a proton , it has a total electric charge of plus one .	所以當兩個上方的夸克和一個下夸克結合成一個質子時 , 總電荷加上1 。
these particles also have antiparticles , which have opposite charges .	這些粒子也有反粒子 , 有相反的載荷 。
now , it turns out the electric charge is actually a combination of two other charges: hypercharge and weak charge .	結果發現 , 電荷其實是兩種載荷的組合:超荷和弱荷 。
if we spread out the hypercharge and weak charge and plot the charges of particles in this twodimensional charge space , the electric charge is where these particles sit along the vertical direction .	如果我們把超連結和弱載荷散開 , 並在這個二維載荷空間中畫出粒子的載荷 , 電荷就是這些粒子在垂直方向的位置 。
the electromagnetic and weak forces interact with matter according to their hypercharge and weak charge , which make this pattern .	電磁力和弱力相互作用 , 根據他們的超連結和弱荷 , 產生這種模式 。
this is called the unified electroweak model , and it was put together back in 1967 .	這叫做 「 統一的電子爆炸模型 」 , 它在1967年被組合起來 。
the reason most of us are only familiar with electric charge and not both of these is because of the higgs particle .	我們之所以熟悉電荷 , 是因為希格斯粒子 。
the higgs , over here on the left , has a large mass and breaks the symmetry of this electroweak pattern .	左邊的是希格斯 , 有一個很大的質量 , 打破了這次發射模式的對稱性 。
it makes the weak force very weak by giving the weak particles a large mass .	它使弱力非常弱 , 藉由給弱粒子一個大質量 。
since this massive higgs sits along the horizontal direction in this diagram , the photons of electromagnetism remain massless and interact with electric charge along the vertical direction in this charge space .	由於這個巨大的希格斯位於這個圖形的水平方向 , 電磁學的光子仍然沒有質量 , 與電荷在這個載荷空間的垂直方向相互作用 。
so the electromagnetic and weak forces are described by this pattern of particle charges in twodimensional space .	所以電磁力和弱力被二維空間中的粒子載荷所描述 。
we can include the strong force by spreading out its two charge directions and plotting the charges of the force particles in quarks along these directions .	我們可以把強大的力量擴散出兩個載荷方向 , 畫出這些粒子的載荷 。
the charges of all known particles can be plotted in a fourdimensional charge space , and projected down to two dimensions like this so we can see them .	所有已知粒子的載荷可以在四度載荷空間中繪製 , 投射到像這樣的二維空間 , 這樣我們就能看見它們 。
whenever particles interact , nature keeps things in a perfect balance along all four of these charge directions .	每當粒子相互作用時 , 大自然就會在四個載荷方向中保持完美的平衡 。
if a particle and an antiparticle collide , it creates a burst of energy and a total charge of zero in all four charge directions .	如果粒子和反粒子相撞 , 它會產生能量爆炸 , 總共有四個載荷方向 。
at this point , anything can be created as long as it has the same energy and maintains a total charge of zero .	在這個時點 , 任何東西都可以產生 , 只要它有相同的能量 , 維持總量的0 。
for example , this weak force particle and its antiparticle can be created in a collision .	例如 , 這種弱力粒子和它的反粒子在碰撞中產生 。
in further interactions , the charges must always balance .	在更進一步的互動中 , 載荷必須總是平衡 。
one of the weak particles could decay into an electron and an antineutrino , and these three still add to zero total charge .	其中一個微弱的粒子會腐爛成電子和一個反中子 , 這三種仍然加上零載荷 。
nature always keeps a perfect balance .	大自然總是保持完美的平衡 。
so these patterns of charges are not just pretty .	所以這些載荷的模式不僅很漂亮 。
they tell us what interactions are allowed to happen .	他們告訴我們什麼是互動的發生 。
and we can rotate this charge space in four dimensions to get a better look at the strong interaction , which has this nice hexagonal symmetry .	我們可以在四度空間中旋轉載荷空間 , 來更好地看一下強大的互動 , 這種對稱性很棒 。
in a strong interaction , a strong force particle , such as this one , interacts with a colored quark , such as this green one , to give a quark with a different color charge this red one .	在強力的互動中 , 強力粒子 , 例如這個 , 與有色的夸克互動 , 例如這個綠色的方塊 , 給夸克一個不同的顏色載荷 。
and strong interactions are happening millions of times each second in every atom of our bodies , holding the atomic nuclei together .	強烈的互動每秒鐘都會發生數百萬次在我們身體的每個原子中 , 將原子核結合在一起 。
but these four charges corresponding to three forces are not the end of the story .	但這四個載荷對應三種力量並不是故事的結局 。
we can also include two more charges corresponding to the gravitational force .	我們還可以再加上兩個載荷 , 與重力相對應 。
when we include these , each matter particle has two different spin charges , spinup and spindown .	當我們把它們納入其中 , 每個粒子都有兩個不同的旋轉 , 旋轉和旋轉 。
so they all split , and give a nice pattern in sixdimensional charge space .	所以它們都分裂了 , 在六度載荷空間中 , 給出一個很好的圖案 。
we can rotate this pattern in six dimensions , and see that it's quite pretty .	我們可以在六度空間中旋轉這個模式 , 看看它相當漂亮 。
right now , this pattern matches our best current knowledge of how nature is built at the tiny scales of these elementary particles .	目前 , 這種模式符合我們目前最好的知識 , 了解大自然是如何在這些基本粒子的小尺度上建造出來的 。
this is what we know for certain .	這就是我們所知道的 。
some of these particles are at the very limit of what we've been able to reach with experiments .	有些粒子正處於非常極限的實驗中 。
from this pattern , we already know the particle physics of these tiny scales . the way the universe works with these tiny scales is very beautiful .	從這個圖案中 , 我們已經知道這些小尺度的粒子物理 。 宇宙與這些微小的尺度合作的方式非常漂亮 。
but now i'm going to discuss some new and old ideas about things we don't know yet .	但現在我要討論一些我們還不知道的新想法 。
we want to expand this pattern using mathematics alone , and see if we can get our hands on the whole enchilada .	我們只想用數學來拓展這個模式 , 看看我們能不能掌握整個enchilada的手 。
we want to find all the particles and forces that make a complete picture of our universe .	我們想要找到所有的粒子和力 , 讓整個宇宙的全貌 。
and we want to use this picture to predict new particles that we'll see when experiments reach higher energies .	我們想要用這張照片來預測新粒子當實驗達到更高的能量時 。
so there's an old idea in particle physics that this known pattern of charges , which is not very symmetric , could emerge from a more perfect pattern that gets broken similar to how the higgs particle breaks the electroweak pattern to give electromagnetism .	在粒子物理學中有一個古老的想法 , 這種已知的載荷模式 , 不對稱 , 可以從一個更完美的模式中浮現出來 , 讓希格斯粒子斷裂 , 讓電磁體產生電磁性 。
in order to do this , we need to introduce new forces with new charge directions .	為了做到這一點 , 我們需要用新的載荷方向介紹新力量 。
when we introduce a new direction , we get to guess what charges the particles have along this direction , and then we can rotate it in with the others .	當我們介紹一個新的方向時 , 我們會猜測這些粒子的載荷方向 , 然後我們可以和其他的粒子旋轉 。
if we guess wisely , we can construct the standard charges in six charge dimensions as a broken symmetry of this more perfect pattern in seven charge dimensions .	假如我們有智慧 , 我們可以在六度載荷中建立標準載荷 , 在七度載荷的對稱中 , 建立一個更完美的模式 。
this particular choice corresponds to a grand unified theory introduced by pati and salam in 1973 .	在1973年 , 這個特殊的選擇對應了1973年由pati和salam所引導 。
when we look at this new unified pattern , we can see a couple of gaps where particles seem to be missing .	當我們看這個新的統一模式時 , 我們可以看到粒子似乎缺少了幾個落差 。
this is the way theories of unification work .	這就是統一理論的運作方式 。
a physicist looks for larger , more symmetric patterns that include the established pattern as a subset .	物理學家尋求更大、更對稱的模式 , 把既有的模式當作一個子組 。
the larger pattern allows us to predict the existence of particles that have never been seen .	更大的模式讓我們能夠預測從未見過的粒子存在 。
this unification model predicts the existence of these two new force particles , which should act a lot like the weak force , only weaker .	這個統一模型預測了這兩種新力粒子的存在 , 應該要像弱力一樣 , 只會變弱 。
now we can rotate this set of charges in seven dimensions and consider an odd fact about the matter particles: the second and third generations of matter have exactly the same charges in sixdimensional charge space as the first generation .	現在 , 我們可以在七度空間中旋轉載荷 , 考慮到物質粒子的奇怪事實:第二代和第三代物質在六度載荷空間中有完全相同的載荷 。
these particles are not uniquely identified by their six charges .	這些粒子沒有獨特辨識出它們的六個載荷 。
they sit on top of one another in the standard charge space .	他們坐在標準載荷空間的另一端 。
however , if we work in eightdimensional charge space , then we can assign unique new charges to each particle .	然而 , 如果我們在八度載荷空間中工作 , 那麼我們就能將獨特的新載荷分配給每個粒子 。
then we can spin these in eight dimensions , and see what the whole pattern looks like .	接著 , 我們可以在八度空間中旋轉 , 看看整體的圖案是什麼樣子 。
here we can see the second and third generations of matter now related to the first generation by a symmetry called " triality . "	在這裡 , 我們可以看到第二代和第三代的物質 , 與第一個世代的對稱性有關 , 叫做 「 試驗 」 。
this particular pattern of charges in eight dimensions is actually part of the most beautiful geometric structure in mathematics .	在八度空間中 , 這種特殊的載荷是數學中最美麗的幾何結構之一 。
it's a pattern of the largest exceptional lie group , e8 .	這是最大的例外謊言團體 , e8 。
this lie group is a smooth , curved shape with 248 dimensions .	這個謊言團體是平滑的曲線形狀有248度的維度
each point in this pattern corresponds to a symmetry of this very complex and beautiful shape .	這個圖案中的每個點都對應著這個非常複雜且美麗的形狀 。
one small part of this e8 shape can be used to describe the curved spacetime of einstein's general relativity , explaining gravity .	這個e8形狀的一小部分可以用來描述愛因斯坦廣義相對論的曲線 , 解釋重力 。
together with quantum mechanics , the geometry of this shape could describe everything about how the universe works at the tiniest scales .	隨著量子力學 , 這個形狀的幾何圖形可以描述宇宙如何在最小的尺度上運作 。
the pattern of this shape living in eightdimensional charge space is exquisitely beautiful , and it summarizes thousands of possible interactions between these elementary particles , each of which is just a facet of this complicated shape .	這種形狀在八度載荷空間中生存的模式是非常美麗的 , 它總結了數以千計的基本粒子之間的交互作用 , 每一種都只是面對這種複雜的形狀 。
as we spin it , we can see many of the other intricate patterns contained in this one .	當我們旋轉時 , 我們可以看到許多其他複雜的圖案 , 包含在這個圖案中 。
and with a particular rotation , we can look down through this pattern in eight dimensions along a symmetry axis and see all the particles at once .	通過一個特定的旋轉 , 我們可以從這八度的角度看下去 , 在對稱軸上 , 一次看到所有粒子 。
it's a very beautiful object , and as with any unification , we can see some holes where new particles are required by this pattern .	它是一個非常美麗的物品 , 就像任何一致性的物體一樣 , 我們可以看到一些由這種模式所需的新粒子 。
there are 20 gaps where new particles should be , two of which have been filled by the patisalam particles .	新粒子應該有20個缺口 , 其中兩個是帕帕帕拉姆粒子填滿的 。
from their location in this pattern , we know that these new particles should be scalar fields like the higgs particle , but have color charge and interact with the strong force .	從這些圖案的位置我們知道這些新粒子應該是像希格斯粒子一樣的大小但有顏色的載荷和強力相互作用
filling in these new particles completes this pattern , giving us the full e8 .	填充這些新粒子 , 完成了這個圖案 , 給我們全部的e8 。
this e8 pattern has very deep mathematical roots .	這個e8模式有很深的數學根 。
it's considered by many to be the most beautiful structure in mathematics .	它被許多人認為是數學中最美麗的結構 。
it's a fantastic prospect that this object of great mathematical beauty could describe the truth of particle interactions at the smallest scales imaginable .	這個偉大的數學美的物品可以描述粒子相互作用的真相在最小尺度可以想像的
and this idea that nature is described by mathematics is not at all new .	大自然是用數學來描述的 , 並不是全新的 。
in 1623 , galileo wrote this: " nature's grand book , which stands continually open to our gaze , is written in the language of mathematics .	1623年 , 伽利略寫了這句話: 「 大自然的大書 , 一直在我們的視線上展開 , 寫在數學的語言中 。
its characters are triangles , circles and other geometrical figures , without which it is humanly impossible to understand a single word of it ; without these , one is wandering around in a dark labyrinth . "	它的角色是三角形、圓形 , 和其他幾何圖形 , 若沒有它 , 就不可能明白它的單字 ; 若沒有這些 , 就會在黑暗的迷宮中四處遊蕩 。 」
i believe this to be true , and i've tried to follow galileo's guidance in describing the mathematics of particle physics using only triangles , circles and other geometrical figures .	我相信這是真的 , 我試著遵循伽利略的指引 , 用粒子物理學的數學 , 只用三角形、圓形和其他幾何圖形 。
of course , when other physicists and i actually work on this stuff , the mathematics can resemble a dark labyrinth .	當然 , 當其他物理學家和我真的在研究這些東西時 , 數學可以是黑暗的迷宮 。
but it's reassuring that at the heart of this mathematics is pure , beautiful geometry .	但 , 要確保數學的核心是純粹、美麗的幾何學 。
joined with quantum mechanics , this mathematics describes our universe as a growing e8 coral , with particles interacting at every location in all possible ways according to a beautiful pattern .	加入量子力學 , 這個數學描述了我們的宇宙 , 隨著成長的e8珊瑚 , 粒子在每個位置相互作用 , 根據美麗的圖案來描述宇宙 。
and as more of the pattern comes into view using new machines like the large hadron collider , we may be able to see whether nature uses this e8 pattern or a different one .	隨著越來越多的模式使用大型強子對撞機 , 我們可能會看到大自然是否使用e8模式 , 或另一個 。
this process of discovery is a wonderful adventure to be involved in .	這項發現的過程是一段很棒的冒險旅程 。
if the lhc finds particles that fit this e8 pattern , that will be very , very cool .	如果lhc找到符合e8模式的粒子 , 那會非常、非常、非常酷 。
if the lhc finds new particles , but they don't fit this pattern well , that will be very interesting , but bad for this e8 theory .	如果lhc找到新粒子 , 但它們不符合這個模式 , 那對e8理論來說是很有意思的 。
and , of course , bad for me personally .	當然 , 對我個人來說是壞的 。
now how bad would that be ?	那會多糟 ?
well , pretty bad .	嗯 , 非常糟糕 。
but predicting how nature works is a very risky game .	但預測大自然是非常危險的遊戲 。
this theory and others like it are long shots .	這個理論和其他類似的理論都很長 。
one does a lot of hard work knowing that most of these ideas probably won't end up being true about nature .	其中一份工作很辛苦 , 知道大部分的思想最終不會是對大自然的真實 。
that's what doing theoretical physics is like: there are a lot of wipeouts .	理論物理就是這樣:有很多野生動物 。
in this regard , new physics theories are a lot like startup companies .	在這方面 , 新的物理理論就像新創公司一樣 。
as with any large investment , it can be emotionally difficult to abandon a line of research when it isn't working out .	只要有大額投資 , 就可能很難放棄一系列的研究 。
but in science , if something isn't working , you have to toss it out and try something else .	但在科學上 , 如果有些東西沒有用 , 你就必須去嘗試其他東西 。
now , the only way to maintain sanity and achieve happiness in the midst of this uncertainty is to keep balance and perspective in life .	唯一能維持理智和成就幸福的方法就是維持生活的平衡和觀點 。
i've tried the best i can to live a balanced life .	我盡力去生活平衡生活 。
i try to balance my life equally between physics , love and surfing my own three charge directions .	我試著平衡我的人生 , 包括物理、愛和衝浪我自己三個載荷方向 。
this way , even if the physics i work on comes to nothing , i still know i've lived a good life .	這樣的方式 , 即使我工作的物理完全沒有 , 我仍然知道我過著好的生活 。
and i try to live in beautiful places .	我試著生活在美麗的地方 。
for most of the past ten years i've lived on the island of maui , a very beautiful place .	在過去的十年裡 , 我所居住的大部份時間 , 都位在毛伊島 , 是個非常美麗的地方 。
now it's one of the greatest mysteries in the universe to my parents how i managed to survive all that time without engaging in anything resembling fulltime employment .	現在 , 這是宇宙中最偉大的謎團之一 , 對我父母來說 , 我一直以來都無法全職投入任何全職員工 。
i'm going to let you in on that secret .	我要告訴你們這個秘密 。
this was a view from my home office on maui .	這是我在maui家的家庭辦公室的景象 。
and you may have noticed that these beautiful views are similar , but in slightly different places .	你可能已經注意到這些美麗的景觀是相似的 , 但在一些稍微不同的地方 。
that's because this used to be my home and office on maui .	那是因為這曾經是我在毛伊的家和辦公室 。
i've chosen a very unusual life .	我選擇了非常不尋常的人生 。
but not worrying about rent allowed me to spend my time doing what i love .	但不擔心租金讓我花時間做我所愛的事 。
living a nomadic existence has been hard at times , but it's allowed me to live in beautiful places and keep a balance in my life that i've been happy with .	有時 , 居住遊牧的存在很困難 , 但它讓我能住在美麗的地方 , 保持平衡 , 在我人生中 , 我一直很快樂 。
it allows me to spend a lot of my time hanging out with hyperintelligent coral .	它允許我花很多時間和超級聰明的珊瑚在一起 。
but i also greatly enjoy the company of hyperintelligent people .	但我也很享受超級聰明的人的公司 。
so i'm very happy to have been invited here to ted .	我很高興被邀請來ted 。
chris anderson: i probably understood two percent of that , but i still absolutely loved it . so i'm going to sound dumb .	克里斯•安德森:我大概懂了百分之二 , 但我仍然很喜歡 。 所以我會聽起來很蠢 。
your theory of everything garrett lisi: i'm used to coral .	你的萬物理論:我習慣珊瑚 。
ca: that's right . the reason it's got a few people at least excited is because , if you're right , it brings gravity and quantum theory together .	克里斯:沒錯 。 這裡有幾個人至少感到興奮的原因是 , 如果你是對的 , 它將重力和量子理論結合在一起 。
so are you saying that we should think of the universe , at its heart that the smallest things that there are , are somehow an e8 object of possibility ?	所以 , 你是說 , 我們應該考慮宇宙 , 在它的核心中 , 最小的東西 , 可能性是e8的物體嗎 ?
i mean , is there a scale to it , at the smallest scale , or . . . ?	我的意思是 , 在最小的尺度上 , 是否有規模 ?
gl: well , right now the pattern i showed you that corresponds to what we know about elementary particle physics that already corresponds to a very beautiful shape .	格林:現在 , 我給你們看的模式 , 是對應我們對基本粒子物理的認識 , 已經對應到一個非常漂亮的形狀 。
and that's the one that i said we knew for certain .	這就是我所說的我們知道的 。
and that shape has remarkable similarities and the way it fits into this e8 pattern could be the rest of the picture .	這種形狀有很了不起的相似性 , 以及它適合這個e8圖案的其他部分 , 可能是圖片的其他部分 。
and these patterns of points that i've shown for you actually represent symmetries of this highdimensional object that would be warping and moving and dancing over the space time that we experience .	我向你們展示的這些圖案 , 其實代表了這個高維度物體的對稱性 , 在我們體驗的時空中 , 會扭曲、移動、跳舞 。
and that would be what explains all these elementary particles that we see .	那就是解釋我們所看到的這些基本粒子 。
ca: but a string theorist , as i understand it , explains electrons in terms of much smaller strings vibrating i know you don't like string theory vibrating inside it .	克:但是弦理論學家 , 如我所知 , 解釋電子 , 以更小的弦振動我知道你不喜歡弦理論震動 。
how should we think of an electron in relation to e8 ?	我們該怎麼看待e8的電子呢 ?
gl: no , it would be one of the symmetries of this e8 shape .	蓋爾:不 , 它會是e8形狀的對稱性之一 。
so what's happening is , as the shape is moving over spacetime , it's twisting . and the direction it's twisting as it moves is what particle we see . so it would be ca: the size of the e8 shape , how does that relate to the electron ?	所以 , 當這個形狀在時空移動時 , 它在扭轉 。 當它移動時 , 它的方向是我們看到的粒子 。 所以 , 克里斯:e8形狀的大小 , 和電子的關係如何 ?
i kind of feel like i need that for my picture .	我覺得我需要這張照片 。
is it bigger ? is it smaller ?	變大了嗎 ? 變小嗎 ?
gl: well , as far as we know electrons are point particles , so this would be going down to the smallest possible scales .	蓋瑞:目前我們所知的電子是點粒子 , 所以這會降到最小的可能尺度 。
so the way these things are explained in quantum field theory is , all possibilities are expanding and developing at once .	所以這些東西在量子場理論中解釋的方式是 , 所有可能性同時在擴展和發展中 。
and this is why i use the analogy to coral .	這就是為什麼我用珊瑚的類比 。
and in this way , the way that e8 comes in is it will be as a shape that's attached at each point in spacetime .	以這種方式來看 , e8會出現的方式 , 就是它的形狀 , 在時空中 , 它會是固定的形狀 。
and , as i said , the way the shape twists the directional along which way the shape is twisting as it moves over this curved surface is what the elementary particles are , themselves .	如我所說的 , 形狀的扭曲方向 , 形狀在曲線的表面上扭曲 , 正是基本粒子本身 。
so through quantum field theory , they manifest themselves as points and interact that way .	透過量子場理論 , 他們把自己當作點 , 用這種方式互動 。
i don't know if i'll be able to make this any clearer .	我不知道我能不能讓它更清楚 。
ca: it doesn't really matter .	克:這並不重要 。
it's evoking a kind of sense of wonder , and i certainly want to understand more of this .	它在喚起一種奇妙的感覺 , 我當然想要了解更多 。
but thank you so much for coming . that was absolutely fascinating .	但非常謝謝你來 。 這絕對是令人著迷的 。
the legendary chimpanzee researcher jane goodall talks about tacare and her other community projects , which help people in booming african towns live sidebyside with threatened animals .	傳奇的黑猩猩研究員珍•古德爾談到坦貝爾和她的其他社區計畫 , 協助非洲小鎮居住在邊緣 , 威脅動物 。
africa , animals , biodiversity , environment , global issues , pollution , primates , science	非洲、動物、生物多樣性、環境、全球議題、污染、靈長類、科學、科學等 。
jane goodall helps humans and animals live together	珍•古德幫助人類和動物一起生活
good afternoon , good evening , whatever .	午安 , 晚安 , 等等 。
we can go , jambo , guten abend , bonsoir , but we can also ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh .	我們可以去 , 珍博 , 吉他 , 波諾 , 我們也可以 , 喔 , ~ ~ 噢 , 喔 ~ ~ ~ ~ 喔 ~ ~ ~ 喔 ~ ~ 喔 ~ ~ 喔 ~ ~ ~ 喔 ~ ~ ~ ~ ~ ~ ~ ~ ~ ~ ~ ~ ~ ~ ~ ~ ~ ~ ~
that is the call that chimpanzees make before they go to sleep in the evening .	這是黑猩猩在晚上睡覺前所發出的通訊 。
you hear it going from one side of the valley to the other , from one group of nests to the next .	從山谷的一邊到另一邊 , 從一群巢穴到下一個 。
and i want to pick up with my talk this evening from where zeray left off yesterday .	今天晚上 , 我想從昨天zeray離開的地方來談談談我的演講 。
he was talking about this amazing , threeyearold australopithecine child , selam .	他在談論這個驚人的三歲的澳洲流行病童 , 塞拉姆 。
and we've also been hearing about the history , the family tree , of mankind through dna genetic profiling .	我們也聽說過歷史、家庭樹 , 透過dna獲利 , 人類的資料 。
and it was a paleontologist , the late louis leakey , who actually set me on the path for studying chimpanzees .	這是古生物學家 , 最近路易斯.雷克 , 他讓我踏上研究黑猩猩的道路 。
and it was pretty extraordinary , way back then .	那時候是非常了不起的 。
it's kind of commonplace now , but his argument was because he'd been searching for the fossilized remains of early humans in africa .	現在有點普遍 , 但他的論點是因為他一直在尋找非洲早期人類的化石 。
and you can tell an awful lot about what those beings looked like from the fossils , from the shape of the muscle attachments , something about the way they lived from the various artifacts found with them .	你可以從化石中看出這些生物的樣貌 , 從肌肉附著的形狀 , 看他們從各式各樣的工藝品中生活的方式 。
but what about how they behaved ? that's what he wanted to know .	但他們怎麼做呢 ? 這是他想要知道的 。
and of course , behavior doesn't fossilize .	當然 , 行為不會化石 。
he argued and it's now a fairly common theory that if we found behavior patterns similar or the same in our closest living relatives , the great apes , and humans today , then maybe those behaviors were present in the apelike , humanlike ancestor some seven million years ago .	他主張和現在是一個相當常見的理論如果我們在近壽的親戚身上找到相似或相同的行為模式或是人類今日的偉大猿類和人類 , 也許這些行為在七百萬年前出現 , 像是人類的祖先 。
and therefore , perhaps we had brought those characteristics with us from that ancient , ancient past .	因此 , 也許我們從古老、古老的過去帶給了我們這些特質 。
well , if you look in textbooks today that deal with human evolution , you very often find people speculating about how early humans may have behaved , based on the behavior of chimpanzees .	嗯 , 如果你看看現今的教科書 , 處理人類演化 , 你通常會發現人們推測早期人類的行為 , 基於黑猩猩的行為 。
they are more like us than any other living creature , and we've heard about that during this ted conference .	它們比任何其他生物更像我們 , 在ted會議中 , 我們也都聽過這種說法 。
so it remains for me to comment on the ways in which chimpanzees are so like us , in certain aspects of their behavior .	所以 , 我一直在評論黑猩猩和我們一樣的行為 。 在某些方面 , 黑猩猩是如此相似 。
every chimpanzee has his or her own personality .	每隻黑猩猩都有自己的個性 。
of course , i gave them names . they can live to be 60 years or more , although we think most of them probably don't make it to 60 in the wild .	當然 , 我給他們名字 。 他們可以活到60年或更多 , 雖然我們認為大部分的人可能不會在野外製造到60歲 。
mr . wurzel . the female has her first baby when she's 11 or 12 .	沃茲先生 , 雌蟲在11或12歲時有她的第一個寶寶 。
thereafter , she has one baby only every five or six years , a long period of childhood dependency when the child is nursing , sleeping with the mother at night , and riding on her back .	在那裡 , 她每五到六年就有一個嬰兒 , 一個長期的童年依賴 , 當孩子在養育時 , 晚上和母親一起睡覺 , 騎著她的背 。
and we believe that this long period of childhood is important for chimpanzees , just as it is for us , in relation to learning .	我們相信這段長期的童年對黑猩猩來說很重要 , 就如同對我們而言 , 與學習有關 。
as the brain becomes ever more complex during evolution in different forms of animals , so we find that learning plays an ever more important role in an individual's life history .	隨著大腦在演化過程中變得更複雜 , 所以我們發現學習在個人的生命史上扮演著更重要的角色 。
and young chimpanzees spend a lot of time watching what their elders do .	年輕的黑猩猩花了很多時間觀察牠們的長輩們做了什麼 。
we know now that they're capable of imitating behaviors that they see .	我們現在知道它們能夠模仿它們所看到的行為 。
and we believe that it's in this way that the different toolusing behaviors that have now been seen in all the different chimpanzee populations studied in africa how these are passed from one generation to the next , through observation , imitation and practice , so that we can describe these toolusing behaviors as primitive culture .	我們相信 , 這種方式 , 這種不同的工具行為 , 如今在非洲各地的黑猩猩群體都在研究這些世代 , 透過觀察、模仿和練習 , 我們就能把這些工具行為描述成原始文化 。
chimpanzees don't have a spoken language . we've talked about that .	黑猩猩沒有口語 , 我們已經談過了 。
they do have a very rich repertoire of postures and gestures , many of which are similar , or even identical , to ours and formed in the same context . greeting chimpanzees embracing .	他們確實有非常豐富的姿勢 , 其中許多類似 , 甚至相同 , 形成同一個情境 。 希臘黑猩猩擁抱 。
they also kiss , hold hands , pat one another on the back .	他們也親吻、握手、拍下彼此 。
and they swagger and they throw rocks .	然後他們轉動 , 扔石頭 。
in chimpanzee society , we find many , many examples of compassion , precursors to love and true altruism .	在黑猩猩社會中 , 我們發現許多關於同情心的例子 , 前輩們去愛和真正的利他主義 。
unfortunately , they , like us , have a dark side to their nature .	不幸的是 , 他們和我們一樣 , 有一面漆黑的天性 。
they're capable of extreme brutality , even a kind of primitive war .	他們有能力極端殘暴 , 甚至一種原始的戰爭 。
and these really aggressive behaviors , for the most part , are directed against individuals of the neighboring social group .	而這些非常具侵略性的行為 , 大部分的原因是針對鄰近社會群體的個人 。
they are very territorially aggressive .	它們非常的具攻擊性 。
chimpanzees , i believe , more than any other living creature , have helped us to understand that , after all , there is no sharp line between humans and the rest of the animal kingdom .	我相信 , 比起其他生物 , 黑猩猩已經幫助我們了解 , 畢竟 , 人類和其他動物王國之間沒有尖銳的線 。
it's a very blurry line , and it's getting more blurry all the time as we make even more observations .	這是一條非常模糊的線 , 當我們做更多的觀察時 , 它會變得更模糊 。
the study that i began in 1960 is still continuing to this day .	我1960年開始的研究仍然持續著 。
and these chimpanzees , living their complex social lives in the wild , have helped more than anything else to make us realize we are part of , and not separated from , the amazing animals with whom we share the planet .	這些黑猩猩 , 在野外生活著複雜的社會生活 , 已經幫助我們了解到我們是其中的一部分 , 而不是分離 , 我們共享地球的神奇動物 。
so it's pretty sad to find that chimpanzees , like so many other creatures around the world , are losing their habitats .	所以 , 很可悲的是 , 發現黑猩猩 , 就像世界上許多其他生物一樣 , 正在失去牠們的棲息地 。
this is just one photograph from the air , and it shows you the forested highlands of gombe .	這只是空氣中的一張照片 , 它告訴你森林的高地 。
and it was when i flew over the whole area , about 16 years ago , and realized that outside the park , this forest , which in 1960 had stretched almost unbroken along the eastern shore of lake tanganyika , which is where the tiny , 30squaremile gombe national park lies , that a question came to my mind .	大約16年前 , 我飛越整個區域 , 發現在公園外面的森林 , 在1960年 , 這片森林幾乎在塔吉尼卡的東岸幾乎沒有破壞 , 那裡有三十四平方的山羊公園 , 來到我的腦海 。
" how can we even try to save these famous chimpanzees , when the people living around the national park are struggling to survive ? "	「 我們要如何拯救這些著名的黑猩猩 ? 當住在國家公園附近的人們在掙扎生存的時候 ? 」
more people are living there than the land could possibly support .	比起土地能支持更多人 。
the numbers increased by refugees pouring in from burundi and over the lake from congo .	難民的數量增加 , 來自緬甸和剛果湖的數量 。
and very poor people they couldn't afford to buy food from elsewhere .	非常貧窮的人買不起其他地方的食物 。
this led to a program , which we call tacare .	這導致了一個計畫 , 我們稱之為tacare 。
it's a very holistic way of improving the lives of the people living in the villages around the park .	這是一種非常全面的方法來改善住在公園周圍的村民的生活 。
it started small with 12 villages . it's now in 24 .	它從12個村落開始 , 現在是24歲 。
there isn't time to go into it , but it's including things like tree nurseries , methods of farming most suitable to this now very degraded , almost desertlike land up in these mountains .	沒有時間深入探討 , 但包括樹木護理師的方法 , 這種農業最適合目前的水準非常惡劣 , 幾乎像沙漠般降落在這些山上 。
ways of controlling , preventing soil erosion .	控制的方式 , 防止土壤侵蝕 。
ways of reclaiming overused farmland , so that within two years they can again be productive .	重建過度使用的農地方法 , 所以在兩年內 , 它們能再次發揮生產力 。
working to help the villagers obtain fresh water from wells .	努力協助村民從井裡取得淡水 。
perhaps build some schoolrooms .	也許建造一些學校室 。
most important of all , i believe , is working with small groups of women , providing them with opportunities for microcredit loans .	最重要的是 , 我相信 , 和一小群婦女合作 , 提供她們給微額貸款的機會 。
and we've got , as is the case around the world , about 95 percent of all loans returned .	我們有 , 如同全世界的案例 , 大約有95%的貸款回報 。
empowering women , working with education , providing scholarships for girls so they can finish secondary school , in the clear understanding that , all around the world , as women's education improves , family size drops .	賦予女性權力 , 和教育合作 , 提供獎學金給女孩們 , 讓他們可以完成二年級的學校 , 清楚明白 , 世界各地 , 隨著女性的教育改善 , 家庭規模降低 。
we provide information about family planning and about hiv/aids .	我們提供家庭規劃和愛滋病的資訊 。
and as a result of this program , something's happening for conservation .	由於這個計畫 , 保育計畫發生了什麼事 。
what's happening for conservation is that the farmers living in these 24 villages , instead of looking on us as a bunch of white people coming to study a whole bunch of monkeys and by the way , many of the staff are now tanzanian but when we began the tacare program , it was a tanzanian team going into the villages .	保育的原因是 , 那些住在24個村落的農民 , 而不是把我們當成一群白人來研究一群猴子 , 順道一提 , 許多員工現在已經是坦尚尼亞人 , 但當我們開始計劃時 , 這是坦尚尼亞人進入村落 。
it was a tanzanian team talking to the villagers , asking what they were interested in .	那是坦尚尼亞的團隊和村民對話 , 問他們感興趣的是什麼 。
were they interested in conservation ? absolutely not .	他們對保育有興趣嗎 ? 絕對不是 。
they were interested in health ; they were interested in education .	他們對健康有興趣 , 他們對教育有興趣 。
and as time went on , and as their situation began to improve , they began to understand ever more about the need for conservation .	隨著時間過去 , 他們的情況開始改善 , 他們開始更了解保育的需求 。
they began to understand that as the upper levels of the hills were denuded of trees , so you've got this terrible soil erosion and mudslides .	他們開始了解 , 隨著山丘上升的水平被破壞了 , 所以你有種可怕的土壤侵蝕和泥土 。
today , we are developing what we call the greater gombe ecosystem .	現今 , 我們正在發展所謂的更大的gombe生態系統 。
this is an area way outside the national park , stretching out into all these very degraded lands .	這是國家公園外面的一個地區 , 延伸到這些非常退化的土地上 。
and as these villages have a better standard of life , they are actually agreeing to put between 10 percent and 20 percent of their land in the highlands aside , so that once again , as the trees grow back , the chimpanzees will have leafy corridors through which they can travel to interact as they must for genetic viability with other remnant groups outside the national park .	當這些村落有更好的生活標準時 , 他們其實同意把百分之十到二十的土地放到高地 , 所以再一次 , 隨著樹木長回來 , 黑猩猩會透過這些小猩猩的走廊 , 牠們可以和國家公園外的其他殘留族群互動 。
so tacare is a success .	所以 , 塔卡爾是個成功 。
we're replicating it in other parts of africa , around other wilderness areas which are faced with extreme population pressure .	我們在非洲的其他地方複製它 , 其它的荒野區域面臨極端人口壓力 。
the problems in africa , however , as we've been discussing for the whole of these first couple of days of ted , are major problems .	然而 , 非洲的問題 , 正如我們一直在討論ted的前幾天 , 都是重大的問題 。
there is a great deal of poverty .	有很大的貧窮 。
and when you get large numbers of people living in land that is not that fertile , particularly when you cut down trees , and you leave the soil open to the wind for erosion , as desperate populations cut down more and more trees , so that they can try and grow food for themselves and their families , what's going to happen ? something's got to give .	當你有大量的居民住在土地上 , 尤其是當你砍樹時 , 你將土壤開放給風力侵蝕 , 如絕望的人口砍下越來越多的樹木 , 這樣他們就可以為自己和家人種種食物 , 會發生什麼事 ?
and the other problems in not only africa , but the rest of the developing world and , indeed , everywhere what are we doing to our planet ?	另外一個問題 , 不僅是非洲 , 其他發展中國家 , 並且 , 不論我們對地球做了什麼事 ?
you know , the famous scientist , e . o . wilson said that if every person on this planet attains the standard of living of the average european or american , we need three new planets .	你知道的 , 著名的科學家e.wilson說 , 如果地球上每個人都能維持平均歐洲或美國人的生活水準 , 我們需要三個新的行星 。
today , they are saying four . but we don't have them . we've got one .	今天 , 他們說的是四個 。 但是我們沒有 。 我們有一個 。
and what's happened ? i mean , the question here is , here we are , arguably the most intelligent being that's ever walked planet earth , with this extraordinary brain , capable of the kind of technology that is so well illustrated by these ted conferences , and yet we're destroying the only home we have .	發生了什麼事 ? 我的意思是 , 問題是 , 這裡 , 我們的確是地球上最有智慧的生物 , 帶著這個非凡的大腦 , 能夠被ted會議所描述的科技所描繪出來 , 但我們卻在摧毀我們唯一的家園 。
the indigenous people around the world , before they made a major decision , used to sit around and ask themselves , " how does this decision affect our people seven generations ahead ? "	世界各地的原住民 , 在他們做了重大決定之前 , 常常會自問: 「 這個決定會如何影響我們的七代人 ? 」
today , major decisions and i'm not particularly talking about africa here , but the developed world major decisions involving millions of dollars , and millions of people , are often based on , " how will this affect the next shareholders' meeting ? "	現今 , 主要的決策──我不是特別談論非洲 , 而是已開發國家的決策──數百萬美元 , 數百萬人 , 通常是基於: 「 這會如何影響下一個股東會議 ? 」
and these decisions affect africa .	這些決定會影響非洲 。
as i began traveling around africa talking about the problems faced by chimpanzees and their vanishing forests , i realized more and more how so many of africa's problems could be laid at the door of previous colonial exploitation .	當我開始在非洲四處旅行時 , 談到黑猩猩和牠們消失的森林 , 我發現越來越多非洲問題在以前殖民地剝削的門口 。
so i began traveling outside africa , talking in europe , talking in the united states , going to asia .	所以我開始在非洲外行走 , 在歐洲 , 和美國談話 , 去亞洲 。
and everywhere there were these terrible problems .	到處都有這些可怕的問題 。
and you know the kind i'm talking about . i'm talking about pollution .	你們都知道我在說什麼 。 我在說污染 。
the air that we breathe that often poisons us .	我們呼吸的空氣通常會毒害我們 。
the earth is poisoning our foods .	地球正在毒害我們的食物 。
the water water is perhaps one of the most crucial issues that we're going to face in this century and everywhere water is being polluted by agricultural , industrial and household chemicals that still are being sprayed around the world , seemingly with the inability to profit from past experience .	水可能是我們在這個世紀所面臨的最關鍵議題之一 , 水被農業、工業和家庭污染 , 仍然被世界各地的化學物所污染 , 似乎沒有辦法從過去的經驗中獲利 。
the mangroves are being cut down ; the effects of things like the tsunami get worse .	紅樹林被砍伐 ; 海嘯的影響會更糟 。
we've talked about the soil erosion .	我們談過土壤侵蝕 。
we have the reckless burning of fossil fuels along with other greenhouse gasses , so called , leading to climate change .	我們的燃燒化石燃料還有其他溫室氣體 , 所以 , 導致氣候變遷 。
finally , all around the world , people have begun to believe that there is something going on very wrong with our climate .	最後 , 全世界的人都開始相信我們的氣候有一些問題 。
all around the world climates are mixed up .	世界各地的氣候都混合起來了 。
and it's the poor people who are affected worse .	貧窮的人會受到更嚴重的影響 。
it's africa that already is affected .	非洲已經受到影響 。
in many parts of subsaharan africa , the droughts are so much worse .	在撒哈拉以南非洲的許多地區 , 乾旱更糟 。
and when the rain does come , it so often leads to flooding and added distress , and the cycle of poverty and hunger and disease .	當雨季來臨時 , 它通常會造成洪水、加入痛苦 , 以及貧窮、飢餓和疾病的循環 。
and the numbers of people living in an area that the land cannot support , who are too poor to buy food , who can't move away because the whole land is degraded .	居住的地區的人數不多 , 無法支援 , 他們太貧窮 , 無法離開 , 因為整片土地被破壞了 。
and so you get desertification creeping , creeping , creeping as the last of the trees are cut down .	所以你會得到沙漠化的珊瑚礁、珊瑚礁 , 隨著最後一棵樹被砍掉 。
and this kind of thing is not just in africa . it's all over the world .	這種東西不只在非洲 , 世界各地都有 。
so it wasn't surprising to me that as i was traveling around the world i met so many young people who seemed to have lost hope .	所以 , 我並不意外 , 當我在世界各地旅行時 , 我遇到許多年輕人 , 他們似乎失去了希望 。
we seem to have lost wisdom , the wisdom of the indigenous people .	我們似乎失去了智慧 , 原住民的智慧 。
i asked a question . " why ? "	我問了一個問題: 「 為什麼 ? 」
well , do you think there could be some kind of disconnect between this extraordinarily clever brain , the kind of brain that the ted technologies exemplify , and the human heart ? talking about it in the nonscientific term , in terms of love and compassion . is there some disconnect ?	嗯 , 你認為在這種非比尋常聰明的大腦之間是否有某種程度的差異 ? ted科技的出現和人的心 ? 以非科學的角度來說 , 在愛和同理心之間 , 是否有某種差異 ?
and these young people , when i talk to them , basically they were either depressed or apathetic , or bitter and angry . and they said more or less the same thing , " we feel this way because we feel you've compromised our future and there's nothing we can do about it . "	這些年輕人 , 當我跟他們說話時 , 基本上 , 他們不是憂鬱、冷靜、苦痛、憤怒 。 他們說的 , 或多或少是同樣的話: 「 我們會這樣感覺 , 因為我們覺得你已經妥協了我們的未來 , 我們什麼都做不了 。 」
we have compromised their future .	我們已經破壞了他們的未來 。
i've got three little grandchildren , and every time i look at them and i think how we've harmed this beautiful planet since i was their age , i feel this desperation .	我有三個小孫子 , 每當我看著她們時 , 我想我們如何傷害這個美麗的星球 , 從我年紀開始 , 我感受到絕望 。
and that led to this program we call roots and shoots , which began right here in tanzania and has now spread to 97 countries around the world .	這導致了我們稱之為根和芽的計畫 , 開始於坦尚尼亞 , 現在已經擴展到全世界97個國家 。
it's symbolic . roots make a firm foundation .	它是象徵性的 。 樹根製造了一間公司基金會 。
shoots seem tiny ; to reach the sun they can break through a brick wall .	射擊看起來很小 ; 為了抵達太陽 , 它們可以穿過磚牆 。
see the brick wall as all these problems we've inflicted on the planet , environmental and social . it's a message of hope .	把磚牆視為我們對地球造成的所有問題 , 環保和社會的影響 。 這是一種希望的訊息 。
hundreds and thousands of young people around the world can break through and can make this a better world for all living things .	世界各地數十萬名年輕人可以突破並為所有生物創造一個更好的世界 。
the most important message of roots and shoots: every single one of us makes a difference , every single day .	根和芽的最重要的訊息是:我們每一個人每天都能做出改變 。
we have a choice . every one of us in this room , we have a choice as to what kind of difference we want to make .	我們有選擇 。 在座的每個人 , 我們都有選擇要做什麼改變 。
the very poor have no choice . it's up to us to change things so that the poor have choice as well .	貧窮的人沒有選擇 , 要改變事物 , 才能讓窮人有選擇 。
the roots and shoots groups all choose three projects .	根和芽團體都選了三個項目 。
it depends on how old they are , and which country , whether they're in a city or rural , as to what kinds of projects .	它取決於它們的年齡 , 以及哪個國家 , 不論他們在城市或鄉村 , 和什麼樣的計畫 。
but basically , we have programs now from preschool right through university , with more and more adults starting their own roots and shoots groups .	但基本上 , 我們有從幼兒園到大學的程式 , 有越來越多的成年人開始自己根部和芽團體 。
and every group chooses , between them , three different kinds of project to make this a better world , recognizing that all these different problems are interconnected and impinge on each other .	每個團體都選擇在兩者之間 , 三個不同的項目 , 讓這個世界變得更美好 , 認知到 , 所有這些不同的問題都互相連結 , 加強彼此之間 。
so one of their projects will be to help their own human community .	其中一項計畫是要協助他們自己的人類社群 。
and then , if they're able , they may raise money to help communities in other parts of the world .	如果他們能的話 , 他們可能會募集資金 , 來協助世界其他地區的社區 。
one of their projects will be to help animals not just wildlife , domestic animals as well .	其中一項計畫是要協助動物 , 不只是野生動物 , 還有家畜動物 。
and one of their projects will be to help the environment that we all share .	其中一項計畫是要協助我們共享的環境 。
and woven throughout all of this is a message of learning to live in peace and harmony within ourselves , in our families , in our communities , between nations , between cultures , between religions and between us and the natural world .	整件事都包含了一種訊息 , 來學習生活在和平和和諧中 , 在我們的家庭、我們的社區、國家、文化、文化、宗教之間 , 和我們和自然界之間 。
we need the natural world . we cannot go on destroying it at the rate we are .	我們需要自然世界 。 我們不能以我們現在的速度來破壞它 。
we not do have more than this one planet .	我們沒有超過這個星球 。
just picking one or two of the projects right here in africa that the roots and shoots groups are doing , one or two projects only in tanzania , in uganda , kenya , south africa , congobrazzaville , sierra leone , cameroon and other groups . and as i say , it's in 97 countries around the world .	只要在非洲這裡挑一個或兩個項目 , 就是根和芽群體在做 , 只有在坦尚尼亞、烏干達、肯亞、南非、剛果利亞、獅子山共和國 , 還有其他團體 。 如我所說的 , 它在世界上97個國家 。
of course , they're planting trees . they're growing organic vegetables .	當然 , 他們在種樹 , 種植有機蔬菜 。
they're working in the refugee camps , with chickens and selling the eggs for a little amount of money , or just using them to feed their families , and feeling a sense of pride and empowerment , because they're no longer helpless and depending on others with their vegetables and their chickens .	他們在難民營工作 , 帶著雞來賣蛋 , 只用一些錢 , 只用它們來餵養他們的家人 , 感覺到驕傲和賦權 , 因為他們不再無助 , 依靠他人的蔬菜和雞 。
it's being used in uganda to give some psychological help to exchild soldiers .	它被用在烏干達 , 給予一些心理上的幫助 , 來讓士兵們去做 。
doing projects like this is bringing them out of themselves .	做像這樣的項目 , 將它們帶出自己 。
once again , they're useful members of society .	再一次 , 他們是社會中有用的成員 。
we have this program in prisons as well .	我們也在監獄裡有這個計畫 。
so , there's no time for more roots and shoots now .	所以 , 現在沒有更多根和芽的時間了 。
but oh , they're also working on hiv/aids .	但 , 喔 , 他們也在研究愛滋病 。
that's a very important component of roots and shoots , with older kids talking to younger ones .	那是根和芽的重要部分 , 年紀較小的孩子和年輕的孩子談話 。
and unwanted pregnancies and things like that , which young people listen to better from other youth , rather than adults .	這種不尋常的懷孕和諸如此類的 , 年輕人從其他年輕人身上聽得更好 , 而非成年人 。
hope . that's the question i get asked as i'm going around the world: " jane , you've seen so many terrible things , you've seen your chimpanzees decrease in number from about one million , at the turn of the century , to no more than 150 , 000 now , and the same with so many other animals .	希望 。 這就是我在世界各地被問到的問題: 「 珍 , 你看過這麼多可怕的事情 , 你已經看到黑猩猩數以百萬計的數量 , 從一個世紀到現在 , 到現在沒有超過十五萬隻 , 和許多其他動物一樣 。
forests disappearing , deserts where once there was forest .	森林消失了 , 曾經有森林的沙漠 。
do you really have hope ? " well , yes .	你真的有希望嗎 ? 」 是的 。
you can't come to a conference like ted and not have hope , can you ?	你不能來參加像ted這樣的會議 , 沒有希望 , 你能嗎 ?
and of course , there's hope . one is this amazing human brain .	當然 , 還有希望 。 一個是令人驚嘆的人類大腦 。
and i mean , think of the technologies .	我的意思是 , 想想科技 。
and i've just been so thrilled , finally , to come to people talking about compost latrines .	最後 , 我很興奮 , 最後 , 要來談談合成的廁所 。
it's one of my hobbyhorses .	這是我的嗜好者之一 。
we just flush all this water down the lavatory , it's terrible .	我們剛剛把這些水沖到電梯下 , 很糟糕 。
and then talking about renewable energy desperately important .	接著 , 談到再生能源極為重要 。
do we care about the planet for our children ?	我們在乎我們的孩子嗎 ?
how many of us have children or grandchildren , nieces , nephews ?	有多少人有孩子或孫子、姪子、姪子 ?
do we care about their future ?	我們在乎他們的未來嗎 ?
and if we care about their future , we , as the elite around the world , we can do something about it . we can make choices as to how we live each day .	如果我們在乎他們的未來 , 我們 , 身為世界菁英的未來 , 我們能為它做點什麼 。 我們可以為我們每天的生活做些選擇 。
what we buy . what we wear .	我們買什麼 , 穿什麼 。
and choose to make these choices with the question , how will this affect the environment around me ?	選擇用問題做這些選擇 , 這會如何影響我身邊的環境 ?
how will it affect the life of my child when he or she grows up ?	當他或她長大後 , 會如何影響我的孩子的生活 ?
or my grandchild , or whatever it is .	或是我的孫子 , 不管是什麼 。
so the human brain , coupled with the human heart , and we join hands around the world .	人類的大腦 , 與人的心結合 , 我們加入了全世界的手 。
and that's what ted is helping so well with , and google who help us , and esri are helping us with mapping in gombe national park .	這就是ted的幫助 , 和谷歌幫助我們 , esri正在幫我們繪製gombe國家公園的地圖 。
all of these technologies we can use .	所有這些我們能使用的科技 。
now let's link them , and it's beginning to happen , isn't it ?	現在讓我們把它們連結起來 , 開始發生了 , 對吧 ?
you've heard about it this afternoon . it's beginning to happen .	下午你聽說過了 。 事情開始發生了 。
this change , this change . to see change that we must have if we care about the future .	這種改變 , 這種改變 。 如果我們在乎未來 , 我們必須要有改變 。
and the next reason for hope nature is amazingly resilient .	希望大自然的下一個理由是驚人的恢復力 。
you can take an area that's absolutely destroyed , with time and perhaps some help it can regenerate .	你可以拿一個完全摧毀的區域 , 帶著時間 , 或許有些幫助它再生 。
and an example is the tacare program .	舉個例子 , 就是醫療方案 。
i told you , where a seemingly dead tree stump if you stop hacking them for firewood , which you don't need to because you have wood lots , then in five years you can have a 30foot tree .	我跟你說 , 看似死了的樹木 , 如果你停止砍伐樹木 , 那你不需要因為你有很多木材 , 五年後 , 你就可以有30英尺高的樹 。
and animals , almost on the brink of extinction , can be given a second chance . that's my next book .	而動物幾乎在滅絕的邊緣 , 可以得到第二次機會 。 這是我的下一本書 。
it's inspiring . and it brings me to my last category of hope , and we've heard about this so much in the last two days: this indomitable human spirit . this determination of people , the resilience of the human spirit , so that people who you would think would be battered by poverty , or disease , or whatever , can pull themselves up out of it , sometimes with a helping hand , and take their part in society , and take their part in changing the world .	它很鼓舞人心 。 它帶我到最後一類的希望 , 我們在過去的兩天中 , 聽過這麼多關於這種不屈不撓的人類精神 。 這決定了人類精神的韌性 , 使你認為會受到貧窮或疾病的影響 , 或疾病的影響 , 可以把自己拉出去 , 有時有助手 , 帶到社會中 , 帶他們參與改變世界的一部分 。
and just to think of one or two people out of africa who are just really inspiring .	想想非洲有一兩個人 , 他們真的很鼓舞人心 。
we could make a very long list , but obviously nelson mandela , emerging from 17 years of hard physical labor , 23 years of imprisonment , with this amazing ability to forgive , so that he could lead his nation out the evil regime of apartheid without a bloodbath .	我們可以做個很長的清單 , 但很明顯地 , 曼德拉從17年的辛苦勞工興起 , 23年的監禁 , 承受了這個驚人的原諒能力 , 讓他能把他的國家帶出種族隔離的邪惡政權 , 沒有血浴 。
ken sarowiwa , in nigeria , who took on the giant oil companies , and although people around the world tried their best , was executed .	奈及利亞的肯薩洛瓦採用巨型石油公司 , 儘管全世界的人都竭盡所能 , 卻被處決 。
people like this are so inspirational .	像這樣的人是如此鼓舞人心 。
people like this are the role models we need for young africans .	像這樣的人是我們年輕非洲人所需要的榜樣 。
and we need some environmental role models as well , and i've been hearing some of them today .	我們也需要一些環境的榜樣 , 我今天也在聽過其中一些例子 。
so i'm really grateful for this opportunity to share this message again , with everyone at ted .	所以我很感激這個機會再次分享這個訊息給ted的每個人 。
and i hope that some of us can get together and talk about some of these things , especially the roots and shoots program .	我希望我們當中有些人能聚在一起談論這些事 , 特別是根與芽計畫 。
and just a last word on that the young woman who's running this entire conference center , i met her today .	最後一個詞是年輕女性參加這整個會議中心 , 我今天遇見她 。
she came up so excited , with her certificate . she was [in] roots and shoots .	她非常興奮 , 有了她的證書 。 她是根和芽 。
she was in the leadership in dar es salaam .	她在沙拉姆的領導階層 。
she said it's helped her to do what she's doing .	她說 , 幫助她做她在做的事 。
and it was very , very exciting for me to meet her and see just one example of how young people , when they are empowered , given the opportunity to take action , to make the world a better place , truly are our hope for tomorrow .	我很興奮能見到她 , 看到一個例子 , 說明年輕人是如何被賦權的 , 給予他們行動的機會 , 讓這個世界變得更美好 , 真正是我們明天的希望 。
artist dianna cohen shares some tough truths about plastic pollution in the ocean and in our lives and some thoughts on how to free ourselves from the plastic gyre .	藝術家dannacohen分享了一些關於海洋中塑膠污染的棘手真相 , 在我們的生活中 , 以及一些關於如何解放我們自己 , 避免塑膠垃圾 。
