consumerism , global issues , green , mission blue , oceans , plastic	消費主義、全球議題、綠色、使命藍色、海洋、塑膠塑膠、塑膠、塑膠等 。
dianna cohen: tough truths about plastic pollution	黛安娜柯恩:很難說出塑膠污染的真相 。
i'm a visual artist , and i'm also one of the cofounders of the plastic pollution coalition .	我是視覺藝術家 , 我也是塑膠污染聯盟的共同創辦人之一 。
i've been working with plastic bags , which i cut up and sew back together as my primary material for my artwork for the last 20 years .	我和塑膠袋一起工作 , 在過去20年 , 我把塑膠袋剪下來 , 再縫合成我的作品的主要材料 。
i turn them into two and threedimensional pieces and sculptures and installations .	我把它們變成二、三維的零件、雕塑和裝置 。
upon working with the plastic , after about the first eight years , some of my work started to fissure and break down into smaller little bits of plastic .	和塑膠合作 , 大約八年後 , 我的一些作品開始裂縫 , 分解成更小的塑膠 。
and i thought , " great .	我心想: 「 太好了 。
it's ephemeral just like us . "	它和我們一樣短暫 。 」
upon educating myself a little further about plastics , i actually realized this was a bad thing .	我更進一步教育塑膠 , 事實上我意識到這是件壞事 。
it's a bad thing that plastic breaks down into smaller little bits , because it's always still plastic .	塑膠分解成小塊是壞事 , 因為它總是塑膠 。
and what we're finding is that a lot of it is in the marine environment .	我們發現 , 很多是在海洋環境中 。
i then , in the last few years , learned about the pacific garbage patch and the gyre .	過去幾年 , 我學到太平洋垃圾和健身房 。
and my initial reaction and i think this is a lot of people's first reaction to learning about it is , " oh my god !	我最初的反應和我認為這是很多人第一次了解這件事的反應: 「 天啊 !
we've got to go out there and clean this thing up . "	我們得走出去 , 把這東西清理乾淨 。 」
so i actually developed a proposal to go out with a cargo ship and two decommissioned fishing trawlers , a crane , a chipping machine and a coldmolding machine .	於是我開發了一個提案 , 帶著一艘貨船出去 , 兩艘退化的漁船 , 一艘船 , 一台拖車 , 一台拖車 , 一台冰冷的機器 。
and my intention was to go out to the gyre , raise awareness about this issue and begin to pick up the plastic , chip it into little bits and cold mold it into bricks that could potentially be used as building materials in underdeveloped communities .	我的意圖是 , 出去到健身房 , 提高對這個議題的認知 , 並開始將塑膠晶片放入小片和冷冷的模塊中 , 可以用來當建築在未開發的社區裡 。
i began talking with people who actually had been out to the gyre and were studying the plastic problem in the marine environment and upon doing so , i realized actually that cleaning it up would be a very small drop in the bucket relative to how much is being generated every day around the world , and that actually i needed to back up and look at the bigger picture .	我開始和那些真的去過健身房的人談話 , 研究海洋環境中的塑膠問題 , 並且在做這件事時 , 我意識到 , 清理乾淨會是一個非常小的滴落 , 和全世界每天產生多少東西 , 其實我需要回頭看更大的景象 。
and the bigger picture is: we need to find a way to turn off the faucet .	更大的圖片是:我們需要找到一個方法來關掉這個錯覺 。
we need to cut the spigot of singleuse and disposable plastics , which are entering the marine environment every day on a global scale .	我們需要切斷單一用途和無形塑膠的位置 , 每天都要進入海洋環境 , 在全球範圍內 。
so in looking at that , i also realized that i was really angry .	仔細看 , 我意識到我真的很生氣 。
i wasn't just concerned about plastic that you're trying to imagine out in the middle of the pacific ocean of which i have learned there are now 11 gyres , potentially , of plastic in five major oceans in the world .	我不只在乎塑膠 , 你還在試著想像在太平洋中央 , 我學到現在有11個塑膠在世界上五個大洋裡 。
it's not just that gyre of plastic that i'm concerned about it's the gyre of plastic in the supermarket .	不只是我關心的塑膠垃圾 , 而是超市的塑膠 。
i'd go to the supermarket and all of my food is packaged in plastic .	我會去超市 , 我所有的食物都是塑膠包裝的 。
all of my beverages are packaged in plastic , even at the health food market .	我所有的飲料都包裝在塑膠上 , 甚至在健康的食物市場 。
i'm also concerned about the plastic in the refrigerator , and i'm concerned about the plastic and the toxins that leach from plastic into us and into our bodies .	我也關心冰箱裡的塑膠 , 我對塑膠和毒素的關心 , 從塑膠到我們身體的塑膠和毒素 。
so i came together with a group of other people who were all looking at this issue , and we created the plastic pollution coalition .	所以我和一群人一起研究這個議題 , 我們創造了塑膠污染聯盟 。
we have many initiatives that we're working on , but some of them are very basic .	我們有許多我們正在努力的倡議 , 但其中有些是非常基本的 。
one is: if 80 to 90 percent of what we're finding in the ocean of the marine debris that we're finding in the ocean is plastic , then why don't we call it what it is .	第一:如果我們在海洋中發現的海洋碎片有80%到90%是塑膠 , 那麼我們為什麼不把它稱為它 。
recycling everybody kind of ends their books about being sustainable and greening with the idea of recycling .	回收每個人的書 , 終止了他們的永續和綠色 , 想著回收這個概念 。
you put something in a bin and you don't have to think about it again .	你把某樣東西放進一個罐子裡 , 你不需要再想一想 。
what is the reality of that ?	到底是怎麼回事 ?
in the united states , less than seven percent of our plastics are recycled .	在美國 , 少於7%的塑膠被回收 。
and if you really look into it , particularly when it comes to plastic bottles , most of it is only downcycled , or incinerated , or shipped to china .	如果你真的仔細觀察 , 特別是在塑膠瓶的時候 , 大部分的瓶子只會被倒退 , 或被刺激 , 或運送到中國 。
it is downcycled and turned into lesser things , while a glass bottle can be a glass bottle again or can be used again a plastic bottle can never be a plastic bottle again .	它被倒退化 , 轉變為更少的東西 , 而玻璃瓶可以再次使用玻璃瓶 , 或者再次使用塑膠瓶 , 再也不會是塑膠瓶 。
so this is a big issue for us .	這對我們來說是個大問題 。
another thing that we're looking at and asking people to think about is we've added a fourth r onto the front of the " reduce , reuse , recycle , " three r's , and that is refuse .	另一件我們正在研究並要求人們思考的事 , 就是我們在 「 減少、再利用、回收 」 的前面加上第四個r , 也就是拒絕了 。
whenever possible , refuse singleuse and disposable plastics .	不論何時 , 都拒絕單一用途和可丟棄的塑膠 。
alternatives exist ; some of them are very oldschool .	替代方案存在 , 有些是非常古老的學者 。
i myself am now collecting these cool pyrex containers and using those instead of glad and tupperware containers to store food in .	我現在在收集這些很酷的皮箱 , 用這些裝置 , 而不是很高興、很高興能容器來儲存食物 。
and i know that i am doing a service to myself and my family .	我知道我正在為自己和家人服務 。
it's very easy to pick up a stainlesssteel bottle or a glass bottle , if you're traveling and you've forgotten to bring your stainlesssteel bottle and fill that up with water or filtered water , versus purchasing plastic bottled water .	很容易拿起一瓶水 , 或一瓶玻璃瓶 , 如果你在旅行 , 你忘了帶著你的永續瓶子 , 填滿水或過濾水 , 和購買塑膠瓶的塑膠瓶 。
i guess what i want to say to everybody here and i know that you guys know a lot about this issue is that this is a huge problem in the oceans , but this is a problem that we've created as consumers and we can solve .	我想對在座的各位說些話 , 我知道你們對這個議題知道很多 , 就是這在海洋中是個大問題 , 但這是我們作為消費者所創造出來的問題 , 我們可以解決這個問題 。
we can solve this by raising awareness of the issue and teaching people to choose alternatives .	我們可以藉由提高注意力來解決這個問題 , 並教導人們選擇替代方案 。
so whenever possible , to choose alternatives to singleuse plastics .	所以 , 不論何時 , 要選擇單一的塑膠替代方案 。
we can cut the stem tide the stem of this into our oceans and in doing so , save our oceans , save our planet , save ourselves .	我們可以把幹細胞切割成我們的海洋 , 這麼做 , 拯救我們的海洋 , 拯救我們的地球 , 拯救我們自己 。
this demo from pattie maes' lab at mit , spearheaded by pranav mistry was the buzz of ted . it's a wearable device with a projector that paves the way for profound interaction with our environment . imagine " minority report " and then some .	這位來自麻省理工學院的帕蒂•瑪斯實驗室的展示 , 由帕拉夫•密斯特雷特所引導的 , 是ted的buzz 。 這是個可以穿戴的裝置 , 讓它與我們的環境互動 。 想像一下 「 少數性報告 」 和一些人 。
demo , design , interface design , technology	民主、設計、界面設計、科技、科技設計、設計、界面設計、科技 。
pattie maes and pranav mistry demo sixthsense	派蒂馬斯和帕拉夫•梅伊斯 , 示範第六道感 。
i've been intrigued by this question of whether we could evolve or develop a sixth sense a sense that would give us seamless access and easy access to metainformation or information that may exist somewhere that may be relevant to help us make the right decision about whatever it is that we're coming across .	我對這個問題很有興趣 , 探討我們是否能進化或發展出一種第六感感 , 能給予我們安全的取得、容易取得的資訊 , 或可能存在的資訊 , 來協助我們做出正確的決定 。
and some of you may argue , well , don't today's cell phones do that already ?	你們當中有些人可能會爭辯 , 嗯 , 今天的手機已經做到了嗎 ?
but i would say no .	但我會說不 。
when you meet someone here at ted and this is the top networking place , of course , of the year you don't shake somebody's hand and then say , " can you hold on for a moment while i take out my phone and google you ? "	當你在ted見面的時候 , 這當然是網絡最高的地方 , 你不搖別人的手 , 然後說: 「 你能不能暫時拿出手機和google搜尋你嗎 ? 」
or when you go to the supermarket and you're standing there in that huge aisle of different types of toilet papers , you don't take out your cell phone , and open a browser , and go to a website to try to decide which of these different toilet papers is the most ecologically responsible purchase to make .	或是當你去超市時 , 你站在那邊 , 上面有各種不同類型的衛生紙 , 你不會拿出手機 , 打開瀏覽器 , 去一個網站 , 試著決定這些不同的衛生紙中哪些是最環保的購買 。
so we don't really have easy access to all this relevant information that can just help us make optimal decisions about what to do next and what actions to take .	所以 , 我們沒有很容易取得所有相關的資訊 , 能夠協助我們做出最佳決定 , 來決定下一步該做什麼、採取什麼行動 。
and so my research group at the media lab has been developing a series of inventions to give us access to this information in a sort of easy way , without requiring that the user changes any of their behavior .	所以我在媒體實驗室的研究團隊開發了一系列的發明 , 以一種簡單的方式 , 不需要使用者改變他們的行為 。
and i'm here to unveil our latest effort , and most successful effort so far , which is still very much a work in process .	我來這裡是要揭開我們最新的努力 , 目前最成功的努力 , 這仍然是一個過程中的工作 。
i'm actually wearing the device right now and we've sort of cobbled it together with components that are off the shelf and that , by the way , only cost 350 dollars at this point in time .	我現在戴著這個裝置 , 我們把它和架子上的零件結合在一起 , 順道一提 , 目前只有350美元 。
i'm wearing a camera , just a simple webcam , a portable , batterypowered projection system with a little mirror .	我穿著攝影機 , 只是一個簡單的網路攝影機 , 一個可攜帶、電動投影系統 , 裡面有一面鏡子 。
these components communicate to my cell phone in my pocket which acts as the communication and computation device .	這些元件在我的口袋裡傳達我的手機 , 它是通訊和計算裝置 。
and in the video here we see my student pranav mistry , who's really the genius who's been implementing and designing this whole system .	在影片中 , 我們看到我的學生帕拉夫•米特里 , 他真的是實施和設計整個系統的天才 。
and we see how this system lets him walk up to any surface and start using his hands to interact with the information that is projected in front of him .	我們看到這個系統讓他走上任何表面 , 開始使用他的雙手 , 和他前面投射的資訊互動 。
the system tracks the four significant fingers .	系統追蹤了四個重要的手指 。
in this case , he's wearing simple marker caps that you may recognize .	在這個例子中 , 他戴著你可能認出的簡單標記帽子 。
but if you want a more stylish version you could also paint your nails in different colors .	但如果你想要更堅固的版本 , 你也可以用不同顏色來畫你的指甲 。
and the camera basically tracks these four fingers and recognizes any gestures that he's making so he can just go to , for example , a map of long beach , zoom in and out , etc .	基本上攝影機追蹤這四隻手指 , 並辨識出他所做的任何姿勢 , 例如 , 他可以直接去看一張長灘的地圖 , 放大 , 等等 。
the system also recognizes iconic gestures such as the " take a picture " gesture , and then takes a picture of whatever is in front of you .	系統也能辨識出 「 拍照 」 的標誌姿勢 , 然後拍下你面前的任何東西 。
and when he then walks back to the media lab , he can just go up to any wall and project all the pictures that he's taken , sort through them and organize them , and resize them , etc . , again using all natural gestures .	當他走回媒體實驗室時 , 他可以爬上任何牆壁 , 把他拍下來的照片 , 整理起來 , 重新組織它們 , 再次使用各種天然的手勢 。
so , some of you most likely were here two years ago and saw the demo by jeff han or some of you may think , " well , doesn't this look like the microsoft surface table ? "	兩年前 , 有些人可能在場 , 看到傑夫•漢的示範 , 或者有些人可能會想: 「 嗯 , 這看起來不像微軟的表面桌子嗎 ? 」
and yes , you also interact using natural gestures , both hands , etc .	是的 , 你也用天然手勢 , 雙手等等 。
but the difference here is that you can use any surface , you can walk to up to any surface , including your hand if nothing else is available and interact with this projected data .	但差別在於你可以用任何表面 , 你可以走到任何表面 , 包括你的手 , 如果沒有任何東西可以使用 , 和這個投影資料互動 。
the device is completely portable , and can be . . .	這個裝置是完全可攜帶的 , 可以是......
so one important difference is that it's totally mobile .	其中一個重要的差異是它完全是移動的 。
another even more important difference is that in mass production this would not cost more tomorrow than today's cell phones and would actually not sort of be a bigger packaging could look a lot more stylish than this version that i'm wearing around my neck .	另外一個更重要的差異是 , 在大規模生產時 , 比今天的手機還要多 , 實際上 , 不會比我在脖子上穿的這個更大的包裝 , 看起來比我穿著的這個版本還要多 。
but other than letting some of you live out your fantasy of looking as cool as tom cruise in " minority report , " the reason why we're really excited about this device is that it really can act as one of these sixthsense devices that gives you relevant information about whatever is in front of you .	但 , 除了讓你們當中一些人過得像湯姆•克魯斯在《少數報告》中很酷的幻想 , 我們之所以對這個裝置感到興奮 , 是因為它真的可以作為第六感的裝置之一 , 讓你知道在你面前的任何東西 。
so we see pranav here going into the supermarket and he's shopping for some paper towels .	我們看到帕拉夫走進超市 , 他購買了一些紙巾 。
and , as he picks up a product the system can recognize the product that he's picking up , using either image recognition or marker technology , and give him the green light or an orange light .	當他拿起一個產品時 , 這個系統可以辨識出他拿出來的產品 , 用影像辨識或標記技術 , 給他綠燈或橘光 。
he can ask for additional information .	他可以要求更多的資訊 。
so this particular choice here is a particularly good choice , given his personal criteria .	所以這個選擇是特別好的選擇 , 因為他的個人標準 。
some of you may want the toilet paper with the most bleach in it rather than the most ecologicallyresponsible choice .	有些人可能想要馬桶紙 , 上面有最多漏洞 , 而不是最有生態責任的選擇 。
if he picks up a book in the bookstore , he can get an amazon rating it gets projected right on the cover of the book .	如果他在書店裡拿起一本書 , 他可以得到亞馬遜評分 , 會直接投入書的封面 。
this is juan's book , our previous speaker , which gets a great rating , by the way , at amazon .	這是胡安的書 , 我們之前的講者 , 順便說一下 , 在亞馬遜 , 會得到很棒的評分 。
and so , pranav turns the page of the book and can then see additional information about the book reader comments , maybe sort of information by his favorite critic , etc .	所以 , 帕拉夫轉換了這本書的頁面 , 就可以看到關於讀者評論的額外資訊 , 或許他最喜歡的評論家 , 等等 。
if he turns to a particular page he finds an annotation by maybe an expert of a friend of ours that gives him a little bit of additional information about whatever is on that particular page .	如果他轉到某個特定的頁面 , 他可能會找到我們的朋友專家 , 給他一些額外的資訊 , 關於那個頁面上的任何東西 。
reading the newspaper it never has to be outdated .	閱讀報紙從來不需要過期 。
you can get video annotations of the event that you're reading about you can get the latest sports scores etc .	你可以收到關於你所讀到最新的運動分數 。
this is a more controversial one .	這是一個更具爭議性的 。
as you interact with someone at ted , maybe you can see a word cloud of the tags , the words that are associated with that person in their blog and personal web pages .	當你和ted的某人互動時 , 也許你可以看到標籤的一個字雲 , 和那個人的部落格和個人網頁相關的詞彙 。
in this case , the student is interested in cameras , etc .	在這個例子中 , 學生對攝影機很感興趣 , 等等 。
on your way to the airport , if you pick up your boarding pass , it can tell you that your flight is delayed , that the gate has changed , etc .	在你去機場的路上 , 如果你拿起你的登機車 , 它可以告訴你 , 你的班機延遲了 , 大門已經改變了 , 等等 。
and , if you need to know what the current time is it's as simple as drawing a watch on your arm .	如果你需要知道現在的時間是什麼 , 就如同在手臂上畫手錶一樣簡單 。
so that's where we're at so far in developing this sixth sense that would give us seamless access to all this relevant information about the things that we may come across .	所以 , 這就是我們目前正在發展的第六感感 , 讓我們能無縫地取得所有相關資訊 , 關於我們可能碰到的事物 。
my student pranav , who's really , like i said , the genius behind this .	我的學生帕拉夫 , 像我說的 , 這背後的天才 。
he does deserve a lot of applause because i don't think he's slept much in the last three months , actually .	他的確值得掌聲 , 因為我不認為他在過去三個月裡睡得太多 。
and his girlfriend is probably not very happy about him either .	他的女朋友可能也不高興 。
but it's not perfect yet , it's very much a work in progress .	但這還不是完美的 , 它是進步的一份工作 。
and who knows , maybe in another 10 years we'll be here with the ultimate sixth sense brain implant .	誰知道 , 也許在接下來的十年內 , 我們會帶著終極的第六感腦植入 。
phyllis rodriguez and aicha elwafi have a powerful friendship born of unthinkable loss . rodriguez' son was killed in the world trade center attacks on september 11 , 2001 ; elwafi's son zacarias moussaoui was convicted of a role in those attacks and is serving a life sentence . in hoping to find peace , these two moms have come to understand and respect one another .	菲莉絲•羅德里格和艾瑞克•伊瓦菲很有力的友誼 , 源自於世界上貿易中心的兒子在2001年9月11日被殺害 ; 埃爾瓦夫的兒子薩洛伊在這些攻擊中被定罪 , 希望能找到和平的句子 。 這兩個媽媽已經開始了解並尊重彼此 。
culture , global issues , politics	文化、全球議題、政治 , 和文化 , 和文化、全球議題、政治 。
9/11 healing: the mothers who found forgiveness , friendship	9/11的治癒:那些發現寬恕的母親 , 友誼 , 友誼 。
phyllis rodriguez: we are here today because of the fact that we have what most people consider an unusual friendship .	菲莉絲•羅德里格茲:我們今天來到這裡 , 是因為我們大多數人認為一個不尋常的友誼 。
and yet , it feels natural to us now .	然而 , 現在我們感覺很自然 。
i first learned that my son had been in the world trade center on the morning of september 11th , 2001 .	我第一次了解到 , 我兒子在2001年9月11日的早晨在世界貿易中心 。
we didn't know if he had perished yet until 36 hours later .	我們不知道他是否在36小時後死去 。
at the time , we knew that it was political .	當時 , 我們知道那是政治的 。
we were afraid of what our country was going to do in the name of our son my husband , orlando , and i and our family .	我們害怕我們的國家將以我們兒子的名字為名 , 我的丈夫奧蘭多 , 我和我們的家人 。
and when i saw it and yet , through the shock , the terrible shock , and the terrible explosion in our lives , literally , we were not vengeful .	當我看到它 , 然而 , 透過震驚 , 可怕的震驚 , 和我們生活中糟糕的爆炸 , 真的是 , 我們還沒有復仇 。
and a couple of weeks later when zacarias moussaoui was indicted on six counts of conspiracy to commit terrorism , and the u . s . government called for a death penalty for him , if convicted , my husband and i spoke out in opposition to that , publicly .	幾個星期後 , zacariasmosaoui被指示要犯下恐怖主義 , 美國政府要求對他做死刑 , 如果被定罪 , 我的丈夫和我公開對談 。
through that and through human rights groups , we were brought together with several other victims' families .	透過人權團體 , 我們和其他幾個受害者的家人聚在一起 。
when i saw aicha in the media , coming over when her son was indicted , and i thought , " what a brave woman .	當我在媒體上看到aicha , 她兒子被指控時 , 我心想: 「 什麼是勇敢的女人 。
someday i want to meet that woman when i'm stronger . "	有一天 , 我會想在我更強的時候認識那個女人 。 」
i was still in deep grief ; i knew i didn't have the strength .	我仍然在深深的悲慟中 , 我知道我沒有力量 。
i knew i would find her someday , or we would find each other .	我知道有一天我會找到她 , 或找到彼此 。
because , when people heard that my son was a victim , i got immediate sympathy .	因為 , 當人們聽到我兒子是受害者時 , 我馬上就同情了 。
but when people learned what her son was accused of , she didn't get that sympathy .	但當人們知道她兒子被指控時 , 她沒有得到同情 。
but her suffering is equal to mine .	但她的痛苦與我同等 。
so we met in november 2002 , and aicha will now tell you how that came about .	我們在2002年11月見面 , aicha現在會告訴你這是怎麼回事 。
aicha elwafi: good afternoon , ladies and gentlemen .	aichaelwafi:午安 , 各位先生女士
i am the mother of zacarias moussaoui .	我是zacariasmosaoui的母親 。
and i asked the organization of human rights to put me in touch with the parents of the victims .	我請人權組織把我和受害者的父母聯繫起來 。
so they introduced me to five families .	所以他們介紹我到五個家庭 。
and i saw phyllis , and i watched her .	我看到phyllis , 看著她 。
she was the only mother in the group .	她是團隊中唯一的母親 。
the others were brothers , sisters .	其他人則是兄弟姐妹 。
and i saw in her eyes that she was a mother , just like me .	我在她的眼中看到她是母親 , 就像我一樣 。
i suffered a lot as a mother .	我身為母親所苦 。
i was married when i was 14 .	我14歲就結婚了 。
i lost a child when i was 15 , a second child when i was 16 .	我十五歲時失去了一個孩子 , 一個我十六歲的第二個孩子 。
so the story with zacarias was too much really .	zacarias的故事實在太多了 。
and i still suffer , because my son is like he's buried alive .	我仍然受苦 , 因為我的兒子就像被埋葬一樣 。
i know she really cried for her son .	我知道她真的為她的兒子哭了 。
but she knows where he is .	但她知道他在哪裡 。
my son , i don't know where he is .	我兒子不知道他在哪裡 。
i don't know if he's alive . i don't know if he's tortured .	我不知道他是否活著 。 我不知道他是否被虐待 。
i don't know what happened to him .	我不知道他發生了什麼事 。
so that's why i decided to tell my story , so that my suffering is something positive for other women .	這就是為什麼我決定要說我的故事 , 所以我的痛苦對其他女性來說是正面的 。
for all the women , all the mothers that give life , you can give back , you can change .	對所有的婦女來說 , 所有給予生命的媽媽 , 你可以回饋 , 你可以改變 。
it's up to us women , because we are women , because we love our children .	因為我們是女性 , 因為我們是女性 , 因為我們愛我們的孩子 。
we must be handinhand and do something together .	我們一定是手工的 , 一起做點什麼 。
it's not against women , it's for us , for us women , for our children .	不是反對女性 , 而是為了我們女性 , 為我們的孩子 。
i talk against violence , against terrorism .	我對抗暴力 , 反對恐怖主義 。
i go to schools to talk to young , muslim girls so they don't accept to be married against their will very young .	我去學校和年輕的穆斯林女孩談話 , 讓他們不接受和她們結婚的意志很年輕 。
so if i can save one of the young girls , and avoid that they get married and suffer as much as i did , well this is something good .	所以 , 如果我能拯救其中一個年輕女孩 , 避免她們和我一樣結婚、受苦 , 這是件好事 。
this is why i'm here in front of you .	這就是為什麼我要站在你們面前 。
pr: i would like to say that i have learned so much from aicha , starting with that day we had our very first meeting with other family members which was a very private meeting with security , because it was november 2002 , and , frankly , we were afraid of the superpatriotism of that time in the country those of us family members .	pr:我想說 , 我從阿加汗學到很多 , 從那天開始 , 我們和其他家庭成員見面是非常私人的會議 , 因為那是2002年11月 , 坦白說 , 我們害怕當時國家的超級病態 , 那些家庭成員 。
but we were all so nervous .	但我們都很緊張 。
" why does she want to meet us ? "	「 為什麼她想要見我們 ? 」
and then she was nervous .	接著 , 她很緊張 。
" why did we want to meet her ? "	「 為什麼我們要見她 ? 」
what did we want from each other ?	我們彼此想要什麼 ?
before we knew each others' names , or anything , we had embraced and wept .	在我們認識彼此的名字之前 , 我們已經擁抱和哭泣 。
then we sat in a circle with support , with help , from people experienced in this kind of reconciliation .	接著 , 我們坐在一個圓圈裡 , 帶著協助 , 從人們體驗到這種協調 。
and aicha started , and she said , " i don't know if my son is guilty or innocent , but i want to tell you how sorry i am for what happened to your families .	aicha開始 , 她說: 「 我不知道我的兒子是有罪或無辜 , 但我想告訴各位 , 我對你的家庭發生了多麼的抱歉 。
i know what it is to suffer , and i feel that if there is a crime , a person should be tried fairly and punished . "	我知道痛苦是什麼 , 我覺得如果有犯罪 , 一個人應該被懲罰 。 」
but she reached out to us in that way , and it was , i'd like to say , it was an icebreaker .	但她以這種方式向我們伸出援手 , 我想要說 , 那是個冰箱 。
and what happened then is we all told our stories , and we all connected as human beings .	接下來發生的是 , 我們都說自己的故事 , 我們都以人類的身分連結在一起 。
by the end of the afternoon it was about three hours after lunch we'd felt as if we'd known each other forever .	下午結束後 , 午餐後大約三小時 , 我們感覺好像永遠認識對方一樣 。
now what i learned from her , is a woman , not only who could be so generous under these present circumstances and what it was then , and what was being done to her son , but the life she's had .	我從她身上學到的是 , 一個女人 , 不只是在這些情況下 , 誰會這麼慷慨 , 以及當時的狀況 , 以及她兒子做了什麼 , 還有她的生活 。
i never had met someone with such a hard life , from such a totally different culture and environment from my own .	我從來沒有遇過這麼辛苦的人生 , 來自我自己的文化和環境 。
and i feel that we have a special connection , which i value very much .	我覺得我們有一個特殊的連結 , 我非常重視它 。
and i think it's all about being afraid of the other , but making that step and then realizing , " hey , this wasn't so hard .	我覺得這全是害怕對方的 , 但要踏出那一步 , 然後意識到: 「 嘿 , 這並不難 。
who else can i meet that i don't know , or that i'm so different from ? "	還有誰能見到我不知道的 , 或我和他是如此不同 ? 」
so , aicha , do you have a couple of words for conclusion ?	所以 , aicha , 你有幾個字來做結論嗎 ?
because our time is up .	因為我們的時間到了 。
aw: i wanted to say that we have to try to know other people , the other .	aw:我想說 , 我們必須試著認識別人 , 另一個人 。
you have to be generous , and your hearts must be generous , your mind must be generous .	你必須慷慨 , 你的心臟一定是慷慨的 , 你的心智一定是慷慨的 。
you must be tolerant .	你必須要容忍 。
you have to fight against violence .	你必須對抗暴力 。
and i hope that someday we'll all live together in peace and respecting each other .	我希望有一天 , 我們都會一起生活在和平和尊重彼此 。
this is what i wanted to say .	這是我想要說的 。
too much of the world lacks access to clean drinking water . engineer michael pritchard did something about it inventing the portable lifesaver filter , which can make the most revolting water drinkable in seconds . an amazing demo from tedglobal 2009 .	世界上太多人無法取得乾淨飲用水 。 工程師麥可•普里奇 , 針對它發明可攜式的生活過濾器 , 可以在幾秒鐘內完成最精彩的飲用水 。 一個來自tedglobal的演示 。

i'd like to talk about a couple of things today .	今天我想談談幾件事 。
the first thing is water .	第一是水 。
now i see you've all been enjoying the water that's been provided for you here at the conference , over the past couple of days .	現在我看到你們都很享受這場研討會所提供的水 , 過去幾天 。
and i'm sure you'll feel that it's from a safe source .	我相信你們會覺得這是安全來源的 。
but what if it wasn't ?	但如果不是呢 ?
what if it was from a source like this ?	如果是像這樣的來源呢 ?
then statistics would actually say that half of you would now be suffering with diarrhea .	接著 , 統計數字會說 , 你們當中有一半的人會遭到腹瀉 。
i talked a lot in the past about statistics , and the provision of safe drinking water for all .	在過去 , 我談了很多關於統計 , 以及所有人的安全飲用水 。
but they just don't seem to get through .	但它們似乎沒有穿過 。
and i think i've worked out why .	我想我已經知道為什麼 。
it's because , using current thinking , the scale of the problem just seems too huge to contemplate solving .	因為 , 利用目前的思維 , 問題的規模似乎太大 , 無法思考解決問題 。
so we just switch off: us , governments and aid agencies .	所以我們就關掉了:我們、政府和援助機構 。
well , today , i'd like to show you that through thinking differently , the problem has been solved .	今天 , 我想用不同的角度來展示 , 這個問題已經解決了 。
by the way , since i've been speaking , another 13 , 000 people around the world are suffering now with diarrhea .	順帶一提 , 自從我說話之後 , 全世界還有一萬三千人正在受腹瀉所苦 。
and four children have just died .	四個孩子剛過世了 。
i invented lifesaver bottle because i got angry .	我發明了救生瓶 , 因為我生氣了 。
i , like most of you , was sitting down , the day after christmas in 2004 , when i was watching the devastating news of the asian tsunami as it rolled in , playing out on tv .	我和大部分人一樣 , 在2004年聖誕節後的那一天 , 我看著亞洲海嘯爆炸的消息 , 在電視上播放 。
the days and weeks that followed , people fleeing to the hills , being forced to drink contaminated water or face death .	接下來的日子 , 人們逃到山丘上 , 被迫喝污染的水或死亡 。
that really stuck with me .	這真的困住了我 。
then , a few months later , hurricane katrina slammed into the side of america .	接著 , 幾個月後 , 卡崔娜颶風溜到美國的一邊 。
" okay , " i thought , " here's a first world country , let's see what they can do . "	我心想: 「 好吧 , 這裡是第一個國家 , 讓我們看看他們能做什麼 。 」
do you know it took five days to get water to the superdome ?	你知道這花了五天才能把水送到超級迷因上嗎 ?
people were shooting each other on the streets for tv sets and water .	人們在街上為電視設施和水開槍 。
that's when i decided i had to do something .	那是我決定要做點什麼的時候 。
now i spent a lot of time in my garage , over the next weeks and months , and also in my kitchen much to the dismay of my wife .	現在我花了很多時間在我的車庫裡 , 在接下來的幾週、幾個月 , 我也在廚房裡 , 把我太太的苦惱都花了很多時間 。
however , after a few failed prototypes , i finally came up with this , the lifesaver bottle .	然而 , 在幾次失敗的原型之後 , 我終於想出了這個 , 救生瓶 。
okay , now for the science bit .	好 , 現在來談科學 。
before lifesaver , the best hand filters were only capable of filtering down to about 200 nanometers .	在生命saver之前 , 最好的過濾器只能過濾到大約200奈米 。
the smallest bacteria is about 200 nanometers .	最小的細菌大約是200奈米 。
so a 200nanometer bacteria is going to get through a 200nanometer hole .	一個200奈米的細菌將會經歷200奈米的洞 。
the smallest virus , on the other hand , is about 25 nanometers .	另一方面 , 最小的病毒大約是25奈米 。
so that's definitely going to get through those 200 nanometer holes .	這肯定會穿過那200奈米的洞 。
lifesaver pores are 15 nanometers .	救生器是15奈米長 。
so nothing is getting through .	所以 , 沒有什麼事情發生 。
okay , i'm going to give you a bit of a demonstration .	好 , 我要給你們一些示範 。
would you like to see that ?	你會想看到嗎 ?

so someone's done that up .	有人這樣做 。
fine city of oxford , so what i've done is i've gone and got some water from the river cherwell , and the river thames , that flow through here . and this is the water .	牛津的好城市 , 我所做的是 , 我從河流cherwell取得一些水 , 河流 , 流過這裡 。 這就是水 。
but i got to thinking , you know , if we were in the middle of a flood zone in bangladesh , the water wouldn't look like this .	但我必須想 , 如果我們在孟加拉的洪水區中間 , 水就不會像這樣 。
so i've gone and got some stuff to add into it .	所以 , 我已經有了一些東西來加入它 。
and this is from my pond .	這是我的池塘 。
have a smell of that , mister cameraman .	聞一下 , 攝影師 。
we're just going to pour that in there .	我們只會把它倒進去 。
michael pritchard: okay . we've got some runoff from a sewage plant farm .	michaelpritchard:好的 , 我們有一些從污水農場中跑出來的 。
so i'm just going to put that in there .	所以我就把這個放進去 。
put that in there . there we go .	把它放進去 , 開始 。
and some other bits and pieces , chuck that in there .	還有其他的部分和碎片 , 把它抓進去 。
and i've got a gift here from a friend of mine's rabbit .	我這裡有一位朋友的兔子的禮物 。
so we're just going to put that in there as well .	所以 , 我們也要把它放進去 。
the lifesaver bottle works really simply .	救生瓶真的很簡單 。
you just scoop the water up .	你只要把水拿起來 。
today i'm going to use a jug just to show you all . let's get a bit of that poo in there .	今天我要用一個袋子給你們看 。 讓我們看看裡面的那個小便 。
that's not dirty enough . let's just stir that up a little bit .	那還不夠髒 。 讓我們稍微攪拌一下 。
okay , so i'm going to take this really filthy water , and put it in here . do you want a drink yet ?	好吧 , 我要用這個非常骯髒的水 , 把它放進這裡 。 你想喝杯嗎 ?
okay . there we go .	好 , 開始了 。
give it a few pumps . okay ?	給它一些幫浦 。 好嗎 ?
that's all that's necessary .	這些都是必要的 。
now as soon as i pop the teat , sterile drinking water is going to come out .	一旦我採用茶 , 無菌的飲用水就會出現 。
i've got to be quick . okay , ready ?	我得快點 。 好 , 準備好了嗎 ?
there we go . mind the electrics .	開始了 。 請注意電源 。
that is safe , sterile drinking water .	那是安全、無菌的飲用水 。
there you go chris .	克里斯 。
what's it taste of ?	它的味道是什麼 ?
let's see chris's program throughout the rest of the show . okay ?	我們來看看克里斯的節目在整個節目中 。 好嗎 ?
okay . lifesaver bottle is used by thousands of people around the world .	好吧 , 世界各地數以千計的人使用生命瓶 。
it'll last for 6 , 000 liters .	它會維持六千公升 。
and when it's expired , using failsafe technology , the system will shut off , protecting the user .	當它被啟發時 , 使用失敗的技術 , 系統會關閉 , 保護使用者 。
pop the cartridge out . pop a new one in .	把地毯拿出來 , 放進去 。
it's good for another 6 , 000 liters .	這對六千公升來說是好的 。
so let's look at the applications .	我們來看看應用程式 。
traditionally , in a crisis , what do we do ?	傳統上 , 在危機中 , 我們該怎麼做 ?
then , after a few weeks , we set up camps .	幾週後 , 我們成立了營地 。
and people are forced to come into the camps to get their safe drinking water .	人們被迫進入營地 , 以取得安全的飲用水 。
what happens when 20 , 000 people congregate in a camp ?	當兩萬人聚集在營地時會發生什麼事 ?
diseases spread . more resources are required .	疾病散播 。 需要更多的資源 。
the problem just becomes selfperpetuating .	問題就在於自我延續 。
but by thinking differently , and shipping these , people can stay put .	但藉由不同的思考方式 , 運送這些人可以留下 。
they can make their own sterile drinking water , and start to get on with rebuilding their homes and their lives .	他們可以製造自己的無菌飲用水 , 開始重建家園和生活 。
now , it doesn't require a natural disaster for this to work .	這樣做並不需要天然的災難 。
using the old thinking , of national infrastructure and pipe work , is too expensive .	用舊的想法 , 國家基礎建設和管道工作太貴了 。
when you run the numbers on a calculator , you run out of noughts .	當你在計算機上運算數字時 , 你就會跑出音符 。
so here is the " thinking different " bit .	這是 「 不同的思考 」 的一部分 。
instead of shipping water , and using manmade processes to do it , let's use mother nature . she's got a fantastic system .	不用運送水 , 用人造過程來做 , 咱們用大自然 。 她有一個很棒的系統 。
she picks the water up from there , desalinates it , for free , transports it over there , and dumps it onto the mountains , rivers , and streams .	她從那裡撿起水 , 免費運送到那裡 , 把它丟到山上 , 河流和溪流 。
and where do people live ? near water .	人們住在哪裡 ? 靠近水 。
all we've go to do is make it sterile . how do we do that ?	我們要做的就是讓它變得無效 。 我們該怎麼做 ?
well , we could use the lifesaver bottle .	嗯 , 我們可以用救生瓶 。
or we could use one of these .	或者 , 我們可以用其中一個 。
the same technology , in a jerry can .	同樣的技術 , 在jerry可以 。
this will process 25 , 000 liters of water ; that's good enough for a family of four , for three years .	這個過程會處理2萬5千公升的水 ; 這足夠給一個四、三年的家庭 。
and how much does it cost ?	要花多少錢 ?
about half a cent a day to run .	每天大約有半分錢可以跑 。
so , by thinking differently , and processing water at the point of use , mothers and children no longer have to walk four hours a day to collect their water .	所以 , 用不同的方式思考 , 處理水 , 母親和孩子不再需要每天四小時去收集他們的水 。
they can get it from a source nearby .	他們可以從附近的來源取得 。
so with just eight billion dollars , we can hit the millennium goal's target of halving the number of people without access to safe drinking water .	只要八十億美元 , 我們就能達到千禧目標的目標 , 避免飲用水的人口數目 。
to put that into context , the u . k . government spends about 12 billion pounds a year on foreign aid .	要把這句話說成 , 英國政府每年花費大約120億英鎊在國外援助上 。
but why stop there ?	但為什麼要停在那裡 ?
with 20 billion dollars , everyone can have access to safe drinking water .	有了20億美金 , 每個人都可以取得安全飲用水 。
so the threeandahalf billion people that suffer every year as a result , and the two million kids that die every year , will live .	因此 , 每年有三十五億人受苦 , 每年有兩百萬名孩童會活下來 。
paddy ashdown claims that we are living in a moment in history where power is changing in ways it never has before . in a spellbinding talk at tedxbrussels he outlines the three major global shifts that he sees coming .	帕迪•阿許諾聲稱我們生活在歷史上的某個時刻 , 權力正在改變 。 在tedxbrsel的拼字演說中 , 他推出了他所看到的三大全球轉變 。
foreign policy , global issues , politics , world cultures	外交政策、全球議題、政治、世界文化文化、外交政策、全球議題、議題、政治、世界議題、文化、文化、文化 。
paddy ashdown: the global power shift	paddyashown:全球權力轉移 。
there's a poem written by a very famous english poet at the end of the 19th century .	在十九世紀末 , 有一首詩寫了一首著名的英文詩 。
it was said to echo in churchill's brain in the 1930s .	在1930年代 , 它被告知在教堂的大腦 。
and the poem goes: " on the idle hill of summer , lazy with the flow of streams , hark i hear a distant drummer , drumming like a sound in dreams , far and near and low and louder on the roads of earth go by , dear to friend and food to powder , soldiers marching , soon to die . "	這首詩說: 「 在夏天的小山丘上 , 懶惰著河流 , 我聽到一個遙遠的鼓聲 , 像個在夢裡的聲音 , 距離很遠、很低、很大聲 , 在地球的路上 , 親愛的朋友、食物到粉碎 , 士兵們很快就死了 。 」
those who are interested in poetry , the poem is " a shropshire lad " written by a . e . housman .	那些對詩有興趣的人 , 這首詩是《shropshirelad》 , 由a.housman寫的 。
but what housman understood , and you hear it in the symphonies of nielsen too , was that the long , hot , silvan summers of stability of the 19th century were coming to a close , and that we were about to move into one of those terrifying periods of history when power changes .	但 , 休士曼明白的 , 你也在尼爾森的交響曲中聽到 , 就是十九世紀的長、熱、銀的穩定夏天即將要接近 , 我們即將進入歷史上最可怕的時期 , 那時權力改變了 。
and these are always periods , ladies and gentlemen , accompanied by turbulence , and all too often by blood .	這些都是時期 , 各位先生女士 , 伴隨著亂流 , 通常都是血液 。
and my message for you is that i believe we are condemned , if you like , to live at just one of those moments in history when the gimbals upon which the established order of power is beginning to change and the new look of the world , the new powers that exist in the world , are beginning to take form .	我告訴你們的是 , 我相信我們被迫生活在歷史上的那一刻當權力所建立的秩序開始改變世界的新看法 , 現有的新勢力開始形成
and these are and we see it very clearly today nearly always highly turbulent times , highly difficult times , and all too often very bloody times .	而我們今天看到的這些是非常清楚的 , 幾乎都是高度衝動、高度困難的時光 , 很多時候都太血腥了 。
by the way , it happens about once every century .	順帶一提 , 它每世紀都會發生一次 。
you might argue that the last time it happened and that's what housman felt coming and what churchill felt too was that when power passed from the old nations , the old powers of europe , across the atlantic to the new emerging power of the united states of america the beginning of the american century .	你可能會說 , 上次發生了 , 那就是休士曼的感受 , 以及教堂的感受 , 當權力從舊的國家傳遞 , 歐洲的舊勢力 , 跨越大西洋 , 到美國一開始的新興勢力 。
and of course , into the vacuum where the tooold european powers used to be were played the two bloody catastrophes of the last century the one in the first part and the one in the second part: the two great world wars .	當然 , 在真空中 , 過去歐洲的權力在上個世紀的兩場血腥災難 , 第一部分和第二部分:世界大戰 。
mao zedong used to refer to them as the european civil wars , and it's probably a more accurate way of describing them .	毛澤東曾經稱之為歐洲內戰 , 這可能是更精確的描述方式 。
well , ladies and gentlemen , we live at one of those times .	各位先生女士 , 我們生活在其中之一 。
but for us , i want to talk about three factors today .	但對我們來說 , 我今天想談三個因素 。
and the first of these , the first two of these , is about a shift in power .	首先 , 前兩個是權力的轉變 。
and the second is about some new dimension which i want to refer to , which has never quite happened in the way it's happening now .	第二個是關於一些我想要指的新維度 , 它從來沒有發生過 。
but let's talk about the shifts of power that are occurring to the world .	但 , 讓我們來談談 「 權力 」 的轉變 。
and what is happening today is , in one sense , frightening because it's never happened before .	今天發生的是 , 某種程度上 , 恐怖的原因是它從來沒有發生過 。
we have seen lateral shifts of power the power of greece passed to rome and the power shifts that occurred during the european civilizations but we are seeing something slightly different .	我們已經看過後續的權力轉換 , 希臘通過羅馬的力量 , 以及在歐洲文明中發生的權力轉變 , 但我們看到了稍微不同的東西 。
for power is not just moving laterally from nation to nation .	權力不僅是從國家轉移到國家 。
it's also moving vertically .	它也垂直移動 。
what's happening today is that the power that was encased , held to accountability , held to the rule of law , within the institution of the nation state has now migrated in very large measure onto the global stage .	今天正在發生的事是 , 被監禁的權力 , 被責任歸咎於法律的規則 , 在國家的制度中 , 現在已經在全球的舞台上遷移了 。
the globalization of power we talk about the globalization of markets , but actually it's the globalization of real power .	全球化的權力 , 我們談論全球化的市場 , 但實際上是全球化的權力 。
and where , at the nation state level that power is held to accountability subject to the rule of law , on the international stage it is not .	在這個國家的權力層面上 , 權力在法律的規則上 , 在國際舞台上 , 權力並非如此 。
the international stage and the global stage where power now resides: the power of the internet , the power of the satellite broadcasters , the power of the money changers this vast moneygoround that circulates now 32 times the amount of money necessary for the trade it's supposed to be there to finance the money changers , if you like , the financial speculators that have brought us all to our knees quite recently , the power of the multinational corporations now developing budgets often bigger than mediumsized countries .	國際舞台和全球舞台現在仍然存在:網路的力量 , 衛星廣播的力量 , 金錢改變了這巨大的貨幣 , 現在流通了32倍 , 交易必要的金錢數目 , 應該是為了金錢改善 , 如果你喜歡 , 金融業者最近才把我們全部帶到我們的膝關節 , 這些金融企業的力量 , 比起中型國家的預算還要大 。
these live in a global space which is largely unregulated , not subject to the rule of law , and in which people may act free of constraint .	這些生活在一個大部份沒有規範的全球空間中 , 不受法律規範 , 而在這些空間中 , 人們可能免於限制 。
now that suits the powerful up to a moment .	這套裝置有強大的力量 。
it's always suitable for those who have the most power to operate in spaces without constraint , but the lesson of history is that , sooner or later , unregulated space space not subject to the rule of law becomes populated , not just by the things you wanted international trade , the internet , etc . but also by the things you don't want international criminality , international terrorism .	對那些在沒有限制的空間中運作最適合的人來說 , 但歷史的教訓是 , 不久後 , 不受規範的空間 , 不受法律規範的限制 , 不僅僅是你想要國際貿易、網路等等的東西 。 還有那些你不想要國際犯罪、國際恐怖主義的東西 。
the revelation of 9/11 is that even if you are the most powerful nation on earth , nevertheless , those who inhabit that space can attack you even in your most iconic of cities one bright september morning .	911的揭示是 , 即使你是地球上最強大的國家 , 儘管如此 , 那些居住的空間可以攻擊你 , 即使是在一個明亮的九月的早晨 , 一個明亮的城市 。
it's said that something like 60 percent of the four million dollars that was taken to fund 9/11 actually passed through the institutions of the twin towers which 9/11 destroyed .	據說 , 大約百分之六十萬美元被拿來資助9/11的資金實際上通過了雙胞胎塔的機構 , 911摧毀了 。
you see , our enemies also use this space the space of mass travel , the internet , satellite broadcasters to be able to get around their poison , which is about destroying our systems and our ways .	我們的敵人也使用這個空間 , 大眾旅行、網路、衛星廣播 , 能夠在它們的毒藥中四處走動 , 重點在摧毀我們的系統和我們的方式 。
sooner or later , sooner or later , the rule of history is that where power goes governance must follow .	很快 , 不久之後 , 歷史的規則是權力的治理必須遵循 。
and if it is therefore the case , as i believe it is , that one of the phenomenon of our time is the globalization of power , then it follows that one of the challenges of our time is to bring governance to the global space .	如果我相信 , 如同我所說的 , 我們這個時代的一個現象就是權力全球化 , 那麼我們這個時代的挑戰之一就是把治理帶到全球 。
and i believe that the decades ahead of us now will be to a greater or lesser extent turbulent the more or less we are able to achieve that aim: to bring governance to the global space .	我相信 , 未來的幾十年將會變成更大或更少的亂流 , 我們能達成目標:將治理帶給全球空間 。
now notice , i'm not talking about government .	請注意 , 我不是在說政府 。
i'm not talking about setting up some global democratic institution .	我不是在說要設立全球民主制度 。
my own view , by the way , ladies and gentlemen , is that this is unlikely to be done by spawning more u . n . institutions .	順道一提 , 我自己的觀點是 , 女士們先生們 , 不太可能通過聯合國的機構來完成這件事 。
if we didn't have the u . n . , we'd have to invent it .	如果我們沒有聯合國 , 我們就得發明它 。
the world needs an international forum .	世界需要國際論壇 。
it needs a means by which you can legitimize international action .	它需要一種方法 , 讓國際行動合法化 。
but when it comes to governance of the global space , my guess is this won't happen through the creation of more u . n . institutions .	但 , 當談到全球空間的治理時 , 我猜這不會發生在聯合國的創建中 。
it will actually happen by the powerful coming together and making treatybased systems , treatybased agreements , to govern that global space .	它會發生在強大的團結並建立以治療為基礎的系統 , 以治療為基礎的協議 , 來管理這個全球空間 。
and if you look , you can see them happening , already beginning to emerge .	如果你看 , 你可以看到他們正在發生 , 已經開始出現了 。
the world trade organization: treatybased organization , entirely treatybased , and yet , powerful enough to hold even the most powerful , the united states , to account if necessary .	世界貿易組織:以條約為基礎的組織 , 完全以條約為基礎 , 然而 , 強大到能夠容納最強大的美國 , 如果必要的話 。
kyoto: the beginnings of struggling to create a treatybased organization .	kyoto:努力創造一個以條約為基礎的組織 。
the g20: we know now that we have to put together an institution which is capable of bringing governance to that financial space for financial speculation .	g20:我們現在知道 , 我們必須建立一個機構 , 能夠將治理帶到金融空間 , 來推測金融空間 。
and that's what the g20 is , a treatybased institution .	這就是g20所謂的基礎機構 。
now there's a problem there , and we'll come back to it in a minute , which is that if you bring the most powerful together to make the rules in treatybased institutions , to fill that governance space , then what happens to the weak who are left out ?	現在有一個問題 , 我們等一下會再回來談 , 那就是 , 如果你把最強大的力量集合起來 , 建立以條約為基礎的機構 , 來填補那些治理空間 , 那麼剩下的弱點呢 ?
and that's a big problem , and we'll return to it in just a second .	這是個大問題 , 我們只要一秒鐘就回來 。
so there's my first message , that if you are to pass through these turbulent times more or less turbulently , then our success in doing that will in large measure depend on our capacity to bring sensible governance to the global space .	所以 , 我的第一個訊息是 , 如果你要通過這些亂流 , 或多或少的亂流 , 那麼 , 我們的成功將會取決於我們的能力 , 將可感應的治理帶給全球空間 。
and watch that beginning to happen .	看看這個開始發生的 。
my second point is , and i know i don't have to talk to an audience like this about such a thing , but power is not just shifting vertically , it's also shifting horizontally .	我的第二點是 , 我知道我不需要和像這樣的觀眾談這樣的話 , 但權力不只是垂直轉移 , 它也在橫向轉移 。
you might argue that the story , the history of civilizations , has been civilizations gathered around seas with the first ones around the mediterranean , the more recent ones in the ascendents of western power around the atlantic .	你可能會說 , 文明的歷史 , 已經在海裡聚集了文明 , 和地中海的第一批人 , 最近在大西洋的西方權力 。
well it seems to me that we're now seeing a fundamental shift of power , broadly speaking , away from nations gathered around the atlantic [seaboard] to the nations gathered around the pacific rim .	對我來說 , 我們現在看到的是權力的基本轉變 , 廣泛的說話 , 遠離大西洋的國家 , 聚集在太平洋的河岸邊 。
now that begins with economic power , but that's the way it always begins .	經濟力量始於此 , 但這一直是它的起源 。
you already begin to see the development of foreign policies , the augmentation of military budgets occurring in the other growing powers in the world .	你已經開始看到外交政策的發展 , 軍事預算的擴增發生在世界上其他發展勢力的發展中 。
i think actually this is not so much a shift from the west to the east ; something different is happening .	我認為這並不是從西方轉變到東方 , 而是不同的事正在發生 。
my guess is , for what it's worth , is that the united states will remain the most powerful nation on earth for the next 10 years , 15 , but the context in which she holds her power has now radically altered ; it has radically changed .	我的猜測是 , 對於值得什麼 , 美國將保留地球上最強大的國家 , 未來十年、15年 , 但她握有權力的情境現在已經徹底改變了 ; 它徹底地改變了 。
we are coming out of 50 years , most unusual years , of history in which we have had a totally monopolar world , in which every compass needle for or against has to be referenced by its position to washington a world bestrode by a single colossus .	我們從五十年來 , 最不尋常的歷史 , 我們有完全單一的世界 , 每一根針或對它的位置都需要被華盛頓世界最佳世界 。
but that's not a usual case in history .	但這不是歷史上常見的案例 。
in fact , what's now emerging is the much more normal case of history .	事實上 , 現在出現的是更正常的歷史案例 。
you're beginning to see the emergence of a multipolar world .	你已經開始看到多重世界的出現了 。
up until now , the united states has been the dominant feature of our world .	目前為止 , 美國一直是世界主要的特徵 。
they will remain the most powerful nation , but they will be the most powerful nation in an increasingly multipolar world .	他們會維持最強大的國家 , 但在越來越多世界中 , 他們將會是最強大的國家 。
and you begin to see the alternative centers of power building up in china , of course , though my own guess is that china's ascent to greatness is not smooth .	當然 , 你開始看到在中國建立權力中心的替代方案 , 當然 , 我的猜測是 , 中國對偉大的重要性並不平滑 。
it's going to be quite grumpy as china begins to democratize her society after liberalizing her economy .	中國將開始在自由化經濟後讓她的社會民主化 。
but that's a subject of a different discussion .	但這是個討論的主題 。
you see india , you see brazil .	你看印度 , 你看到巴西 。
you see increasingly that the world now looks actually , for us europeans , much more like europe in the 19th century .	你可以看到 , 越來越多世界現在看起來 , 對我們歐洲人來說 , 在十九世紀 , 比較像歐洲 。
europe in the 19th century: a great british foreign secretary , lord canning , used to describe it as the " european concert of powers . "	歐洲在十九世紀 , 一個偉大的英國外國秘書長 , 羅德•坎德 , 曾經把它描述為 「 歐洲的權力協會 」 。
there was a balance , a fivesided balance .	有一個平衡 , 一個五方的平衡 。
britain always played to the balance .	英國總是在平衡上演 。
if paris got together with berlin , britain got together with vienna and rome to provide a counterbalance .	如果巴黎和柏林團結起來 , 英國和維也納和羅馬合作 , 提供平衡 。
now notice , in a period which is dominated by a monopolar world , you have fixed alliances nato , the warsaw pact .	請注意 , 在一個由單一世界主導的時代 , 你有固定的聯盟nato , 華薩維特 。
a fixed polarity of power means fixed alliances .	固定的兩極性意味著聯盟 。
but a multiple polarity of power means shifting and changing alliances .	但 , 權力的兩極性意味著改變和改變盟友 。
and that's the world we're coming into , in which we will increasingly see that our alliances are not fixed .	我們即將進入這個世界 , 我們將漸漸看到我們的聯盟並沒有固定 。
canning , the great british foreign secretary once said , " britain has a common interest , but no common allies . "	坎寧 , 英國外國秘書長曾說: 「 英國有一個共同的利益 , 但沒有共通盟友 。 」
and we will see increasingly that even we in the west will reach out , have to reach out , beyond the cozy circle of the atlantic powers to make alliances with others if we want to get things done in the world .	我們會越來越明顯地看到 , 即使我們在西方也會伸出援手 , 必須伸出援手 , 超越大西洋力量範圍 , 來和他人聯盟 , 如果我們想要在世界上做些事情 。
note , that when we went into libya , it was not good enough for the west to do it alone ; we had to bring others in .	注意 , 當我們進入利比亞時 , 西方人不夠好 , 我們必須把其他人帶進去 。
we had to bring , in this case , the arab league in .	我們必須把阿拉伯聯盟帶進來 。
my guess is iraq and afghanistan are the last times when the west has tried to do it themselves , and we haven't succeeded .	我的猜測是伊拉克和阿富汗是西方試圖自己做這件事的最後一次 , 我們沒有成功 。
my guess is that we're reaching the beginning of the end of 400 years i say 400 years because it's the end of the ottoman empire of the hegemony of western power , western institutions and western values .	我的猜測是 , 我們已經達到了400年的開始 , 我說400年了 , 因為這是西方權力的統治中心的終點 , 西方制度和西方價值觀 。
you know , up until now , if the west got its act together , it could propose and dispose in every corner of the world .	你知道 , 一直到現在 , 如果西方一起行動 , 它可以在世界各個角落提出和分散 。
but that's no longer true .	但這不再是事實了 。
take the last financial crisis after the second world war .	以第二次世界大戰後的最後一次金融危機為例 。
the west got together the bretton woods institution , world bank , international monetary fund the problem solved .	西方集合了布雷頓森林機構 , 世界銀行 , 國際貨幣基金會解決了問題 。
now we have to call in others .	現在我們必須打電話給其他人 。
now we have to create the g20 .	現在我們要創造g20 。
now we have to reach beyond the cozy circle of our western friends .	現在 , 我們必須超越西方朋友的昏迷圈 。
let me make a prediction for you , which is probably even more startling .	讓我為你們做個預測 , 這可能更令人驚訝 。
i suspect we are now reaching the end of 400 years when western power was enough .	我猜我們現在已經達到400年了 , 當時西方的權力已經夠了 。
people say to me , " the chinese , of course , they'll never get themselves involved in peacemaking , multilateral peacemaking around the world . "	人們對我說: 「 中國 , 當然 , 他們永遠不會參與世界上的和平 , 多邊的和平 。 」
oh yes ? why not ?	噢 ? 為什麼不 ?
how many chinese troops are serving under the blue beret , serving under the blue flag , serving under the u . n . command in the world today ?	有多少中國軍隊在藍色的貝雷特下服務 , 在藍旗下服務 , 在聯合國的指令下服務 ?
how many americans ? 11 .	有多少美國人 ? 十一歲 。
what is the largest naval contingent tackling the issue of somali pirates ?	什麼是索馬利海盜最大的海軍呢 ?
the chinese naval contingent .	中國的海軍同意 。
of course they are , they are a mercantilist nation .	當然他們是商業主義的國家 。
they want to keep the sea lanes open .	他們想要讓海平線開放 。
increasingly , we are going to have to do business with people with whom we do not share values , but with whom , for the moment , we share common interests .	漸漸地 , 我們得要和那些我們不分享價值的人做生意 , 同時 , 我們共享共同利益 。
it's a whole new different way of looking at the world that is now emerging .	這是一種全新的角度來看世界 , 現在正在興起 。
and here's the third factor , which is totally different .	第三個因素完全不同 。
today in our modern world , because of the internet , because of the kinds of things people have been talking about here , everything is connected to everything .	現今 , 在我們的現代世界 , 因為網路 , 人們一直在談論的事物 , 一切都與所有事物連結在一起 。
we are now interdependent .	我們現在是互相依賴的 。
we are now interlocked , as nations , as individuals , in a way which has never been the case before , never been the case before .	身為一個個體 , 我們現在是互相連結的 , 從來沒有發生過這種情況 , 從來沒有發生過 。
the interrelationship of nations , well it's always existed .	國際間的關係 , 總是存在著 。
diplomacy is about managing the interrelationship of nations .	外交是要管理國家之間的關係 。
but now we are intimately locked together .	但現在我們被關起來了 。
you get swine flu in mexico , it's a problem for charles de gaulle airport 24 hours later .	在墨西哥 , 查爾斯德高爾機場24小時後你會得到流感 。
lehman brothers goes down , the whole lot collapses .	雷曼兄弟下降了 , 全部都倒了 。
there are fires in the steppes of russia , food riots in africa .	俄羅斯有火災 , 非洲的糧食暴動 。
we are all now deeply , deeply , deeply interconnected .	我們現在都非常、非常、非常緊密 。
and what that means is the idea of a nation state acting alone , not connected with others , not working with others , is no longer a viable proposition .	這意味著 , 一個國家單獨行動的概念 , 而不是與他人連結 , 不是與他人合作 , 不再是可行的提案 。
because the actions of a nation state are neither confined to itself , nor is it sufficient for the nation state itself to control its own territory , because the effects outside the nation state are now beginning to affect what happens inside them .	因為一個國家的行動 , 不論是自身的 , 也不足以控制自己的國家 , 因為外國國家的影響已經開始影響他們內在的狀況 。
i was a young soldier in the last of the small empire wars of britain .	我是英國最後一個小帝國戰爭的年輕士兵 。
at that time , the defense of my country was about one thing and one thing only: how strong was our army , how strong was our air force , how strong was our navy and how strong were our allies .	那時 , 我國家的防禦是一回事 , 只有一件事:我們的軍隊有多強壯 , 我們的空軍有多強 , 我們的海軍有多強壯 , 以及我們的盟友有多強 。
that was when the enemy was outside the walls .	那時候敵人就在牆外 。
now the enemy is inside the walls .	敵人就在牆上 。
now if i want to talk about the defense of my country , i have to speak to the minister of health because pandemic disease is a threat to my security , i have to speak to the minister of agriculture because food security is a threat to my security , i have to speak to the minister of industry because the fragility of our hitech infrastructure is now a point of attack for our enemies as we see from cyber warfare i have to speak to the minister of home affairs because who has entered my country , who lives in that terraced house in that inner city has a direct effect on what happens in my country as we in london saw in the 7/7 bombings .	如果我想要談我的國家國防部 , 我得要和健康部長談 , 因為流行病對我的安全有威脅 , 我得要和農業部長談談 , 因為食物安全對我的國家是威脅 , 我得要和工業部談談 , 因為我們希臘基礎設施的脆弱 , 是我們的敵人 , 是我們從網路戰爭看到的攻擊 , 我得要和國內部談 , 因為在國內的國內的國會受到威脅 。
it's no longer the case that the security of a country is simply a matter for its soldiers and its ministry of defense .	不再是國家的安全對軍人和國防的重要性 。
it's its capacity to lock together its institutions .	它的能力是將它的機構鎖在一起 。
and this tells you something very important .	這告訴我們一件非常重要的事 。
it tells you that , in fact , our governments , vertically constructed , constructed on the economic model of the industrial revolution vertical hierarchy , specialization of tasks , command structures have got the wrong structures completely .	它告訴你 , 事實上 , 我們的政府 , 垂直建構 , 建立在工業革命的經濟模式上 , 包括垂直層級、專業任務、指令結構 , 完全有錯誤的結構 。
you in business know that the paradigm structure of our time , ladies and gentlemen , is the network .	各位在商業界知道我們這個時代的典範結構 , 各位先生女士 , 就是網路 。
it's your capacity to network that matters , both within your governments and externally .	這是你對網路很重要的能力 , 無論是在你的政府或外部 。
so here is ashdown's third law .	這裡是shown的第三法律 。
by the way , don't ask me about ashdown's first law and second law because i haven't invented those yet ; it always sounds better if there's a third law , doesn't it ?	順道一提 , 不要問我關於阿什沃恩的第一法律和第二定律 , 因為我還沒發明這些法律 ; 如果有第三條定律的話 , 聽起來比較好 , 對吧 ?
ashdown's third law is that in the modern age , where everything is connected to everything , the most important thing about what you can do is what you can do with others .	shown的第三定律是 , 在現代 , 每件事都和每件事有關 , 最重要的是你能做的 , 就是你能對別人做些什麼 。
the most important bit about your structure whether you're a government , whether you're an army regiment , whether you're a business is your docking points , your interconnectors , your capacity to network with others .	最重要的一點是 , 不論你是政府 , 不論你是軍隊註冊 , 不論你是企業 , 你的交叉點 , 你的交叉點 , 你和他人建立的能力 。
you understand that in industry ; governments don't .	在工業界 , 政府不了解 。
but now one final thing .	但 , 最後一件事 。
if it is the case , ladies and gentlemen and it is that we are now locked together in a way that has never been quite the same before , then it's also the case that we share a destiny with each other .	如果是這樣的情況 , 各位先生女士們 , 我們現在已經以以前從未相同的方式聯繫在一起 , 那也是我們彼此之間的命運 。
suddenly and for the very first time , collective defense , the thing that has dominated us as the concept of securing our nations , is no longer enough .	突然間 , 第一次 , 集體防禦 , 主宰我們國家的概念 , 不再是足夠的 。
it used to be the case that if my tribe was more powerful than their tribe , i was safe ; if my country was more powerful than their country , i was safe ; my alliance , like nato , was more powerful than their alliance , i was safe .	以前 , 如果我的部落比他們的部落更強大 , 我很安全 ; 如果我的國家比他們的強大 , 我更安全 ; 我的聯盟 , 像是納粹 , 比他們的盟友更強大 , 我就安全了 。
it is no longer the case .	它不再是案例 。
the advent of the interconnectedness and of the weapons of mass destruction means that , increasingly , i share a destiny with my enemy .	相互關聯性和大規模毀滅的武器意味著 , 越來越多 , 我和敵人有了命運 。
when i was a diplomat negotiating the disarmament treaties with the soviet union in geneva in the 1970s , we succeeded because we understood we shared a destiny with them .	當我還是外交官時 , 我和1970年代日內瓦的蘇聯和蘇聯的蘇聯談判 , 我們成功了 , 因為我們知道我們和他們共享一個命運 。
collective security is not enough .	集體安全還不夠 。
peace has come to northern ireland because both sides realized that the zerosum game couldn't work .	和平已經來到北愛爾蘭 , 因為兩者都意識到零和遊戲無法運作 。
they shared a destiny with their enemies .	他們和敵人共享命運 。
one of the great barriers to peace in the middle east is that both sides , both israel and , i think , the palestinians , do not understand that they share a collective destiny .	在中東和平的一個大障礙 , 就是雙方 , 以色列 , 我想 , 巴勒斯坦人 , 不明白他們有共同的命運 。
and so suddenly , ladies and gentlemen , what has been the proposition of visionaries and poets down the ages becomes something we have to take seriously as a matter of public policy .	所以 , 各位先生女士們 , 先生女士們 , 在這個時代 , 視力和詩人的提議變成了我們必須認真看待公共政策的問題 。
i started with a poem , i'll end with one .	我從一首詩開始 , 用一首詩結束 。
the great poem of john donne's .	約翰•唐納的偉大詩 。
" send not for whom the bell tolls . "	「 派別給誰鈴聲 。 」
the poem is called " no man is an island . "	這首詩叫做 「 沒有人是孤島 」 。
and it goes: " every man's death affected me , for i am involved in mankind , send not to ask for whom the bell tolls , it tolls for thee . "	上面寫著: 「 每個人的死亡都會影響我 , 為了我參與人類 , 不去問誰是貝殼 , 會幫我取帳 。 」
for john donne , a recommendation of morality .	對約翰•唐恩 , 道德建議 。
for us , i think , part of the equation for our survival .	對我們來說 , 我認為 , 是我們生存的公式之一 。
to find the path to long life and health , dan buettner and team study the world's " blue zones , " communities whose elders live with vim and vigor to recordsetting age . at tedxtc , he shares the 9 common diet and lifestyle habits that keep them spry past age 100 .	為了尋找長壽、健康、丹布特納和團隊的路徑 , 研究世界上的 「 藍色區域 」 , 他們的長者和維格爾一起生活在tedxc , 他分享了9種常見的飲食和生活習慣 , 這些習慣會讓他們過去一百歲 。
biology , culture , exploration , food , health , life , science	生物、文化、探索、食物、健康、生命、科學、科學、科學、科學、科學、知識 。
dan buettner: how to live to be 100+	danbuettner:如何活到100+100 。
something called the danish twin study established that only about 10 percent of how long the average person lives , within certain biological limits , is dictated by our genes .	丹麥雙胞胎研究發現 , 一般人的壽命只有百分之十 , 在某些生物限制中 , 只有我們的基因 。
the other 90 percent is dictated by our lifestyle .	另外九成是由我們的生活方式決定的 。
so the premise of blue zones: if we can find the optimal lifestyle of longevity we can come up with a de facto formula for longevity .	所以藍色區域的前提是:如果我們能找到長壽的最佳生活方式 , 我們就能提出一個事實的公式來長壽 。
but if you ask the average american what the optimal formula of longevity is , they probably couldn't tell you .	但如果你問一般美國人 , 長壽的最佳公式是什麼 , 他們可能無法告訴你 。
they've probably heard of the south beach diet , or the atkins diet .	他們可能聽過南海灘飲食 , 或皮膚飲食 。
you have the usda food pyramid .	你有美國食品金字塔 。
there is what oprah tells us .	歐普拉告訴我們 。
there is what doctor oz tells us .	奧茲博士告訴我們什麼 。
the fact of the matter is there is a lot of confusion around what really helps us live longer better .	事實是 , 對於真正幫助我們活得更好 , 有很多困惑 。
should you be running marathons or doing yoga ?	你是不是要跑馬拉松還是瑜伽 ?
should you eat organic meats or should you be eating tofu ?	你該吃有機肉還是吃豆腐 ?
when it comes to supplements , should you be taking them ?	談到補充品 , 你該把它們帶走嗎 ?
how about these hormones or resveratrol ?	那麼這些荷爾蒙還是反轉劇情呢 ?
and does purpose play into it ?	是否有目的呢 ?
spirituality ? and how about how we socialize ?	靈性 ? 我們要如何社交呢 ?
well , our approach to finding longevity was to team up with national geographic , and the national institute on aging , to find the four demographically confirmed areas that are geographically defined .	我們找到長壽的方法是和國家地理學院合作 , 國家老化研究所合作 , 找出四個人口確認地理位置 。
and then bring a team of experts in there to methodically go through exactly what these people do , to distill down the crosscultural distillation .	接著 , 帶一組專家來到那裡 , 以合法的方式穿透這些人的做法 , 來移除跨文化的分裂 。
and at the end of this i'm going to tell you what that distillation is .	最後我要告訴各位 , 那個區分是什麼 。
but first i'd like to debunk some common myths when it comes to longevity .	但首先 , 我想破壞一些常見的迷思 , 談到長壽時 。
and the first myth is if you try really hard you can live to be 100 .	第一個迷思是 , 如果你真的很努力 , 你可以活到100歲 。
the problem is , only about one out of 5 , 000 people in america live to be 100 .	問題是 , 美國5 , 000人當中只有1人活到100歲 。
your chances are very low .	你的機會非常低 。
even though it's the fastest growing demographic in america , it's hard to reach 100 .	即使它是美國成長最快的人口 , 很難達到100歲 。
the problem is that we're not programmed for longevity .	問題是 , 我們沒有長壽計畫 。
we are programmed for something called procreative success .	我們被編寫為 「 促進成功 」 。
i love that word .	我喜歡這個詞 。
it reminds me of my college days .	它提醒了我大學的日子 。
biologists term procreative success to mean the age where you have children and then another generation , the age when your children have children .	生物學家稱它為 「 優秀的成功 」 , 代表你有孩子的年齡 , 接著是另一個世代 , 當你的孩子有孩子時的年齡 。
after that the effect of evolution completely dissipates .	在演化的效果完全消失了 。
if you're a mammal , if you're a rat or an elephant , or a human , in between , it's the same story .	如果你是哺乳類動物 , 如果你是老鼠或大象 , 或人類 , 在兩者之間 , 則是同一個故事 。
so to make it to age 100 , you not only have to have had a very good lifestyle , you also have to have won the genetic lottery .	所以 , 要讓它變老100歲 , 你不只需要有好的生活方式 , 你還得贏得基因彩票 。
the second myth is , there are treatments that can help slow , reverse , or even stop aging .	第二個迷思是 , 有治療可以幫助緩慢、逆轉 , 甚至阻止老化 。
when you think of it , there is 99 things that can age us .	想想看 , 有99件事能讓我們變老 。
deprive your brain of oxygen for just a few minutes , those brain cells die , they never come back .	只要幾分鐘 , 那些腦細胞就會死亡 , 它們永遠不會回來 。
play tennis too hard , on your knees , ruin your cartilage , the cartilage never comes back .	彈網球太硬 , 在你的膝蓋上 , 毀了你的軟骨 , 軟骨永遠不會回來 。
our arteries can clog . our brains can gunk up with plaque , and we can get alzheimer's .	我們的動脈可以堵塞 。 我們的大腦可以用普拉克來推動 , 我們可以得到阿茲海默症 。
there is just too many things to go wrong .	有太多事情要出錯 。
our bodies have 35 trillion cells , trillion with a " t . " we're talking national debt numbers here .	我們的身體有35兆個細胞 , 上面有t 。 我們正在說國家債務的數字 。
those cells turn themselves over once every eight years .	這些細胞每八年就會自轉一次 。
and every time they turn themselves over there is some damage . and that damage builds up .	每當他們把自己轉到那裡時 , 就會造成傷害 , 那會造成損害 。
and it builds up exponentially .	它是指數型的 。
it's a little bit like the days when we all had beatles albums or eagles albums and we'd make a copy of that on a cassette tape , and let our friends copy that cassette tape , and pretty soon , with successive generations that tape sounds like garbage .	有點像當我們有披頭四或老鷹專輯時 , 我們會在錄音帶上做複製 , 讓朋友複製錄音帶 , 很快地 , 帶有成功的世代 , 錄音帶聽起來像是垃圾 。
well , the same things happen to our cells .	同樣的事也發生在我們的細胞身上 。
that's why a 65yearold person is aging at a rate of about 125 times faster than a 12yearold person .	這就是為什麼一個65歲的人老化速度比12歲的人快125倍 。
so , if there is nothing you can do to slow your aging or stop your aging , what am i doing here ?	所以 , 如果沒有任何事可以減緩老化或阻止老化 , 我在這裡做什麼 ?
well , the fact of the matter is the best science tells us that the capacity of the human body , my body , your body , is about 90 years , a little bit more for women .	事實上 , 最棒的科學告訴我們人類身體的能力 , 我的身體 , 你的身體大約是90年 , 對於女性來說 , 多一點點 。
but life expectancy in this country is only 78 .	但這個國家的平均壽命只有78 。
so somewhere along the line , we're leaving about 12 good years on the table .	在這條線的某處 , 我們在桌子上留下了12年的美好處 。
these are years that we could get .	我們能做到這些年 。
and research shows that they would be years largely free of chronic disease , heart disease , cancer and diabetes .	研究顯示 , 牠們會多年免於慢性疾病、心臟疾病、癌症和糖尿病 。
we think the best way to get these missing years is to look at the cultures around the world that are actually experiencing them , areas where people are living to age 100 at rates up to 10 times greater than we are , areas where the life expectancy is an extra dozen years , the rate of middle age mortality is a fraction of what it is in this country .	我們認為 , 最好的方法就是去看世界上的文化 , 那些實際上正在經歷的文化 , 人們活到一百歲的地區 , 比我們多十倍 , 平均壽命是十多年 , 中年死亡率是少數的一部分 。
we found our first blue zone about 125 miles off the coast of italy , on the island of sardinia .	我們在義大利海岸發現我們的第一個藍色區域 , 距離義大利海岸大約125英里 。
and not the entire island , the island is about 1 . 4 million people , but only up in the highlands , an area called the nuoro province .	不是整個島嶼 , 島嶼大約有140萬人 , 但只有在高地 , 一個叫做努羅省的區域 。
and here we have this area where men live the longest , about 10 times more centenarians than we have here in america .	在這裡 , 我們有這個區域 , 男人壽命最長 , 比美國多出十倍 。
and this is a place where people not only reach age 100 , they do so with extraordinary vigor .	這個地方 , 人們不僅達到一百歲 , 還帶著非凡的惡魔 。
places where 102 year olds still ride their bike to work , chop wood , and can beat a guy 60 years younger than them .	那裡有102歲的老人仍然騎腳踏車去上班 , 可比他們年輕60歲 。
their history actually goes back to about the time of christ .	他們的歷史回溯到基督的時代 。
it's actually a bronze age culture that's been isolated .	它其實是一個被孤立的青銅文化 。
because the land is so infertile , they largely are shepherds , which occasions regular , lowintensity physical activity .	因為土地是如此的不穩定 , 大多是牧羊人 , 偶爾會規律、低密度的身體活動 。
their diet is mostly plantbased , accentuated with foods that they can carry into the fields .	他們的飲食大部分是以植物為基礎 , 以食物為主 , 以它們能帶入田野 。
they came up with an unleavened whole wheat bread called carta musica made out of durum wheat , a type of cheese made from grassfed animals so the cheese is high in omega3 fatty acids instead of omega6 fatty acids from cornfed animals , and a type of wine that has three times the level of polyphenols than any known wine in the world .	他們想出了一道無盡的麥麵包 , 叫做卡塔音樂 , 由杜魯米麥製成 , 一種乳酪是由草餵養的動物所製成 , 所以乳酪在omega-3脂肪酸中 , 而不是omega-6脂肪酸 , 而是來自玉米的動物 , 一種葡萄酒的類型 , 比世界上任何已知的葡萄酒含量高三倍 。
but the real secret i think lies more in the way that they organize their society .	但我認為真正的秘密是他們組織社會的方式 。
and one of the most salient elements of the sardinian society is how they treat older people .	薩丁尼亞社會中最重要的元素之一就是他們如何治療老年人 。
you ever notice here in america , social equity seems to peak at about age 24 ?	你有沒有注意到在美國 , 社會平等似乎在24歲時達到高峰 ?
just look at the advertisements .	看看廣告 。
here in sardinia , the older you get the more equity you have , the more wisdom you're celebrated for .	在斯丁尼亞 , 你得到越多平等 , 你所慶祝的智慧越多 。
you go into the bars in sardinia , instead of seeing the sports illustrated swimsuit calendar , you see the centenarian of the month calendar .	你走進薩丁尼亞州的酒吧 , 而不是看到運動畫出游泳日曆 , 你會看到一個月曆的中年人 。
this , as it turns out , is not only good for your aging parents to keep them close to the family it imparts about four to six years of extra life expectancy research shows it's also good for the children of those families , who have lower rates of mortality and lower rates of disease .	事實證明 , 這不只對老年的父母保持親近家庭的好處 , 預期壽命短短短四至六年的研究顯示 , 對那些家庭的孩子來說 , 死亡率和疾病的比率較低 。
that's called the grandmother effect .	這叫做祖母效應 。
we found our second blue zone on the other side of the planet , about 800 miles south of tokyo , on the archipelago of okinawa .	我們在地球的另一邊找到了第二塊藍色區域 , 大約是東京的800英里南部 , 俄亥俄州的阿基比拉哥 。
okinawa is actually 161 small islands .	okinawa其實是161個小島 。
and in the northern part of the main island , this is ground zero for world longevity .	在主要島的北部 , 這是世界永續發展的地點 。
this is a place where the oldest living female population is found .	這個地方是最古老的女性族群 。
it's a place where people have the longest disabilityfree life expectancy in the world .	在這個地方 , 人們有世界上最長的殘疾壽命 。
they have what we want .	他們有我們想要的 。
they live a long time , and tend to die in their sleep , very quickly , and often , i can tell you , after sex .	牠們活得很久 , 通常在牠們的睡眠中很快 , 通常 , 我可以告訴你 , 在性交之後 , 我會告訴你 。
they live about seven good years longer than the average american .	他們比一般美國人活得更久七年 。
five times as many centenarians as we have in america .	美國有五倍以上的百歲人 。
one fifth the rate of colon and breast cancer , big killers here in america .	五分之一的殖民地癌症和乳癌 , 在美國 , 大型殺手 。
and one sixth the rate of cardiovascular disease .	第六種心血管疾病的速率 。
and the fact that this culture has yielded these numbers suggests strongly they have something to teach us .	而這個文化已經產生了這些數字 , 顯然他們有可以教導我們的東西 。
what do they do ?	他們會怎麼做 ?
once again , a plantbased diet , full of vegetables with lots of color in them .	再一次 , 以植物為基礎的飲食 , 裡面有許多顏色的蔬菜 。
and they eat about eight times as much tofu as americans do .	他們吃的食物 , 比美國人多8倍 。
more significant than what they eat is how they eat it .	比牠們吃的更重要 , 就是牠們如何吃它 。
they have all kinds of little strategies to keep from overeating , which , as you know , is a big problem here in america .	他們有各式各樣的小策略 , 來避免過度濫用 , 如你所知 , 在美國這裡是個大問題 。
a few of the strategies we observed: they eat off of smaller plates , so they tend to eat fewer calories at every sitting .	我們觀察到的一些策略是:它們從小盤子中吃掉 , 所以它們通常會在每個坐下比較少吃卡路里 。
instead of serving family style , where you can sort of mindlessly eat as you're talking , they serve at the counter , put the food away , and then bring it to the table .	與其提供家庭風格 , 不如你在說話時 , 可以無心地吃飯 , 他們在櫃台上服務 , 把食物送出去 , 然後把它帶到桌子上 。
they also have a 3 , 000yearold adage , which i think is the greatest sort of diet suggestion ever invented .	他們還有3000歲的廣告 , 我認為這是史上最偉大的飲食建議 。
it was invented by confucius .	它是由混淆所發明的 。
and that diet is known as the hara , hatchi , bu diet .	這種飲食被稱為 「 哈拉 」 、 「 哈拉契 」 。
it's simply a little saying these people say before their meal to remind them to stop eating when their stomach is [80] percent full .	簡單來說 , 這些人在吃飯之前就說過要提醒他們 , 不要再吃八成 。
it takes about a half hour for that full feeling to travel from your belly to your brain .	整個感覺需要半小時 , 才能從你的肚子傳到你的大腦 。
and by remembering to stop at 80 percent it helps keep you from doing that very thing .	記得80%的時間 , 它能幫助你阻止你去做這件事 。
but , like sardinia , okinawa has a few social constructs that we can associate with longevity .	但 , 像sardinia , okinawa有幾個社交建設 , 我們可以和長壽相關 。
we know that isolation kills .	我們知道孤立殺戮 。
fifteen years ago , the average american had three good friends .	15年前 , 美國人平均有三個好朋友 。
we're down to one and half right now .	我們現在已經降到一半了 。
if you were lucky enough to be born in okinawa , you were born into a system where you automatically have a half a dozen friends with whom you travel through life .	如果你夠幸運 , 出生在okinawa , 你就出生在一個系統中 , 你自動擁有半十個朋友 , 和你經歷過生命的旅行 。
they call it a moai . and if you're in a moai you're expected to share the bounty if you encounter luck , and if things go bad , child gets sick , parent dies , you always have somebody who has your back .	他們稱之為 「 摩艾 」 。 如果你在摩艾 」 裡 , 你預期會分享你的責任 , 如果你幸運的話 , 如果事情不好 , 孩子生病了 , 父母死了 , 你總是有你的背心 。
this particular moai , these five ladies have been together for 97 years .	這個獨特的摩艾 , 這五位女士已經九十七年了 。
their average age is 102 .	平均年齡是102歲 。
typically in america we've divided our adult life up into two sections .	通常在美國 , 我們把成人的生活分成兩區 。
there is our work life , where we're productive .	我們的工作是有生產力的 。
and then one day , boom , we retire .	有一天 , 我們退休了 。
and typically that has meant retiring to the easy chair , or going down to arizona to play golf .	一般來說 , 這意味著退休到簡單的椅子上 , 或是去亞利桑那州玩高爾夫 。
in the okinawan language there is not even a word for retirement .	在okinawan的語言中 , 甚至沒有退休的詞語 。
instead there is one word that imbues your entire life , and that word is " ikigai . "	取而代之的是 , 一生中有一種詞 , 那就是 「 ikigai 」 。
and , roughly translated , it means " the reason for which you wake up in the morning . "	差不多翻譯了 , 意思是 「 早上醒來的原因 。 」
for this 102yearold karate master , his ikigai was carrying forth this martial art .	至於這個102歲的karate大師 , 他的伊基加伊基加尼帶著這場戰術 。
for this hundredyearold fisherman it was continuing to catch fish for his family three times a week .	對這百歲的漁夫而言 , 每週捕魚三次 。
and this is a question . the national institute on aging actually gave us a questionnaire to give these centenarians .	這是個問題 。 國家老化研究所給了我們一個問卷 , 來給予這些百歲人 。
and one of the questions , they were very culturally astute , the people who put the questionnaire .	其中一個問題是 , 他們是非常文化化的研究者 , 那些把問卷放在一起的人 。
one of the questions was , " what is your ikigai ? "	其中一個問題是: 「 你的ikigai是什麼 ? 」
they instantly knew why they woke up in the morning .	他們馬上就知道為什麼早上起床 。
for this 102 year old woman , her ikigai was simply her greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	對於這位102歲的女子來說 , 她的伊基加伊只是她的曾曾曾孫女 。
two girls separated in age by 101 and a half years .	兩個女孩在101年分離 。
and i asked her what it felt like to hold a greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	我問她 , 拿著一位曾曾曾祖父的感覺是什麼樣的感覺 。
and she put her head back and she said , " it feels like leaping into heaven . "	她回頭說: 「 感覺就像跳進天堂 。 」
i thought that was a wonderful thought .	我覺得那是個很棒的想法 。
my editor at geographic wanted me to find america's blue zone .	我在地理學的編輯希望我能找到美國的藍色區域 。
and for a while we looked on the prairies of minnesota , where actually there is a very high proportion of centenarians .	一陣子我們看了明尼蘇達的草原 , 實際上 , 百歲人的比例非常高 。
but that's because all the young people left .	但那是因為所有的年輕人都離開了 。
so , we turned to the data again .	所以 , 我們又轉向資料 。
and we found america's longestlived population among the seventhday adventists concentrated in and around loma linda , california .	我們發現美國在加州洛馬林達州的第七天冒險人數最長的族群 。
adventists are conservative methodists .	激進分子是保守的方法主義者 。
they celebrate their sabbath from sunset on friday till sunset on saturday .	他們在星期五日的日落慶祝他們的安息日 , 直到星期六 。
a " 24hour sanctuary in time , " they call it .	他們稱之為 「 24小時的庇護所 」 。
and they follow five little habits that conveys to them extraordinary longevity , comparatively speaking .	他們遵循五個小習慣 , 傳達給他們非凡的長壽 。
in america here , life expectancy for the average woman is 80 .	在美國 , 平均女性的平均壽命是80歲 。
but for an adventist woman , their life expectancy is 89 .	但對於一個先進的女人而言 , 他們的壽命是89歲 。
and the difference is even more pronounced among men , who are expected to live about 11 years longer than their american counterparts .	差別在於男性中更有發音 , 他們預期能活到比美國人多11年 。
now , this is a study that followed about 70 , 000 people for 30 years .	這個研究追蹤了大約七萬人三十年 。
sterling study . and i think it supremely illustrates the premise of this blue zone project .	史特林研究 。 我認為它總說明了這個藍色區域計畫的前提 。
this is a heterogeneous community .	這是個異型的社區 。
it's white , black , hispanic , asian .	是白人、黑人、西班牙人、亞洲人 。
the only thing that they have in common are a set of very small lifestyle habits that they follow ritualistically for most of their lives .	他們唯一共通之處是一組非常小型的生活習慣 , 他們大部分的時間都遵循著儀式 。
they take their diet directly from the bible .	他們直接從聖經中獲得飲食 。
genesis: chapter one , verse [29] , where god talks about legumes and seeds , and on one more stanza about green plants , ostensibly missing is meat .	辛蒂斯:第一章 , 詩句 , 上帝談到法律和種子 , 在另一個斯坦扎亞 , 關於綠色植物 , 很明顯地缺少肉類 。
they take this sanctuary in time very serious .	他們認真看待這個庇護所 。
for 24 hours every week , no matter how busy they are , how stressed out they are at work , where the kids need to be driven , they stop everything and they focus on their god , their social network , and then , hardwired right in the religion , are nature walks .	每週24小時 , 不論他們多忙、工作有多緊張 , 孩子需要被開車 , 停下一切 , 把焦點放在上帝、社交網路 , 接著 , 在宗教中 , 天性會走路 。
and the power of this is not that it's done occasionally , the power is it's done every week for a lifetime .	這種力量並不是偶爾會完成 , 它的力量是每週完成的 , 一生都在做 。
none of it's hard . none of it costs money .	沒有一個是困難的 。 沒有一個花錢 。
adventists also tend to hang out with other adventists .	激進份子也傾向於與其他先進份子混在一起 。
so , if you go to an adventist's party you don't see people swilling jim beam or rolling a joint .	所以 , 如果你去參加一個冒險家的派對 , 你看不到人們在揮舞吉姆貝姆或轉動關節 。
instead they're talking about their next nature walk , exchanging recipes , and yes , they pray .	相反地 , 他們在談論他們的下一天行走 , 交換食譜 , 是的 , 他們祈禱 。
but they influence each other in profound and measurable ways .	但它們會以深刻且可測量的方式影響彼此 。
this is a culture that has yielded ellsworth whareham .	這是一種文化 , 產生了 「 埃爾斯威爾斯 」 的文化 。
ellsworth whareham is 97 years old .	埃爾斯威爾斯•沃雷罕是97歲 。
he's a multimillionaire , yet when a contractor wanted 6 , 000 dollars to build a privacy fence , he said , " for that kind of money i'll do it myself . "	他是百萬富翁 , 但當一個承包商想要六千美金來建造一個隱私的柵欄時 , 他說: 「 為了那類的錢 , 我會自己做 。 」
so for the next three days he was out shoveling cement , and hauling poles around .	接下來的三天 , 他出去吃水泥 , 四處游泳 。
and predictably , perhaps , on the fourth day he ended up in the operating room .	或許 , 在第四天 , 他最後進了手術室 。
but not as the guy on the table ; the guy doing openheart surgery .	但不是坐在桌上的人 ; 那個做開心手術的人 。
at 97 he still does 20 openheart surgeries every month .	九十七歲時 , 他仍然每個月進行二十次開心手術 。
ed rawlings , 103 years old now , an active cowboy , starts his morning with a swim .	艾德•萊恩斯 , 103歲 , 一位活躍的牛仔 , 早上開始游泳 。
and on weekends he likes to put on the boards , throw up rooster tails .	在週末 , 他喜歡把板子放在板子上 , 丟出rooster尾巴 。
her grandson actually lives in the twin cities here .	她的孫子其實住在雙胞胎城市 。
she starts her day with lifting weights .	她每天從舉重開始 。
she rides her bicycle .	她騎腳踏車 。
and then she gets in her rootbeer colored 1994 cadillac seville , and tears down the san bernardino freeway , where she still volunteers for seven different organizations .	然後她在她的根部裡彩色了1994年的卡迪拉克•塞維爾 , 在聖貝納迪諾的高速公路上流淚 , 她仍然為七個不同的組織志工 。
i've been on 19 hardcore expeditions .	我已經在十九次探險 。
i'm probably the only person you'll ever meet who rode his bicycle across the sahara desert without sunscreen .	我可能是唯一一個穿越撒哈拉沙漠的自行車的人 , 卻沒有陽光 。
but i'll tell you , there is no adventure more harrowing than riding shotgun with marge deton .	但我要告訴各位 , 沒有冒險比發生馬奇德頓騎士更嚴厲的冒險 。
" a stranger is a friend i haven't met yet ! " she'd say to me .	「 陌生人是我還沒見過的朋友 ! 」 她對我說 。
so , what are the common denominators in these three cultures ?	所以 , 這三種文化中有什麼共同點 ?
what are the things that they all do ?	他們會怎麼做 ?
and we managed to boil it down to nine .	我們成功把它歸結為九個 。
in fact we've done two more blue zone expeditions since this and these common denominators hold true .	事實上 , 自此之後 , 我們再做了兩次藍色區域探險 , 和這些共同的決策者持有真相 。
and the first one , and i'm about to utter a heresy here , none of them exercise , at least the way we think of exercise .	首先 , 我將要說一個在這裡 , 沒有一個運動 , 至少我們對運動的看法 。
instead , they set up their lives so that they are constantly nudged into physical activity .	相反的 , 他們設立了自己的人生 , 以便他們不斷地被導入實體活動 。
these 100yearold okinawan women are getting up and down off the ground , they sit on the floor , 30 or 40 times a day .	這些百歲的okinawan女性在地面上上上下 , 她們每天坐著30到40次 。
sardinians live in vertical houses , up and down the stairs .	薩丁尼亞人住在垂直的房子裡 , 上下樓 。
every trip to the store , or to church or to a friend's house occasions a walk .	每趟到商店 , 或教堂 , 或朋友的家裡偶爾會走路 。
they don't have any conveniences .	他們沒有任何方便 。
there is not a button to push to do yard work or house work .	不需要按下按鈕去做院子或房子工作 。
if they want to mix up a cake , they're doing it by hand .	如果他們想混合蛋糕 , 他們會用手做 。
that burns calories just as much as going on the treadmill does .	那種燃燒卡路里和跑步機一樣 。
when they do do intentional physical activity , it's the things they enjoy . they tend to walk , the only proven way to stave off cognitive decline , and they all tend to have a garden .	當他們做實體活動時 , 他們很享受 。 他們傾向於走路 , 唯一能證明認知衰退的方法 , 且他們都傾向有花園 。
they know how to set up their life in the right way so they have the right outlook .	他們知道如何以正確的方式建立自己的人生 , 讓他們有正確的外觀 。
each of these cultures take time to downshift .	每一種文化都需要時間降低轉變 。
the sardinians pray . the seventhday adventists pray .	沙丁尼亞人祈禱 , 第七天的冒險家祈禱 。
the okinawans have this ancestor veneration .	okinawans有這種祖先的陰謀 。
but when you're in a hurry or stressed out , that triggers something called the inflammatory response , which is associated with everything from alzheimer's disease to cardiovascular disease .	但當你急著或緊張時 , 會觸發一種叫做發炎反應的東西 , 它會和阿茲海默症及心血管疾病有關 。
when you slow down for 15 minutes a day you turn that inflammatory state into a more antiinflammatory state .	當你一天放慢15分鐘 , 你會把這種發炎狀態轉變成更加抗炎的狀態 。
they have vocabulary for sense of purpose , ikigai , like the okinawans .	他們有詞彙的意義 , 伊基加 , 就像okinawans一樣 。
you know the two most dangerous years in your life are the year you're born , because of infant mortality , and the year you retire .	你知道你生命中最危險的兩年是你出生的那一年 , 因為嬰兒死亡率 , 而你退休的那一年 。
these people know their sense of purpose , and they activate in their life , that's worth about seven years of extra life expectancy .	這些人知道自己的目的 , 他們在生命中活化 , 價值約七年的預期壽命 。
there's no longevity diet .	沒有長壽的飲食 。
instead , these people drink a little bit every day , not a hard sell to the american population .	相反地 , 這些人每天都喝一點飲料 , 而不是賣給美國人口 。
they tend to eat a plantbased diet .	他們傾向會吃植物的飲食 。
doesn't mean they don't eat meat , but lots of beans and nuts .	不代表他們不吃肉 , 而是很多豆子和堅果 。
and they have strategies to keep from overeating , little things that nudge them away from the table at the right time .	他們有策略 , 避免過度侵蝕 , 一些小東西 , 讓它們在適當的時間離開桌子 。
and then the foundation of all this is how they connect .	所有這些都是他們如何連結的基礎 。
they put their families first , take care of their children and their aging parents .	他們先照顧他們的家人 , 照顧他們的孩子和老年父母 。
they all tend to belong to a faithbased community , which is worth between four and 14 extra years of life expectancy if you do it four times a month .	他們都歸屬於信仰型社區 , 每月四到十四年的預期壽命是值得的 。
and the biggest thing here is they also belong to the right tribe .	最重要的是 , 它們也屬於正確的部落 。
