in fact , who would like to drive a robot ?	事實上 , 誰想開機器人 ?
thank you , scott .	謝謝 , 史考特 。
and even cooler , you actually don't have to be in the same geographic location as the robot to control him .	甚至更酷的是 , 你不需要在同一個地理位置來控制他 。
so he actually streams twoway audio and video between any two smart devices .	所以他實際上在任何兩個智慧型裝置之間雙向雙向音頻和視頻之間 。
so you can log in through the browser , and it's kind of like skype on wheels .	你可以透過瀏覽器登入 , 有點像輪子上的skype 。
so we were talking before about telepresence , and this is a really cool example .	我們之前談到遠端 , 這是個很酷的例子 。
you can imagine an eightyearold girl , for example , who has an iphone , and her mom buys her a robot .	舉例來說 , 你可以想像一個八歲的女孩 , 她有iphone , 她媽媽會買一個機器人 。
that girl can take her iphone , put it on the robot , send an email to grandma , who lives on the other side of the country .	那個女孩可以拿她的iphone , 把它放在機器人上 , 寄一封電子郵件給那個國家的另一端的祖母 。
grandma can log into that robot and play hideandgoseek with her granddaughter for fifteen minutes every single night , when otherwise she might only be able to get to see her granddaughter once or twice a year .	祖母可以登入那個機器人 , 和她孫女一起玩躲藏藏藏品 , 每晚十五分鐘 , 否則她可能只能一年一次或兩次看到她的孫女 。
so those are a couple of the really cool things that romo can do today .	這就是romo今天能做的一些很酷的事 。
but i just want to finish by talking about something that we're working on in the future .	但我只想談談未來我們正在努力的事物 。
this is actually something that one of our engineers , dom , built in a weekend .	這是我們其中一個工程師 , 多姆 , 在週末建造的 。
it's built on top of a google open framework called blockly .	它是建立在google開放架構上 , 叫做 「 街區 」 。
this allows you to drag and drop these blocks of semantic code and create any behavior for this robot you want .	這樣你就可以拖下這些字體 , 把這些字體放下來 , 為這個你想要的機器人創造任何行為 。
you do not have to know how to code to create a behavior for romo .	你不需要知道編碼如何為romo創造一個行為 。
and you can actually simulate that behavior in the browser , which is what you see romo doing on the left .	你可以在瀏覽器中模擬這個行為 , 這就是你在左邊看到romo在做的事 。
and then if you have something you like , you can download it onto your robot and execute it in real life , run the program in real life .	如果你有你喜歡的東西 , 你可以把它下載到你的機器人上 , 並在現實生活中執行這個計畫 。
and then if you have something you're proud of , you can share it with every other person who owns a robot in the world .	如果你有一些你很驕傲的東西 , 你可以和世界上任何一個擁有機器人的人分享 。
so all of these wifi–enabled robots actually learn from each other .	所以這些wi-fi可以互相學習的機器人 。
the reason we're so focused on building robots that everyone can train is that we think the most compelling use cases in personal robotics are personal .	我們之所以專注於建造所有人都能訓練的機器人 , 是因為我們認為 , 個人機器人中最有吸引力的例子是個人機器人 。
they change from person to person .	他們從人轉變為人 。
so we think that if you're going to have a robot in your home , that robot ought to be a manifestation of your own imagination .	所以我們認為 , 如果你在家裡有機器人 , 機器人應該是你自己的想像力的展現 。
so i wish that i could tell you what the future of personal robotics looks like .	所以我希望我能告訴你個人機器人的未來是什麼樣子 。
to be honest , i have no idea .	老實說 , 我不知道 。
but what we do know is that it isn't 10 years or 10 billion dollars or a large humanoid robot away .	但我們確實知道 , 不是十年或一千億美金 , 或大型人類機器人 。
the future of personal robotics is happening today , and it's going to depend on small , agile robots like romo and the creativity of people like yourselves .	個人機器人的未來正在發生 , 它依賴像romo這樣的小型、敏捷機器人 , 以及像你一樣的人的創造力 。
so we can't wait to get you all robots , and we can't wait to see what you build .	所以 , 我們等不及給你所有機器人 , 我們等不及去看看你建造什麼 。
author and activist isabel allende discusses women , creativity , the definition of feminism and , of course , passion in this talk .	作者和積極主義者討論女性、創意、女性主義的定義 , 當然 , 在這場演說中 , 熱情也是 。
entertainment , global issues , love , parenting , storytelling , women , world cultures	娛樂、全球議題、愛、養育、說故事、婦女、世界文化、文化、文化、文化、文化、文化、文化、文化 。
isabel allende tells tales of passion	伊莎貝爾•艾倫告訴人們熱情的故事 , 關於熱情的故事 。
thank you so much . it's really scary to be here among the smartest of the smart .	非常謝謝各位 。 很可怕 , 在這裡是聰明人中最聰明的人 。
i'm here to tell you a few tales of passion .	我來這裡要告訴各位幾個關於熱情的故事 。
there's a jewish saying that i love .	有一個猶太人說我愛的 。
what is truer than truth ? answer: the story .	什麼比真相更真實 ? 答案:故事 。
i'm a storyteller . i want to convey something that is truer than truth about our common humanity .	我是個說故事的人 , 我想傳達一些比我們人類更真實的東西 。
all stories interest me , and some haunt me until i end up writing them .	所有的故事都對我感興趣 , 有些讓我痛恨 , 直到最後我寫了這些故事 。
certain themes keep coming up: justice , loyalty , violence , death , political and social issues , freedom .	有些主題不斷出現:正義、忠誠、暴力、死亡、政治和社會議題、自由 。
i'm aware of the mystery around us , so i write about coincidences , premonitions , emotions , dreams , the power of nature , magic .	我意識到我們身邊的奧秘 , 所以我寫的是巧合、預兆、情感、夢想、自然的力量、魔法 。
in the last 20 years i have published a few books , but i have lived in anonymity until february of 2006 , when i carried the olympic flag in the winter olympics in italy .	過去20年 , 我出版了幾本書 , 但在2006年二月 , 我在義大利的奧林匹克總統住了 。
that made me a celebrity . now people recognize me in macy's , and my grandchildren think that i'm cool .	這使我成為名人 。 現在人們在macy的作品中認識我 , 而我的孫子認為我很酷 。
allow me to tell you about my four minutes of fame .	讓我告訴你我四分鐘的名聲 。
one of the organizers of the olympic ceremony , of the opening ceremony , called me and said that i had been selected to be one of the flagbearers .	奧林匹克典禮的組織者之一 , 打電話給我 , 說我被選為旗幟家之一 。
i replied that surely this was a case of mistaken identity because i'm as far as you can get from being an athlete .	我回答說 , 這是個錯誤認同的案例 , 因為我很可能從運動員到現在 。
actually , i wasn't even sure that i could go around the stadium without a walker .	事實上 , 我甚至不確定我可以在沒有步行者的體育場四處走動 。
i was told that this was no laughing matter .	我被告知這一點都不重要 。
this would be the first time that only women would carry the olympic flag .	這是第一次 , 只有女性會帶著奧林匹克國旗 。
five women , representing five continents , and three olympic gold medal winners .	五個女人 , 代表五大洲 , 三座奧運金牌贏家 。
my first question was , naturally , what was i going to wear ?	我第一個問題是 , 很自然地 , 我要穿什麼 ?
a uniform , she said , and asked for my measurements .	她說 , 她要求我的測量 。
i had a vision of myself in a fluffy anorak , looking like the michelin man .	我對自己有一個遠景 , 看上去像米其林人 。
by the middle of february , i found myself in turin , where enthusiastic crowds cheered when any of the 80 olympic teams was in the street .	到了二月的中期 , 我發現自己在土耳其 , 在那裡 , 當八十個奧運隊伍都在街上歡呼 。
those athletes had sacrificed everything to compete in the games .	這些運動員犧牲了所有能在遊戲中競爭的一切 。
they all deserved to win , but there's the element of luck .	他們都值得獲勝 , 但有運氣的元素 。
a speck of snow , an inch of ice , the force of the wind , can determine the result of a race or a game .	一片雪 , 一英吋的冰 , 風的力量 , 可以決定種族或遊戲的結果 。
however , what matters most more than training or luck is the heart .	然而 , 最重要的是訓練或運氣是心臟 。
only a fearless and determined heart will get the gold medal .	只有無懼且堅定的心才會得到金牌 。
it is all about passion .	重點是熱情 。
the streets of turin were covered with red posters announcing the slogan of the olympics .	渦輪的街道被紅海報覆蓋 , 宣佈奧運的口號 。
passion lives here . isn't it always true ?	熱情生活在這裡 , 不是一直都是真的嗎 ?
heart is what drives us and determines our fate .	心是驅使我們決定我們的命運 。
that is what i need for my characters in my books: a passionate heart .	這就是我在書中需要的角色:熱情的心 。
i need mavericks , dissidents , adventurers , outsiders and rebels , who ask questions , bend the rules and take risks .	我需要駭客、異議、冒險家、外人、反叛者 , 他們會問問題、彎曲規則、冒險 。
people like all of you in this room .	像在座所有人一樣 。
nice people with common sense do not make interesting characters .	有常識的好人並不會創造有趣的角色 。
they only make good former spouses .	它們只會製造好的前配偶 。
in the green room of the stadium , i met the other flag bearers: three athletes , and the actresses susan sarandon and sophia loren .	在體育館的綠色房間裡 , 我遇見另一位國旗的熊:三位運動員 , 和蘇珊•薩蘭登和蘇菲亞洛倫 。
also , two women with passionate hearts: wangari maathai , the nobel prizewinner from kenya who has planted 30 million trees . and by doing so , she has changed the soil , the weather , in some places in africa , and of course the economic conditions in many villages .	另外 , 兩個充滿熱情的女人:瓦加里•馬塔伊 , 來自肯亞的諾貝爾獎得主 , 她種植了三千萬棵樹 。 順便一提 , 她改變了土壤 , 天氣 , 在非洲的某些地方 , 當然還有許多村莊的經濟條件 。
and somaly mam , a cambodian activist who fights passionately against child prostitution .	蘇瑪莉莉 , 柬埔寨活動家對抗兒童賣淫的熱情 。
when she was 14 years old , her grandfather sold her to a brothel .	當她十四歲時 , 她的祖父把她賣給妓院 。
she told us of little girls raped by men who believe that having sex with a very young virgin will cure them from aids .	她告訴我們 , 小女孩被男人強暴 , 相信和一個非常年輕的處女做愛 , 會治癒愛滋病 。
and of brothels where children are forced to receive five , 15 clients per day , and if they rebel , they are tortured with electricity .	孩童被迫每天收到五、十五個客戶的妓院 , 如果他們反叛 , 他們會被電力折磨 。
in the green room i received my uniform .	我在綠色房間收到制服 。
it was not the kind of outfit that i normally wear , but it was far from the michelin man suit that i had anticipated . not bad , really .	這不是我平常穿的服裝 , 但它離我預期的米其林男子服裝很遠 , 真的很糟糕 。
i looked like a refrigerator .	我看起來像是冰箱 。
but so did most of the flagbearers , except sophia loren , the universal symbol of beauty and passion .	除了索菲亞•洛倫 , 普遍的美和熱情的象徵 。
sophia is over 70 and she looks great .	蘇菲雅已經超過70歲了 , 她看起來很棒 。
she's sexy , slim and tall , with a deep tan .	她很性感、很瘦、很高 , 且有很深的坦丁 。
now , how can you have a deep tan and have no wrinkles ?	那麼 , 你要如何有深層的坦丁 , 沒有皺紋 ?
when asked in a tv interview , " how could she look so good ? "	當電視訪談問: 「 她怎麼看起來這麼好 ? 」
she replied , " posture . my back is always straight , and i don't make old people's noises . "	她回答: 「 姿勢 。 我的背總是很直接 , 我不會讓老人的噪音 。 」
so , there you have some free advice from one of the most beautiful women on earth .	這裡有一些來自地球上最美麗的女性的自由建議 。
no grunting , no coughing , no wheezing , no talking to yourselves , no farting .	沒有打力、沒有咳嗽、沒有輪子 , 沒有交談 , 沒有給自己說話 , 沒有放棄 。
well , she didn't say that exactly .	嗯 , 她並沒有這麼說 。
at some point around midnight , we were summoned to the wings of the stadium , and the loudspeakers announced the olympic flag , and the music started by the way , the same music that starts here , the aida march .	在午夜的某個時點 , 我們被召喚到體育場的翅膀 , 大聲說出奧林匹克旗 , 一開始的音樂 , 一開始 , 同樣的音樂 , 從這裡開始 , 愛迪達遊行 。
sophia loren was right in front of me she's a foot taller than i am , not counting the poofy hair .	蘇菲雅羅倫就在我面前 , 她比我高一點 , 而不是在計算小頭髮 。
she walked elegantly , like a giraffe on the african savannah , holding the flag on her shoulder . i jogged behind on my tiptoes holding the flag on my extended arm , so that my head was actually under the damn flag .	她很優雅地走路 , 就像非洲大草原上的長頸鹿 , 把她的肩膀拿著旗子 。 我在我的小提琴背後抱著我的旗子 , 所以我的頭其實是在該死的旗幟下 。
all the cameras were , of course , on sophia .	當然 , 所有的攝影機都在索菲亞 。
that was fortunate for me , because in most press photos i appear too , although often between sophia's legs .	這對我很幸運 , 因為在大部分的媒體照片中 , 我也出現了 , 雖然通常在蘇菲亞的腿之間 。
a place where most men would love to be .	大部分男人都想要去的地方 。
the best four minutes of my entire life were those in the olympic stadium .	我一生中最棒的四分鐘是奧林匹克體育場中的那些人 。
my husband is offended when i say this although i have explained to him that what we do in private usually takes less than four minutes so he shouldn't take it personally .	當我說這句話時 , 我先生被冒犯了 , 雖然我已經向他解釋 , 我們私人的做法通常要花不到四分鐘 , 所以他不應該親自接受這件事 。
i have all the press clippings of those four magnificent minutes , because i don't want to forget them when old age destroys my brain cells .	我有這四分鐘的按鈕 , 因為我不想忘記 , 老年人摧毀我的大腦細胞時 。
i want to carry in my heart forever the key word of the olympics passion .	我想要永遠帶著我的心 , 奧林匹克的關鍵字 。
so here's a tale of passion .	這裡有個熱情的故事 。
the year is 1998 , the place is a prison camp for tutsi refugees in congo .	1998年 , 那個地方是剛果的托西難民營 。
by the way , 80 percent of all refugees and displaced people in the world are women and girls .	順道一提 , 世界上80%的難民和流離失所的難民都是女人和女孩 。
we can call this place in congo a death camp , because those who are not killed will die of disease or starvation .	我們可以稱之為剛果的死亡營地 , 因為那些沒有殺死疾病或餓死的人 。
the protagonists of this story are a young woman , rose mapendo , and her children .	這個故事的主角是年輕女性 , 蘿絲•布羅多和她的孩子 。
she's pregnant and a widow .	她懷孕、寡婦 。
soldiers have forced her to watch as her husband was tortured and killed .	士兵強迫她看著她的丈夫被虐待和殺害 。
somehow she manages to keep her seven children alive , and a few months later , she gives birth to premature twins .	不知怎麼的 , 她能讓她的七個孩子活下來 , 幾個月後 , 她產下了早產的雙胞胎 。
two tiny little boys .	兩個小男孩 。
she cuts the umbilical cord with a stick , and ties it with her own hair .	她用棍子切斷了腫瘤線 , 把頭髮和頭髮結合 。
she names the twins after the camp's commanders to gain their favor , and feeds them with black tea because her milk cannot sustain them .	她把雙胞胎命名為營地指揮官的名字 , 用黑茶餵給他們 , 因為她的牛奶無法維持它們 。
when the soldiers burst in her cell to rape her oldest daughter , she grabs hold of her and refuses to let go , even when they hold a gun to her head .	當士兵在她的牢房裡被摧毀 , 強暴她最老的女兒時 , 她抓住她 , 拒絕放手 , 即使他們拿著槍到她的頭上 。
somehow , the family survives for 16 months , and then , by extraordinary luck , and the passionate heart of a young american man , sasha chanoff , who manages to put her in a u . s . rescue plane , rose mapendo and her nine children end up in phoenix , arizona , where they're now living and thriving .	不知怎麼的 , 家庭存活了十六個月 , 接著 , 幸運的是 , 一位年輕的美國男子 , 薩薩薩哈•夏諾夫 , 他把她放在美國救援飛機上 , 蘿絲•馬德羅多和她的九個孩子 , 最後到了亞利桑那州的鳳凰城 , 他們現在生活和茁壯 。
mapendo , in swahili , means great love .	在斯瓦希里的地圖上 , 意味著偉大的愛 。
the protagonists of my books are strong and passionate women like rose mapendo .	我書籍的主角是堅強且熱情的女性 , 像蘿絲•布羅多 。
i don't make them up . there's no need for that .	我不把它們弄好 , 也不需要這樣 。
i look around and i see them everywhere .	我環顧四周 , 到處都看得到 。
i have worked with women and for women all my life .	我一生都在為女性和女性工作 。
i know them well .	我很清楚他們 。
i was born in ancient times , at the end of the world , in a patriarchal catholic and conservative family .	我出生於古代 , 在世界末日 , 在父權教派和保守家庭 。
no wonder that by age five i was a raging feminist although the term had not reached chile yet , so nobody knew what the heck was wrong with me .	難怪 , 五歲時 , 我是個憤怒的女權主義者 , 雖然當時還沒達到智利 , 所以沒有人知道我有什麼問題 。
i would soon find out that there was a high price to pay for my freedom , and for questioning the patriarchy .	我很快就會發現 , 有很高的代價可以支付我的自由 , 並且質疑父權 。
but i was happy to pay it , because for every blow that i received , i was able to deliver two .	但我很高興能付錢 , 因為每次我收到的炸 , 我都能遞送兩次 。
once , when my daughter paula was in her twenties , she said to me that feminism was dated , that i should move on .	有一次 , 我女兒保羅在她二十多歲時 , 她告訴我女權主義是約會的 , 我應該繼續下去 。
we had a memorable fight . feminism is dated ?	我們有可回憶的鬥爭 , 女權主義被約會了嗎 ?
yes , for privileged women like my daughter and all of us here today , but not for most of our sisters in the rest of the world who are still forced into premature marriage , prostitution , forced labor they have children that they don't want or they cannot feed .	是的 , 對於像我女兒這樣的特權女性 , 今天在座的我們所有人 , 但對世界上大部分的姊妹來說 , 仍然被迫結婚、賣淫、強迫勞工 , 他們有孩子 , 他們不想要或不能餵飽 。
they have no control over their bodies or their lives .	他們無法掌控自己的身體或生命 。
they have no education and no freedom .	他們沒有教育 , 也沒有自由 。
they are raped , beaten up and sometimes killed with impunity .	他們被強暴、被打、被打 , 有時會因為不幸而被殺 。
for most western young women of today , being called a feminist is an insult .	對於現今大部分的西方女性 , 被稱為女性主義者是侮辱 。
feminism has never been sexy , but let me assure you that it never stopped me from flirting , and i have seldom suffered from lack of men .	女權主義從來沒有性感 , 但讓我向你保證 , 它從來沒有阻止我 , 而我缺乏男性 。
feminism is not dead , by no means .	女性主義並不是死的 , 絕對沒有 。
it has evolved . if you don't like the term , change it , for goddess' sake .	它演化了 。 如果你不喜歡這個詞 , 改變它 , 改變它 , 為女神的樣子 。
call it aphrodite , or venus , or bimbo , or whatever you want ; the name doesn't matter , as long as we understand what it is about , and we support it .	稱之為 「 孤兒 」 , 或維納斯 , 或你想要的任何東西 ; 這個名字並不重要 , 只要我們了解它的意義 , 我們就會支持它 。
so here's another tale of passion , and this is a sad one .	這是另一個關於熱情的故事 , 這是個悲傷的故事 。
the place is a small women's clinic in a village in bangladesh .	這個地方是一個孟加拉村莊的小女子診所 。
the year is 2005 .	一年是2005年
jenny is a young american dental hygienist who has gone to the clinic as a volunteer during her threeweek vacation .	珍妮是一位年輕的美國牙醫 , 她在三週假期間當志工 。
she's prepared to clean teeth , but when she gets there , she finds out that there are no doctors , no dentists , and the clinic is just a hut full of flies .	她準備乾淨牙齒 , 但當她到了那裡時 , 她發現沒有醫生 , 沒有牙醫 , 診所只是一間滿是蒼蠅的小屋 。
outside , there is a line of women who have waited several hours to be treated .	外面有一系列的女性等待好幾個小時被治療 。
the first patient is in excruciating pain because she has several rotten molars .	第一位病人非常痛苦 , 因為她有好幾個腐爛的肌肉 。
jenny realizes that the only solution is to pull out the bad teeth .	珍妮知道唯一的解決方案就是拉出壞牙齒 。
she's not licensed for that ; she has never done it .	她沒有授權 , 她從來沒有做過 。
she risks a lot and she's terrified .	她的風險很大 , 她很害怕 。
she doesn't even have the proper instruments , but fortunately she has brought some novocaine .	她甚至沒有適當的樂器 , 但幸運的是她帶了一些諾瓦卡因 。
jenny has a brave and passionate heart .	珍妮有勇氣和熱情的心 。
she murmurs a prayer and she goes ahead with the operation .	她謀殺了祈禱 , 然後她繼續前進 。
at the end , the relieved patient kisses her hands .	最後 , 病患親吻了她的手 。
that day the hygienist pulls out many more teeth .	那天衛生學家抽出更多牙齒 。
the next morning , when she comes again to the socalled clinic , her first patient is waiting for her with her husband .	隔天早上 , 當她再次到所謂的診所時 , 她的第一個病人正在等著她的丈夫 。
the woman's face looks like a watermelon .	那位女士的臉看起來像是一個水手 。
it is so swollen that you can't even see the eyes .	你甚至看不到眼睛的腫脹 。
the husband , furious , threatens to kill the american .	丈夫、憤怒、威脅要殺死美國人 。
jenny is horrified at what she has done , but then the translator explains that the patient's condition has nothing to do with the operation .	珍妮對她所做的事感到害怕 , 但翻譯解釋病人的狀況和手術無關 。
the day before , her husband beat her up because she was not home in time to prepare dinner for him .	前一天 , 她的丈夫打敗了她 , 因為她沒時間為他準備晚餐 。
millions of women live like this today .	現今有數百萬的女性像這樣的生活 。
they are the poorest of the poor .	他們是窮人的最窮人 。
although women do twothirds of the world's labor , they own less than one percent of the world's assets .	雖然世界上三分之二的勞工 , 他們擁有不到1%的全球資產 。
they are paid less than men for the same work if they're paid at all , and they remain vulnerable because they have no economic independence , and they are constantly threatened by exploitation , violence and abuse .	他們的薪水遠低於男性的薪水 , 如果他們薪水完全沒有經濟獨立 , 而且他們經常受到剝削、暴力和虐待的威脅 。
it is a fact that giving women education , work , the ability to control their own income , inherit and own property , benefits the society .	事實上 , 給予女性教育、工作能力、控制她們自己的收入、繼承和財產的能力 , 讓社會受益 。
if a woman is empowered , her children and her family will be better off .	如果一個女人被賦予權力 , 她的孩子和她的家人會更好 。
if families prosper , the village prospers , and eventually so does the whole country .	如果家庭繁榮 , 村落的繁榮者 , 最終整個國家都如此 。
wangari maathai goes to a village in kenya .	wangarimaathai去了肯亞的村莊
she talks with the women and explains that the land is barren because they have cut and sold the trees .	她和婦女說話 , 解釋土地是貧瘠的 , 因為他們已經砍掉和賣掉了樹木 。
she gets the women to plant new trees and water them , drop by drop .	她讓婦女來種新樹 , 用它們 , 滴下水 。
in a matter of five or six years , they have a forest , the soil is enriched , and the village is saved .	在五、六年之內 , 他們有一片森林 , 土壤被豐富 , 村莊被拯救了 。
the poorest and most backward societies are always those that put women down .	最貧窮、最後退的社會總是把女性放下來的人 。
yet this obvious truth is ignored by governments and also by philanthropy .	然而 , 這種顯而易見的事實卻被政府和慈善機構忽視 。
for every dollar given to a women's program , 20 dollars are given to men's programs .	每一塊一塊錢給婦女專案 , 20塊美金給男性的計畫 。
women are 51 percent of humankind .	女性是51%的人 。
empowering them will change everything more than technology and design and entertainment .	授權他們會改變一切 , 勝過科技、設計、娛樂 。
i can promise you that women working together linked , informed and educated can bring peace and prosperity to this forsaken planet .	我可以向各位保證 , 女性一起合作 , 連結、知情、受過教育 , 能為這個星球帶來和平和繁榮 。
in any war today , most of the casualties are civilians , mainly women and children . they are collateral damage .	在今天的任何戰爭中 , 大部分的傷害都是平民百姓 , 主要是婦女和兒童 。 她們是殖民地的傷害 。
men run the world , and look at the mess we have .	男人經營這個世界 , 看看我們有的混亂 。
what kind of world do we want ?	我們想要什麼樣的世界 ?
this is a fundamental question that most of us are asking .	這是我們大多數人在問的基本問題 。
does it make sense to participate in the existing world order ?	是否合理地參與現有的世界秩序 ?
we want a world where life is preserved and the quality of life is enriched for everybody , not only for the privileged .	我們想要一個生活被保存的世界 , 生活的品質都被賦予每個人 , 不只是為了特權 。
in january i saw an exhibit of fernando botero's paintings at the uc berkeley library .	一月 , 我在柏克萊圖書館看到了費南多波特羅的畫作 。
no museum or gallery in the united states , except for the new york gallery that carries botero's work , has dared to show the paintings because the theme is the abu ghraib prison .	美國沒有博物館或畫廊 , 除了紐約的畫廊 , 博特羅的作品 , 敢展示這幅畫 , 因為主題是阿布格萊布監獄 。
they are huge paintings of torture and abuse of power , in the voluminous botero style .	它們是巨大的折磨和濫用權力的畫作 , 用大量的波特羅風格風格 。
i have not been able to get those images out of my mind or my heart .	我沒有辦法把這些影像從我心中或心中拿出來 。
what i fear most is power with impunity .	我最害怕的是無罪的力量 。
i fear abuse of power , and the power to abuse .	我害怕濫用權力和濫用權力 。
in our species , the alpha males define reality , and force the rest of the pack to accept that reality and follow the rules .	在我們的物種中 , 雄性領袖定義了現實 , 強迫其他的群體接受現實 , 並遵循規則 。
the rules change all the time , but they always benefit them , and in this case , the trickledown effect , which does not work in economics , works perfectly .	規則會隨時改變 , 但他們總是受益 , 在這個案例中 , 缺陷效應在經濟上行不通 , 完美地運作 。
abuse trickles down from the top of the ladder to the bottom .	從梯子的頂端 , 到底部 。
women and children , especially the poor , are at the bottom .	女人和小孩 , 特別是窮人 , 都在底部 。
even the most destitute of men have someone they can abuse a woman or a child .	即使是最缺乏男性的人 , 也有可能會虐待女人或小孩的人 。
i'm fed up with the power that a few exert over the many through gender , income , race , and class .	我得到的力量是透過性別、收入、種族、階級的少數人 。
i think that the time is ripe to make fundamental changes in our civilization .	我認為 , 時間是興起在我們的文明中做出根本的改變 。
but for real change , we need feminine energy in the management of the world .	但對於真正的改變 , 我們需要女性化的能量來管理世界 。
we need a critical number of women in positions of power , and we need to nurture the feminine energy in men .	我們需要一群女性在權力的位置 , 我們需要培養男性的女性能量 。
i'm talking about men with young minds , of course .	當然我在說的是年輕人 。
old guys are hopeless ; we have to wait for them to die off .	老人是無望的 , 我們得等他們死去 。
yes , i would love to have sophia loren's long legs and legendary breasts .	是的 , 我想要有蘇菲雅羅倫的長腿和傳奇胸 。
but given a choice , i would rather have the warrior hearts of wangari maathai , somaly mam , jenny and rose mapendo .	但 , 根據一個選擇 , 我寧願有華格里•馬塔伊的勇士心 , 索馬里、珍妮、羅絲•地圖 。
i want to make this world good .	我想讓這個世界變得更好 。
not better , but to make it good .	不是更好 , 而是要把它做得更好 。
why not ? it is possible . look around in this room all this knowledge , energy , talent and technology .	為什麼不 ? 它是有可能的 。 看看這個房間裡所有的知識、能源、才華和科技 。
let's get off our fannies , roll up our sleeves and get to work , passionately , in creating an almost perfect world .	讓我們擺脫我們的粉絲 , 捲起袖子 , 熱情地工作 , 創造一個幾乎完美的世界 。
every day , in a city the size of london , 30 million meals are served . but where does all the food come from ? architect carolyn steel discusses the daily miracle of feeding a city , and shows how ancient food routes shaped the modern world .	每天 , 在倫敦大小的城市中 , 有三千萬份餐會被服務 。 但是所有的食物從哪裡來 ? 建築師carolyns鋼鐵討論如何養活城市的奇蹟 , 展現出古老的食物路線如何塑造現代世界 。
cities , culture , food , global issues	城市、文化、食物、全球議題 。
carolyn steel: how food shapes our cities	卡羅琳•史黛爾:食物如何塑造我們的城市 , 如何塑造我們的城市 。
how do you feed a city ?	你要如何餵飽一個城市 ?
it's one of the great questions of our time .	這是我們這個時代最偉大的問題之一 。
yet it's one that's rarely asked .	但很少被問到 。
we take it for granted that if we go into a shop or restaurant , or indeed into this theater's foyer in about an hour's time , there is going to be food there waiting for us , having magically come from somewhere .	我們視為理所當然 , 如果我們走進商店或餐廳 , 或在這個劇院的旅程中 , 大約一小時內 , 就會有食物等待著我們 , 魔幻地來自某處 。
but when you think that every day for a city the size of london , enough food has to be produced , transported , bought and sold , cooked , eaten , disposed of , and that something similar has to happen every day for every city on earth , it's remarkable that cities get fed at all .	但當你認為 , 每一天 , 對於倫敦大小的城市而言 , 足夠的食物必須被生產、運送、購買、煮飯、吃掉、丟棄、丟棄的城市 , 都必須每天發生類似的事情 , 才能讓所有城市都能滿足 。
we live in places like this as if they're the most natural things in the world , forgetting that because we're animals and that we need to eat , we're actually as dependent on the natural world as our ancient ancestors were .	我們生活在這樣的環境 , 彷彿它們是世界上最自然的東西 , 因為我們是動物 , 且我們需要吃東西 , 我們其實是依賴自然世界 , 就像我們的古老祖先一樣 。
and as more of us move into cities , more of that natural world is being transformed into extraordinary landscapes like the one behind me it's soybean fields in mato grosso in brazil in order to feed us .	隨著我們愈來愈多人進入城市 , 越多的自然世界被轉變為非凡的地景 , 就像我身後的景觀一樣 , 巴西的馬托格索州的黃豆田 , 為了餵飽我們 。
these are extraordinary landscapes , but few of us ever get to see them .	這些是非凡的地景 , 但我們當中少數人能看到它們 。
and increasingly these landscapes are not just feeding us either .	越來越多的地景 , 不僅是餵飽我們 。
as more of us move into cities , more of us are eating meat , so that a third of the annual grain crop globally now gets fed to animals rather than to us human animals .	隨著更多人搬進城市 , 更多人吃肉 , 所以 , 全球每年有三分之一的穀物被餵給動物 , 而不是我們人類的動物 。
and given that it takes three times as much grain actually ten times as much grain to feed a human if it's passed through an animal first , that's not a very efficient way of feeding us .	假設它要花上三倍的穀物 , 實際上是十倍以上才能餵飽人類 , 如果它首先通過動物 , 那就不太有效率地餵飽我們 。
and it's an escalating problem too .	這也是一個越來越嚴重的問題 。
by 2050 , it's estimated that twice the number of us are going to be living in cities .	到了2050年 , 估計我們居住在城市的兩倍 。
and it's also estimated that there is going to be twice as much meat and dairy consumed .	據估計 , 有兩倍的肉和奶油消耗量 。
so meat and urbanism are rising hand in hand .	所以肉和城市主義正在舉手 。
and that's going to pose an enormous problem .	這將會帶來巨大的問題 。
six billion hungry carnivores to feed , by 2050 .	到2050年 , 飢餓的食肉動物會餵飽六十億人 。
that's a big problem . and actually if we carry on as we are , it's a problem we're very unlikely to be able to solve .	這是個大問題 。 事實上 , 如果我們像我們一樣繼續下去 , 這是我們無法解決的問題 。
nineteen million hectares of rainforest are lost every year to create new arable land .	每年有九百萬公頃的熱帶雨林消失了 , 創造出新的可耕地 。
although at the same time we're losing an equivalent amount of existing arables to salinization and erosion .	雖然同時 , 我們也失去了相當大量的現有的可耕地 , 來消滅和侵蝕 。
we're very hungry for fossil fuels too .	我們也非常渴望化石燃料 。
it takes about 10 calories to produce every calorie of food that we consume in the west .	我們在西方所消耗的每一卡路里要花十卡路里 。
and even though there is food that we are producing at great cost , we don't actually value it .	儘管我們在生產成本很高的食物 , 我們其實不重視它 。
half the food produced in the usa is currently thrown away .	美國有一半生產的食物被丟掉了 。
and to end all of this , at the end of this long process , we're not even managing to feed the planet properly .	最後 , 在這個長期的過程結束時 , 我們甚至無法適當地處理地球的食物 。
a billion of us are obese , while a further billion starve .	我們有十億人過胖 , 更深入的挨餓 。
none of it makes very much sense .	沒有什麼意義 。
and when you think that 80 percent of global trade in food now is controlled by just five multinational corporations , it's a grim picture .	當你認為全球80%的糧食交易只受五家跨國企業控制時 , 這是一張很辛苦的圖片 。
as we're moving into cities , the world is also embracing a western diet .	當我們進入城市時 , 世界也在擁抱西方的飲食 。
and if we look to the future , it's an unsustainable diet .	如果我們看看未來 , 這是個不永續的飲食 。
so how did we get here ?	我們是怎麼來到這裡的 ?
and more importantly , what are we going to do about it ?	更重要的是 , 我們要怎麼做 ?
well , to answer the slightly easier question first , about 10 , 000 years ago , i would say , is the beginning of this process in the ancient near east , known as the fertile crescent .	首先 , 要回答這個問題稍微簡單一點 , 大約一萬年前 , 我會說 , 這是在東方的古老過程的開端 , 也就是所謂的 「 肥料危機近期 」 。
because , as you can see , it was crescent shaped .	因為 , 如你所見 , 它的形狀很近 。
and it was also fertile .	同時也是肥沃的 。
and it was here , about 10 , 000 years ago , that two extraordinary inventions , agriculture and urbanism , happened roughly in the same place and at the same time .	大約一萬年前 , 這裡有兩個非凡的發明 , 農業和城市主義 , 大約在同一個地方和同時發生 。
this is no accident , because agriculture and cities are bound together . they need each other .	這不是意外 , 因為農業和城市是互相連結的 。 他們需要彼此 。
because it was discovery of grain by our ancient ancestors for the first time that produced a food source that was large enough and stable enough to support permanent settlements .	因為這是我們古老祖先第一次發現穀物 , 製造出足夠大且穩定的食物來源 , 足以支持永久定居地 。
and if we look at what those settlements were like , we see they were compact .	如果我們看看這些定居處是什麼樣子 , 我們會看到它們是互補的 。
they were surrounded by productive farm land and dominated by large temple complexes like this one at ur , that were , in fact , effectively , spiritualized , central food distribution centers .	他們被生產力的農地包圍 , 由大型寺廟複合物所組成 , 實際上 , 是靈性化、中央食物分配中心 。
because it was the temples that organized the harvest , gathered in the grain , offered it to the gods , and then offered the grain that the gods didn't eat back to the people .	因為它是組織收割的寺廟 , 聚集在穀物裡 , 提供給神 , 然後給予神的穀物 。
so , if you like , the whole spiritual and physical life of these cities was dominated by the grain and the harvest that sustained them .	所以 , 如果你喜歡 , 這些城市的靈性和實體生活是由穀物和收割所支配的 。
and in fact , that's true of every ancient city .	事實上 , 每一座古老城市都是如此 。
but of course not all of them were that small .	當然 , 不是所有人都這麼小 。
famously , rome had about a million citizens by the first century a . d .	很有名的是 , 羅馬在第一世紀就有大約一百萬個市民 。
so how did a city like this feed itself ?	所以 , 像這樣的城市是怎麼餵飽的 ?
the answer is what i call " ancient food miles . "	答案就是我所謂的 「 古老食物哩 」 。
basically , rome had access to the sea , which made it possible for it to import food from a very long way away .	基本上 , 羅馬能接觸到海洋 , 讓它可以在很遠的地方進口食物 。
this is the only way it was possible to do this in the ancient world , because it was very difficult to transport food over roads , which were rough .	這是我們在古代世界唯一能做到的方法 , 因為在路上運輸食物是非常困難的 。
and the food obviously went off very quickly .	食物很快就消失了 。
so rome effectively waged war on places like carthage and egypt just to get its paws on their grain reserves .	羅馬有效率地打擊了像卡片和埃及的戰爭 , 只為了在他們的穀物儲備上拿到他的筆 。
and , in fact , you could say that the expansion of the empire was really sort of one long , drawn out militarized shopping spree , really .	事實上 , 你可以說 , 帝國的擴張其實是一塊很長的 , 用軍事化購物的速度 ,
in fact i love the fact , i just have to mention this: rome in fact used to import oysters from london , at one stage . i think that's extraordinary .	事實上 , 我很喜歡這個事實 , 我只需要提到羅馬實際上是從倫敦進口牡蠣的 , 我覺得那是不凡的 。
so rome shaped its hinterland through its appetite .	羅馬用它的胃口塑造了它的印度地 。
but the interesting thing is that the other thing also happened in the preindustrial world .	但有趣的是 , 在工業前的世界也發生了另一件事 。
if we look at a map of london in the 17th century , we can see that its grain , which is coming in from the thames , along the bottom of this map .	如果我們看看十七世紀的倫敦地圖 , 我們可以看到它的穀物 , 沿著這張地圖的底部 。
so the grain markets were to the south of the city .	所以穀物市場到城市的南方 。
and the roads leading up from them to cheapside , which was the main market , were also grain markets .	道路從它們變成便宜 , 也就是主要市場 , 也是穀物市場 。
and if you look at the name of one of those streets , bread street , you can tell what was going on there 300 years ago .	如果你看看其中一條街道的名字 , 麵包街 , 你可以知道300年前那裡發生了什麼事 。
and the same of course was true for fish .	當然 , 魚也是如此 。
fish was , of course , coming in by river as well . same thing .	當然 , 魚也來自河裡 。 同樣的事 。
and of course billingsgate , famously , was london's fish market , operating onsite here until the mid1980s .	當然 , billingsgate是倫敦的魚市場 , 直到1980年代中期 。
which is extraordinary , really , when you think about it .	真的 , 這真的是很了不起的 。
everybody else was wandering around with mobile phones that looked like bricks and sort of smelly fish happening down on the port .	每個人 , 都帶著手機 , 看起來像磚頭 , 有點像是魚在港口上流動 。
this is another thing about food in cities: once its roots into the city are established , they very rarely move .	這是城市裡食物的另一件事:一旦城市的根根被建立起來 , 它們就很少移動 。
meat is a very different story because , of course , animals could walk into the city .	肉是一種截然不同的故事 , 因為動物可以走進城市裡 。
so much of london's meat was coming from the northwest , from scotland and wales .	倫敦的肉大多來自西北部 , 來自蘇格蘭和威爾斯 。
so it was coming in , and arriving at the city at the northwest , which is why smithfield , london's very famous meat market , was located up there .	所以它進來了 , 抵達西北部 , 這就是為什麼斯密菲爾德倫敦非常著名的肉市場 , 位在那邊 。
poultry was coming in from east anglia and so on , to the northeast .	來自東孟加拉 , 諸如此類 , 到東北部 。
i feel a bit like a weather woman doing this . anyway , and so the birds were coming in with their feet protected with little canvas shoes .	我覺得我有點像天氣女士那樣做 。 總之 , 鳥會帶著牠們的腳 , 帶著小型的帆布鞋 。
and then when they hit the eastern end of cheapside , that's where they were sold , which is why it's called poultry .	當他們撞到便宜的東端時 , 這就是他們被賣的地方 , 這就是為什麼它被稱為 「 波里 」 。
and , in fact , if you look at the map of any city built before the industrial age , you can trace food coming in to it .	事實上 , 如果你看任何一個城市的地圖 , 在工業時代之前 , 你可以追蹤食物進來 。
you can actually see how it was physically shaped by food , both by reading the names of the streets , which give you a lot of clues .	你可以看到它是如何被食物所塑造的 , 兩者都透過閱讀街道的名字 , 給你很多線索 。
friday street , in a previous life , is where you went to buy your fish on a friday .	星期五街 , 在過去的生活中 , 你在星期五去買你的魚 。
but also you have to imagine it full of food .	但你也得要想像它充滿食物 。
because the streets and the public spaces were the only places where food was bought and sold .	因為街道和公共空間是唯一買賣食物的地方 。
and if we look at an image of smithfield in 1830 you can see that it would have been very difficult to live in a city like this and be unaware of where your food came from .	如果我們看看1830年史密斯菲菲爾德的圖像 , 你可以看到 , 在這樣的城市中 , 很難生存 , 無法察覺你的食物從哪裡來 。
in fact , if you were having sunday lunch , the chances were it was mooing or bleating outside your window about three days earlier .	事實上 , 如果你有星期日午餐 , 很可能是在你的窗外沖天或在窗外流血 , 大約三天前 。
so this was obviously an organic city , part of an organic cycle .	這顯然是個有機城市 , 是有機循環的一部分 。
and then 10 years later everything changed .	十年後 , 一切都改變了 。
this is an image of the great western in 1840 .	這是1840年西部大西部的照片 。
and as you can see , some of the earliest train passengers were pigs and sheep .	如你所見 , 一些最早的火車乘客是豬和羊 。
so all of a sudden , these animals are no longer walking into market .	突然間 , 這些動物不再走進市場了 。
they're being slaughtered out of sight and mind , somewhere in the countryside .	他們被視覺和思想屠宰了 , 在鄉下的某處 。
and they're coming into the city by rail .	他們以鐵路來到城市裡 。
and this changes everything .	這改變了一切 。
to start off with , it makes it possible for the first time to grow cities , really any size and shape , in any place .	首先 , 它是有可能第一次種植城市 , 幾乎任何大小和形狀的 。
cities used to be constrained by geography ; they used to have to get their food through very difficult physical means .	過去的城市被地理學所限制 , 以前他們必須透過非常困難的實體方式取得食物 。
all of a sudden they are effectively emancipated from geography .	突然間 , 它們都被地理解放了 。
and as you can see from these maps of london , in the 90 years after the trains came , it goes from being a little blob that was quite easy to feed by animals coming in on foot , and so on , to a large splurge , that would be very , very difficult to feed with anybody on foot , either animals or people .	如你所見 , 從倫敦地圖所看到的 , 在火車來臨的90年後 , 它從一個很容易被動物吸食的小石塊 , 到大型的噴泉 , 很難餵飽任何人 , 不論是動物或人類 。
and of course that was just the beginning . after the trains came cars , and really this marks the end of this process .	當然 , 這只是開端 。 在火車來臨後 , 真的是這個過程的終點 。
it's the final emancipation of the city from any apparent relationship with nature at all .	它是城市的最後解放 , 完全與大自然之間的關係 。
and this is the kind of city that's devoid of smell , devoid of mess , certainly devoid of people , because nobody would have dreamed of walking in such a landscape .	這是一種無法聞到的城市 , 除非混亂 , 肯定沒有人 , 因為沒有人會夢想在這樣的地景中走路 。
in fact , what they did to get food was they got in their cars , drove to a box somewhere on the outskirts , came back with a week's worth of shopping , and wondered what on earth to do with it .	事實上 , 他們在車子裡拿到食物 , 開車到外圍的盒子裡 , 帶著一週的購物品回來 , 想知道在地球上怎麼做 。
and this really is the moment when our relationship , both with food and cities , changes completely .	這才是我們與食物和城市之間的關係 , 完全改變了 。
here we have food that used to be the center , the social core of the city at the periphery .	這裡我們有食物 , 以前是該城市的社會核心 。
it used to be a social event , buying and selling food .	以前是社會活動 , 買賣和賣食物 。
we used to cook ; now we just add water , or a little bit of an egg if you're making a cake or something .	我們以前會煮飯 , 現在我們加入水 , 或加一點蛋 , 如果你在做蛋糕或其他東西的話 。
we don't smell food to see if it's okay to eat .	我們不會聞到食物的味道 , 看看它是否可以吃 。
we just read the back of a label on a packet .	我們只是在包裝上讀取標籤的後面 。
and we don't value food . we don't trust it .	我們不珍視食物 , 我們不信任它 。
so instead of trusting it , we fear it .	所以我們不信任它 , 而是害怕它 。
and instead of valuing it , we throw it away .	而不是評估它 , 而是把它丟掉 。
one of the great ironies of modern food systems is that they've made the very thing they promised to make easier much harder .	現代食物系統的最諷刺之一 , 就是它們已經做出了他們承諾要更加困難的事 。
by making it possible to build cities anywhere and any place , they've actually distanced us from our most important relationship , which is that of us and nature .	藉由讓它能夠在任何地方建造城市 , 它們實際上已經讓我們與我們最重要的關係連結在一起 , 那就是我們和大自然 。
and also they've made us dependent on systems that only they can deliver , that , as we've seen , are unsustainable .	他們也讓我們依賴只能傳遞的系統 , 如我們所見 , 它們是無法永續的 。
so what are we going to do about that ?	那我們要怎麼做呢 ?
it's not a new question .	這不是一個新問題 。
500 years ago it's what thomas more was asking himself .	500年前 , 湯瑪斯更是問自己 。
this is the frontispiece of his book " utopia . "	這是他的書《烏托邦》的頭版 。
and it was a series of semiindependent citystates , if that sounds remotely familiar , a day's walk from one another where everyone was basically farmingmad , and grew vegetables in their back gardens , and ate communal meals together , and so on .	那是一系列半獨立的城邦 , 如果聽起來很遙遠 , 一個人基本上是農夫 , 並且在他們背後的花園中長出蔬菜 , 吃飯的餐點等等 。
and i think you could argue that food is a fundamental ordering principle of utopia , even though more never framed it that way .	我認為你可以主張食物是烏托邦最基本的秩序原則 , 即使從來沒有用這種方式騙過它 。
and here is another very famous " utopian " vision , that of ebenezer howard , " the garden city . "	這裡還有另一個著名的 「 烏托邦 」 視覺 , 埃比塞內斯霍華德 , 「 花園城市 」 。
same idea: series of semiindependent citystates , little blobs of metropolitan stuff with arable land around , joined to one another by railway .	同樣的點子:半獨立的城市 , 大都市的一小塊土地 , 加入一條鐵路 。
and again , food could be said to be the ordering principle of his vision .	再一次 , 食物可以被說是他的願景定序原則 。
it even got built , but nothing to do with this vision that howard had .	它甚至建造了 , 但和霍華的這個遠景無關 。
and that is the problem with these utopian ideas , that they are utopian .	這就是這些烏托邦的想法的問題 , 他們是烏托邦人 。
utopia was actually a word that thomas moore used deliberately .	烏托邦其實是湯瑪斯•摩爾在刻意使用的詞 。
it was a kind of joke , because it's got a double derivation from the greek .	那是個笑話 , 因為希臘有雙倍的誘惑 。
it can either mean a good place , or no place .	它可能是好地方 , 或沒有地方 。
because it's an ideal . it's an imaginary thing . we can't have it .	因為這是理想的 , 這是個虛構的東西 。 我們不能擁有它 。
and i think , as a conceptual tool for thinking about the very deep problem of human dwelling , that makes it not much use .	我認為 , 作為一個概念性的工具 , 來思考人類居住的深層問題 , 讓它不太有用 。
so i've come up with an alternative , which is sitopia , from the ancient greek , " sitos " for food , and " topos " for place .	所以我想出了一個替代方案 , 也就是西托邦 , 古希臘的《西托》 , 用食物和 「 地點 」 。
i believe we already live in sitopia .	我相信我們已經住在西托邦 。
we live in a world shaped by food , and if we realize that , we can use food as a really powerful tool a conceptual tool , design tool , to shape the world differently .	我們生活在一個被食物所塑造的世界 , 如果我們意識到 , 我們可以把食物當成強大的工具 , 一種概念工具 , 設計工具 , 以不同的方式塑造世界 。
so if we were to do that , what might sitopia look like ?	所以如果我們這樣做 , 西托邦會長什麼樣子 ?
well i think it looks a bit like this .	我覺得它看起來有點像這樣 。
i have to use this slide . it's just the look on the face of the dog .	我必須用這張投影片 , 只是狗臉上的表情 。
but anyway , this is it's food at the center of life , at the center of family life , being celebrated , being enjoyed , people taking time for it .	總之 , 這是生活的中心 , 在家庭生活的中心 , 被慶祝 , 享受 , 人們花時間做這件事 。
this is where food should be in our society .	這就是我們社會裡應該要有食物的地方 。
but you can't have scenes like this unless you have people like this .	但除非你有這樣的人 , 你不能有像這樣的景象 。
by the way , these can be men as well .	順道一提 , 這些人也可以是男性 。
it's people who think about food , who think ahead , who plan , who can stare at a pile of raw vegetables and actually recognize them .	那些想到食物的人 , 先想到食物 , 他們的計畫 , 能夠盯著一堆原料的蔬菜 , 並且認出它們 。
we need these people . we're part of a network .	我們需要這些人 , 我們是網路的一部分 。
because without these kinds of people we can't have places like this .	因為如果沒有這些人 , 我們就沒有像這樣的地方 。
here , i deliberately chose this because it is a man buying a vegetable .	在這裡 , 我刻意選擇這一點 , 因為它是一個男人買蔬菜 。
but networks , markets where food is being grown locally .	但網路、市場 , 食物在當地生長的市場 。
it's common . it's fresh .	它很常見 , 很新鮮 。
it's part of the social life of the city .	它是城市社會生活的一部分 。
because without that , you can't have this kind of place , food that is grown locally and also is part of the landscape , and is not just a zerosum commodity off in some unseen hellhole .	因為 , 若沒有這點 , 你就不能有這種地方 , 當地的食物也是地景的一部分 , 而不只是在一些不起眼的地獄裡的零和商品 。
cows with a view .	牛的觀點是 。
steaming piles of humus .	蒸汽的幽默 。
this is basically bringing the whole thing together .	這基本上是把整個東西湊在一起 。
and this is a community project i visited recently in toronto .	這是我最近去過多倫多的一個社區計畫 。
it's a greenhouse , where kids get told all about food and growing their own food .	這是一間溫室 , 孩子們被告知關於食物和種植自己的食物 。
here is a plant called kevin , or maybe it's a plant belonging to a kid called kevin . i don't know .	這裡有個叫做kevin的植物 , 或者是植物屬於一個叫kevin的孩子 。 我不知道 。
but anyway , these kinds of projects that are trying to reconnect us with nature is extremely important .	但無論如何 , 這些計畫正試圖將我們和大自然重新連結起來是非常重要的 。
so sitopia , for me , is really a way of seeing .	所以 , 對我來說 , 西托邦真的是一種看待的方式 。
it's basically recognizing that sitopia already exists in little pockets everywhere .	基本上 , 意識到西托邦已經存在於各地的小口袋裡 。
the trick is to join them up , to use food as a way of seeing .	訣竅是要加入它們 , 把食物當作一種看法 。
and if we do that , we're going to stop seeing cities as big , metropolitan , unproductive blobs , like this .	如果我們這樣做 , 我們就會停止把城市看成是大城市 , 大都市 , 沒有生產力的泡沫 , 就像這樣 。
we're going to see them more like this , as part of the productive , organic framework of which they are inevitably a part , symbiotically connected .	我們將把它們視為是有生產力、有機架構的一部分 , 不可避免地連接在一起 。
but of course , that's not a great image either , because we need not to be producing food like this anymore .	當然 , 這也不是一個很棒的圖像 , 因為我們不需要再生產這樣的食物 。
we need to be thinking more about permaculture , which is why i think this image just sums up for me the kind of thinking we need to be doing .	我們需要更深入思考永續栽培 , 這就是為什麼我認為這張影像只是總結出我們需要做的事 。
it's a reconceptualization of the way food shapes our lives .	這是食物如何塑造我們的生活 。
the best image i know of this is from 650 years ago .	我所知最好的圖片是650年前的 。
it's ambrogio lorenzetti's " allegory of good government . "	這是ambrogiolorenzetti的 「 好政府的寓言 」 。
it's about the relationship between the city and the countryside .	重點在於城市和鄉村之間的關係 。
and i think the message of this is very clear .	我認為這個訊息非常清楚 。
if the city looks after the country , the country will look after the city .	如果城市照顧這個國家 , 國家就會照顧這個城市 。
and i want us to ask now , what would ambrogio lorenzetti paint if he painted this image today ?	我現在要我們問 , 如果他今天畫了這張圖 , 安布羅吉歐•羅倫澤蒂會是什麼樣子 ?
what would an allegory of good government look like today ?	今天好政府的寓言會是什麼樣子 ?
because i think it's an urgent question .	因為我認為這是個迫切的問題 。
it's one we have to ask , and we have to start answering .	我們必須問一個問題 , 我們必須開始回答 。
we know we are what we eat .	我們知道我們在吃什麼 。
we need to realize that the world is also what we eat .	我們需要意識到 , 世界是我們所吃的 。
but if we take that idea , we can use food as a really powerful tool to shape the world better .	但如果我們採取這個想法 , 我們可以把食物當作強大的工具來塑造世界 。
weeks from the charter for compassion launch , karen armstrong looks at religion's role in the 21st century: will its dogmas divide us ? or will it unite us for common good ? she reviews the catalysts that can drive the world's faiths to rediscover the golden rule .	從 「 同情心發射 」 的那幾週 , karenarmstrong看著宗教在21世紀的角色:它的教條會分裂我們嗎 ? 還是它會讓我們團結好事 ? 她會審視世界上的信仰 , 來重新發現黃金法則 。
god , ted prize , global issues , politics , religion , tedglobal2009 , violence	上帝 , tedprize , 全球議題 , 政治 , 宗教 , tedglobal2009 , 暴力 , 暴力 。
karen armstrong: let's revive the golden rule	karenarmstrong:讓我們重建黃金法則 。
for years i've been feeling frustrated , because as a religious historian , i've become acutely aware of the centrality of compassion in all the major world faiths .	多年來 , 我覺得很挫折 , 因為身為宗教歷史學家 , 我很敏銳地意識到在世界各大宗教中 , 同情心的核心 。
every single one of them has evolved their own version of what's been called the golden rule .	每一個人都演化出他們所謂的黃金法則 。
sometimes it comes in a positive version " always treat all others as you'd like to be treated yourself . "	有時會出現正面的版本 「 總是對待別人 , 就像你想要被對待一樣 。 」
and equally important is the negative version " don't do to others what you would not like them to do to you . "	同樣重要的是 , 負面的版本: 「 不要對別人做你不喜歡的事 。 」
look into your own heart , discover what it is that gives you pain and then refuse , under any circumstance whatsoever , to inflict that pain on anybody else .	看看你自己的心 , 發現它給你痛苦 , 然後在任何情況下拒絕 , 去衝突別人的痛苦 。
and people have emphasized the importance of compassion , not just because it sounds good , but because it works .	人們強調同情心的重要性 , 不只是因為它聽起來很好 , 也因為它有用 。
people have found that when they have implemented the golden rule as confucius said , " all day and every day , " not just a question of doing your good deed for the day and then returning to a life of greed and egotism , but to do it all day and every day , you dethrone yourself from the center of your world , put another there , and you transcend yourself .	人們發現當他們實施黃金法則時 , 說: 「 一整天 , 每一天都在做好事 , 不只想在一天中做好事 , 再回到一個貪婪和自我主義的人生 , 而是每天都在做 , 你從你的世界的中心 , 把自己放在那裡 , 然後你超越你自己 。
and it brings you into the presence of what's been called god , nirvana , rama , tao .	它帶你進入了所謂的 「 神 」 、 「 nirvana、rama、tao 」 的存在 。
something that goes beyond what we know in our egobound existence .	超越我們對自我的了解 。
but you know you'd never know it a lot of the time , that this was so central to the religious life .	但你知道你永遠都不知道 , 這對宗教生活是非常重要的 。
because with a few wonderful exceptions , very often when religious people come together , religious leaders come together , they're arguing about abstruse doctrines or uttering a council of hatred or inveighing against homosexuality or something of that sort .	因為有一些美好的例外 , 通常當宗教人士聚集在一起時 , 宗教領袖會聚集在一起 , 他們在爭論抽象的教義 , 或是說出仇恨或對同性戀或某種程度的同性戀 。
often people don't really want to be compassionate .	通常人們並不想要有同情心 。
i sometimes see when i'm speaking to a congregation of religious people a sort of mutinous expression crossing their faces because people often want to be right instead .	有時候我會看到 , 當我和一群宗教人士說話時 , 我會看到 , 一群獨立的表情會跨越他們的臉 , 因為人們通常會想要做對的事 。
and that of course defeats the object of the exercise .	這當然會擊敗運動的物體 。
now why was i so grateful to ted ?	為什麼我這麼感激ted呢 ?
because they took me very gently from my booklined study and brought me into the 21st century , enabling me to speak to a much , much wider audience than i could have ever conceived .	因為他們從我的書籍研究中帶我到21世紀 , 讓我能和一個比我想像的更廣的觀眾說話 。
because i feel an urgency about this .	因為我對此感到緊急 。
if we don't manage to implement the golden rule globally , so that we treat all peoples , wherever and whoever they may be , as though they were as important as ourselves , i doubt that we'll have a viable world to hand on to the next generation .	如果我們不辦法在全球實施黃金法則 , 這樣我們才能對待所有人 , 不論他們在哪裡 , 不論他們在哪裡 , 我都懷疑我們將會有一個可行的世界 , 把下一代交給下一代 。
the task of our time , one of the great tasks of our time , is to build a global society , as i said , where people can live together in peace .	我們這個時代的任務之一 , 是建立一個全球社會 , 如我所說的 , 在那裡 , 人們可以在和平生活在一起 。
and the religions that should be making a major contribution are instead seen as part of the problem .	而應該要做出重大貢獻的宗教卻被視為是問題的一部分 。
and of course it's not just religious people who believe in the golden rule .	當然 , 這不僅是宗教信仰黃金法則的人 。
this is the source of all morality , this imaginative act of empathy , putting yourself in the place of another .	這是所有道德的來源 , 這種想像性的行動 , 讓自己陷入另一個地方 。
and so we have a choice , it seems to me .	所以 , 我們有一個選擇 , 似乎對我來說是如此 。
we can either go on bringing out or emphasizing the dogmatic and intolerant aspects of our faith , or we can go back to the rabbis . rabbi hillel , the older contemporary of jesus , who , when asked by a pagan to sum up the whole of jewish teaching while he stood on one leg , said , " that which is hateful to you , do not do to your neighbor .	我們要不就是要帶出或強調我們的信仰 , 要麼我們回到拉比山脈 。 拉比希爾 , 他是耶穌的當代人 , 他要求一個猶太教教導他在一腿上挺身而出 , 說: 「 那些仇恨你 , 不要對你的鄰居做事 。
that is the torah and everything else is only commentary . "	這就是托拉 , 其他的都只是留言 。 」
and the rabbis and the early fathers of the church who said that any interpretation of scripture that bred hatred and disdain was illegitimate .	拉比斯和教堂的早期父親說 , 任何關於經文的詮釋 , 都是違法的 。
and we need to revive that spirit .	我們需要復興這精神 。
and it's not just going to happen because a spirit of love wafts us down .	這不只會發生 , 因為愛的精神讓我們失望 。
we have to make this happen , and we can do it with the modern communications that ted has introduced .	我們必須實現這一點 , 我們可以用ted所引導的現代溝通來實現 。
already i've been tremendously heartened at the response of all our partners .	我已經對所有伴侶的回應感到非常深刻 。
in singapore , we have a group going to use the charter to heal divisions recently that have sprung up in singaporean society , and some members of the parliament want to implement it politically .	在新加坡 , 我們有一群人要用章節來治療新加坡社會的分歧 , 議會的成員也想在政治上實施 。
in malaysia , there is going to be an art exhibition in which leading artists are going to be taking people , young people , and showing them that compassion also lies at the root of all art .	在馬來西亞 , 將會有一場藝術展覽 , 引領藝術家會帶領人們 , 年輕人 , 讓他們看到同情心也是所有藝術的根源 。
throughout europe , the muslim communities are holding events and discussions , are discussing the centrality of compassion in islam and in all faiths .	在歐洲 , 穆斯林社區都舉辦了事件和討論 , 討論的是伊斯蘭和所有信仰中央同情心 。
but it can't stop there . it can't stop with the launch .	但它不能停止 。 它不能停止發射 。
religious teaching , this is where we've gone so wrong , concentrating solely on believing abstruse doctrines .	宗教教導 , 這就是我們錯了的地方 , 只專注於相信抽象教條 。
religious teaching must always lead to action .	宗教教導一定會導致行動 。
and i intend to work on this till my dying day .	直到我的死日 , 我就要努力工作 。
and i want to continue with our partners to do two things educate and stimulate compassionate thinking .	我想繼續和我們的夥伴一起做兩件事 , 教育和刺激同情心思考 。
education because we've so dropped out of compassion .	教育是因為我們失去了同情心 。
people often think it simply means feeling sorry for somebody .	人們通常認為這只是對某人感到抱歉 。
but of course you don't understand compassion if you're just going to think about it .	但如果你想一想的話 , 你當然不了解同情心 。
you also have to do it .	你也得這麼做 。
i want them to get the media involved because the media are crucial in helping to dissolve some of the stereotypical views we have of other people , which are dividing us from one another .	我希望他們能讓媒體參與 , 因為媒體是很重要的 , 協助我們解開一些我們對別人的刻板印象 , 把我們從中分開 。
the same applies to educators .	教育家也一樣 。
i'd like youth to get a sense of the dynamism , the dynamic and challenge of a compassionate lifestyle .	我希望年輕人能感受到動態主義、動態和挑戰同情心的生活方式 。
and also see that it demands acute intelligence , not just a gooey feeling .	同時也看到它需要敏銳的智能 , 不單單單是優美的感覺 。
i'd like to call upon scholars to explore the compassionate theme in their own and in other people's traditions .	我想打電話給學者 , 去探索他們自己和其他人傳統中的同情心主題 。
and perhaps above all , to encourage a sensitivity about uncompassionate speaking , so that because people have this charter , whatever their beliefs or lack of them , they feel empowered to challenge uncompassionate speech , disdainful remarks from their religious leaders , their political leaders , from the captains of industry .	或許最重要的是 , 為了鼓勵不熱情的說話 , 為了鼓勵大家 , 不論他們的信仰或缺乏信仰 , 他們都覺得有能力挑戰不熱情的言論 , 來自他們宗教領袖、政治領袖 , 來自工業界的首長 。
because we can change the world , we have the ability .	因為我們可以改變世界 , 我們有能力 。
i would never have thought of putting the charter online .	我從來沒有想過要把這篇章放在網路上 。
i was still stuck in the old world of a whole bunch of boffins sitting together in a room and issuing yet another arcane statement .	我仍然被困在舊世界裡 , 一大群人坐在房間裡 , 一起發表另一種形容 。
and ted introduced me to a whole new way of thinking and presenting ideas .	ted向我介紹了一個全新的思考方式 , 展示想法 。
because that is what is so wonderful about ted .	因為這正是ted的美妙之處 。
in this room , all this expertise , if we joined it all together , we could change the world .	在這個房間裡 , 所有的專業知識 , 如果我們把這些都加在一起 , 我們就能改變世界 。
and of course the problems sometimes seem insuperable .	當然 , 有時候問題似乎是不可思議的 。
but i'd just like to quote , finish at the end with a reference to a british author , an oxford author whom i don't quote very often , c . s . lewis .	但我想引用的話 , 最後用英國作者的參考 , 牛津的作者我不常引用路易斯.路易斯的話 。
but he wrote one thing that stuck in my mind ever since i read it when i was a schoolgirl .	但他寫了一件事 , 從我讀書的時候就一直困在我腦海裡 。
it's in his book " the four loves . "	在他的書《四愛》中 。
he said that he distinguished between erotic love , when two people gaze , spellbound , into each other's eyes .	他說他分辨了愛情 , 當兩個人聚焦、拼字 , 彼此的眼睛 。
and then he compared that to friendship , when two people stand side by side , as it were , shoulder to shoulder , with their eyes fixed on a common goal .	接著 , 他比較了友誼 , 當兩個人站在旁邊 , 肩膀肩膀 , 雙眼固定在共同目標上 。
we don't have to fall in love with each other , but we can become friends .	我們不需要愛彼此 , 但我們能成為朋友 。
and i am convinced .	我深信 。
i felt it very strongly during our little deliberations at vevey , that when people of all different persuasions come together , working side by side for a common goal , differences melt away .	在我們對vey的小小小小的解讀中 , 我感覺非常強烈 , 當所有不同的說服者聚在一起 , 一起工作 , 一邊為共同目標而努力 , 差異會消失 。
and we learn amity .	我們也學會了野心 。
and we learn to live together and to get to know one another .	我們學會一起生活 , 去認識彼此 。
thank you very much .	謝謝大家 。

they keep on motoring towards the campo de' fiori , which they soon reach . ajax the dog is put in a basket and lowered with a list of food into the marketplace , which flourishes there until about one in the afternoon , and then is completely removed and doesn't appear again until six or seven the following morning .	牠們持續朝馬馬波的方向前進 , 牠們很快就到達了 。 阿賈克斯把狗放在籃子裡 , 把一份食物列入市場中 , 在那裡繁盛 , 直到下午一次 , 然後完全消失 , 直到六、七個早上才出現 。
anyway , the pooch gets back to the dirigible with the stuff .	總之 , 大便會回歸這些東西 。
unfortunately , when she goes to unwrap the prosciutto , ajax makes a lunge for it .	不幸的是 , 當她去解開檢體時 , ajax為它做一個午餐 。
she's managed to save the prosciutto , but in the process she loses the tablecloth , which you can see flying away in the upper lefthand corner .	她成功拯救了代理人 , 但在她失去桌布的過程中 , 你可以看到在左上角飛走 。
they continue without their tablecloth , looking for a place to land this thing so that they can actually have lunch .	他們不用桌布繼續 , 尋找一個地方降落這個東西 , 讓它們真的可以吃午餐 。
they eventually discover a huge wall that's filled with small holes , ideal for docking a dirigible because you've got a place to tie up .	他們最終發現了一道巨大的牆 , 充滿了小洞的理想 , 因為你有地方可以連接起來 。
turns out to be the exterior wall that part of it that remains of the coliseum , so they park themselves there and have a terrific lunch and have a spectacular view .	結果發現 , 是哥倫坡剩下的那一部分的外牆 , 所以他們自己停在那裡 , 吃了很棒的午餐 , 有一個很棒的景象 。
at the end of lunch , they untie the anchor , they set off through the baths of caracalla and over the walls of the city and then an abandoned gatehouse and decide to take one more look at the pyramid of cestius , which has this lightning rod on top .	在午餐結束時 , 他們解開了房間 , 穿過卡卡卡拉的浴室 , 穿過城市的牆壁 , 然後一個廢棄的大門 , 決定再來看看cestius的金字塔 , 上面有個閃電板在上面 。
unfortunately , that's a problem: they get a little too close , and when you're in a dirigible you have to be very careful about spikes .	不幸的是 , 那是個問題:他們太靠近了 , 而當你在潛意識中 , 你必須非常謹慎地處理漏洞 。
so that sort of brings her little story to a conclusion .	所以這會讓她的故事成為一個結論 。
marcello , on the other hand , is sort of a lazy guy , but he's not due at work until about noon .	另一方面 , 馬可洛是個懶惰的傢伙 , 但他在工作之前 , 並不是在工作 。
so , the alarm goes off and it's five to 12 or so .	所以 , 警報響起了 , 只剩5到12歲 。
he gets up , leaps onto his scooter , races through the city past the church of santa maria della pace , down the alleys , through the streets that tourists may be wandering through , disturbing the quiet backstreet life of rome at every turn .	他站起來 , 跳上他的混亂 , 穿過城市的種族 , 穿越聖馬拉雅山脈的教堂 , 走下巷子 , 穿過遊說的街道 , 可能每次都會穿過羅馬的安靜背景生活 。
that speed with which he is moving , i hope i have suggested in this little image , which , again , can be turned around and read from both sides because there's text on the bottom and text on the top , one of which is upside down in this image .	他移動的速度 , 我希望我在這個小圖片中提出 , 同樣的 , 可以從兩邊轉過來閱讀 , 因為底部的文字和文字在上面 , 其中一個是顛倒的圖像 。
so , he keeps on moving , approaching an unsuspecting waiter who is trying to deliver two plates of linguine in a delicate white wine clam sauce to diners who are sitting at a table just outside of a restaurant in the street .	所以 , 他繼續走下去 , 接近一個不可思議的服務生 , 他試圖在一個精細的白葡萄酒店裡遞送兩塊語言的袋狼醬 , 到坐在餐廳外面的餐廳 。
waiter catches on , but it's too late .	服務生接上了 , 但太遲了 。
and marcello keeps moving in his scooter .	marcello繼續走進他的混亂 。
everything he sees from this point on is slightly affected by the linguine , but keeps on moving because this guy's got a job to do .	從這個點來看 , 他所看到的一切都稍微受到語言的影響 , 但繼續繼續下去 , 因為這個人有工作要做 。
removes some scaffolding . one of the reasons rome remains the extraordinary place it is that because of scaffolding and the determination to maintain the fabric , it is a city that continues to grow and adapt to the needs of the particular time in which it finds itself , or we find it .	除去一些支架 。 羅馬的其中一個原因是 , 因為支架和決心要維持結構 , 它是一個持續成長和適應特定時間的需求 , 或我們發現它本身的需求 。
right through the piazza della rotonda , in front of the pantheon again wreaking havoc and finally getting to work .	在萬神廟前面 , 皮亞薩•德拉•羅頓達 , 在萬神廟再次爆發 , 終於開始工作 。
marcello , as it turns out , is the driver of the number 64 bus , and if you've been on the number 64 bus , you know that it's driven with the same kind of exuberance as marcello demonstrated on his scooter .	結果發現 , 馬可洛是第64輛巴士的驅動力 , 如果你曾經搭過64輛巴士 , 你就知道它的驅動力和馬爾細胞在他的分數上展現出的差異 。
and finally carletto . you see his apartment in the upper lefthand corner .	最後 , 卡莉托 , 你可以看到他左上角的公寓 。
he's looking at his table ; he's planning to propose this evening to his girlfriend of 40 years , and he wants it to be perfect .	他看著他的桌子 , 計劃今晚提議他的女朋友40年 , 他希望它能完美 。
he's got candles out , he's got flowers in the middle and he's trying to figure out where to put the plates and the glasses .	他拿出蠟燭 , 中間有花 , 他正在想辦法把盤子和玻璃放在哪裡 。
but he's not happy ; something's wrong .	但他不快樂 ; 有些事是錯的 。
the phone rings anyway , he's called to the palazzo .	總之 , 電話響了 , 他被叫到帕拉佐 。
he saunters he saunters at a good clip , but as compared to all the traveling we've just seen , he's sauntering .	他在一段很棒的片段拍攝 , 但和我們剛剛看到的所有旅程相比 , 他正在散播 。
everybody knows carletto , because he's in entertainment , actually ; he's in television .	大家都知道卡爾圖 , 因為他在娛樂裡 , 其實他在電視上 。
he's actually in television repair , which is why people know him .	他其實是在電視修復室 , 這就是為什麼人們認識他 。
so they all have his number .	所以他們都有他的數字 。
he arrives at the palazzo , arrives at the big front door .	他抵達帕拉索 , 抵達大門 。
enters the courtyard and talks to the custodian , who tells him that there's been a disaster in the palazzo ; nobody's tvs are working and there's a big soccer game coming up , and the crowd is getting a little restless and a little nervous .	進入法庭 , 和顧客談話 , 他告訴他 , 帕拉佐有場災難 ; 沒有人的電視正在運作 , 有一個很大的足球比賽出現 , 群眾越來越不安 , 有點緊張 。
he goes down to the basement and starts to check the wiring , and then gradually works his way up to the top of the building , apartment by apartment , checking every television , checking every connection , hoping to find out what this problem is .	他走到地下室 , 開始檢查天線 , 然後逐漸地工作到建築物的頂端 , 公寓的位置 , 檢查每一間電視 , 檢查每一個連結 , 希望找出問題是什麼 。
he works his way up , finally , the grand staircase and then a smaller staircase until he reaches the attic .	他終於成功了 , 終於 , 巨大的樓梯 , 接著是一間小樓梯 , 直到他到達極點 。
he opens the window of the attic , of course , and there's a tablecloth wrapped around the building's television antenna .	當然 , 他開了房間的窗戶 , 當然 , 還有一張桌布 , 圍繞著建築的電視天線 。
he removes it , the problems are solved , everybody in the palazzo is happy .	他移除它 , 問題解決了 , 在帕拉茲索的每個人都很快樂 。
and of course , he also solves his own problem .	當然 , 他也解決了自己的問題 。
all he has to do now , with a perfect table , is wait for her to arrive .	他現在只需要用一個完美的桌子 , 等著她來到那裡 。
that was the first attempt , but it didn't seem substantial enough to convey whatever it was i wanted to convey about rome .	那是第一次嘗試 , 但似乎沒有足夠傳達我想要傳達的羅馬是什麼 。
so i thought , well , i'll just do piazzas , and i'll get inside and underneath and i'll show these things growing and show why they're shaped the way they are and so on .	所以我想 , 好吧 , 我會做帕薩斯 , 然後我會進去 , 下面我會展示這些東西正在成長 , 展現出它們的形狀 , 以此類推 。
and then i thought , that's too complicated . no , i'll just take my favorite bits and pieces and i'll put them inside the pantheon but keep the scale , so you can see the top of sant'ivo and the pyramid of cestius and the tempietto of bramante all side by side in this amazing space .	然後我想 , 這太複雜了 。 不 , 我把我最喜歡的位元和碎片放進萬神廟裡 , 但保持尺度 , 你可以看到聖西弗和塞西歐金字塔的頂端 , 和巴拉曼神廟的座位都放在這個很棒的空間裡 。
now that's one drawing , so i thought maybe it's time for piranesi to meet escher .	這是一張圖 , 所以我想也許是皮拉尼去見escher的時候了 。
you see that i'm beginning to really lose control here and also hope .	你可以看到我開始失去控制權 , 同時也失去了希望 。
there's a very thin blue line of exhaust that sort of runs through this thing that would be kind of the trail that holds it all together .	有一條非常薄的藍線 , 穿過這個東西 , 有點像是把所有東西黏在一起的軌跡 。
then i thought , " wait a minute , what am i doing ? "	然後我想: 「 等等 , 我在做什麼 ? 」
a book is not only a neat way of collecting and storing information , it's a series of layers .	一本書不只是收集和儲存資訊的好方法 , 它是一系列的層次 。
i mean , you always peel one layer off another ; we think of them as pages , doing it a certain way .	我的意思是 , 你總是把一層一層剝下來 , 我們把它們當成頁面 , 以某種方式做 。
but think of them as layers . i mean , rome is a place of layers horizontal layers , vertical layers and i thought , well just peeling off a page would allow me to if i got you thinking about it the right way would allow me to sort of show you the depth of layers .	但把它們想成一層層 。 我的意思是 , 羅馬是一層層層水層 , 垂直層層 , 我想 , 把頁面剝下來 , 如果我用正確的方式來思考 , 我可以給你們看一層層的深度 。
the stucco on the walls of most of the buildings in rome covers the scars ; the scars of centuries of change as these structures have been adapted rather than being torn down .	羅馬大部份建築物的牆壁覆蓋了疤痕數世紀以來 , 當這些結構被適應時 , 改變的疤痕已經被摧毀 , 而不是被摧毀 。
if i do a foldout page on the lefthand side and let you just unfold it , you see behind it what i mean by scar tissue .	如果我在左手邊做個摺疊頁 , 讓你把它放開 , 你就會看到我所謂的害怕組織 。
you can see that in 1635 , it became essential to make smaller windows because the bad guys were coming or whatever .	你可以看到 , 在1635年 , 製造小窗戶是必要的 , 因為壞人來了或其他東西 。
adaptations all get buried under the stucco .	適應一切都被埋在水底下 。
i could peel out a page of this palazzo to show you what's going on inside of it .	我可以把這帕拉索的一頁剝出來 , 讓你們看看裡面發生了什麼事 。
but more importantly , i could also show you what it looks like at the corner of one of those magnificent buildings with all the massive stone blocks , or the fake stone blocks done with brick and stucco , which is more often the case .	但 , 更重要的是 , 我也能向你們展示在那些偉大的建築物的角落 , 有大量的石塊 , 或假石塊 , 用磚塊和石油做成的 , 通常是這樣 。
so it becomes slightly threedimensional .	所以它變得有點三度空間 。
i could take you down one of those narrow little streets into one of those surprising piazzas by using a double gate fold double foldout page which , if you were like me reading a popup book as a child , you hopefully stick your head into .	我可以把一個狹窄的小街道帶到一個令人驚訝的黑猩猩之一 , 用雙重大門摺疊頁面 , 如果你像我小時候讀一本彈起的書 , 你希望能把你的頭伸進去 。
you wrap the pages around your head and are in that piazza for that brief period of time .	你把頁面包在你的頭上 , 用在那短暫的時間內 。
and i've really not done anything much more complicated than make foldout pages .	我真的沒做任何比摺紙更複雜的事 。
but then i thought , maybe i could be simpler here .	但接著 , 我想 , 也許我可以比較簡單 。
let's look at the pantheon and the piazza della rotonda in front of it .	咱們來看看萬神廟和前面的羅頓達斯.羅頓達 。
here's a book completely wide open .	這是一本完全開放的書
ok , if i don't open the book the whole way , if i just open it 90 degrees , we're looking down the front of the pantheon , and we're looking sort of at the top , more or less down on the square .	好吧 , 如果我不用整本書 , 如果我把它打開90度 , 我們就在看著萬神廟的前面 , 我們看到的是最上方的 , 或下面的 。
and if i turn the book the other way , we're looking across the square at the front of the pantheon .	如果我把這本書換成另一種方式 , 我們會在萬神廟前面看到正方形 。
no foldouts , no tricks just a book that isn't open the whole way .	沒有摺疊術 , 沒有把戲只是一本不打開的書 。
that seemed promising . i thought , maybe i'll do it inside and i can even combine the foldouts with the only partially opened book .	這似乎很有希望 。 我心想 , 也許我會在裡面做 , 我甚至可以把摺疊術和一部分開放的書做結合 。
so we get inside the pantheon and it grows and so on and so forth .	所以 , 我們進入萬神廟 , 它會不斷地成長 。
and i thought , maybe i'm on the right track , but it sort of lost its human quality .	我心想 , 也許我在正確的軌道上 , 但它有點失去了它的人類特質 。
so i went back to the notion of story , which is always a good thing to have if you're trying to get people to pay attention to a book and pick up information along the way .	所以 , 我回到故事的概念 , 如果你想要讓大家注意一本書 , 並沿途收集資訊 , 總是一件好事 。
" pigeon's progress " struck me as a catchy title .	「 鴿子的進步 」 把我當作捕撈標題 。
if it was a homing pigeon , it would be called " homer's odyssey . "	假如它是個宿主鴿子 , 它會被稱為 「 荷馬的奧德西 」 。
but it was the journey of the . . .	但那就是這段旅程......
i mean , if a title works , use it . but it would be a journey that went through rome and showed all the things that i like about rome .	我的意思是 , 如果標題能運作 , 使用它 , 但那會是一趟旅程 , 穿過羅馬 , 展現出我喜歡的東西 。
it's a pigeon sitting on top of a church .	這是一隻鴿子坐在教堂的頂端 。
goes off during the day and does normal pigeon stuff . comes back , the whole place is covered with scaffolding and green netting and there's no way this pigeon can get home .	白天離開 , 做正常的鴿子 。 回來了 , 整個地方都被支架和綠色網路覆蓋 , 沒有辦法回家 。
so it's a homeless pigeon now and it's going to have to find another place to live , and that allows me to go through my catalog of favorite things , and we start with the tall ones and so on .	它現在是個無家可歸的鴿子 , 它必須找到另一個居住的地方 , 這讓我可以通過我最喜歡的東西的目錄 , 我們從最高的鴿子開始 。
maybe it has to go back and live with family members ; that's not always a good thing , but it does sort of bring pigeons together again .	也許它必須回去和家人一起生活 , 這不見得一定是件好事 , 但它會再次將鴿子聚在一起 。
and i thought , that's sort of interesting , but maybe there's a person who should be involved in this in some way .	我心想 , 這有點有趣 , 但或許有一個人應該以某種方式參與其中 。
so i kind of came up with this old guy who spends his life looking after sick pigeons .	所以我想出了一個老人 , 他花了一輩子照顧病鴿 。
he'll go anywhere to get them dangerous places and whatnot and they become really friends with this guy , and learn to do tricks for him and entertain him at lunchtime and stuff like that .	他會到任何地方 , 讓他們危險的地方 , 是什麼 , 他們會和這個人交朋友 , 學會為他打招呼 , 用午餐時間娛樂他 , 等等 。
there's a real bond that develops between this old man and these pigeons .	這個老人和這些鴿子之間有一個真正的聯繫 。
but unfortunately he gets sick . he gets really sick at the end of the story .	但不幸的是 , 他生病了 。 在故事結束後 , 他生病了 。
he's taught them to spell his name , which is aldo .	他教他們拼他的名字 , 就是阿爾多 。
they show up one day after three or four days of not seeing him he lives in this little garret and they spell his name and fly around .	有一天 , 三四天後 , 他們沒有看到他住在這個小小的格言中 , 他們把他的名字拼起來 , 四處飛來 。
and he finally gets enough strength together to climb up the ladder onto the roof , and all the pigeons , a la red balloon , are there waiting for him and they carry him off over the walls of the city .	他終於得到足夠的力量 , 讓梯子爬上屋頂 , 所有的鴿子 , 一顆紅色的氣球 , 等著他 , 把他帶到城市的牆上 。
and i forgot to mention this: whenever he lost a pigeon , he would take that pigeon out beyond the walls of the city .	我忘了提到這一點:每當他失去鴿子時 , 他就會把鴿子拿出來超越城市的牆壁 。
in the old roman custom , the dead were never buried within the walls .	在古羅馬的習俗中 , 死者從未埋葬在牆壁中 。
and i thought that's a really cheery story .	我覺得這是個非常歡呼的故事 。
. that's really going to go a long way .	這真的會走很長的路 。
so anyway , i went through . . . and again , if packaging doesn't work and if the stories aren't going anywhere , i just come up with titles and hope that a title will sort of kick me off in the right direction .	總之 , 我走過...再一次 , 如果包裝沒有用 , 如果故事沒有去任何地方 , 我只是想出標題 , 希望一個頭銜會把我趕出正確的方向 。
and sometimes it does focus me enough and i'll even do a title page .	有時 , 它會讓我夠專注 , 我甚至會做一個標題 。
so , these are all title pages that eventually led me to the solution i settled on , which is the story of a young woman who sends a message on a homing pigeon she lives outside the walls of the city of rome to someone in the city .	所以 , 這些都是標題的頁 , 最終引導我解決我安定的解決方案 , 這是一位年輕女子的故事 , 她在羅馬城牆外傳送訊息給城市裡的人 。
and the pigeon is flying down above the appian way here .	鴿子就在俄國的上方飛過來 。
you can see the tombs and pines and so on and so forth along the way .	你可以看到番茄醬和松鼠等等 。
if you see the red line , you are seeing the trail of the pigeon ; if you don't see the red line , you are the pigeon .	如果你看到紅線 , 你會看到鴿子的軌跡 ; 如果你看不到紅線 , 你就是鴿子 。
and it becomes necessary and possible , at this point , to try to convey what that sense would be like of flying over the city without actually moving .	在這個時點 , 它變得必要且有可能 , 試圖傳達在城市中飛行的感覺 , 沒有真正移動的感覺 。
past the pyramid of cestius these will seem very familiar to you , even if you haven't been to rome recently past the gatehouse .	在塞西斯提烏斯的金字塔 , 似乎對你來說很熟悉 , 即使你最近還沒去過大門 。
this is something that's a little bit unusual .	這有點不尋常 。
this pigeon does something that most homing pigeons do not do: it takes the scenic route , which was a device that i felt was necessary to actually extend this book beyond about four pages .	這隻鴿子做的事 , 大部分的宿主鴿子都做不到:它採用了彩虹路線 , 那是我覺得需要延伸這本書 , 超越四頁 。
so , we circle around the coliseum , past the church of santa maria in cosmedin and the temple of hercules towards the river .	所以 , 我們繞著競技場繞過聖母堂 , 穿過了聖瑪雅教堂 , 穿過了聖母堂的神廟 , 朝著河流前進 。
we almost collide with the cornice of the palazzo farnese designed by michelangelo , built of stone taken from the coliseum narrow escape .	我們幾乎碰撞了palazofrangelo所設計的石頭 , 由米開朗基羅所製成的石頭從哥倫坡狹窄的逃脫 。
we swoop down over the campo de' fiori .	我們沿著柬埔寨的毛利游過了 。
this is one of those things i show to my students because it's a complete bastardization a denial of any rules of perspective .	這是我向學生展示的其中一件事 , 因為這完全是違反任何觀點的規則 。
the only rule of perspective that i think matters is if it looks believable , you've succeeded .	我認為唯一重要的規則是 , 如果看上去是可信的 , 你就成功了 。
but you try and figure out where the vanishing points meet here ; a couple are on mars and a couple of others in cremona .	但你試著去弄清楚這些消失的點在哪裡 , 有幾個在火星上 , 還有一些在克雷莫納州的其他地方 。
but into the piazza in front of santa maria della pace , where invariably a soccer game is going on , and we're hit by a soccer ball .	但在聖馬拉雅山脈的前方 , 一個足球賽正在進行 , 我們被足球球撞擊 。
now this is a terrible illustration of being hit by a soccer ball .	這是個很糟糕的例子 , 被足球撞到 。
i have all the pieces: there's santa maria della pace , there's a soccer ball , there's a little bit of a bird's wing nothing's happening , so i had to rethink it .	我有所有的作品:馬拉雅的速度 , 有足球 , 有些鳥的翅膀沒有發生 , 所以我必須重新思考 。
and if you do want to see santa maria della pace , these books are really flexible , incredibly interactive just turn it around and look at it the other way .	如果你想要看到聖誕節的速度 , 這些書真的很靈活 , 非常互動 , 把它轉過頭 , 用另一種方式來看它 。
through the alley , we can see the impact is captured in the red line .	透過巷子 , 我們可以看到紅線捕捉到的影響 。
and then bird manages to pull itself together past this medieval tower one of the few remaining medieval towers towards the church of sant'agnese and around the dome looking down into piazza navona which we've already mentioned and seen and flown over a couple of times ; there's the bernini statue of the four rivers and then past the wonderful borromini sant'ivo , stopping just long enough on the 26foot diameter oculus of the pantheon to catch our breath .	接著 , 鳥類在中世紀大樓上把自己拉過來 , 只有少數幾個中世紀高塔 , 直到聖阿格尼斯教堂和周圍的圓頂向下看 , 我們已經提到過、看過、流過幾次 ; 還有伯尼雕像的四個河流 , 經過了美妙的邊緣聖母聖母聖誕節 , 在26英尺深處停止了 , 足以抓住我們的呼吸 。
and then we can swoop inside and around ; and because we're flying , we don't really have to worry about gravity at this particular moment in time , so this drawing can be oriented in any way on the page .	然後我們就可以在裡面游動 , 因為我們在飛行 , 我們不需要擔心重力在這個特定的時刻 , 所以這幅圖可以在頁面上以任何方式呈現 。
we get a little exuberant as we pass gesu ; it's not surprising to sort of mimic the architecture in this way .	當我們通過gu時 , 我們得到了一點出乎意料的 。 這樣模仿建築並不讓人意外 。
past the wonderful wall filled with the juxtaposition that i was talking about ; beautiful carvings set into the walls above the neon " ristorante " sign , and so on .	過去的美麗牆上充滿了我剛剛提到的混合體 ; 美麗的雕刻設定在尼子《暴風》的牆壁上 , 等等 。
and eventually , we arrive at the courtyard of the palazzo , which is our destination .	最終 , 我們抵達帕拉茲索的庭院 , 也就是我們的目的地 。
straight up through the courtyard into a little window into the attic , where somebody is working at the drawing board .	直接穿過庭院 , 進入一個小窗口 , 在那裡有人在畫板上工作 。
he removes the message from the leg of the bird ; this is what it says .	他把信息從鳥的腳上移開 , 這是它所說的 。
as we look at the drawing board , we see what he's working on is , in fact , a map of the journey that the pigeon has just taken , and the red line extends through all the sights .	當我們看畫板時 , 我們看到他正在做的事 , 事實上 , 是鴿子剛拍的地圖 , 紅線穿越了所有的視覺 。
and if you want the information , so that we complete this cycle of understanding , all you have to do is read these paragraphs .	如果你想要資訊 , 所以我們完成了理解的循環 , 你只需要讀這些段落 。
thank you very much .	謝謝大家 。
mit researcher skylar tibbits works on selfassembly the idea that instead of building something , we can create materials that build themselves , much the way a strand of dna zips itself together . it's a big concept at early stages ; tibbits shows us three inthelab projects that hint at what a selfassembling future might look like .	麻省理工學院研究者skylartibbit在自組裝的概念上運作 , 取而代之 , 我們能創造出一些東西 , 來建立它們自己 , 讓dna自己形成的方式 。 這是早期階段的一個大概念 ; tibbit展示了我們三個 「 thelab 」 的專案 , 暗示了 「 自我組裝未來 」 的樣子 。
skylar tibbits: can we make things that make themselves ?	skylartebbit:我們能否製造出能自動製造的東西 ?
today i'd like to show you the future of the way we make things .	今天我想向各位展示我們製造東西的方式 。
i believe that soon our buildings and machines will be selfassembling , replicating and repairing themselves .	我相信 , 很快我們的建築物和機器就會自行組合、複製、修復它們 。
so i'm going to show you what i believe is the current state of manufacturing , and then compare that to some natural systems .	我要給你們看我相信的就是目前製造的狀態 , 然後和一些自然系統做比較 。
so in the current state of manufacturing , we have skyscrapers two and a half years [of assembly time] , 500 , 000 to a million parts , fairly complex , new , exciting technologies in steel , concrete , glass .	在目前的製造狀態 , 我們有摩天大樓兩年半的組裝時間 , 五十萬到一百萬個零件 , 相當複雜、更令人興奮的新科技在鋼鐵、混凝土、玻璃 。
we have exciting machines that can take us into space five years [of assembly time] , 2 . 5 million parts .	我們有令人興奮的機器可以將我們帶到太空中五年--組裝時間 , 250萬個零件 。
but on the other side , if you look at the natural systems , we have proteins that have two million types , can fold in 10 , 000 nanoseconds , or dna with three billion base pairs we can replicate in roughly an hour .	但另一方面 , 如果你看一下自然系統 , 我們有兩百萬種類型的蛋白質 , 可以折疊一萬奈秒 , 或dna有三十億個鹼基對 , 我們可以在大約一個小時複製 。
so there's all of this complexity in our natural systems , but they're extremely efficient , far more efficient than anything we can build , far more complex than anything we can build .	所以 , 在我們的自然系統中 , 所有這些複雜性 , 但它們非常有效率 , 比我們能建造的任何東西都有效率 , 遠比任何我們建造的東西還要複雜 。
they're far more efficient in terms of energy .	能源方面的效率更高 。
they hardly ever make mistakes .	他們幾乎沒有犯錯 。
and they can repair themselves for longevity .	他們可以修復自己長壽 。
so there's something super interesting about natural systems .	所以 , 天然系統有個超有趣的東西 。
and if we can translate that into our built environment , then there's some exciting potential for the way that we build things .	如果我們能將它轉化成我們的建設環境 , 那麼我們創造東西的方式有一些令人興奮的潛力 。
and i think the key to that is selfassembly .	我認為關鍵在於自我組裝 。
so if we want to utilize selfassembly in our physical environment , i think there's four key factors .	所以 , 如果我們想要在我們的身體環境中自行組裝 , 我認為有四個關鍵因素 。
the first is that we need to decode all of the complexity of what we want to build so our buildings and machines .	首先 , 我們需要解碼所有我們想要建造的東西的複雜性 , 來解碼我們的建築和機器 。
and we need to decode that into simple sequences basically the dna of how our buildings work .	我們需要把這些解碼成簡單的序列 , 基本上是我們建築物如何運作的dna 。
then we need programmable parts that can take that sequence and use that to fold up , or reconfigure .	接著 , 我們需要可編程的零件 , 可以把序列摺疊起來 , 或重新配置 。
we need some energy that's going to allow that to activate , allow our parts to be able to fold up from the program .	我們需要一些能量來啟動它 , 讓我們的零件能夠從計畫中摺疊起來 。
and we need some type of error correction redundancy to guarantee that we have successfully built what we want .	我們需要某種類型的錯誤修正 , 來保證我們成功地建造出我們想要的東西 。
so i'm going to show you a number of projects that my colleagues and i at mit are working on to achieve this selfassembling future .	所以我要給你們看一些我和我在麻省理工學院的同事正在努力實現這個自我組合的未來 。
the first two are the macrobot and decibot .	前兩位是宏觀機器人和丹麥人 。
so these projects are largescale reconfigurable robots 8 ft . , 12 ft . long proteins .	這些計畫是大規模重新設計的機器人8英尺 , 12呎長的蛋白質 。
they're embedded with mechanical electrical devices , sensors .	他們嵌入了機械電子設備、感應器 。
you decode what you want to fold up into , into a sequence of angles so negative 120 , negative 120 , 0 , 0 , 120 , negative 120 something like that ; so a sequence of angles , or turns , and you send that sequence through the string .	你解碼你想要摺成什麼 , 變成一連串的角度 , 如此負面120、0、120、120、120、負面120 , 像這樣的東西 ; 一連串的角度 , 或旋轉 , 你將序列通過弦 。
each unit takes its message so negative 120 it rotates to that , checks if it got there and then passes it to its neighbor .	每個單位都帶著它的負120個訊息 , 它會旋轉 , 如果它走到那裡 , 然後傳遞給它的鄰居 。
so these are the brilliant scientists , engineers , designers that worked on this project .	這些是傑出的科學家 , 工程師 , 設計師 , 研究這個計畫 。
and i think it really brings to light: is this really scalable ?	我認為這真的會帶來光:這真的很可擴展嗎 ?
i mean , thousands of dollars , lots of man hours made to make this eightfoot robot .	我的意思是 , 數千美金 , 許多人花時間來製造這八英尺的機器人 。
can we really scale this up ? can we really embed robotics into every part ?	我們真的能擴大它嗎 ? 我們能把機器人嵌入每個部分嗎 ?
the next one questions that and looks at passive nature , or passively trying to have reconfiguration programmability .	下一個問題 , 看看被動的大自然 , 或被動地嘗試重新設計程式 。
but it goes a step further , and it tries to have actual computation .	但它更進一步 , 它試圖進行實際的計算 。
it basically embeds the most fundamental building block of computing , the digital logic gate , directly into your parts .	基本上 , 它嵌入了最基本的計算積木 , 數位邏輯大門 , 直接進入你的零件 。
so this is a nand gate .	這是個nand大門 。
you have one tetrahedron which is the gate that's going to do your computing , and you have two input tetrahedrons .	有一個四面體 , 就是蓋茲會做你的計算 , 你有兩個輸入的四面體 。
one of them is the input from the user , as you're building your bricks .	其中一個是使用者的輸入 , 當你在建造你的磚塊時 。
the other one is from the previous brick that was placed .	另外一個是從前幾塊磚塊被放在那裡 。
and then it gives you an output in 3d space .	然後它給你一個輸出在3d空間的輸出 。
so what this means is that the user can start plugging in what they want the bricks to do .	這意味著 , 使用者可以開始加入他們想要的磚塊 。
it computes on what it was doing before and what you said you wanted it to do .	它計算它之前在做什麼 , 以及你說你想要它做什麼 。
and now it starts moving in threedimensional space so up or down .	現在它開始在三維空間中移動 , 或向下移動 。
so on the lefthand side , [1 , 1] input equals 0 output , which goes down .	所以在左手邊 , 輸入等於0輸出 , 輸出就會下降 。
on the righthand side , [0 , 0] input is a 1 output , which goes up .	在右手邊 , 0 , 輸入是1個輸出 , 它會上升 。
and so what that really means is that our structures now contain the blueprints of what we want to build .	這意味著我們的結構現在包含了我們想要建造的東西的藍圖 。
so they have all of the information embedded in them of what was constructed .	所以他們有所有的資訊嵌入其中 , 包含了所構成的 。
so that means that we can have some form of selfreplication .	這意味著我們可以有某種形式的自我複製 。
in this case i call it selfguided replication , because your structure contains the exact blueprints .	在這個例子中 , 我稱它為自動化複製 , 因為你的結構包含了精確的藍圖 。
