if you have errors , you can replace a part .	如果你有錯誤 , 你可以取代一部分 。
all the local information is embedded to tell you how to fix it .	所有地方資訊都嵌入來告訴你如何修復它 。
so you could have something that climbs along and reads it and can output at one to one .	所以你可以有一些可以攀爬的東西 , 閱讀它 , 可以輸出一個到一個 。
it's directly embedded ; there's no external instructions .	它是直接嵌入的 ; 沒有外部的指令 。
so the last project i'll show is called biased chains , and it's probably the most exciting example that we have right now of passive selfassembly systems .	最後一個我要展示的項目叫做 「 偏見鏈 」 , 它可能是我們目前最令人興奮的例子 , 就是被動的自我組裝系統 。
so it takes the reconfigurability and programmability and makes it a completely passive system .	所以 , 它需要重組性和程式設計 , 讓它成為一個完全被動的系統 。
so basically you have a chain of elements .	基本上你有一連串的元素 。
each element is completely identical , and they're biased .	每個元素都完全相同 , 它們是偏見的 。
so each chain , or each element , wants to turn right or left .	所以每一條鏈 , 或每一條元素 , 都想要向右轉或左轉 。
so as you assemble the chain , you're basically programming it .	所以 , 當你組裝鏈時 , 你基本上是在編寫它 。
you're telling each unit if it should turn right or left .	你要告訴每個單位是否應該轉向右或左 。
so when you shake the chain , it then folds up into any configuration that you've programmed in so in this case , a spiral , or in this case , two cubes next to each other .	所以當你搖晃鏈時 , 它會折疊到你設計的任何結構中 , 在這裡 , 螺旋 , 或這個例子 , 兩個立方體相鄰 。
so you can basically program any threedimensional shape or onedimensional , twodimensional up into this chain completely passively .	基本上你可以編寫任何三維形狀或單一的二維形狀 , 完全被動化到這個鏈中 。
so what does this tell us about the future ?	所以 , 這告訴我們未來的什麼 ?
i think that it's telling us that there's new possibilities for selfassembly , replication , repair in our physical structures , our buildings , machines .	我認為它告訴我們 , 對於自我組裝、複製、修復、建築、機器有新的可能性 。
there's new programmability in these parts .	這些部分有新的程式性 。
and from that you have new possibilities for computing .	從那你有新的計算可能性 。
we'll have spatial computing .	我們將會有空間計算 。
imagine if our buildings , our bridges , machines , all of our bricks could actually compute .	想像一下 , 如果我們的建築物、橋樑、機器 , 所有的磚塊都能計算 。
that's amazing parallel and distributed computing power , new design possibilities .	這是很棒的平行和分散式的計算能力 , 新的設計可能性 。
so it's exciting potential for this .	所以這對此是很令人興奮的 。
so i think these projects i've showed here are just a tiny step towards this future , if we implement these new technologies for a new selfassembling world .	所以我認為 , 我在這裡展示的這些專案只是未來的一小步 , 如果我們為新自我組合的世界實施這些新科技 。
we've been to the moon , we've mapped the continents , we've even been to the deepest point in the ocean twice . what's left for the next generation to explore ? biologist and explorer nathan wolfe suggests this answer: almost everything . and we can start , he says , with the world of the unseeably small .	我們去過月球 , 我們繪製了這塊大陸 , 我們甚至去過了海洋最深的一點 。 下一代要探索什麼 ? 生物學家和探索者納森•沃爾夫提出了這個答案:幾乎所有事情 , 我們都可以開始 , 他說 , 在這個不可思議的小世界中 ,
biodiversity , exploration , microbiology , science	生物多樣性、探索、微生物學、科學、科學、科學 。
nathan wolfe: what's left to explore ?	nathanwolfe:還有什麼可以探索的 ?
recently i visited beloit , wisconsin .	最近我拜訪了威斯康辛州的貝洛特 。
and i was there to honor a great 20th century explorer , roy chapman andrews .	我在那裡榮耀一個20世紀的探險家 , 羅伊•查普曼•安德魯斯 。
during his time at the american museum of natural history , andrews led a range of expeditions to uncharted regions , like here in the gobi desert .	在他在美國自然歷史博物館的那段期間 , 安德魯斯帶領了一系列的探險到未知的區域 , 就像在戈比沙漠這裡 。
he was quite a figure .	他是個人物 。
he was later , it's said , the basis of the indiana jones character .	後來他說 , 印第安納瓊斯特徵的基礎 。
and when i was in beloit , wisconsin , i gave a public lecture to a group of middle school students .	當我在威斯康辛州的貝洛特 , 我公開演講給一群中學學生 。
and i'm here to tell you , if there's anything more intimidating than talking here at ted , it'll be trying to hold the attention of a group of a thousand 12yearolds for a 45minute lecture .	我來這裡要告訴各位 , 如果ted的演講比在座各位更嚇人的話 , 它會試著把一群12歲的孩子的注意力放在45分鐘的講座上 。
at the end of the lecture they asked a number of questions , but there was one that's really stuck with me since then .	演講結束後 , 他們問了幾個問題 , 但從那時起 , 有一個真的困住了我 。
there was a young girl who stood up , and she asked the question: " where should we explore ? "	有位年輕女孩站起來 , 她問了問題: 「 我們該去哪裡去探索 ? 」
i think there's a sense that many of us have that the great age of exploration on earth is over , that for the next generation they're going to have to go to outer space or the deepest oceans in order to find something significant to explore .	我想我們當中許多人認為地球上偉大的探索時代已經結束了 , 下一代他們必須去外太空或最深的海洋 , 才能找到重要的探索 。
but is that really the case ?	但這真的是事實嗎 ?
is there really nowhere significant for us to explore left here on earth ?	我們是否真的沒有足夠的意義去探索地球的左邊 ?
it sort of made me think back to one of my favorite explorers in the history of biology .	這讓我回想我最喜歡的生物學探險家之一 。
this is an explorer of the unseen world , martinus beijerinck .	這是未知世界的探險家 , martinusbeijerinck 。
so beijerinck set out to discover the cause of tobacco mosaic disease .	所以beijerinck開始發現菸草的原因 。
what he did is he took the infected juice from tobacco plants and he would filter it through smaller and smaller filters .	他所做的是把被感染的果汁從菸草植物中取出來 , 他會透過更小的過濾器過濾 。
and he reached the point where he felt that there must be something out there that was smaller than the smallest forms of life that were ever known bacteria , at the time .	他到達了他覺得外頭一定有的東西比當時所知的細菌最小的生命形式還要小 。
he came up with a name for his mystery agent .	他為他的神秘代理出了一個名字 。
he called it the virus latin for " poison . "	他稱之為 「 毒藥 」 。
and in uncovering viruses , beijerinck really opened this entirely new world for us .	在解開的病毒中 , 北京人真的為我們開啟了這個全新的世界 。
we now know that viruses make up the majority of the genetic information on our planet , more than the genetic information of all other forms of life combined .	我們現在知道病毒是由地球上大多數基因信息組成的 , 超過所有其他形式的生命的遺傳信息 。
and obviously there's been tremendous practical applications associated with this world things like the eradication of smallpox , the advent of a vaccine against cervical cancer , which we now know is mostly caused by human papillomavirus .	很明顯地 , 和這個世界有關的實用應用很明顯 , 像是天花消滅的疫苗 , 對抗天花疫苗 , 我們現在知道大部分是由人類乳癌所造成的 。
and beijerinck's discovery , this was not something that occurred 500 years ago .	貝尼吉納克的發現 , 500年前就發生了 。
it was a little over 100 years ago that beijerinck discovered viruses .	大約一百多年前 , 北京發現了病毒 。
so basically we had automobiles , but we were unaware of the forms of life that make up most of the genetic information on our planet .	基本上 , 我們有汽車 , 但我們不知道地球上大部分基因信息的形式 。
we now have these amazing tools to allow us to explore the unseen world things like deep sequencing , which allow us to do much more than just skim the surface and look at individual genomes from a particular species , but to look at entire metagenomes , the communities of teeming microorganisms in , on and around us and to document all of the genetic information in these species .	我們現在有了這些驚人的工具 , 讓我們可以探索未知的世界 , 像是深度定序 , 讓我們不僅僅只是滑雪表面 , 觀察不同物種的個別基因組 , 而是去看整個金屬 , 包括我們這些微生物的社群 , 並記錄這些生物中的所有基因資訊 。
we can apply these techniques to things from soil to skin and everything in between .	我們可以將這些技術應用在土壤中的東西上 , 到皮膚上 , 介於兩者之間 。
in my organization we now do this on a regular basis to identify the causes of outbreaks that are unclear exactly what causes them .	在我的組織中 , 我們現在在一個常規的基礎上做這件事 , 來辨識出爆發的原因 , 正是造成它們的原因 。
and just to give you a sense of how this works , imagine that we took a nasal swab from every single one of you .	為了讓各位了解這如何運作 , 想像一下 , 我們從你們每一個人身上拿出一根納莎莎白 。
and this is something we commonly do to look for respiratory viruses like influenza .	這是我們常做的事 , 去尋找呼吸道病毒 , 像是流感病毒 。
the first thing we would see is a tremendous amount of genetic information .	首先我們會看到的是大量的基因信息 。
and if we started looking into that genetic information , we'd see a number of usual suspects out there of course , a lot of human genetic information , but also bacterial and viral information , mostly from things that are completely harmless within your nose .	如果我們開始研究遺傳信息 , 我們會看到很多人類基因信息 , 當然 , 還有細菌和病毒信息 , 大部份來自鼻子裡完全沒有任何傷害的事物 。
but we'd also see something very , very surprising .	但我們也會看到非常非常非常非常驚人的東西 。
as we started to look at this information , we would see that about 20 percent of the genetic information in your nose doesn't match anything that we've ever seen before no plant , animal , fungus , virus or bacteria .	當我們開始研究這些資訊時 , 我們會發現在鼻子裡大約20%的基因信息並不符合我們從未見過的植物、動物、真菌、病毒 , 或細菌 。
basically we have no clue what this is .	基本上 , 我們完全不知道這是什麼 。
and for the small group of us who actually study this kind of data , a few of us have actually begun to call this information biological dark matter .	對我們這些真正研究這種數據的小組而言 , 我們當中的一些人已經開始稱之為 「 生物暗物質 」 。
we know it's not anything that we've seen before ; it's sort of the equivalent of an uncharted continent right within our own genetic information .	我們知道這不是我們以前見過的 ; 相當於我們基因信息中未知的大陸 。
and there's a lot of it .	還有很多 。
if you think 20 percent of genetic information in your nose is a lot of biological dark matter , if we looked at your gut , up to 40 or 50 percent of that information is biological dark matter .	如果你認為你的鼻子裡有20%的基因信息是許多生物暗物質 , 如果我們仔細觀察你的腸子 , 高達40%或50%的信息是生物暗物質 。
and even in the relatively sterile blood , around one to two percent of this information is dark matter can't be classified , can't be typed or matched with anything we've seen before .	即便在相對無菌的血液中 , 大約1%到2%的信息是暗物質無法被分類、打字或配對我們以前所見過的任何東西 。
at first we thought that perhaps this was artifact .	一開始 , 我們以為這可能是人造物 。
these deep sequencing tools are relatively new .	這些深度的定序工具相對比較新 。
but as they become more and more accurate , we've determined that this information is a form of life , or at least some of it is a form of life .	但隨著它們變得越來越精確 , 我們已經決定這些資訊是生命的一種形式 , 至少有些是生命的一種形式 。
and while the hypotheses for explaining the existence of biological dark matter are really only in their infancy , there's a very , very exciting possibility that exists: that buried in this life , in this genetic information , are signatures of as of yet unidentified life .	雖然解釋生物暗物質存在的假設其實只是它們的嬰兒期間 , 但有非常非常非常令人興奮的可能性存在:在這個生命中埋藏在這個基因信息中 , 是無證的生命特徵 。
that as we explore these strings of a's , t's , c's and g's , we may uncover a completely new class of life that , like beijerinck , will fundamentally change the way that we think about the nature of biology .	當我們探索a、t、c、g的這些弦時 , 我們可能會發現一個全新的生命類型 , 例如beijerinck , 基本上會改變我們對生物的本質的看法 。
that perhaps will allow us to identify the cause of a cancer that afflicts us or identify the source of an outbreak that we aren't familiar with or perhaps create a new tool in molecular biology .	這也許可以讓我們辨識出我們害怕的癌症成因 , 或辨識出我們不熟悉的疫情來源 , 或是在分子生物學中創造出新的工具 。
i'm pleased to announce that , along with colleagues at stanford and caltech and ucsf , we're currently starting an initiative to explore biological dark matter for the existence of new forms of life .	我很高興向大家宣布 , 和史丹佛大學的同事加州理工和加州理工和加州理工學院合作 , 目前我們正在開始探討生物暗物質 , 來探索新生命的存在 。
a little over a hundred years ago , people were unaware of viruses , the forms of life that make up most of the genetic information on our planet .	大約一百多年前 , 人們沒有意識到病毒 , 形成了地球上大部分基因信息的生命形式 。
a hundred years from now , people may marvel that we were perhaps completely unaware of a new class of life that literally was right under our noses .	一百年後 , 人們可能很奇妙 , 我們可能完全不知道新類型的生命類型 , 其實就在我們的鼻子底下 。
it's true , we may have charted all the continents on the planet and we may have discovered all the mammals that are out there , but that doesn't mean that there's nothing left to explore on earth .	的確 , 我們可能已經把地球上所有的大陸記錄下來 , 我們可能已經發現了所有的哺乳類動物 , 但這並不表示地球上沒有任何東西可以探索 。
beijerinck and his kind provide an important lesson for the next generation of explorers people like that young girl from beloit , wisconsin .	beijerinck和他為下一代的探險家提供了很重要的教訓 , 像是來自威斯康辛的年輕女孩 。
and i think if we phrase that lesson , it's something like this: don't assume that what we currently think is out there is the full story .	我想如果我們把這一課說出來 , 就是這樣:不要假設我們目前所認為的都是完整的故事 。
go after the dark matter in whatever field you choose to explore .	在你選擇去探索的領域中 , 不論你選擇去探索的領域之後 。
there are unknowns all around us and they're just waiting to be discovered .	我們身邊有未知的事物 , 他們只是在等待被發現 。
legendary scientist david deutsch puts theoretical physics on the back burner to discuss a more urgent matter: the survival of our species . the first step toward solving global warming , he says , is to admit that we have a problem .	傳奇科學家大衛.狄西克把理論物理放在背面 , 討論一個更緊迫的問題:人類的生存 。 解決全球暖化的第一步 , 他說 , 承認我們有一個問題 。
climate change , cosmos , culture , environment , global issues , physics , science , technology , universe	氣候變遷、宇宙、文化、環境、物理、科學、科技、宇宙、宇宙、宇宙、文化、文化、環境、環境、全球議題、物理議題、物理、科學、科學、科學、科技、
david deutsch on our place in the cosmos	大衛•迪斯奇在我們所在的宇宙中位置 。
we've been told to go out on a limb and say something surprising .	我們被告知要走出肢體 , 說出令人驚訝的事 。
so i'll try and do that , but i want to start with two things that everyone already knows .	我會試著這樣做 , 但我想從大家都知道的兩件事開始 。
and the first one , in fact , is something that has been known for most of recorded history .	事實上 , 首先 , 大部分記錄的歷史都是已知的 。
and that is that the planet earth , or the solar system , or our environment or whatever , is uniquely suited to sustain our evolution or creation , as it used to be thought and our present existence , and most important , our future survival .	那就是地球 , 或太陽系 , 或我們的環境 , 獨一無二地適合維持我們的進化或創造 , 因為它以前是思索和現存 , 最重要的是我們未來的生存 。
nowadays this idea has a dramatic name: spaceship earth .	現今這個想法有個很戲劇性的名字:太空船地球 。
and the idea there is that outside the spaceship , the universe is implacably hostile , and inside is all we have , all we depend on .	這個想法是 , 在太空船之外 , 宇宙是無敵的 , 裡面就是我們所擁有的 , 我們全部依賴的 。
and we only get the one chance: if we mess up our spaceship , we've got nowhere else to go .	我們只有一個機會:如果我們搞砸了我們的太空船 , 我們就沒有其他地方可以去 。
now , the second thing that everyone already knows is that contrary to what was believed for most of human history , human beings are not , in fact , the hub of existence .	現在 , 大家已經知道的第二件事是 , 與大多數人類歷史所相信的相反 , 事實上 , 人類並不是存在的中心 。
as stephen hawking famously said , we're just a chemical scum on the surface of a typical planet that's in orbit around a typical star , which is on the outskirts of a typical galaxy , and so on .	如史蒂芬霍金所說的 , 我們只是一個典型的星球表面上的化學污垢 , 繞著一個典型的恆星繞著一個典型銀河系的外圍 , 等等 。
now the first of those two things that everyone knows is kind of saying that we're at a very untypical place , uniquely suited and so on , and the second one is saying that we're at a typical place .	首先 , 大家都知道的這兩件事 , 就是說我們處在一個非常不典型的地方 , 獨一無二的配合等等 , 第二個是說我們處在一個典型的地方 。
and especially if you regard these two as deep truths to live by and to inform your life decisions , then they seem a little bit to conflict with each other .	特別是如果你把這兩種深度的真相視為生活的深刻真相 , 來告知你人生的決策 , 那麼他們似乎有點矛盾 。
but that doesn't prevent them from both being completely false .	但這並不能阻止他們完全錯誤 。
and they are . so let me start with the second one: typical . well is this a typical place ? well , let's look around , you know , and look in a random direction , and we see a wall , and chemical scum and that's not typical of the universe at all .	它們是 。 讓我從第二個開始:典型的 。 嗯 , 這是一個典型的地方嗎 ? 咱們看看四周 , 看看隨機方向 , 我們看到一面牆 , 化學污垢 , 完全不是典型的宇宙 。
all you've got to do is go a few hundred miles in that same direction and look back , and you won't see any walls or chemical scum at all all you see is a blue planet . and if you go further than that , you'll see the sun , the solar system , and the stars and so on .	你所要做的就是向同樣的方向走幾百英哩 , 回頭看 , 你看不到任何牆或化學污垢 , 都是藍色的星球 。 如果你更進一步看 , 太陽、太陽系 , 和恆星等等 。
but that's still not typical of the universe , because stars come in galaxies .	但這仍然不是典型的宇宙 , 因為恆星在星系中出現 。
and most places in the universe , a typical place in the universe , is nowhere near any galaxies .	宇宙中的大部分地方 , 一個典型的地方 , 幾乎沒有任何星系 。
so let's go out further , till we're outside the galaxy , and look back , and yeah , there's the huge galaxy with spiral arms laid out in front of us .	讓我們再往前走 , 直到我們在銀河外 , 回頭看 , 是的 , 有一個巨大的星系 , 在我們面前放置螺旋臂 。
and at this point we've come 100 , 000 light years from here .	此時此刻 , 我們已經有十萬光年了 。
but we're still nowhere near a typical place in the universe .	但 , 我們仍然不在宇宙中典型的地方 。
to get to a typical place , you've got to go 1 , 000 times as far as that into intergalactic space .	要到一個典型的地方 , 你必須走上一千倍的距離空間 。
and so what does that look like ? typical .	那看起來是什麼樣子 ? 典型的 。
what does a typical place in the universe look like ?	宇宙中的典型地方是什麼樣子 ?
well , at enormous expense , ted has arranged a highresolution immersion virtual reality rendering of intergalactic space the view from intergalactic space .	嗯 , 在很大的花費上 , ted已經安排了高解析度的虛擬實境 , 呈現出在銀河空間中從星系空間的觀點 。
so can we have the lights off , please , so we can see it ?	所以 , 我們能不能讓燈亮起來 , 這樣我們就能看到嗎 ?
well , not quite , not quite perfect you see , in intergalactic space intergalactic space is completely dark , pitch dark .	嗯 , 不太完美 , 你可以看到 , 在星系空間中間的星系空間完全是黑暗的 , 音高漆黑 。
it's so dark that if you were to be looking at the nearest star to you , and that star were to explode as a supernova , and you were to be staring directly at it at the moment when its light reached you , you still wouldn't be able to see even a glimmer .	這真是黑暗 , 如果你看著最近的恆星 , 那顆恆星會被超新星爆炸 , 而當你的光線接近你時 , 你仍然無法直接看到它 。
that's how big and how dark the universe is .	宇宙有多大和黑暗 。
and that's despite the fact that a supernova is so bright , so brilliant an event , that it would kill you stone dead at a range of several light years .	儘管超新星這麼亮 , 所以很聰明 , 它會在數光年之內殺死你 。
and yet from intergalactic space , it's so far away you wouldn't even see it .	然而 , 從星系空間 , 到目前為止 , 你根本看不到它 。
it's also very cold out there less than three degrees above absolute zero .	外面的溫度低於絕對零度三度 。
and it's very empty . the vacuum there is one million times less dense than the highest vacuum that our best technology on earth can currently create . so that's how different a typical place is from this place .	它非常空 , 真空 , 比地球上最高的科技還要少一百萬倍 , 我們的地球上最好的科技都能創造出來 。 這也是典型的地方 。
and that is how untypical this place is .	這就是這個地方是如此不典型 。
so can we have the lights back on please ? thank you .	所以 , 我們能把燈打回來嗎 ? 謝謝 。
now how do we know about an environment that's so far away , and so different , and so alien , from anything we're used to ?	現在 , 我們怎麼知道一個遙遠的環境 , 這麼不同 , 外星人 , 從任何我們習慣的環境中 ?
well , the earth our environment , in the form of us is creating knowledge .	嗯 , 地球是我們的環境 , 以我們形式在創造知識 。
well , what does that mean ? well , look out even further than we've just been i mean from here , with a telescope and you'll see things that look like stars .	那意味著什麼 ? 嗯 , 看看比我們剛才說的更遠 , 用望遠鏡 , 看看看起來像星星的東西 。
they're called " quasars . " quasars originally meant quasistellar object .	他們稱之為 「 四軸 」 。 原本是 「 四軸星 」 。
which means things that look a bit like stars . but they're not stars .	這意味著看起來有點像星星 。 但它們不是恆星 。
and we know what they are . billions of years ago , and billions of light years away , the material at the center of a galaxy collapsed towards a supermassive black hole .	我們知道數十億年前 , 數十億光年之外 , 銀河系中心的物質倒塌到超大質量的黑洞 。
and then intense magnetic fields directed some of the energy of that gravitational collapse . and some of the matter , back out in the form of tremendous jets which illuminated lobes with the brilliance of i think it's a trillion suns .	接著 , 強烈的磁場引力會崩塌 。 有些物質 , 以巨大的噴射機的形式呈現 , 以照亮額葉的亮度 。 我認為它是一兆個太陽 。
now , the physics of the human brain could hardly be more unlike the physics of such a jet .	現在 , 人類大腦的物理學幾乎不像噴射機的物理學 。
we couldn't survive for an instant in it . language breaks down when trying to describe what it would be like in one of those jets .	我們不能在它的瞬間存活 。 語言在描述其中一個噴射器時 , 分解了它會是什麼樣子 。
it would be a bit like experiencing a supernova explosion , but at pointblank range and for millions of years at a time .	這可能有點像經歷超新星爆炸 , 但在時間點和數百萬年間 ,
and yet , that jet happened in precisely such a way that billions of years later , on the other side of the universe , some bit of chemical scum could accurately describe , and model , and predict , and explain , above all there's your reference what was happening there , in reality .	然而 , 那個噴射機在幾十億年後發生 , 在宇宙的另一端 , 一些化學污染可以精確地描述、模型 , 並預測 , 最重要的是 , 在現實中發生了什麼事 。
the one physical system , the brain , contains an accurate working model of the other the quasar .	一個物理系統 , 大腦 , 包含一個精確的運作模式 , 位於四軸 。
not just a superficial image of it , though it contains that as well , but an explanatory model , embodying the same mathematical relationships and the same causal structure .	不僅僅是一個超級富足的圖像 , 雖然它包含了它 , 還包含了一種解釋性的模型 , 包含了同樣的數學關係 , 以及同樣的因果結構 。
now that is knowledge . and if that weren't amazing enough , the faithfulness with which the one structure resembles the other is increasing with time . that is the growth of knowledge .	這就是知識 。 如果這還不夠驚人 , 信仰的信念是隨著時間增加而增長 。 那就是知識的增長 。
so , the laws of physics have this special property .	所以 , 物理定律有特殊的特性 。
that physical objects , as unlike each other as they could possibly be , can nevertheless embody the same mathematical and causal structure and to do it more and more so over time .	實體的物體 , 和它們可能性不同 , 儘管它們能體現同樣的數學和因果結構 , 隨時間而來 , 不斷地複製它 。
so we are a chemical scum that is different . this chemical scum has universality .	我們是不同的化學污垢 , 這種化學污垢有普遍性的 。
its structure contains , with everincreasing precision , the structure of everything . this place , and not other places in the universe , is a hub which contains within itself the structural and causal essence of the whole of the rest of physical reality . and so , far from being insignificant , the fact that the laws of physics allow this , or even mandate that this can happen , is one of the most important things about the physical world .	它的結構包含著越來越精確的狀態 , 所有事物的結構 。 這個地方 , 不是宇宙中的其他地方 , 而是一個樞紐 , 內在的結構和因果實的本質 。 到目前為止 , 物理定律允許它發生 , 甚至強調它是物理世界最重要的東西之一 。
now how does the solar system and our environment , in the form of us acquire this special relationship with the rest of the universe ?	太陽系和我們的環境是如何在我們和其它宇宙的特殊關係中取得這種特殊的關係 ?
well , one thing that's true about stephen hawking's remark i mean , it is true , but it's the wrong emphasis . one thing that's true about it is that it doesn't do it with any special physics . there's no special dispensation , no miracles involved . it does it simply with three things that we have here in abundance .	嗯 , 史蒂芬•霍金的標誌有一點是正確的 , 但這是錯誤的強調 。 其中一個事實是 , 沒有任何特殊的物理學 。 沒有奇蹟 。 它只用我們在這裡的三件事情 。
one of them is matter , because the growth of knowledge is a form of information processing . information processing is computation , computation requires a computer there's no known way of making a computer without matter .	其中一個是很重要的 , 因為知識的增長是一種資訊處理 。 資訊處理是計算 , 計算需要一個電腦 , 不知道如何製造出無物質的電腦 。
we also need energy to make the computer , and most important , to make the media in effect onto which we record the knowledge that we discover .	我們也需要能量來製造電腦 , 最重要的是 , 讓媒體能影響我們所發現的知識 。
and then thirdly , less tangible , but just as essential for the openended creation of knowledge , of explanations , is evidence .	第三 , 更不可能 , 但對於開放式的知識、解釋的開放創造 , 是證據 。
now , our environment is inundated with evidence .	我們的環境被證據淹沒了 。
we happen to get round to testing , let's say , newton's law of gravity about 300 years ago .	例如 , 牛頓的重力定律大約300年前 。
but the evidence that we used to do that was falling down on every square meter of the earth for billions of years before that , and will continue to fall on for billions of years afterwards . and the same is true for all the other sciences .	但我們過去所做的證據 , 是在地球上數十億年前 , 每平方公尺下降 , 數十億年後會持續下降 。 其他的科學也是如此 。
as far as we know , evidence to discover the most fundamental truths of all the sciences is here just for the taking on our planet .	據我們所知 , 發現所有科學中最基本的真相 , 只是為了取得地球 。
our location is saturated with evidence , and also with matter and energy .	我們的地點充滿了證據 , 還有物質和能量 。
out in intergalactic space , those three prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge are at their lowest possible supply .	在星系間的空間中 , 開放式知識的三個先例是他們最低的可能供給量 。
as i said , it's empty ; it's cold ; and it's dark out there . or is it ?	如我所說的 , 它是空的 ; 它很冷 , 那裡是黑暗的 。 還是 ?
now actually , that's just another parochial misconception .	其實 , 這只是另一個假釋誤解 。
because imagine a cube out there in intergalactic space , the same size as our home , the solar system . now that cube is very empty by human standards , but that still means that it contains over a million tons of matter .	因為想像一個立方體在星系空間中 , 和我們家的大小一樣 , 太陽系 。 現在這個立方體是非常空的 , 但這仍然意味著它含有超過一百萬噸的物質 。
and a million tons is enough to make , say , a selfcontained space station , on which there's a colony of scientists that are devoted to creating an openended stream of knowledge , and so on .	一百萬噸足以製造 , 例如 , 一個自我控制的太空站 , 在那裡有一群科學家 , 投入創造一個開放式的知識流 , 諸如此類 。
now , it's way beyond present technology to even gather the hydrogen from intergalactic space and form it into other elements and so on .	現在 , 除了現在的科技之外 , 甚至從星系空間收集氫氣 , 將它變成其他元素等等 。
but the thing is , in a comprehensible universe , if something isn't forbidden by the laws of physics , then what could possibly prevent us from doing it , other than knowing how ?	但重點是 , 在一個可理解的宇宙中 , 如果物理定律沒有被禁止 , 那麼 , 什麼可能阻止我們做這件事 , 除了知道如何 ?
in other words , it's a matter of knowledge , not resources .	換句話說 , 這是知識的問題 , 而不是資源 。
and the same well , if we could do that we'd automatically have an energy supply , because the transmutation would be a fusion reactor and evidence ?	同樣的 , 如果我們能自動產生能量供應 , 因為轉變會是核融合反應爐和證據 ?
well , again , it's dark out there to human senses . but all you've got to do is take a telescope , even one of presentday design , look out and you'll see the same galaxies as we do from here .	同樣的 , 外面是黑暗的 。 但你只需要用望遠鏡 , 甚至是現今的設計 , 看看外面 , 你會看到我們從這裡看到的同一個星系 。
and with a more powerful telescope , you'll be able to see stars , and planets .	有了更強大的望遠鏡 , 你可以看見恆星和行星 。
in those galaxies , you'll be able to do astrophysics , and learn the laws of physics .	在這些星系中 , 你可以做天體物理學 , 並學習物理定律 。
and locally there you could build particle accelerators , and learn elementary particle physics , and chemistry , and so on .	在當地 , 你可以建造粒子加速器 , 學習基本粒子物理 , 化學等等 。
probably the hardest science to do would be biology field trips because it would take several hundred million years to get to the nearest lifebearing planet and back .	可能最困難的科學是生物學實地旅行 , 因為要花數億年才能到最近的生命中 , 回到最近的星球 。
but i have to tell you and sorry , richard but i never did like biology field trips much , and i think we can just about make do with one every few hundred million years .	但我得告訴各位 , 抱歉 , 理查 , 但我從來沒有很喜歡生物學領域的旅程 , 我認為我們可以每隔幾億年做一次 。
so in fact , intergalactic space does contain all the prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge . any such cube , anywhere in the universe , could become the same kind of hub that we are , if the knowledge of how to do so were present there .	事實上 , 星系間的空間包含了所有開放式的知識 。 任何一個立方體 , 宇宙中任何一個地方 , 都可能變成同一個樞紐 , 如果我們知道該怎麼做的話 。
so we're not in a uniquely hospitable place .	所以 , 我們不是處在一個獨特的宿主地方 。
if intergalactic space is capable of creating an openended stream of explanations , then so is almost every other environment . so is the earth . so is a polluted earth .	如果星系空間能夠創造出一個開放式的解釋流 , 那麼幾乎所有其他的環境 。 所以 , 地球是污染的地球 。
and the limiting factor , there and here , is not resources , because they're plentiful , but knowledge , which is scarce .	而有限的因素 , 在這裡 , 不是資源 , 因為它們很豐富 , 但知識卻很稀少 。
now this cosmic knowledgebased view may and i think ought to make us feel very special . but it should also make us feel vulnerable , because it means that without the specific knowledge that's needed to survive the ongoing challenges of the universe , we won't survive them .	這種以宇宙為基礎的知識觀點 , 我認為應該讓我們感覺非常特別 。 但這也應該讓我們覺得脆弱 , 因為這意味著 , 若沒有需要存活在宇宙中不斷的挑戰 , 我們就不會存活下來 。
all it takes is for a supernova to go off a few light years away , and we'll all be dead !	只需要一顆超新星才能離開幾光年 , 我們都死了 !
martin rees has recently written a book about our vulnerability to all sorts of things , from astrophysics , to scientific experiments gone wrong , and most importantly to terrorism with weapons of mass destruction .	馬丁•雷斯最近寫了一本關於我們對各種事物的脆弱性書 , 從天體物理學 , 到科學實驗都出了問題 , 最重要的是 , 用大規模毀滅的武器來恐怖主義 。
and he thinks that civilization has only a 50 percent chance of surviving this century .	他認為文明只有50%的機會能在這個世紀存活下來 。
i think he's going to talk about that later in the conference .	我想他晚點要在會議上談談談 。
now i don't think that probability is the right category to discuss this issue in .	我不認為機率是正確的分類來討論這個議題 。
but i do agree with him about this . we can survive , and we can fail to survive .	但我同意他這件事 , 我們可以存活下來 , 我們也無法存活下來 。
but it depends not on chance , but on whether we create the relevant knowledge in time .	但這並不取決於偶然 , 不論我們是否在時間創造相關的知識 。
the danger is not at all unprecedented . species go extinct all the time .	沒有史無前例的危險 , 物種總是滅絕 。
civilizations end . the overwhelming majority of all species and all civilizations that have ever existed are now history .	文明終結了 。 絕大多數物種和所有已存在的文明都是歷史 。
and if we want to be the exception to that , then logically our only hope is to make use of the one feature that distinguishes our species , and our civilization , from all the others namely , our special relationship with the laws of physics , our ability to create new explanations , new knowledge to be a hub of existence .	如果我們想成為例外 , 那麼邏輯上 , 我們唯一的希望就是用一種特徵來區別我們的物種 , 和我們的文明 , 即便是我們與物理定律的特殊關係 , 我們創造出新的解釋 , 新知識成為存在的中心 。
so let me now apply this to a current controversy , not because i want to advocate any particular solution , but just to illustrate the kind of thing i mean .	讓我把這個應用到當前的爭議上 , 並不是因為我想要提倡任何特定的解決方案 , 而是為了說明我的意思 。
and the controversy is global warming .	爭議是全球暖化 。
now , i'm a physicist , but i'm not the right kind of physicist . in regard to global warming , i'm just a layman . and the rational thing for a layman to do is to take seriously the prevailing scientific theory . and according to that theory , it's already too late to avoid a disaster .	我是物理學家 , 但是我不是正確的物理學家 。 在全球暖化上 , 我只是一名懶惰人 。 而理性的事情是認真考慮前的科學理論 。 根據這個理論 , 已經太遲了要避免一個災難 。
because if it's true that our best option at the moment is to prevent co2 emissions with something like the kyoto protocol , with its constraints on economic activity and its enormous cost of hundreds of billions of dollars or whatever it is , then that is already a disaster by any reasonable measure .	因為如果我們目前最好的選擇是預防二氧化碳排放 , 例如京都議定書 , 其經濟活動的限制 , 以及它數百億美元或其他的費用 , 那已經是不合理的測量 。
and the actions that are advocated are not even purported to solve the problem , merely to postpone it by a little . so it's already too late to avoid it , and it probably has been too late to avoid it ever since before anyone realized the danger .	倡導者的行動 , 甚至還沒被求助來解決這個問題 , 僅僅僅只是稍微稍稍稍做後的 。 所以 , 太遲了 , 它可能已經太遲了 , 以至於任何人意識到危險之前 , 都太晚了 。
it was probably already too late in the 1970s , when the best available scientific theory was telling us that industrial emissions were about to precipitate a new ice age in which billions would die .	在1970年代可能已經太晚了 , 當時最好的科學理論告訴我們 , 工業排放將要降低數十億人的新冰河年齡 。
now the lesson of that seems clear to me , and i don't know why it isn't informing public debate .	對我來說 , 這教訓似乎很清楚 , 我不知道為什麼沒有公開辯論 。
it is that we can't always know . when we know of an impending disaster , and how to solve it at a cost less than the cost of the disaster itself , then there's not going to be much argument , really .	我們不能永遠知道 。 當我們知道即將發生災難時 , 以及如何在災難本身的成本低於災難本身的成本 , 那麼真的不會有太多的爭論 。
but no precautions , and no precautionary principle , can avoid problems that we do not yet foresee .	但沒有預防措施 , 也沒有預防原則 , 可以避免我們還沒預料到的問題 。
hence , we need a stance of problemfixing , not just problemavoidance .	因此 , 我們需要一個固定的問題 , 不只是問題性 。
and it's true that an ounce of prevention equals a pound of cure , but that's only if we know what to prevent .	的確 , 一大堆預防等同於一磅解藥 , 但只有在我們知道如何預防 。
if you've been punched on the nose , then the science of medicine does not consist of teaching you how to avoid punches .	如果你被擊中鼻子 , 那麼醫學的科學並不包含教你如何避免穿刺 。
if medical science stopped seeking cures and concentrated on prevention only , then it would achieve very little of either .	如果醫學界停止尋求治癒和專注於預防 , 那它也幾乎沒有成就 。
the world is buzzing at the moment with plans to force reductions in gas emissions at all costs .	目前世界正在興起 , 計畫會強迫減少氣體排放的排放量 。
it ought to be buzzing with plans to reduce the temperature , and with plans to live at the higher temperature and not at all costs , but efficiently and cheaply . and some such plans exist , things like swarms of mirrors in space to deflect the sunlight away , and encouraging aquatic organisms to eat more carbon dioxide .	它應該要被計劃降低溫度 , 並且計劃在更高的溫度上生活 , 不用花費任何成本 , 而是有效率且便宜的 。 有些計畫存在 , 例如在太空中大量的鏡子 , 以反射陽光 , 並且鼓勵水生有機體吃更多的二氧化碳 。
at the moment , these things are fringe research .	目前 , 這些東西正在進行調查 。
they're not central to the human effort to face this problem , or problems in general .	他們不是人類努力面對這個問題的核心 , 或一般的問題 。
and with problems that we are not aware of yet , the ability to put right not the sheer good luck of avoiding indefinitely is our only hope , not just of solving problems , but of survival .	我們還沒意識到問題 , 要解決的能力 , 不是無限可能避免的好運 , 是我們唯一的希望 , 不只是解決問題 , 而是為了生存 。
so take two stone tablets , and carve on them .	拿兩個石桌來雕刻 。
on one of them , carve: " problems are soluble . "	其中一個 , 卡維爾: 「 問題很容易解決 。 」
and on the other one carve: " problems are inevitable . "	另外一個是: 「 問題是不可避免的 。 」
how can a struggling country break out of poverty if it's trapped in a system of bad rules ? economist paul romer unveils a bold idea: " charter cities , " cityscale administrative zones governed by a coalition of nations .	如果它被困在一個不好的規則系統中 , 一個掙扎的國家要如何破除貧窮 ? 經濟學家保羅•羅默揭開了一個大膽的想法: 「 查爾斯城市 」 、 「 城市規模的行政區 」 , 由國家聯盟統治 。
business , culture , economics , global issues , politics	商業、文化、經濟、全球議題、政治、
paul romer's radical idea: charter cities	保羅羅羅•羅默的激進想法: 「 特區城市城市 」 。
take a look at this picture .	看看這張照片 。
it poses a very fascinating puzzle for us .	它對我們來說是非常有趣的謎題 。
these african students are doing their homework under streetlights at the airport in the capital city because they don't have any electricity at home .	這些非洲學生在首都機場的路燈下做功課 , 因為他們家裡沒有電力 。
now , i haven't met these particular students , but i've met students like them .	我還沒見過這些特別的學生 , 但我見過像他們這樣的學生 。
let's just pick one for example , the one in the green shirt .	舉例來說 , 綠色襯衫的那個 。
let's give him a name , too: nelson .	我們也給他一個名字:nelson 。
i'll bet nelson has a cellphone .	我打賭nelson有手機 。
so here is the puzzle .	這就是謎題 。
why is it that nelson has access to a cuttingedge technology , like the cellphone , but doesn't have access to a 100yearold technology for generating electric light in the home ?	為什麼nelson可以接觸到最先進的科技 , 像手機 , 但在家裡沒有辦法使用一百歲的科技來發電燈 ?
now , in a word , the answer is " rules . "	簡單來說 , 答案是 「 規則 」 。
bad rules can prevent the kind of winwin solution that's available when people can bring new technologies in and make them available to someone like nelson .	不好的規則可以防止這種雙贏的解決方案 , 當人們可以把新的科技帶入像尼爾森這樣的人身上 , 讓他們可以使用 。
what kinds of rules ?	什麼樣的規則 ?
the electric company in this nation operates under a rule , which says that it has to sell electricity at a very low , subsidized price in fact , a price that is so low it loses money on every unit that it sells .	這個國家的電力公司在一個規則下運作 , 說它必須在低、補貼的價格上販賣電力 , 事實上 , 價格非常低 , 每一單位銷售的每一單位都輸了錢 。
so it has neither the resources , nor the incentives , to hook up many other users .	所以 , 它沒有資源 , 也沒有動機 , 要補充許多其他使用者 。
the president wanted to change this rule .	總統想改變這個規則 。
he's seen that it's possible to have a different set of rules , rules where businesses earn a small profit , so they have an incentive to sign up more customers .	他見識到有不同的規則 , 企業賺得很小的利潤 , 所以他們有動機來簽更多客戶 。
that's the kind of rules that the cellphone company that nelson purchases his telephony from operates under .	那是尼爾森的手機公司的規則 , 把他的電信用在運作之下 。
the president has seen how those rules worked well .	總統看過這些規則如何運作良好 。
so he tried to change the rules for pricing on electricity , but ran into a firestorm of protest from businesses and consumers who wanted to preserve the existing subsidized rates .	所以他試著改變電力價格的規則 , 但他跑到企業和消費者的抗議運動中 , 他們想要保存現有的補貼率 。
so he was stuck with rules that prevented him from letting the winwin solution help his country .	所以他被卡住了規則 , 阻止他讓雙贏的解決方案能幫助他的國家 。
and nelson is stuck studying under the streetlights .	納爾遜在街燈下進行研究 。
the real challenge then , is to try to figure out how we can change rules .	真正的挑戰是要想辦法改變規則 。
are there some rules we can develop for changing rules ?	有沒有一些規則可以用來改變規則 ?
i want to argue that there is a general abstract insight that we can make practical , which is that , if we can give more choices to people , and more choices to leaders who , in many countries , are also people .	我想主張 , 有一個一般的抽象觀點 , 是我們能實踐的 , 那就是 , 如果我們能給更多人更多選擇 , 更多選擇給在許多國家的領導者 , 也是人 。
but , it's useful to present the opposition between these two .	但這兩者之間的反對是有用的 。
because the kind of choice you might want to give to a leader , a choice like giving the president the choice to raise prices on electricity , takes away a choice that people in the economy want .	因為你可能會想給領袖這種選擇 , 像是給總統選擇在電力上提高價格的選擇 , 奪走經濟想要的選擇 。
they want the choice to be able to continue consuming subsidized electric power .	他們希望能選擇繼續消耗補貼式電力 。
so if you give just to one side or the other , you'll have tension or friction .	所以如果你只給一邊或另一邊 , 你會有張力或摩擦力 。
but if we can find ways to give more choices to both , that will give us a set of rules for changing rules that get us out of traps .	但如果我們能找到方法讓兩者都能做出更多選擇 , 那就能給我們一套改變規則 , 來讓我們脫離陷阱的規則 。
now , nelson also has access to the internet .	尼爾森也能取得網路 。
and he says that if you want to see the damaging effects of rules , the ways that rules can keep people in the dark , look at the pictures from nasa of the earth at night .	他說 , 如果你想看到規則的破壞效應 , 規則會讓人們在黑暗中 , 看著地球的照片 。
in particular check out asia .	特別是在亞洲 。
if you zoom in here , you can see north korea , in outline here , which is like a black hole compared to its neighbors .	如果你放大來看 , 你可以看到北韓 , 在線上 , 這就像是與鄰居相比的黑洞 。
now , you won't be surprised to learn that the rules in north korea keep people there in the dark .	現在 , 你不會驚訝地發現北韓的規則讓人們處於黑暗之中 。
but it is important to recognize that north korea and south korea started out with identical sets of rules in both the sense of laws and regulations , but also in the deeper senses of understandings , norms , culture , values and beliefs .	但 , 很重要的是 , 北韓和南韓始於法律和法規的相同規則 , 同時也在更深層的理解、規範、文化、價值觀和信仰 。
when they separated , they made choices that led to very divergent paths for their sets of rules .	當他們分開時 , 他們做出選擇 , 導致他們一組規則中非常多元的路徑 。
so we can change we as humans can change the rules that we use to interact with each other , for better , or for worse .	所以 , 我們可以改變我們身為人類可以改變我們用來互相互動的規則 , 更好 , 更糟的是 。
now let's look at another region , the caribbean .	現在我們來看看另一個地區 , 加勒比海 。
zoom in on haiti , in outline here .	放大海地 , 這裡是線上的 。
haiti is also dark , compared to its neighbor here , the dominican republic , which has about the same number of residents .	海地也是黑暗的 , 與其鄰居相比 , 多明尼加共和國有相同數量的居民 。
both of these countries are dark compared to puerto rico , which has half as many residents as either haiti or the dominican republic .	這兩個國家都和波多黎各相比 , 那裡有一半的居民是海地或多明尼加共和國 。
what haiti warns us is that rules can be bad because governments are weak .	海地警告我們 , 規則可能很糟 , 因為政府很弱 。
it's not just that the rules are bad because the government is too strong and oppressive , as in north korea .	不只是規則很糟 , 因為政府太強大、太壓迫 , 和北韓一樣 。
so that if we want to create environments with good rules , we can't just tear down .	所以 , 如果我們想要創造出有好規則的環境 , 我們就不能把環境撕下來 。
we've got to find ways to build up , as well .	我們也需要找到建立起的方法 。
now , china dramatically demonstrates both the potential and the challenges of working with rules .	如今 , 中國大幅展現出與規則合作的潛力和挑戰 。
back in the beginning of the data presented in this chart , china was the world's hightechnology leader .	回到這個圖表的開端 , 中國是世界上高科技領袖 。
chinese had pioneered technologies like steel , printing , gunpowder .	中國的先驅技術如鋼鐵、列印、槍枝 。
but the chinese never adopted , at least in that period , effective rules for encouraging the spread of those ideas a profit motive that could have encouraged the spread .	但中國從來沒有採用過 , 至少在那個時期 , 有效的規則 , 鼓勵這些想法的散播 , 能鼓勵傳播出去的利潤動機 。
and they soon adopted rules which slowed down innovation and cut china off from the rest of the world .	他們很快就採用了一些規則 , 減緩了創新 , 把中國從世界各地砍掉 。
so as other countries in the world innovated , in the sense both of developing newer technologies , but also developing newer rules , the chinese were cut off from those advances .	所以 , 隨著世界上其他國家創新 , 在發展新科技的同時 , 同時也發展出新的規則 , 中國人從這些進步中切斷 。
income there stayed stagnant , as it zoomed ahead in the rest of the world .	收入一直停滯不前 , 因為它在世界其他地方縮小了 。
this next chart looks at more recent data .	接下來的圖表是比較近期的數據 。
it plots income , average income in china as a percentage of average income in the united states .	在中國 , 平均收入是美國平均收入的百分比 。
in the '50s and '60s you can see that it was hovering at about three percent .	在1950和60年代 , 你們可以看到 , 大約佔了百分之三 。
but then in the late '70s something changed .	但在70年代末期 , 發生了改變 。
growth took off in china . the chinese started catching up very quickly with the united states .	中國的經濟成長很快就開始趕上美國
if you go back to the map at night , you can get a clue to the process that lead to the dramatic change in rules in china .	如果你在晚上回到地圖上 , 你就能得到一個線索 , 引導中國規則的巨大改變 。
the brightest spot in china , which you can see on the edge of the outline here , is hong kong .	中國最明亮的地點 , 你可以看到在線上最亮的地方 , 是香港 。
hong kong was a small bit of china that , for most of the 20th century , operated under a very different set of rules than the rest of mainland china rules that were copied from working market economies of the time , and administered by the british .	香港是中國的一小部分 , 在20世紀 , 大部分的中國 , 都被一套非常不一樣的規則所操作 , 和中國其他地方的規則 , 都是由當時的市場經濟所複製 , 並由英國負責 。
in the 1950s , hong kong was a place where millions of people could go , from the mainland , to start in jobs like sewing shirts , making toys .	在1950年代 , 香港是一個有數百萬人可以去的地方 , 從大陸開始 , 像縫製衣服 , 製作玩具的地方 。
but , to get on a process of increasing income , increasing skills led to very rapid growth there .	但 , 為了達到越來越多收入的過程 , 增加技能 , 導致在那裡快速成長 。
hong kong was also the model which leaders like deng xiaoping could copy , when they decided to move all of the mainland towards the market model .	香港也是那種領導者 , 如傑出xiaoping可以複製的模式 , 當他們決定把整個大陸搬到市場模式上 。
but deng xiaoping instinctively understood the importance of offering choices to his people .	但註冊xia選手直覺地明白提供給他的人民選擇的重要性 。
so instead of forcing everyone in china to shift immediately to the market model , they proceeded by creating some special zones that could do , in a sense , what britain did: make the opportunity to go work with the market rules available to the people who wanted to opt in there .	所以 , 與其要求中國的每個人立即轉移到市場模式 , 他們透過創造一些特殊的區域 , 在某種意義上 , 英國的做法是:讓這個機會和市場規則合作 , 讓那些想要在裡面採取行動的人 。
so they created four special economic zones around hong kong: zones where chinese could come and work , and cities grew up very rapidly there ; also zones where foreign firms could come in and make things .	所以他們在香港附近創造了四個經濟特區:中國人可以來到那裡工作 , 城市成長得非常迅速 ; 外國公司也能進來製造東西 。
one of the zones next to hong kong has a city called shenzhen .	香港旁邊的一個區塊有個叫做雪梨的城市 。
in that city there is a taiwanese firm that made the iphone that many of you have , and they made it with labor from chinese who moved there to shenzhen .	在那個城市 , 有台灣公司 , 讓許多人都擁有的iphone , 他們用中國的勞工來製作 。
so after the four special zones , there were 14 coastal cites that were open in the same sense , and eventually demonstrated successes in these places that people could opt in to , that they flocked to because of the advantages they offered .	在四個特區之後 , 有十四個海岸線也同樣開放 , 最終 , 在這些地方 , 人們可以選擇的成功 , 他們會被鎖住 , 因為他們提供的優勢 。
demonstrated successes there led to a consensus for a move toward the market model for the entire economy .	證實了成功 , 導致了整個經濟模式的共識 。
now the chinese example shows us several points .	中國的例子顯示了幾點 。
one is: preserve choices for people .	第一:為人保存選擇 。
two: operate on the right scale .	第二:在正確的比例上運作 。
if you try to change the rules in a village , you could do that , but a village would be too small to get the kinds of benefits you can get if you have millions of people all working under good rules .	如果你試著改變村子裡的規則 , 你可以這樣做 , 但村落會太小 , 如果有數百萬人在好的規則下工作 , 就能得到你能得到的益處 。
on the other hand , the nation is too big .	另一方面 , 國家太大了 。
if you try to change the rules in the nation , you can't give some people a chance to hold back , see how things turn out , and let others zoom ahead and try the new rules .	如果你試著改變國家的規則 , 你就不能給別人一個機會 , 看看事情是怎麼發生的 , 讓其他人放大 , 嘗試新的規則 。
but cities give you this opportunity to create new places , with new rules that people can opt in to .	但城市給你這個機會 , 創造出新的地方 , 新的規則 , 讓人們可以選擇 。
and they're large enough to get all of the benefits that we can have when millions of us work together under good rules .	它們夠大 , 可以得到我們能擁有的所有好處 , 只要我們在好的規則下合作 , 我們就能得到好處 。
so the proposal is that we conceive of something called a charter city .	所以 , 我們的建議是 , 一個叫做 「 查爾斯城市 」 的東西 。
we start with a charter that specifies all the rules required to attract the people who we'll need to build the city .	我們從一個特定規則開始 , 來吸引我們建造城市的人 。
we'll need to attract the investors who will build out the infrastructure the power system , the roads , the port , the airport , the buildings .	我們需要吸引投資者 , 他們會建立基礎建設系統、道路、港口、機場、建築物 。
you'll need to attract firms , who will come hire the people who move there first .	你需要吸引公司 , 他們會僱用先前搬到那裡的人 。
and you'll need to attract families , the residents who will come and live there permanently , raise their children , get an education for their children , and get their first job .	你需要吸引家庭 , 居民會永久住在那裡 , 養育他們的孩子 , 為他們的孩子取得教育 , 得到第一份工作 。
with that charter , people will move there .	有了這個章節 , 人們會搬到那裡 。
the city can be built .	城市可以被建造出來 。
and we can scale this model .	我們可以擴展這個模型 。
we can go do it over and over again .	我們可以一遍又一遍 。
to make it work , we need good rules . we've already discussed that .	要成功 , 我們需要好的規則 。 我們已經討論過了 。
those are captured in the charter .	這些都被收集在圖表裡 。
we also need the choices for people .	我們也需要人們的選擇 。
that's really built into the model if we allow for the possibility of building cities on uninhabited land .	這真的是建立在模型中 , 如果我們能在無人居住的土地上建造城市的可能性 。
you start from uninhabited territory .	你從未居住的領域開始 。
people can come live under the new charter , but no one is forced to live under it .	人們可以生活在新的憲章之下 , 但沒有人被迫住在它下面 。
the final thing we need are choices for leaders .	最後 , 我們需要的是對領導者的選擇 。
and , to achieve the kind of choices we want for leaders we need to allow for the potential for partnerships between nations: cases where nations work together , in effect , de facto , the way china and britain worked together to build , first a little enclave of the market model , and then scale it throughout china .	為了達成我們想要的那種選擇 , 我們需要讓國家之間的合作潛力:國家合作的可能性 , 實際上 , 中國和英國合作的方式 , 首先是市場模式的一小塊奴隸 , 然後擴展到全中國 。
in a sense , britain , inadvertently , through its actions in hong kong , did more to reduce world poverty than all the aid programs that we've undertaken in the last century .	在某種意義上 , 英國 , 不經意地 , 透過香港的行動 , 降低世界貧窮 , 比上個世紀所缺乏的愛滋計畫還要多 。
so if we allow for these kind of partnerships to replicate this again , we can get those kinds of benefits scaled throughout the world .	所以如果我們允許這些合作夥伴再次複製 , 我們就能得到全世界各地的好處 。
in some cases this will involve a delegation of responsibility , a delegation of control from one country to another to take over certain kinds of administrative responsibilities .	在某些情況下 , 這會涉及到責任 , 一個國家的控制權 , 從一個國家 , 到另一個國家 , 來負責某些行政責任 。
now , when i say that , some of you are starting to think , " well , is this just bringing back colonialism ? "	現在 , 當我這麼說的時候 , 有些人開始想: 「 嗯 , 這是否會帶回殖民主義 ? 」
it's not . but it's important to recognize that the kind of emotions that come up when we start to think about these things , can get in the way , can make us pull back , can shut down our ability , and our interest in trying to explore new ideas .	不是的 。 但很重要的是 , 當我們開始思考這些事情時 , 會有一種情緒 , 可以讓我們退出 , 可以閉嘴 , 並且我們想要探索新點子的興趣 。
why is this not like colonialism ?	為什麼這不像殖民主義 ?
the thing that was bad about colonialism , and the thing which is residually bad in some of our aid programs , is that it involved elements of coercion and condescension .	殖民主義的壞處在於 , 在某些援助計畫中 , 仍然是壞事 , 就是它涉及了強烈和自信的元素 。
this model is all about choices , both for leaders and for the people who will live in these new places .	這個模式是關於選擇 , 無論是為了領導者 , 還是為了住在這些新地方的人 。
and , choice is the antidote to coercion and condescension .	選擇是對強迫和自主的解藥 。
so let's talk about how this could play out in practice .	咱們來談談如何在實踐上演出 。
let's take a particular leader , raul castro , who is the leader of cuba .	讓我們帶一個特定的領導者 , 拉爾卡斯楚 , 他是古巴的領導者 。
it must have occurred to castro that he has the chance to do for cuba what deng xiaoping did for china , but he doesn't have a hong kong there on the island in cuba .	卡斯楚一定有機會為古巴做些什麼 , 但他在古巴的島上沒有香港 。
he does , though , have a little bit of light down in the south that has a very special status .	不過 , 他的確在南方有一點點光 , 有很特別的地位 。
there is a zone there , around guantanamo bay , where a treaty gives the united states administrative responsibility for a piece of land that's about twice the size of manhattan .	這裡有一區 , 位於瓜地亞摩灣 , 在那裡 , 一塊美國政府為一塊土地負責 , 大約是曼哈頓的兩倍 。
castro goes to the prime minister of canada and says , " look , the yankees have a terrible pr problem .	卡斯tro去加拿大總理 , 說: 「 聽著 , yankees有一個糟糕的pr問題 。
they want to get out .	他們想要出去 。
why don't you , canada , take over ?	為什麼你不 , 加拿大 ?
build run a special administrative zone .	建造一個特殊的行政區 。
allow a new city to be built up there .	讓一個新的城市在那裡建造 。
allow many people to come in .	讓許多人進來 。
let us have a hong kong nearby .	讓我們在附近有個香港 。
some of my citizens will move into that city as well .	我的一些市民也會搬進那個城市 。
others will hold back . but this will be the gateway that will connect the modern economy and the modern world to my country . "	其他人會保持住 。 但這將會是將現代經濟和現代世界連結到我的國家的通道 。 」
now , where else might this model be tried ?	現在 , 這個模型還在哪裡呢 ?
well , africa . i've talked with leaders in africa .	嗯 , 非洲 , 我和非洲的領導人談過 。
many of them totally get the notion of a special zone that people can opt into as a rule .	許多人完全得到了一種特殊區塊的概念 , 讓人們可以當作一個規則 。
it's a rule for changing rules .	它是一種改變規則的規則 。
it's a way to create new rules , and let people optin without coercion , and the opposition that coercion can force .	它是一種創造新規則的方式 , 讓人們不用強烈的力量 , 和強迫的反對 。
they also totally get the idea that in some instances they can make more credible promises to longterm investors the kind of investors who will come build the port , build the roads , in a new city they can make more credible promises if they do it along with a partner nation .	他們也完全了解 , 在某些情況下 , 他們可以做出更可信的承諾 , 給長期投資者 , 來建造港口、建造道路 , 在新城市中 , 他們可以做出更可信的承諾 , 如果他們與另一方國家合作 , 就能做出更好的承諾 。
perhaps even in some arrangement that's a little bit like an escrow account , where you put land in the escrow account and the partner nation takes responsibility for it .	甚至在某些安排中 , 有點像偷渡帳戶 , 在那裡 , 你把土地放進人工帳戶中 , 另一方國家為此負責 。
there is also lots of land in africa where new cities could be built .	在非洲也有許多土地 , 可以建造新的城市 。
this is a picture i took when i was flying along the coast .	這是我在海岸飛行時拍的照片 。
there are immense stretches of land like this land where hundreds of millions of people could live .	像這片土地上有巨大的延伸區 , 在那裡 , 數以億計的人可以活下來 。
now , if we generalize this and think about not just one or two charter cites , but dozens cities that will help create places for the many hundreds of millions , perhaps billions of people who will move to cities in the coming century is there enough land for them ?	現在 , 如果我們將這點歸納並不僅僅是一、兩張圖片 , 而是數十個城市 , 可以為數十億的城市創造空間 , 也許數十億人會搬到未來世紀的城市 , 是否有足夠的土地 ?
well , throughout the world , if we look at the lights at night , the one thing that's misleading is that , visually , it looks like most of the world is already built out .	在世界各地 , 如果我們在晚上看著燈光 , 誤導的一件事是 , 視覺上來說 , 大部分的世界已經被建造出來了 。
so let me show you why that's wrong .	所以 , 讓我告訴你為什麼那是錯的 。
take this representation of all of the land .	以所有土地的代表為例 。
turn it into a square that stands for all the arable land on earth .	把它變成一個正方形 , 代表著地球上所有可耕地 。
and let these dots represent the land that's already taken up by the cities that three billion people now live in .	讓這些點代表已經被30億人口居住的城市所佔據的土地 。
if you move the dots down to the bottom of the rectangle you can see that the cities for the existing three billion urban residents take up only three percent of the arable land on earth .	如果你把這些點移到矩形的底部你可以看到現有30億個城市居民只佔地球上30%的可耕地
so if we wanted to build cities for another billion people , they would be dots like this .	所以如果我們想為其他十億人建造城市 , 他們就會像這樣 。
we'd go from three percent of the arable land , to four percent .	我們從三分之三的可耕地 , 到四分之一 。
we'd dramatically reduce the human footprint on earth by building more cities that people can move to .	我們會大幅降低地球上的人類足跡 , 藉由建造更多人們可以移動的城市 。
and if these are cities governed by good rules , they can be cities where people are safe from crime , safe from disease and bad sanitation , where people have a chance to get a job .	如果這些城市被好的規則管理 , 他們可能會成為城市 , 人們安全地從犯罪、疾病和不良衛生 , 在那裡 , 人們有機會得到工作 。
they can get basic utilities like electricity .	它們能得到像電力這樣的基本設施 。
their kids can get an education .	他們的孩子可以接受教育 。
so what will it take to get started building the first charter cities , scaling this so we build many more ?	所以 , 要花什麼才能開始建立第一座章節城市 , 這樣我們才能建立更多 ?
it would help to have a manual .	可以幫忙做手冊 。
what university professors could do is write some details that might go into this manual .	大學教授可以做的是寫一些細節 , 可以寫進這個手冊中 。
you wouldn't want to let us run the cities , go out and design them .	你不想讓我們跑城市 , 出去設計它們 。
you wouldn't let academics out in the wild .	你不會在野外放棄學術 。
but , you could set us to work thinking about questions like , suppose it isn't just canada that does the deal with raul castro .	但 , 你可以讓我們開始思考像這樣的問題 , 假設這不只是加拿大對抗拉爾卡斯楚 。
perhaps brazil comes in as a participant , and spain as well . and perhaps cuba wants to be one of the partners in a fourway joint venture .	或許巴西也有參與者 , 西班牙也想成為四條通路的夥伴之一 。
how would we write the treaty to do that ?	我們要如何寫出條約來做到這一點 ?
there is less precedent for that , but that could easily be worked out .	之前的情況比較少 , 但這很容易就解決 。
how would we finance this ?	我們要如何資助這個 ?
turns out singapore and hong kong are cities that made huge gains on the value of the land that they owned when they got started .	結果發現新加坡和香港是城市 , 讓它們在開始時擁有的土地價值很大 。
you could use the gains on the value of the land to pay for things like the police , the courts , but the school system and the health care system too , which make this a more attractive place to live , makes this a place where people have higher incomes which , incidentally , makes the land more valuable .	你可以利用土地的價值來支付像警察、法庭等的東西 , 但學校和健康照護體制 , 這也讓土地更吸引人居住 , 讓人們擁有較高的收入 , 順帶一提 , 讓土地更有價值 。
so the incentives for the people helping to construct this zone and build it , and set up the basic rules , go very much in the right direction .	所以 , 協助建造這個區域的人們的動機 , 設定基本規則 , 向正確的方向發展 。
so there are many other details like this .	所以還有很多其他的細節 。
how could we have buildings that are low cost and affordable for people who work in a first job , assembling something like an iphone , but make those buildings energy efficient , and make sure that they are safe , so they don't fall down in an earthquake or a hurricane .	我們要如何有低成本和可負擔得起的建築 , 像是iphone , 讓這些建築物更有效率 , 確保它們安全 , 所以它們不會落在地震或颶風中 。
many technical details to be worked out , but those of us who are already starting to pursue these things can already tell that there is no roadblock , there's no impediment , other than a failure of imagination , that will keep us from delivering on a truly global winwin solution .	許多技術上的細節要被發揮出來 , 但我們這些已經開始追求這些事情的人已經知道沒有路障 , 除了想像之外 , 還沒有阻礙 , 還會讓我們不用真正的全球雙贏解決方案 。
let me conclude with this picture .	讓我用這張照片來總結 。
the reason we can be so well off , even though there is so many people on earth , is because of the power of ideas .	我們之所以能如此順利 , 即使地球上有這麼多人 , 是因為想法的力量 。
we can share ideas with other people , and when they discover them , they share with us .	我們可以和其他人分享想法 , 當他們發現他們時 , 他們會和我們分享 。
it's not like scarce objects , where sharing means we each get less .	它不像稀有物品 , 在那裡 , 分享的意思是 , 我們每次都變得比較少 。
when we share ideas we all get more .	當我們分享想法時 , 我們會得到更多 。
when we think about ideas in that way , we usually think about technologies .	當我們用這種方式思考想法時 , 我們通常會想到科技 。
but there is another class of ideas: the rules that govern how we interact with each other ; rules like , let's have a tax system that supports a research university that gives away certain kinds of knowledge for free .	但還有另一類想法:規則我們彼此互動的規則 ; 例如 , 讓我們有一個稅收系統 , 支持研究大學 , 免費提供某些知識 。
let's have a system where we have ownership of land that is registered in a government office , that people can pledge as collateral .	讓我們有一個系統 , 在政府辦公室裡 , 我們有一塊土地的所有權 , 讓人們可以把土地保留成殖民地 。
if we can keep innovating on our space of rules , and particularly innovate in the sense of coming up with rules for changing rules , so we don't get stuck with bad rules , then we can keep moving progress forward and truly make the world a better place , so that people like nelson and his friends don't have to study any longer under the streetlights . thank you .	如果我們能在規則的空間中不斷創新 , 尤其是創新 , 以改變規則 , 這樣我們就不會陷入不好的規則 , 那麼我們才能繼續前進 , 真正讓世界變得更美好 , 像尼爾森和他的朋友 , 不用再在街燈下學習 。 謝謝 。
genomics pioneer craig venter takes a break from his epic roundtheworld expedition to talk about the millions of genes his team has discovered so far in its quest to map the ocean’s biodiversity .	基因先驅craigventer在史詩般的探險中休息 , 談到他的團隊發現了數百萬個基因 , 到目前為止 , 地圖海洋生物多樣性 。
dna , biosphere , biotech , entrepreneur , genetics , invention , oceans , science , technology	dna、生物圈、生物科技、創業家、遺傳學、發明、海洋、科學、科技、科技、科技、科技、科技、科技、科技、科技、科技、科技、科技、科技、科技、科技、科技、科技、科技、
craig venter on dna and the sea	克萊格•凡特在dna和海上 。
at the break , i was asked by several people about my comments about the aging debate .	在休息時 , 我被幾個人問到我關於老化辯論的評論 。
and this will be my only comment on it .	這將會是我唯一的評論 。
and that is , i understand that optimists greatly outlive pessimists .	那就是 , 我知道樂觀主義者大大勝過悲觀主義者 。
what i'm going to tell you about in my 18 minutes is how we're about to switch from reading the genetic code to the first stages of beginning to write the code ourselves .	在我十八分鐘內 , 我要告訴各位 , 我們要如何從閱讀基因密碼轉換到開始寫程式的第一階段 。
it's only 10 years ago this month when we published the first sequence of a freeliving organism , that of haemophilus influenzae .	只有10年前這個月 , 我們發表了第一個免疫有機體的序列 , 也就是大氣流感病毒 。
that took a genome project from 13 years down to four months .	這花了13年到4個月的基因組計畫 。
we can now do that same genome project in the order of two to eight hours .	我們現在可以在兩到八個小時內完成同樣的基因組計畫 。
so in the last decade , a large number of genomes have been added: most human pathogens , a couple of plants , several insects and several mammals , including the human genome .	所以 , 在過去的十年中 , 許多基因組被加入了:大部分人類的病原體 , 幾種植物 , 幾種昆蟲和數個哺乳類動物 , 包括人類基因組 。
genomics at this stage of the thinking from a little over 10 years ago was , by the end of this year , we might have between three and five genomes sequenced ; it's on the order of several hundred .	十多年前的思想基因組學在今年底 , 我們可能有三到五個基因組序列 , 正是數百個基因序列 。
we just got a grant from the gordon and betty moore foundation to sequence 130 genomes this year , as a side project from environmental organisms .	我們剛從戈登和貝蒂摩爾基金會得到獎金 , 到今年排序130個基因組 , 作為環保有機體的一邊計畫 。
so the rate of reading the genetic code has changed .	所以閱讀基因密碼的速度已經改變了 。
but as we look , what's out there , we've barely scratched the surface on what is available on this planet .	但當我們看 , 外面的是什麼 , 我們幾乎沒有抓住地球上可用的地表 。
most people don't realize it , because they're invisible , but microbes make up about a half of the earth's biomass , whereas all animals only make up about one onethousandth of all the biomass .	大部分的人不會意識到 , 因為它們是看不見的 , 但微生物佔地球生物量的一半 , 而所有的生物量只佔了大約1/4 。
and maybe it's something that people in oxford don't do very often , but if you ever make it to the sea , and you swallow a mouthful of seawater , keep in mind that each milliliter has about a million bacteria and on the order of 10 million viruses .	也許是牛津的人們不常常做的事 , 但如果你去過海 , 吞下一口海水 , 請記住每一毫升的海水 , 每一毫升都有大約一百萬種細菌和一千萬種病毒 。
less than 5 , 000 microbial species have been characterized as of two years ago , and so we decided to do something about it .	兩年前 , 少於五千種微生物種類就被特徵化了 , 所以我們決定為它做點什麼 。
and we started the sorcerer ii expedition , where we were , as with great oceanographic expeditions , trying to sample the ocean every 200 miles .	我們開始了srcerii探險 , 我們在海洋學探險中 , 每200英哩 , 嘗試採集海洋樣本 。
we started in bermuda for our test project , then moved up to halifax , working down the u . s . east coast , the caribbean sea , the panama canal , through to the galapagos , then across the pacific , and we're in the process now of working our way across the indian ocean .	我們從bermuda開始進行實驗 , 然後搬到哈利法克斯 , 下到美國東岸 , 加勒比海 , 巴拿馬運河 , 穿過加拉巴哥群島 , 橫跨太平洋 , 我們現在正在橫跨印度洋 。
it's very tough duty ; we're doing this on a sailing vessel , in part to help excite young people about going into science .	這很困難 ; 我們在帆船上做這件事 , 有一部分是要協助年輕人進入科學 。
the experiments are incredibly simple .	實驗非常簡單 。
we just take seawater and we filter it , and we collect different size organisms on different filters , and then take their dna back to our lab in rockville , where we can sequence a hundred million letters of the genetic code every 24 hours .	我們只用海水來過濾它 , 我們收集不同過濾器的大小生物 , 然後把它們的dna帶回我們在洛克維爾的實驗室 , 在那裡 , 我們可以每24小時排序一億個基因編碼的字母 。
and with doing this , we've made some amazing discoveries .	藉由這樣做 , 我們發現了一些驚人的發現 。
for example , it was thought that the visual pigments that are in our eyes there was only one or two organisms in the environment that had these same pigments .	例如 , 被認為在我們的眼睛中 , 眼睛中只有一兩種有機體在環境中有同樣的顏料 。
it turns out , almost every species in the upper parts of the ocean in warm parts of the world have these same photoreceptors , and use sunlight as the source of their energy and communication .	結果發現 , 幾乎所有在地球溫暖地區的生物都有相同的攝影器 , 把陽光當作它們的能量和溝通來源 。
from one site , from one barrel of seawater , we discovered 1 . 3 million new genes and as many as 50 , 000 new species .	從一桶海水中 , 我們發現了130萬個新基因 , 還有5萬種新物種 。
we've extended this to the air now with a grant from the sloan foundation .	我們已經將它延伸到空氣中 , 帶著來自史隆基金會的補助 。
we're measuring how many viruses and bacteria all of us are breathing in and out every day , particularly on airplanes or closed auditoriums .	我們在測量我們所有人每天都在呼吸 , 尤其是在飛機或關閉聽器上 。
we filter through some simple apparatuses ; we collect on the order of a billion microbes from just a day filtering on top of a building in new york city .	我們過濾過一些簡單的外觀 ; 我們收集了十億微生物的順序 , 在紐約市的一棟大樓上過濾 。
and we're in the process of sequencing all that at the present time .	我們正處於定序這一切的過程中 。
just on the data collection side , just where we are through the galapagos , we're finding that almost every 200 miles , we see tremendous diversity in the samples in the ocean .	僅僅在收集資料的一邊 , 是我們穿過加拉帕戈斯的位置 , 我們發現幾乎每200英里 , 我們在海洋的樣本中看到了非常多樣性 。
some of these make logical sense , in terms of different temperature gradients .	有些是合理的 , 以不同溫度的角度來說 。
so this is a satellite photograph based on temperatures red being warm , blue being cold and we found there's a tremendous difference between the warm water samples and the cold water samples , in terms of abundant species .	這是一張衛星照片 , 以紅色表示溫度 , 藍色是冷的 , 我們發現溫暖的水樣本和冷水樣本之間有著巨大的差異 。
the other thing that surprised us quite a bit is these photoreceptors detect different wavelengths of light , and we can predict that based on their amino acid sequence .	另一件令我們驚訝的事是這些攝影器偵測到不同波長的光 , 我們可以根據它們的胺基酸序列來預測它 。
and these vary tremendously from region to region .	而這些區域從各個區域到區域都不同 。
maybe not surprisingly , in the deep ocean , where it's mostly blue , the photoreceptors tend to see blue light .	也許不意外地 , 在深海裡 , 大部分是藍色的 , 攝影器通常會看到藍光 。
when there's a lot of chlorophyll around , they see a lot of green light .	當有很多葉綠色的環狀物時 , 它們會看到很多綠色的光 。
but they vary even more , possibly moving towards infrared and ultraviolet in the extremes .	但他們更加不同 , 可能會朝極端的紅外線和紫外線移動 。
just to try and get an assessment of what our gene repertoire was , we assembled all the data including all of ours thus far from the expedition , which represents more than half of all the gene data on the planet and it totaled around 29 million genes .	只是為了找出我們的基因複製品的評估 , 我們組合了所有資料 , 包括我們遠離探險的所有基因資料 , 這代表了地球上超過一半的基因資料 , 總共有大約2900萬個基因 。
and we tried to put these into gene families to see what these discoveries are: are we just discovering new members of known families , or are we discovering new families ?	我們試著把這些基因家庭放進基因中 , 看看這些發現是什麼:我們只是發現已知家庭的新成員 , 還是我們發現新的家庭 ?
and it turns out we have about 50 , 000 major gene families , but every new sample we take in the environment adds in a linear fashion to these new families .	結果發現 , 我們有大約五萬個主要的基因家庭 , 但每個我們在環境中的新樣本都加上線性時尚給這些新家庭 。
so we're at the earliest stages of discovery about basic genes , components and life on this planet .	我們正處於地球上最早的發現關於基本基因、元件和生命的最早階段 。
when we look at the socalled evolutionary tree , we're up on the upper righthand corner with the animals .	當我們看著所謂的演化樹 , 我們和動物的右上角 。
of those roughly 29 million genes , we only have around 24 , 000 in our genome .	其中大約有2900萬個基因 , 我們的基因組只有24 , 000個 。
and if you take all animals together , we probably share less than 30 , 000 and probably maybe a dozen or more thousand different gene families .	如果你把所有的動物集合起來 , 我們大概有不到三萬個 , 也許十幾個以上不同的基因家庭 。
i view that these genes are now not only the design components of evolution .	我覺得這些基因現在不僅是演化的設計元件 。
and we think in a genecentric view maybe going back to richard dawkins' ideas than in a genomecentric view , which are different constructs of these gene components .	我們認為 , 在普通的觀點上 , 或許可以回到理查德•達爾金斯的觀點 , 比起基因組成的觀點 , 這和這些基因組成的不同 。
synthetic dna , the ability to synthesize dna , has changed at sort of the same pace that dna sequencing has over the last decade or two , and is getting very rapid and very cheap .	合成dna , 合成dna的能力在過去十年或二十年間 , 改變了dna定序的速度 , 越來越快、非常便宜 。
our first thought about synthetic genomics came when we sequenced the second genome back in 1995 , and that from mycoplasma genitalium .	我們首先想到合成基因組學在1995年我們將第二種基因組定序然後從菌群生殖器中
and we have really nice tshirts that say , you know , " i heart my genitalium . "	我們有很棒的t恤 , 上面寫著: 「 我愛我的生殖器 。 」
this is actually just a microorganism .	這只是一個微生物 。
but it has roughly 500 genes .	但大約有500個基因 。
haemophilus had 1 , 800 genes .	hemophilus有180個基因
and we simply asked the question , if one species needs 800 , another 500 , is there a smaller set of genes that might comprise a minimal operating system ?	我們簡單地問這個問題 , 如果一個物種需要800種 , 另外500種 , 有一組小組的基因會組成一個最小的操作系統 ?
so we started doing transposon mutagenesis .	所以我們開始進行轉錄突變 。
transposons are just small pieces of dna that randomly insert in the genetic code .	傳播器只是基因編碼中隨機插入的小片段 。
and if they insert in the middle of the gene , they disrupt its function .	如果它們在基因的中間插入 , 它們會破壞它的功能 。
so we made a map of all the genes that could take transposon insertions and we called those " nonessential genes . "	所以我們做了一張地圖 , 所有可以接受轉換插入的基因 , 我們稱之為 「 無遺傳基因 」 。
but it turns out the environment is very critical for this , and you can only define an essential or nonessential gene based on exactly what's in the environment .	但事實證明 , 環境對此非常重要 , 你只能定義一個必要或無必要的基因 , 基於環境的本質 。
we also tried to take a more directly intellectual approach with the genomes of 13 related organisms , and we tried to compare all of those , to see what they had in common .	我們也試著用一個更直接的智力方法和13種相關生物的基因組進行比較 , 我們試著比較所有這些基因 , 看看它們有什麼共同點 。
and we got these overlapping circles . and we found only 173 genes common to all 13 organisms .	我們找到了這些重疊的圓形 。 我們發現 , 只有173個基因和13個有機體共通處 。
the pool expanded a little bit if we ignored one intracellular parasite ; it expanded even more when we looked at core sets of genes of around 310 or so .	如果我們忽略了一個細胞寄生蟲 , 它會擴展到更大的範圍 , 當我們看到大約310歲左右的核心基因組時 。
so we think that we can expand or contract genomes , depending on your point of view here , to maybe 300 to 400 genes from the minimal of 500 .	所以我們認為我們可以擴展或收縮基因組 , 取決於你這裡的觀點 , 到大約500到400個基因 。
the only way to prove these ideas was to construct an artificial chromosome with those genes in them , and we had to do this in a cassettebased fashion .	唯一能證明這些點子的方法是建立一個人造染色體 , 用這些基因組建構出 , 我們必須在一個基礎的時尚做這件事 。
we found that synthesizing accurate dna in large pieces was extremely difficult .	我們發現 , 在大片碎片中合成正確的dna是非常困難的 。
ham smith and clyde hutchison , my colleagues on this , developed an exciting new method that allowed us to synthesize a 5 , 000base pair virus in only a twoweek period that was 100 percent accurate , in terms of its sequence and its biology .	哈姆.史密斯和克萊德•哈特森 , 我同事開發了一種令人興奮的新方法 , 讓我們能在兩週期間合成五千多個鹼基對病毒 , 只有百分之百精確 , 以它的序列和生物學為基礎 。
it was a quite exciting experiment when we just took the synthetic piece of dna , injected it in the bacteria and all of a sudden , that dna started driving the production of the virus particles that turned around and then killed the bacteria .	這是個非常令人興奮的實驗 , 當我們把合成的dna注入細菌中 , 突然間 , dna開始啟動病毒粒子的生產 , 然後殺死細菌 。
this was not the first synthetic virus a polio virus had been made a year before but it was only one tenthousandth as active and it took three years to do .	這不是第一個合成病毒 , 一個小兒麻痺病毒在一年前被製造出來 , 但它只有一萬噸的活性 , 花了三年的時間 。
this is a cartoon of the structure of phi x 174 .	這是phhix174的圖形 。
this is a case where the software now builds its own hardware , and that's the notions that we have with biology .	這是一個軟體現在建立自己的硬體的案例 , 這就是我們對生物學的概念 。
people immediately jump to concerns about biological warfare , and i had recent testimony before a senate committee , and a special committee the u . s . government has set up to review this area .	人們馬上就開始關心生物戰事 , 我最近在參議院委員會之前有證詞 , 和美國政府設立了特殊委員會 , 來審查這個區域 。
and i think it's important to keep reality in mind , versus what happens with people's imaginations .	我認為 , 要讓現實保持在心中是很重要的 , 對抗人們的想像 。
basically , any virus that's been sequenced today that genome can be made .	基本上 , 任何現今已經被定序的病毒 , 基因組就可以完成 。
and people immediately freak out about things about ebola or smallpox , but the dna from this organism is not infective .	人們馬上對伊波拉或天花的事物感到驚訝 , 但這些有機體的dna並沒有感染 。
so even if somebody made the smallpox genome , that dna itself would not cause infections .	所以即使有人做出天花基因組 , dna本身不會造成感染 。
the real concern that security departments have is designer viruses .	真正關心的是安全部門是設計師的病毒 。
and there's only two countries , the u . s . and the former soviet union , that had major efforts on trying to create biological warfare agents .	只有兩個國家 , 美國和前蘇聯 , 試圖創造生物戰的代理 。
if that research is truly discontinued , there should be very little activity on the knowhow to make designer viruses in the future .	如果這項研究真的不停地持續下去 , 將來應該要有非常少的活動才能讓設計師的病毒在未來 。
i think singlecell organisms are possible within two years .	我認為單細胞生物在兩年內可能發生 。
and possibly eukaryotic cells , those that we have , are possible within a decade .	可能是真菌細胞 , 我們這些細胞 , 在十年內就有可能發生 。
so we're now making several dozen different constructs , because we can vary the cassettes and the genes that go into this artificial chromosome .	我們現在製造了數十種不同的構造 , 因為我們可以改變這種人造染色體的類型和基因 。
the key is , how do you put all of the others ?	關鍵在於 , 你要如何把所有其他的東西放進去 ?
we start with these fragments , and then we have a homologous recombination system that reassembles those into a chromosome .	我們從這些碎片開始 , 然後我們有一個同質的重組系統 , 將它們重新組合成染色體 。
this is derived from an organism , deinococcus radiodurans , that can take three million rads of radiation and not be killed .	這是從一個有機體中衍生出來的 , 排斥無線電的無線電生物 , 可以承受三百萬的輻射 , 而不是被殺 。
it reassembles its genome after this radiation burst in about 12 to 24 hours , after its chromosomes are literally blown apart .	在輻射爆發後 , 它會重新組合它的基因體大約12到24小時 , 在它的染色體被拆解之後 。
this organism is ubiquitous on the planet , and exists perhaps now in outer space due to all our travel there .	這種生物在地球上無所不在 , 也許現在存在於外太空 , 是因為我們在那裡的旅程 。
this is a glass beaker after about half a million rads of radiation .	這是個玻璃賭場 , 經過50萬次的輻射之後 。
the glass started to burn and crack , while the microbes sitting in the bottom just got happier and happier .	玻璃開始燃燒和裂縫 , 而微生物在底部的微生物就變得更快樂、更快樂 。
here's an actual picture of what happens: the top of this shows the genome after 1 . 7 million rads of radiation .	這張照片是實際發生的狀況:這張圖表顯示了170萬次的輻射後的基因組 。
the chromosome is literally blown apart .	染色體的確分裂了 。
and here's that same dna automatically reassembled 24 hours later .	同樣的dna在24小時後自動重新組合 。
it's truly stunning that these organisms can do that , and we probably have thousands , if not tens of thousands , of different species on this planet that are capable of doing that .	真正令人驚訝的是 , 這些生物能做到這一點 , 我們可能有數千種 , 如果地球上沒有成千上萬種不同的物種 , 能夠做到 。
after these genomes are synthesized , the first step is just transplanting them into a cell without a genome .	在這些基因組合之後 , 第一步就是將它們移植到一個沒有基因組的細胞中 。
so we think synthetic cells are going to have tremendous potential , not only for understanding the basis of biology but for hopefully environmental and society issues .	所以我們認為合成細胞將會有巨大的潛力 , 不僅是為了了解生物學的基礎 , 還為了希望環境和社會問題 。
for example , from the third organism we sequenced , methanococcus jannaschii it lives in boiling water temperatures ; its energy source is hydrogen and all its carbon comes from co2 it captures back from the environment .	例如 , 從我們所測定的第三個有機體 , 珍納西 , 它住在沸騰的水溫 ; 它的能量來源是氫和碳 , 來自於環境中的二氧化碳 。
so we know lots of different pathways , thousands of different organisms now that live off of co2 , and can capture that back .	所以我們知道許多不同的路徑 , 成千上萬的生物 , 活在二氧化碳之外 , 還能捕捉到它 。
so instead of using carbon from oil for synthetic processes , we have the chance of using carbon and capturing it back from the atmosphere , converting that into biopolymers or other products .	所以 , 我們不用石油來製造合成過程 , 我們有機會使用碳 , 從大氣中捕捉它 , 將它轉換成生物聚合物或其它產品 。
we have one organism that lives off of carbon monoxide , and we use as a reducing power to split water to produce hydrogen and oxygen .	我們有一種有機體存在於一氧化碳之外 , 我們用它來分解水來產生氫和氧氣 。
also , there's numerous pathways that can be engineered metabolizing methane .	此外 , 有許多通路可以被工程代謝甲烷 。
and dupont has a major program with statoil in norway to capture and convert the methane from the gas fields there into useful products .	杜邦有一個重大的計畫 , 在挪威 , 用來捕捉並將甲烷從氣體領域轉換成有用的產品 。
within a short while , i think there's going to be a new field called " combinatorial genomics , " because with these new synthesis capabilities , these vast gene array repertoires and the homologous recombination , we think we can design a robot to make maybe a million different chromosomes a day .	短短時間內 , 我認為會有一種新的領域叫做 「 組合基因組 」 , 因為這些新合成的能力 , 這些巨大的基因組組組組組合 , 以及同性組合 , 我們認為我們可以設計一個機器人 , 一天可以製造出百萬種不同的染色體 。
and therefore , as with all biology , you get selection through screening , whether you're screening for hydrogen production , or chemical production , or just viability .	因此 , 如同所有的生物學 , 透過篩選 , 不論你在篩選氫化生產或化學產量 , 或只是可行性 。
to understand the role of these genes is going to be well within reach .	若要了解這些基因的角色 , 會很快就會到達 。
we're trying to modify photosynthesis to produce hydrogen directly from sunlight .	我們試著修改光合作用 , 直接從陽光中產生氫 。
photosynthesis is modulated by oxygen , and we have an oxygeninsensitive hydrogenase that we think will totally change this process .	光合作用被氧氣調節 , 我們有一種氧氣敏感性氫氣 , 我們認為會徹底改變這個過程 。
we're also combining cellulases , the enzymes that break down complex sugars into simple sugars and fermentation in the same cell for producing ethanol .	我們也在結合纖維 , 酵素會將複雜的糖分解成簡單的糖和發酵 , 在同一個細胞中產生乙醇的酵素 。
pharmaceutical production is already under way in major laboratories using microbes .	製藥生產已經在使用微生物的主要實驗室裡進行 。
the chemistry from compounds in the environment is orders of magnitude more complex than our best chemists can produce .	環境中的化合物所產生的化學成分比我們最好的化學家所產生的複雜得多 。
i think future engineered species could be the source of food , hopefully a source of energy , environmental remediation and perhaps replacing the petrochemical industry .	我認為 , 未來的工程物種可能是食物的來源 , 希望是能源、環境復甦 , 也許取代石化產業 。
let me just close with ethical and policy studies .	讓我用道德和政策研究來結束 。
we delayed the start of our experiments in 1999 until we completed a yearandahalf bioethical review as to whether we should try and make an artificial species .	我們在1999年把實驗的開端延遲 , 直到我們完成了一年半的生物倫理審查 , 來審查我們是否應該嘗試製造一個人造物種 。
every major religion participated in this .	每個主要的宗教都參與其中 。
it was actually a very strange study , because the various religious leaders were using their scriptures as law books , and they couldn't find anything in them prohibiting making life , so it must be ok . the only ultimate concerns were biological warfare aspects of this , but gave us the go ahead to start these experiments for the reasons we were doing them .	這其實是一項非常奇怪的研究 , 因為各式各樣的宗教領袖用他們的文字作為法律書籍 , 他們找不到禁止製造生命的任何東西 , 所以這一定是好的 。 最後的關注是生物戰的面向 , 但給了我們 , 要開始這些實驗 , 原因是我們在做這些實驗的原因 。
right now the sloan foundation has just funded a multiinstitutional study on this , to work out what the risk and benefits to society are , and the rules that scientific teams such as my own should be using in this area , and we're trying to set good examples as we go forward .	現在 , 史隆基金會剛資助了一份多體制的研究 , 來找出對社會的風險和利益是什麼 , 以及科學團隊的規則 , 如同我自己的團隊應該在這個領域中使用的 , 我們正試著設立好的例子 。
these are complex issues .	這些都是複雜的問題 。
except for the threat of bioterrorism , they're very simple issues in terms of , can we design things to produce clean energy , perhaps revolutionizing what developing countries can do and provide through various simple processes .	除了生物恐怖主義的威脅之外 , 它們是非常簡單的議題 , 我們能設計東西來產生乾淨能源 , 也許革新開發中國家能做什麼 , 提供各種簡單的過程 。
psychologist philip zimbardo says happiness and success are rooted in a trait most of us disregard: the way we orient toward the past , present and future . he suggests we calibrate our outlook on time as a first step to improving our lives .	心理學家philipzimbardo說幸福和成功根源於我們大多數人對過去的看法、現在和未來的看法 。 他建議我們在時代的第一步以改善我們的生活 。
brain , business , happiness , mind , psychology , science	大腦、商業、快樂、心智、心理學、科學、科學、
philip zimbardo prescribes a healthy take on time	philipzimbardo的處方是一段健康的時期
i want to share with you some ideas about the secret power of time , in a very short time .	我想和大家分享一些關於時間的秘密力量的想法 , 在很短的時間內 。
video: all right , start the clock please . 30 seconds studio .	影片:好的 , 開始時鐘 。 三十秒的工作室 。
keep it quiet please . settle down .	讓它安靜下來 。 安頓下來 。
it's about time . end sequence . take one .	時間到了 , 結束序列 。 拿一個 。
10 , nine , eight , seven , six , five , four , three , two . . .	10、9、8、7、6、5、4、3、2......
philip zimbardo: let's tune into the conversation of the principals in adam's temptation .	菲利浦辛巴巴多:咱們來談談亞當的誘惑 。
" come on adam , don't be so wishywashy . take a bite . " " i did . "	「 拜託 , 不要太清醒了 。 拿一點點 。 」 「 我真的 。 」
" one bite , adam . don't abandon eve . "	「 一隻咬 , 亞當 , 不要放棄eve 。 」
" i don't know , guys .	「 我不知道 , 各位 。
i don't want to get in trouble . "	我不想惹麻煩 。 」
" okay . one bite . what the hell ? "	「 好吧 。 稍微一點 。 地獄到底是什麼 ? 」
life is temptation . it's all about yielding , resisting , yes , no , now , later , impulsive , reflective , present focus and future focus .	生命是誘惑 。 重點是產量、抗拒 , 是的 , 之後 , 衝動、反射、焦點和未來的焦點 。
promised virtues fall prey to the passions of the moment .	承諾美德會陷入當下的熱情 。
of teenage girls who pledged sexual abstinence and virginity until marriage thank you george bush the majority , 60 percent , yielded to sexual temptations within one year .	在十幾歲的女孩中 , 她們的性別缺陷和處女 , 直到婚姻 , 感謝你喬治布希大多 , 百分之六十 , 在一年內得到性誘惑 。
and most of them did so without using birth control .	大部分的人不用生育控制 。
so much for promises .	許多的承諾 。
now lets tempt fouryearolds , giving them a treat .	現在讓我們嘗試四歲的孩子 , 給他們一個治療 。
they can have one marshmallow now . but if they wait until the experimenter comes back , they can have two .	他們現在可以有一顆棉花糖 , 但如果他們等到實驗人員回來 , 他們就能有兩顆 。
of course it pays , if you like marshmallows , to wait .	當然 , 要是你喜歡棉花糖 , 才能等待 。
what happens is twothirds of the kids give in to temptation .	接下來發生的是三分之二的孩子給誘惑 。
they cannot wait . the others , of course , wait .	他們不能等 。 當然 , 其他的 , 等等 。
they resist the temptation . they delay the now for later .	他們抗拒誘惑 , 等一下會延遲 。
walter mischel , my colleague at stanford , went back 14 years later , to try to discover what was different about those kids .	我在史丹佛大學的同事 , 回到14年後 , 試著去發現那些孩子的不同之處 。
there were enormous differences between kids who resisted and kids who yielded , in many ways .	有很大的差異 , 他們抗拒和孩子的差異 , 在許多層面上都很大 。
the kids who resisted scored 250 points higher on the sat .	那些抗拒分數的孩子在現場高出250分 。
that's enormous . that's like a whole set of different iq points .	這很巨大 。 這就像是一整組不同的智商點 。
they didn't get in as much trouble . they were better students .	他們沒有遇到太多麻煩 , 他們是更好的學生 。
they were selfconfident and determined . and the key for me today , the key for you , is , they were futurefocused rather than presentfocused .	他們是自信且有決心的 。 今天 , 對你來說 , 關鍵在於 , 他們是未來的專注 , 而不是現在的專注 。
so what is time perspective ? that's what i'm going to talk about today .	所以 , 時間的觀點是什麼 ? 這就是我今天要談的 。
