time perspective is the study of how individuals , all of us , divide the flow of your human experience into time zones or time categories .	時間觀點是研究個人、我們所有人 , 將你人類的經驗分割成時間區或時間分類 。
and you do it automatically and nonconsciously .	而且你會自動且無意識地做 。
they vary between cultures , between nations , between individuals , between social classes , between education levels .	他們在文化、國家、個人、社會階級、教育層面之間的差異 。
and the problem is that they can become biased , because you learn to overuse some of them and underuse the others .	問題是 , 它們會變得偏見 , 因為你會學會過度使用它們 , 因而破壞其他的 。
what determines any decision you make ?	你做了什麼決定 ?
you make a decision on which you're going to base an action .	你做一個決定 , 決定你要採取行動 。
for some people it's only about what is in the immediate situation , what other people are doing and what you're feeling .	對某些人而言 , 只有在當下的情況下 , 其他人在做什麼 , 以及你感覺的是什麼 。
and those people , when they make their decisions in that format we're going to call them " presentoriented , " because their focus is what is now .	那些人 , 當他們在那樣的形式中做出決定時 , 我們會稱他們為 「 現狀 」 , 因為他們的焦點是現在的 。
for others , the present is irrelevant .	對其他人來說 , 現在是不相關的 。
it's always about " what is this situation like that i've experienced in the past ? "	總是在說 「 我過去經歷過的情況是什麼 ? 」
so that their decisions are based on past memories .	所以他們的決定是基於過去記憶 。
and we're going to call those people " pastoriented , " because they focus on what was .	我們會把這些人稱之為 「 牧草原 」 , 因為他們專注於什麼 。
for others it's not the past , it's not the present , it's only about the future .	對其他人來說 , 不是過去 , 也不是現在 , 而是關於未來 。
their focus is always about anticipated consequences .	他們的焦點總是在於預期後的結果 。
we're going to call them " futureoriented . " their focus is on what will be .	我們稱他們為 「 未來主義 」 , 他們的焦點在於未來是什麼 。
so , time paradox , i want to argue , the paradox of time perspective , is something that influences every decision you make , you're totally unaware of .	所以 , 時間悖論 , 我想說的是時間觀點的矛盾 , 是影響你做出的每一個決定 , 你完全不知道的 。
namely , the extent to which you have one of these biased time perspectives .	也就是說 , 你有這種偏見時間觀點的程度 。
well there is actually six of them . there are two ways to be presentoriented .	其實有六個 。 有兩種方式可以被呈現出來 。
there is two ways to be pastoriented , two ways to be future .	有兩種方式可以被放牧 , 有兩種方式可以成為未來 。
you can focus on pastpositive , or pastnegative .	你可以把焦點放在正向或負面的 。
you can be presenthedonistic , namely you focus on the joys of life , or presentfatalist it doesn't matter , your life is controlled .	你可以是現代主義者 , 即你專注於人生的喜悅 , 或現代主義者──這無所謂 , 你的人生被控制了 。
you can be futureoriented , setting goals .	你可以是未來的、設定的目標 。
or you can be transcendental future: namely , life begins after death .	或者 , 你可以是超現實的未來:生命始於死亡 。
developing the mental flexibility to shift time perspectives fluidly depending on the demands of the situation , that's what you've got to learn to do .	開發心理靈活性 , 讓時間觀點流暢地依賴情況的需求 , 這就是你要學會做的事 。
so , very quickly , what is the optimal time profile ?	很快地 , 最佳的時間檔案是什麼 ?
high on pastpositive . moderately high on future .	非常正向的 。 在未來 , 現代的高度 。
and moderate on presenthedonism .	現代主義的現代主義 。
and always low on pastnegative and presentfatalism .	總是低於負面和現代主義 。
so the optimal temporal mix is what you get from the past pastpositive gives you roots . you connect your family , identity and your self .	所以 , 最佳的暫停混合是你從過去的傾向給你根 。 你連結你的家庭、身份和你的自我 。
what you get from the future is wings to soar to new destinations , new challenges .	你從未來得到的 , 是翅膀 , 到新的目的地 , 新的挑戰 。
what you get from the present hedonism is the energy , the energy to explore yourself , places , people , sensuality .	你從現在的衛生主義得到的是能量 , 去探索自己、地點、人、感官 。
any time perspective in excess has more negatives than positives .	任何時間 , 過量的負面觀點 , 都比正面多 。
what do futures sacrifice for success ?	未來如何犧牲成功 ?
they sacrifice family time . they sacrifice friend time .	他們犧牲家庭時間 , 犧牲朋友的時間 。
they sacrifice fun time . they sacrifice personal indulgence .	它們犧牲了好玩的時間 , 它們犧牲了個人的成分 。
they sacrifice hobbies . and they sacrifice sleep . so it affects their health .	他們犧牲了嗜好 , 他們犧牲了睡眠 。 所以這會影響他們的健康 。
and they live for work , achievement and control .	他們活在工作上、成就和控制中 。
i'm sure that resonates with some of the tedsters .	我確信和一些ted的演講會產生共鳴 。
and it resonated for me . i grew up as a poor kid in the south bronx ghetto , a sicilian family everyone lived in the past and present .	這對我產生共鳴 。 我在南布朗克斯ghetto的一個貧窮孩子 , 一個西尼裔家庭 , 所有人都住在過去和現在 。
i'm here as a futureoriented person who went over the top , who did all these sacrifices because teachers intervened , and made me future oriented .	我來到這裡 , 身為一個有前途的人 , 他走過頂端 , 做這些犧牲 , 是因為老師介入 , 讓我成為未來的方向 。
told me don't eat that marshmallow , because if you wait you're going to get two of them , until i learned to balance out .	告訴我不要吃棉花糖 , 因為如果你等著你得到兩個 , 直到我學會了平衡 。
i've added presenthedonism , i've added a focus on the pastpositive , so , at 76 years old , i am more energetic than ever , more productive , and i'm happier than i have ever been .	我加入了現在的殖民主義 , 我把焦點放在 「 正面 」 , 在76歲時 , 我比以往更活躍 , 更有生產力 , 我比以前更快樂 。
i just want to say that we are applying this to many world problems: changing the dropout rates of school kids , combating addictions , enhancing teen health , curing vets' ptsd with time metaphors getting miracle cures promoting sustainability and conservation , reducing physical rehabilitation where there is a 50percent drop out rate , altering appeals to suicidal terrorists , and modifying family conflicts as timezone clashes .	我只想說我們應用在許多世界問題上:改變學校的輟學率 , 加強青少年健康 , 治癒創傷後壓力症候群 , 讓奇蹟能夠促進永續發展和保育 , 降低了50%的人口退休率 , 轉變為自殺的恐怖份子 , 轉變為自殺的恐怖分子 , 轉變了家族的衝突 。
so i want to end by saying: many of life's puzzles can be solved by understanding your time perspective and that of others .	最後我想說的是:許多生命的謎題可以透過了解你的時間觀和其他人的觀點來解決 。
and the idea is so simple , so obvious , but i think the consequences are really profound .	這個想法很簡單 , 很明顯 , 但我認為後果很深遠 。
how many of today's headlines will matter in 100 years ? 1000 ? kirk citron's " long news " project collects stories that not only matter today , but will resonate for decades even centuries to come . at ted2010 , he highlights recent headlines with the potential to shape our future .	在一百年內 , 今天的頭條有多少人會很重要 ? 一百年 ? 柯克•克倫的 「 漫長新聞 」 計畫收集現今重要的故事 , 數十年來 , 甚至數十年 , 在ted2010年 , 他針對我們未來的潛力標題 。
future , global issues , media , news , science	未來 , 全球議題、媒體、新聞、科學、科學、科學、科學等問題 。
kirk citron: and now , the real news	kirkcitron:現在 , 真正的消息是真實的消息 。
we are drowning in news .	我們在新聞中淹沒了 。
reuters alone puts out three and a half million news stories a year .	光是路透師一年就提出了三百五十萬則新聞報導 。
that's just one source .	這只是其中一個來源 。
my question is: how many of those stories are actually going to matter in the long run ?	我的問題是:在長期來看 , 這些故事中有多少會被影響 ?
that's the idea behind the long news .	這就是長期新聞背後的想法 。
it's a project by the long now foundation , which was founded by tedsters including kevin kelly and stewart brand .	這是一個長期基金會的計畫 , 由tedsters所創立 , 包括kevinkelly和stewart品牌 。
and what we're looking for is news stories that might still matter 50 or 100 or 10 , 000 years from now .	我們在尋找的新聞 , 可能仍然重要50、100、100 , 000年 。
and when you look at the news through that filter , a lot falls by the wayside .	當你看那些過濾器的消息時 , 通常會被一邊倒下 。
to take the top stories from the a . p . this last year , is this going to matter in a decade ?	為了從a.p.這一年來 , 這在十年內是很重要的嗎 ?
is this going to matter in 50 or 100 years ?	這在50或100年後會有什麼影響嗎 ?
okay , that was kind of cool .	好吧 , 那有點酷 。
but the top story of this past year was the economy , and i'm just betting that , sooner or later , this particular recession is going to be old news .	但 , 去年的頂尖故事是經濟 , 我只是打賭 , 不久之後 , 這個特殊的衰退將會是舊的消息 。
so , what kind of stories might make a difference for the future ?	所以 , 什麼樣的故事對未來有什麼影響 ?
well , let's take science .	嗯 , 咱們來談科學 。
someday , little robots will go through our bloodstreams fixing things .	有一天 , 小機器人會穿過我們的血液循環 , 固定東西 。
that someday is already here if you're a mouse .	有些時候你已經在這裡了 , 如果你是老鼠 。
some recent stories: nanobees zap tumors with real bee venom ; they're sending genes into the brain ; a robot they built that can crawl through the human body .	最近一些故事:奈米粒子用真正的蜜蜂毒液將基因送入腦中 ; 一個機器人 , 可以爬過人體 。
what about resources ? how are we going to feed nine billion people ?	資源呢 ? 我們要如何餵飽九十億人 ?
we're having trouble feeding six billion today .	現今我們有六十億的難題 。
as we heard yesterday , there's over a billion people hungry .	正如昨天我們聽到的 , 有超過十億人挨餓 。
britain will starve without genetically modified crops .	英國會餓死沒有基因改造作物 。
bill gates , fortunately , has bet a billion on [agricultural] research .	幸運的是 , 比爾蓋茲有十億人在虛擬研究上 。
what about global politics ?	那麼全球政治呢 ?
the world's going to be very different when and if china sets the agenda , and they may .	世界將會非常不同 , 如果中國設定了這個議程 , 他們可能會 。
they've overtaken the u . s . as the world's biggest car market , they've overtaken germany as the largest exporter , and they've started doing dna tests on kids to choose their careers .	他們已經超越美國作為世界上最大的汽車市場 , 他們已經超越了德國 , 成為最大的出口國 , 他們開始在孩子身上做dna檢測 , 來選擇他們的職業 。
we're finding all kinds of ways to push back the limits of what we know .	我們在尋找各種方法 , 把我們所知的極限推回來 。
some recent discoveries: there's an ant colony from argentina that has now spread to every continent but antarctica ; there's a selfdirected robot scientist that's made a discovery soon , science may no longer need us , and life may no longer need us either ; a microbe wakes up after 120 , 000 years .	最近的一些發現:阿根廷有一隻螞蟻群 , 現在已經散播到每個大陸 , 但南極洲 , 有一個自主導的機器人科學家很快就發現了 , 科學可能不再需要我們了 , 生命可能也不再需要我們了 ; 一個微生物在120 , 000年之後出現 。
it seems that with or without us , life will go on .	似乎與我們無關 , 生命會繼續下去 。
but my pick for the top long news story of this past year was this one: water found on the moon .	但今年我選的長新聞故事是這個:在月球上發現水 。
makes it a lot easier to put a colony up there .	把蟻群放在那裡 , 讓蟻群變得更容易 。
and if nasa doesn't do it , china might , or somebody in this room might write a big check .	如果美國太空總署不這麼做 , 中國可能 , 或在這間房間裡的人可能會寫一支大支票 。
my point is this: in the long run , some news stories are more important than others .	我的重點是:長期來看 , 有些新聞故事比其他人更重要 。
planetary scientist carolyn porco shows images from the cassini voyage to saturn , focusing on its largest moon , titan , and on frozen enceladus , which seems to shoot jets of ice .	行星科學家卡羅林•波科展示了卡西尼航行到土星的圖像 , 把焦點放在它最大的月球、霸主、冰冷的土衛二上 , 這似乎是用來射擊冰的射線 。
nasa , design , exploration , science , space , technology , universe , visualizations	美國太空總署、設計、探索、科學、太空科技、宇宙、視覺化化、視覺化 。
carolyn porco flies us to saturn	卡奧林•潘朵科飛了我們 , 來土星 。
in the next 18 minutes , i'm going to take you on a journey .	在接下來的18分鐘裡 , 我要帶各位踏上一段旅程 。
and it's a journey that you and i have been on for many years now , and it began some 50 years ago , when humans first stepped off our planet .	這是你和我的旅程 , 已經有好幾年了 , 五十年前 , 人類第一次離開地球 。
and in those 50 years , not only did we literally , physically set foot on the moon , but we have dispatched robotic spacecraft to all the planets all eight of them and we have landed on asteroids , we have rendezvoused with comets , and , at this point in time , we have a spacecraft on its way to pluto , the body formerly known as a planet .	在那五十年間 , 我們不僅僅在月球上設定了一腳 , 我們已經把機器人太空船放到所有行星上 , 我們登陸了小行星 , 我們已經帶著彗星重生 , 此時此刻 , 我們有一艘太空船 , 飛往冥王星的路上 , 前所知的星球 。
and all of these robotic missions are part of a bigger human journey: a voyage to understand something , to get a sense of our cosmic place , to understand something of our origins , and how earth , our planet , and we , living on it , came to be .	所有這些機械任務都是更大的人類旅程的一部分:一趟探險 , 去了解我們的宇宙 , 去了解我們的起源 , 了解我們的起源 , 以及地球、地球、地球、地球、我們 , 都活在其中 。
and of all the places in the solar system that we might go to and search for answers to questions like this , there's saturn . and we have been to saturn before we visited saturn in the early 1980s but our investigations of saturn have become far more indepth in detail since the cassini spacecraft , traveling across interplanetary space for seven years , glided into orbit around saturn in the summer of 2004 , and became at that point the farthest robotic outpost that humanity had ever established around the sun .	在太陽系中的所有地方 , 我們可能去尋找這個問題的答案 , 有土星 。 我們去過土星 。 我們在1980年代初去過土星 , 但我們對土星的調查已經變得更獨立了 , 自卡西尼太空船飛行了七年 , 在2004年夏天 , 飛越了星際空間 , 進入了軌道 , 成為人類在地球上創造出的最遠距離 。
now , the saturn system is a rich planetary system .	土星系統是一個豐富的行星系統 。
it offers mystery , scientific insight and obviously splendor beyond compare , and the investigation of this system has enormous cosmic reach .	它提供了神秘、科學的洞見 , 很明顯地 , 除了相對之外 , 還有這個系統的調查有著巨大的宇宙 。
in fact , just studying the rings alone , we stand to learn a lot about the discs of stars and gas that we call the spiral galaxies .	事實上 , 光是研究環節 , 我們就站在學習很多星體和氣體的圓盤 , 我們稱之為螺旋星系 。
and here's a beautiful picture of the andromeda nebula , which is our closest , largest spiral galaxy to the milky way .	這裡有一張漂亮的andromedanebula的照片 , 它是我們最近的 , 最大的螺旋星系 , 到銀河系 。
and then , here's a beautiful composite of the whirlpool galaxy , taken by the hubble space telescope .	接著 , 這是由哈伯太空望遠鏡所拍攝的美麗的組合 。
so the journey back to saturn is really part of and is also a metaphor for a much larger human voyage to understand the interconnectedness of everything around us , and also how humans fit into that picture .	所以 , 回到土星的旅程是非常重要的 , 也是更大的人類旅程的比喻 , 來了解我們周圍的事物之間的關聯性 , 以及人類如何融入這張圖片中 。
and it pains me that i can't tell you all that we have learned with cassini .	這讓我感到很痛苦 , 我無法告訴你們 , 我們從卡西尼尼學到的所有東西 。
i can't show you all the beautiful pictures that we've taken in the last two and a half years , because i simply don't have the time .	我不能給你們看過去兩年半以來我們拍過的美麗照片 , 因為我根本沒有時間 。
so i'm going to concentrate on two of the most exciting stories that have emerged out of this major exploratory expedition that we are conducting around saturn , and have been for the past two and a half years .	我將專注於其中兩個最令人興奮的故事 , 來自於我們在土星周圍進行的探險 , 過去兩年來一直都是如此 。
saturn is accompanied by a very large and diverse collection of moons .	土星被一大群多樣化的衛星集合在一起 。
they range in size from a few kilometers across to as big across as the u . s .	它們的大小從幾公里長到和美國一樣大 。
most of the beautiful pictures we've taken of saturn , in fact , show saturn in accompaniment with some of its moons . here's saturn with dione , and then , here's saturn showing the rings edgeon , showing you just how vertically thin they are , with the moon enceladus .	大部分我們拍攝過土星的美麗照片 , 事實上 , 土星和它的衛星共存 。 這是土星的土星 , 土星上有石頭 , 接著 , 土星展示了環繞的邊緣 , 向你們展示它們有多薄 , 和月球有多薄 。
now , two of the 47 moons that saturn has are standouts .	土星的四十七個衛星中有兩個是站立的 。
and those are titan and enceladus . titan is saturn's largest moon , and , until cassini had arrived there , was the largest single expanse of unexplored terrain that we had remaining in our solar system .	這些是土衛六和土衛二 。 土衛六是土星最大的月球 , 直到卡西尼抵達那裡 , 是我們太陽系中最大的未探索的地形 。
and it is a body that has long intrigued people who've watched the planets .	它是一個身體有很長的好奇心人士 , 他們看過行星 。
it has a very large , thick atmosphere , and in fact , its surface environment was believed to be more like the environment we have here on the earth , or at least had in the past , than any other body in the solar system .	它有一個很大、很厚的大氣層 , 事實上 , 它的表面環境被認為比較像地球上的環境 , 至少過去的太陽系中任何其他身體 。
its atmosphere is largely molecular nitrogen , like you are breathing here in this room , except that its atmosphere is suffused with simple organic materials like methane and propane and ethane .	它的大氣層主要是分子氮 , 就像你在這裡呼吸 , 除了它的大氣中含有簡單的有機物質 , 如甲烷、丙烷和乙烷 。
and these molecules high up in the atmosphere of titan get broken down , and their products join together to make haze particles .	而這些分子在土衛六的大氣中被分解 , 它們的產品結合在一起 , 製造出大氣粒子 。
this haze is ubiquitous . it's completely global and enveloping titan .	這種混亂是無所不在的 , 完全是全球化的 , 並且包含土衛六 。
and that's why you cannot see down to the surface with our eyes in the visible region of the spectrum .	這就是為什麼在光譜的可見區域看不到表面 。
but these haze particles , it was surmised , before we got there with cassini , over billions and billions of years , gently drifted down to the surface and coated the surface in a thick organic sludge .	但這些黑暗的粒子被推斷 , 在我們和卡西尼一起到達之前 , 數十億年 , 溫柔地漂移到表面 , 並在厚厚的有機煙中覆蓋著表面 。
so like the equivalent , the titan equivalent , of tar , or oil , or what we didn't know what .	像泰坦一樣 , 油 , 油 , 或油 , 或我們不知道什麼 。
but this is what we suspected . and these molecules , especially methane and ethane , can be liquids at the surface temperatures of titan .	但這是我們懷疑的 。 這些分子 , 尤其是甲烷和乙烷 , 可以在土衛二的表面溫度 。
and so it turns out that methane is to titan what water is to the earth .	結果發現 , 甲烷就是土衛六 , 水對地球的意義 。
it's a condensable in the atmosphere , and so recognizing this circumstance brought to the fore a whole world of bizarre possibilities . you can have methane clouds , ok , and above those clouds , you have this hundreds of kilometers of haze , which prevent any sunlight from getting to the surface .	在大氣中 , 它是可以凝結的 , 承認這個環境會帶來整個奇怪的可能性 。 你可以有甲烷雲 , 在這些雲上 , 你有上百公里的霧狀物 , 可以防止太陽到達表面 。
the temperature at the surface is some 350 degrees below zero fahrenheit .	表面的溫度低於華氏零度350度 。
but despite that cold , you could have rain falling down on the surface of titan .	但儘管那寒冷 , 土衛六的表面仍可以下降 。
and doing on titan what rain does on the earth: it carves gullies ; it forms rivers and cataracts ; it can create canyons ; it can pool in large basins and craters .	在土衛六上 , 降雨在地球上 , 它會雕刻猜測 ; 它會形成河流和白內障 ; 它能創造峽谷 ; 它能在大盆地和隕石中戳進來 。
it can wash the sludge off high mountain peaks and hills , down into the lowlands . so stop and think for a minute .	它可以把稀釋的山峰和山丘洗掉 , 進入低地 。 所以停下來思考一下 。
try to imagine what the surface of titan might look like .	試想一下泰坦的表面會是什麼樣子 。
it's dark . high noon on titan is as dark as deep earth twilight on the earth .	它是黑暗的 , 土衛六上的高點跟地球的深光一樣暗 。
it's cold , it's eerie , it's misty , it might be raining , and you might be standing on the shores of lake michigan brimming with paint thinner .	很冷 , 很噁心 , 很噁心 , 可能會下雨 , 你可能會站在密西根湖邊的邊緣 , 用油漆薄薄的薄膜 。
that is the view that we had of the surface of titan before we got there with cassini , and i can tell you that what we have found on titan , though it is not the same in detail , is every bit as fascinating as that story is .	這是我們在泰坦的表面之前所看到的景象 , 是我們和卡西尼一起到達的 , 我可以告訴各位 , 我們在泰坦所發現的 , 雖然細節和故事的真相不同 。
and for us , it has been like the cassini people it has been like a jules verne adventure come true .	對我們來說 , 這就像是卡西尼人 , 它就像是一場朱利•凡內斯的冒險 。
as i said , it has a thick , extensive atmosphere .	如我所說 , 它的大氣層很厚 , 很大 。
this is a picture of titan , backlit by the sun , with the rings as a beautiful backdrop .	這是一張泰坦的照片 , 太陽的背景 , 光環是美麗的背景 。
and yet another moon there i don't even know which one it is . it's a very extensive atmosphere .	另外一個月亮 , 我甚至不知道是哪一個 。 這是個非常廣闊的大氣層 。
we have instruments on cassini which can see down to the surface through this atmosphere , and my camera system is one of them .	我們有卡西尼號的儀器 , 可以透過大氣層看到表面 , 我的攝影系統是其中之一 。
and we have taken pictures like this .	我們拍了像這樣的照片 。
and what you see is bright and dark regions , and that's about as far as it got for us .	你看到的是明亮、黑暗的區域 , 正好是對我們來說的距離 。
it was so mystifying: we couldn't make out what we were seeing on titan .	真是太神秘了:我們無法弄清楚我們在土衛六上所看到的 。
when you look closer at this region , you start to see things like sinuous channels we didn't know . you see a few round things .	當你仔細觀察這個區域 , 你就會看到一些我們不知道的東西 。 你看到一些圓形的東西 。
this , we later found out , is , in fact , a crater , but there are very few craters on the surface of titan , meaning it's a very young surface .	後來我們發現 , 其實是一個坑 , 但土衛六表面上有很少的隕石坑 , 意味著它是非常年輕的表面 。
and there are features that look tectonic .	有些特徵看起來像電子 。
they look like they've been pulled apart .	他們看起來像被拉開一樣 。
whenever you see anything linear on a planet , it means there's been a fracture , like a fault .	每當你在星球上看到任何線條時 , 它就意味著有一個裂痕 , 像是一個錯 。
and so it's been tectonically altered .	所以 , 它已經有了地質上的改變 。
but we couldn't make sense of our images , until , six months after we got into orbit , an event occurred that many have regarded as the highlight of cassini's investigation of titan .	但我們無法理解我們的影像 , 直到我們進入軌道六個月後 , 一個事件發生了 , 許多事件都被視為是泰坦的調查的高點 。
and that was the deployment of the huygens probe , the europeanbuilt huygens probe that cassini had carried for seven years across the solar system . we deployed it to the atmosphere of titan , it took two and a half hours to descend , and it landed on the surface .	這是胡布斯探測器的部署 , 歐洲builthuygens探測器在太陽系中運行了七年 。 我們將它部署到土衛六的大氣層 , 花了兩個半小時 , 才能抵達地表 。
and i just want to emphasize how significant an event this is .	我只想強調這有多重要 。
this is a device of human making , and it landed in the outer solar system for the first time in human history .	這是人類製造的裝置 , 它在人類歷史上第一次登陸太陽系 。
it is so significant that , in my mind , this was an event that should have been celebrated with ticker tape parades in every city across the u . s . and europe , and sadly , that wasn't the case .	很明顯 , 在我看來 , 這是個事件 , 應該要在美國和歐洲各地慶祝 , 不幸的是 , 這並非如此 。
it was significant for another reason . this is an international mission , and this event was celebrated in europe , in germany , and the celebratory presentations were given in english accents , and american accents , and german accents , and french and italian and dutch accents .	這很重要 , 原因是 , 這是國際任務 , 而這個事件在歐洲、德國、慶祝 , 以及慶祝的簡報 , 都是英文的口音、美國口音、德語、法語、義大利語和荷蘭口音 。
it was a moving demonstration of what the words " united nations " are supposed to mean: a true union of nations joined together in a colossal effort for good .	它是關於 「 聯合國 」 這個詞的移動示範 , 應該是:一個真正的國家 , 加入一個很大的努力 。
and , in this case , it was a massive undertaking to explore a planet , and to come to understand a planetary system that , for all of human history , had been unreachable , and now humans had actually touched it .	在這個案例中 , 它是一個巨大的探究一個星球 , 為了所有人類歷史 , 人類的歷史 , 已是不可或缺的 , 現在人類已經接觸到它了 。
so it was i mean , i'm getting goose bumps just talking about it .	所以 , 我的意思是 , 我得到了鵝凸起 , 只是在談論它 。
it was a tremendously emotional event , and it's something that i will personally never forget , and you shouldn't either .	這是非常感情的事件 , 我個人永遠不會忘記 , 你也不該忘記 。
but anyway , the probe took measurements of the atmosphere on the way down , and it also took panoramic pictures .	總之 , 探測器採用大氣層的測量措施 , 同時也拍了全景的照片 。
and i can't tell you what it was like to see the first pictures of titan's surface from the probe . and this is what we saw .	我無法告訴你們泰坦的第一張照片是什麼樣子 。 這是我們看到的 。
and it was a shocker , because it was everything we wanted those other pictures taken from orbit to be .	那是個很震驚的 , 因為那是我們想要從軌道上拍攝的其他照片 。
it was an unambiguous pattern , a geological pattern .	它是一種無形的模式 , 一種地質模式 。
it's a dendritic drainage pattern that can be formed only by the flow of liquids .	它是一種傾向的排泄模式 , 只能由液體的流動形成 。
and you can follow these channels and you can see how they all converge .	你可以追蹤這些通道 , 看看它們如何被轉換 。
and they converge into this channel here , which drains into this region .	然後他們轉換到這條通道 , 排入這個區域 。
you are looking at a shoreline .	你看到的是海岸線 。
was this a shoreline of fluids ? we didn't know .	這是流體的海岸線嗎 ? 我們不知道 。
but this is somewhat of a shoreline .	但這是一條海岸線 。
this picture is taken at 16 kilometers .	這張照片是在16公里拍的 。
this is the picture taken at eight kilometers , ok ? again , the shoreline .	這是8公里拍攝的照片 , 好嗎 ? 再一次 , 海岸線 。
okay , now , 16 kilometers , eight kilometers this is roughly an airline altitude .	好 , 現在 , 16公里 , 8公里 , 大約是航空高度 。
if you were going to take an airplane trip across the u . s . , you would be flying at these altitudes .	如果你要穿越美國的飛機旅行 , 你會在這些高度飛行 。
so , this is the picture you would have at the window of titanian airlines as you fly across the surface of titan .	這是你在鐵達尼亞航空公司的窗口 , 飛越土衛六的表面 。
and then finally , the probe came to rest on the surface , and i'm going to show you , ladies and gentlemen , the first picture ever taken from the surface of a moon in the outer solar system .	最後 , 探測器在表面上休息 , 我要給你們看 , 各位先生女士 , 第一張從外太陽系的表面拍攝的照片 。
and here is the horizon , ok ?	這是地平線 , 好嗎 ?
these are probably water ice pebbles , yes ?	這些可能是冰泡 , 是嗎 ?
and obviously , it landed in one of these flat , dark regions and it didn't sink out of sight . so it wasn't fluid that we landed in .	很顯然 , 它落在一個平坦、黑暗的區域 , 且它沒有從視線下沉 。 所以它不是我們登陸的液體 。
what the probe came down in was basically the titan equivalent of a mud flat .	基本上 , 探測器就跟泥巴平面一樣 。
this is an unconsolidated ground that is suffused with liquid methane .	這是一個與液態甲烷混合的土地 。
and it's probably the case that this material has washed off the highlands of titan through these channels that we saw , and has drained over billions of years to fill in lowlying basins .	可能是這種材料在我們看到的這些通道中已經被沖掉了 , 數十億年以來 , 以便填滿了低沉的盆地 。
and that is what the huygens probe landed in .	這就是huygens探測器登陸的原因 。
but still , there was no sign in our images , or even in the huygens' images , of any large , open bodies of fluids .	但是 , 我們的影像中沒有任何跡象 , 甚至在胡布斯的圖片中 , 任何大型、開放的液體 。
where were they ? it got even more puzzling when we found dunes .	它們在哪裡 ? 當我們發現沙丘時 , 它變得更令人困惑 。
ok , so this is our movie of the equatorial region of titan , showing these dunes . these are dunes that are 100 meters tall , separated by a few kilometers , and they go on for miles and miles and miles .	好 , 這是我們土衛六的赤道地區的電影 , 展示這些沙丘 。 這些沙丘是100公尺高 , 被幾公里分開的沙丘 , 經過幾公里、幾英里、幾英里 。
there's hundreds , up to a 1 , 000 or 1 , 200 miles of dunes .	有數百英哩高達1000或1200英哩的沙丘
this is the saharan desert of titan .	這是土衛六沙漠 。
it's obviously a place which is very dry , or you wouldn't get dunes .	很明顯地 , 一個非常乾燥的地方 , 或者你不會得到沙丘 。
so again , it got puzzling that there were no bodies of fluid , until finally , we saw lakes in the polar regions .	所以 , 同樣的 , 它變得難以置信 , 直到最後 , 我們在極地區域看到湖泊 。
and there is a lake scene in the south polar region of titan .	土衛六南極地區有一個湖景 。
it's about the size of lake ontario .	它大約和安大略湖一樣大 。
and then , only a week and a half ago , we flew over the north pole of titan and found , again , we found a feature here the size of the caspian sea .	然後 , 僅僅在一週半前 , 我們飛越了土衛六的北極 , 再次發現 , 我們發現了像卡薩尼海一樣大的特徵 。
so it seems that the liquids , for some reason we don't understand , or during at least this season , are apparently at the poles of titan .	所以似乎液體 , 基於某些我們不了解的原因 , 或至少在這個季節 , 顯然在泰坦的極端 。
and i think you would agree that we have found titan is a remarkable , mystical place . it's exotic , it's alien , but yet strangely earthlike , and having earthlike geological formations and a tremendous geographical diversity , and is a fascinating world whose only rival in the solar system for complexity and richness is the earth itself .	我認為你會同意 , 我們發現泰坦是個很神秘的地方 , 很奇怪 , 很奇怪 , 但卻像地球一樣 , 擁有類似地球的地質和地理的多樣性 , 也是一個令人著迷的世界 , 在太陽系中 , 只有這麼複雜和豐富的溫度是地球本身 。
and so now we go onto enceladus . enceladus is a small moon , it's about a tenth the size of titan . and you can see it here next to england , just to show you the size . this is not meant to be a threat .	所以現在我們去了土衛二 。 土衛二是一個小的衛星 , 它大約是土衛六的10分 。 你可以看到它在英格蘭旁邊 , 給你看大小 。 這不是威脅 。
and enceladus is very white , it's very bright , and its surface is obviously wrecked with fractures .	土衛二是非常白的 , 非常明亮 , 它的表面顯然是破碎的 。
it is a very geologically active body .	這是個非常活躍的身體 。
but the mother lode of discoveries on enceladus was found at the south pole and we're looking at the south pole here where we found this system of fractures .	但土衛二的發現 , 在南極被發現 , 我們正在研究南極 , 在那裡 , 我們找到了這個碎形系統 。
and they're a different color because they're a different composition .	它們是不同的顏色 , 因為它們是不同的組成 。
they are coated . these fractures are coated with organic materials .	這些碎片和有機物質結合在一起 。
moreover , this whole , entire region , the south polar region , has elevated temperatures . it's the hottest place on the planet , on the body .	此外 , 整個區域 , 南極區域提升了溫度 。 它是地球上最熱的地方 , 位於人體上 。
that's as bizarre as finding that the antarctic on the earth is hotter than the tropics .	這就像是發現地球上的南極比熱帶還要熱 。
and then , when we took additional pictures , we discovered that from these fractures are issuing jets of fine , icy particles extending hundreds of miles into space .	然後 , 當我們拍了額外的圖片 , 我們發現 , 從這些碎形開始噴射出好的噴射機 , 冰柱會延伸數百英哩的空間 。
and when we colorcode this image , to bring out the faint light levels , we see that these jets feed a plume that , in fact , we see , in other images , goes thousands of miles into the space above enceladus .	當我們把這張影像編碼出來時 , 我們會發現這些噴射器的數量增加了一倍 , 事實上 , 在其他的影像中 , 我們可以看到 , 在土衛二上數千英哩的太空中 。
my team and i have examined images like this , and like this one , and have thought about the other results from cassini .	我和我的團隊探討了像這樣的影像 , 就像這張 , 想出了卡西尼尼號的其他結果 。
and we have arrived at the conclusion that these jets may be erupting from pockets of liquid water under the surface of enceladus .	我們得到的結論是這些噴射機可能從土衛二表面下噴出液態水 。
so we have , possibly , liquid water , organic materials and excess heat .	所以 , 我們可能有液態水、有機物質和過量的熱能 。
in other words , we have possibly stumbled upon the holy grail of modern day planetary exploration , or in other words , an environment that is potentially suitable for living organisms .	換句話說 , 我們可能發現了現代地球探索的聖杯 , 換句話說 , 一個可能適合生物的環境 。
and i don't think i need to tell you that the discovery of life elsewhere in our solar system , whether it be on enceladus or elsewhere , would have enormous cultural and scientific implications .	我不認為我需要告訴你們 , 在我們的太陽系中發現了生命 , 不論是在土衛二或其他地方 , 都會有很大的文化和科學的含義 。
because if we could demonstrate that genesis had occurred not once , but twice , independently , in our solar system , then that means , by inference , it has occurred a staggering number of times throughout the universe and its 13 . 7 billion year history .	因為如果我們可以證明遺傳基因不只發生一次 , 而是獨立的在我們的太陽系中 , 那就表示 , 根據推斷 , 它在整個宇宙中發生了驚人的數量 , 並且它137億年的歷史 。
right now , earth is the only planet still that we know is teeming with life .	目前 , 地球是唯一一個我們知道的行星 , 正充滿著生命 。
it is precious , it is unique , it is still , so far , the only home we've ever known .	它很珍貴 , 它是獨一無二的 , 到目前為止 , 我們唯一認識的家 。
and if any of you were alert and coherent during the 1960s and we'd forgive you , if you weren't , ok you would remember this very famous picture taken by the apollo 8 astronauts in 1968 .	如果你們當中有人在1960年代被警告和協調 , 我們會原諒你 , 如果你不是 , 你還記得1968年阿波羅8號太空人拍下這張著名的照片 。
it was the first time that earth was imaged from space , and it had an enormous impact on our sense of place in the universe , and our sense of responsibility for the protection of our own planet .	那是第一次 , 地球是從太空中拍攝的 , 它對我們在宇宙中的位置有很大的影響 , 以及我們對地球保護的責任感 。
well , we on cassini have taken an equivalent first , a picture that no human eye has ever seen before .	嗯 , 我們在卡西尼拍了一張相同的第一張照片 , 照片從來沒有人眼見過 。
it is a total eclipse of the sun , seen from the other side of saturn .	它是土星另一端的太陽的日全日蝕 。
and in this impossibly beautiful picture , you see the main rings backlit by the sun , you see the refracted image of the sun and you see this ring created , in fact , by the exhalations of enceladus .	在這張可能是美麗的圖片中 , 你看到太陽的主要環繞著背景 , 你可以看到太陽的重建圖像 , 看到這個環實際上是由土衛二所產生的 。
but as if that weren't brilliant enough , we can spot , in this beautiful image , sight of our own planet , cradled in the arms of saturn's rings .	但 , 彷彿那還不夠聰明 , 我們可以在這個美麗的圖像中 , 看到我們自己的星球 , 在土星環的手臂中擠滿了 。
now , there is something deeply moving about seeing ourselves from afar , and capturing the sight of our little , blueocean planet in the skies of other worlds .	現在 , 有一個深深感動人心的是從遠處看到自己 , 捕捉到我們在其他世界的小藍綠色的行星 。
and that , and the perspective of ourselves that we gain from that , may be , in the end , the finest reward that we earn from this journey of discovery that started half a century ago .	這也是我們從中獲益的觀點 , 可能是最終 , 我們從這個發現的最好的獎賞 , 從半個世紀前就開始了 。
as of 2005 , only 15 percent of the world was mapped . this slows the delivery of aid after a disaster and hides the economic potential of unused lands and unknown roads . in this short talk , google's lalitesh katragadda demos map maker , a group mapmaking tool that people around the globe are using to map their world .	到了2005年 , 世界上只有15%的人被繪製出來 。 這種減緩了在災難後的遞送 , 隱藏了未知的土地和未知的道路 。 在短篇演講中 , 谷歌的卡達加達•狄摩達繪畫家 , 一個全球各地居民用地地地地地地地地圖繪製的工具 。
collaboration , design , map , technology	合作 , 設計 , 地圖 , 科技 , 科技 , 科技 。
lalitesh katragadda: making maps to fight disaster , build economies	lalishkatragada:繪製對抗災難的地圖 , 建立經濟體 , 來對抗災難 , 建立經濟 。
in 2008 , cyclone nargis devastated myanmar .	2008年 , cyclonenagis摧毀了緬甸 。
millions of people were in severe need of help .	數百萬人有嚴重的幫助 。
the u . n . wanted to rush people and supplies to the area .	聯合國想要把人趕到這個區域 。
but there were no maps , no maps of roads , no maps showing hospitals , no way for help to reach the cyclone victims .	但沒有地圖 , 沒有道路地圖 , 沒有地圖顯示醫院 , 無法協助到達cyclone受害者 。
when we look at a map of los angeles or london , it is hard to believe that as of 2005 , only 15 percent of the world was mapped to a geocodable level of detail .	當我們看到洛杉磯或倫敦的地圖時 , 很難相信在2005年 , 世界上只有15%的人被繪製成地理位置 。
the u . n . ran headfirst into a problem that the majority of the world's populous faces: not having detailed maps .	聯合國成立了大多數人臉龐龐大的問題:沒有詳細的地圖 。
but help was coming .	但協助來了 。
at google , 40 volunteers used a new software to map 120 , 000 kilometers of roads , 3 , 000 hospitals , logistics and relief points .	在google , 40個志願者用一個新軟體繪製十二萬公里的道路 , 三千間醫院、物流和救援點 。
and it took them four days .	他們花了四天 。
the new software they used ? google mapmaker .	他們用的新軟體 ? 谷歌地圖製造者 。
google mapmaker is a technology that empowers each of us to map what we know locally .	google地圖製造者是一項科技 , 讓我們每一個人都能繪製出我們所知的地圖 。
people have used this software to map everything from roads to rivers , from schools to local businesses , and video stores to the corner store .	人們用這個軟體來繪製所有東西 , 從道路到河流 , 從學校到當地的企業 , 視頻店到角落商店 。
nobel prize nominee hernando de soto recognized that the key to economic liftoff for most developing countries is to tap the vast amounts of uncapitalized land .	諾貝爾獎提名赫南多•索托知道 , 對大部分開發中國家而言 , 經濟利益的關鍵是要處理大量未受控制的土地 。
for example , a trillion dollars of real estate remains uncapitalized in india alone .	舉例來說 , 僅在印度 , 一兆美金的房地產仍未被控制 。
in the last year alone , thousands of users in 170 countries have mapped millions of pieces of information , and created a map of a level of detail never thought viable .	光是去年 , 170個國家有成千上萬的使用者已經繪製了數百萬的資訊 , 並創造出一個細節的地圖 。
and this was made possible by the power of passionate users everywhere .	這使得我們有熱情使用者的力量 。
let's look at some of the maps being created by users right now .	現在我們來看看一些使用者的地圖 。
so , as we speak , people are mapping the world in these 170 countries .	所以 , 如同我們所說的 , 在這個170個國家中 , 人們在繪製這個世界 。
you can see bridget in africa who just mapped a road in senegal .	你可以看到非洲的橋 , 剛在塞內加爾畫了一條路 。
and , closer to home , chalua , an n . g . road in bangalore .	更接近家鄉 , 查蘿拉 , 一個n.g.g.g.g.g.s.g.tangalore 。
this is the result of computational geometry , gesture recognition , and machine learning .	這是計算幾何學的結果 , 手勢辨識 , 機器學習 。
this is a victory of thousands of users , in hundreds of cities , one user , one edit at a time .	這是一場勝利 , 在數百個城市裡 , 一個使用者 , 一次編輯 。
this is an invitation to the 70 percent of our unmapped planet .	這是我們70%未適應的星球邀請 。
welcome to the new world .	歡迎來到新世界 。
in 2003 , the palestinian village of budrus mounted a 10monthlong nonviolent protest to stop a barrier being built across their olive groves . did you hear about it ? didn't think so . brazilian filmmaker julia bacha asks why we only pay attention to violence in the israelpalestine conflict and not to the nonviolent leaders who may one day bring peace .	在2003年 , 布德魯斯山脈的巴勒斯坦村落在十個月長的非暴力抗議中 , 阻止一場阻止他們的橄欖球場 。 你聽說過嗎 ? 巴西的電影製作人juliabacha問我們為何只關注以色列巴勒斯坦衝突而非暴力的領導人 , 而非暴力領導者有一天可能會帶來和平 。
arts , communication , compassion , entertainment , film , peace , violence , war	藝術、溝通、同情、娛樂、電影、和平、暴力、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭 。
julia bacha: pay attention to nonviolence	朱莉亞.巴契亞:請注意非暴力的非暴力行為 。
for the last 8 years , i have dedicated my life to documenting the work of israelis and palestinians who are trying to end the conflict using peaceful means .	過去8年來 , 我致力於記錄以色列人和巴勒斯坦人試圖用和平的方式來結束衝突 。
when i travel with my work across europe and the united states , one question always comes up: where is the palestinian gandhi ?	當我在歐洲和美國旅行時 , 一個問題總是出現:巴勒斯坦甘地在哪裡 ?
why aren't palestinians using nonviolent resistance ?	為什麼巴勒斯坦人不使用非暴力抗爭 ?
the challenge i face when i hear this question is that often i have just returned from the middle east where i spent my time filming dozens of palestinians who are using nonviolence to defend their lands and water resources from israeli soldiers and settlers .	當我聽到這個問題時 , 我所面臨的挑戰是 , 通常我剛從中東返回 , 在那裡 , 我花了很多時間拍攝數十位巴勒斯坦人 , 他們用非暴力手段來保護他們的土地和水資源 , 以色列士兵和居民 。
these leaders are trying to forge a massive national nonviolent movement to end the occupation and build peace in the region .	這些領袖正試著要忘記一個大規模的國家非暴力運動 , 來終結這個職業 , 並在該地區建立和平 。
yet , most of you have probably never heard about them .	然而 , 大部分的人可能從來沒有聽過他們 。
this divide between what's happening on the ground and perceptions abroad is one of the key reasons why we don't have yet a palestinian peaceful resistance movement that has been successful .	這種分裂在地面和國外的感知上是我們尚未成功的巴勒斯坦和平抗爭運動的關鍵原因之一
so i'm here today to talk about the power of attention , the power of your attention , and the emergence and development of nonviolent movements in the west bank , gaza and elsewhere but today , my case study is going to be palestine .	所以今天我來這裡是要談注意力的力量 , 你的注意力 , 以及西銀行、加薩和其他地方非暴力運動的崛起和發展 , 但今天 , 我的案例研究將會是巴勒斯坦 。
i believe that what's mostly missing for nonviolence to grow is not for palestinians to start adopting nonviolence , but for us to start paying attention to those who already are .	我相信 , 成長過程中大部分缺少的非暴力行為 , 並不是為了巴勒斯坦人開始採用非暴力行為 , 而是要我們開始注意現有的人 。
allow me to illustrate this point by taking you to this village called budrus .	讓我來說明一下這一點 , 帶你到這個叫做布德魯斯的村莊 。
about seven years ago , they faced extinction , because israel announced it would build a separation barrier , and part of this barrier would be built on top of the village .	大約七年前 , 他們面臨絕種 , 因為以色列宣佈它會建立一個分離障礙 , 其中一部分的障礙會在村落頂端建造 。
they would lose 40 percent of their land and be surrounded , so they would lose free access to the rest of the west bank .	他們會失去百分之四十的土地 , 被圍繞 , 所以他們會失去自由取得西岸的其他地方 。
through inspired local leadership , they launched a peaceful resistance campaign to stop that from happening .	透過當地的領導力 , 他們發起了一個和平的抗拒活動 , 來阻止它發生 。
let me show you some brief clips , so you have a sense for what that actually looked like on the ground .	讓我給你們看一些簡短的片段 , 所以你有一種感覺 , 來說明到底在地上是什麼樣子 。
palestinian woman: we were told the wall would separate palestine from israel .	巴勒斯坦女子:我們被告知牆會和以色列分開巴勒斯坦 。
here in budrus , we realized the wall would steal our land .	在布德魯斯 , 我們意識到牆會偷走我們的土地 。
israeli man: the fence has , in fact , created a solution to terror .	以色列男子:事實上 , 柵欄已經創造出了對恐怖的解答 。
man: today you're invited to a peaceful march .	男子:今天你被邀請去和平遊行 。
you are joined by dozens of your israeli brothers and sisters .	你被數十位以色列兄弟姐妹加入 。
israeli activist: nothing scares the army more than nonviolent opposition .	以色列行動主義者:軍隊比非暴力反對者更害怕 。
woman: we saw the men trying to push the soldiers , but none of them could do that .	女子:我們看到男人試圖推動士兵 , 但他們都無法做到 。
but i think the girls could do it .	但我認為女孩們可以做到 。
fatah party member: we must empty our minds of traditional thinking .	法塔赫派對成員:我們必須清空我們的傳統思維 。
hamas party member: we were in complete harmony , and we wanted to spread it to all of palestine .	哈馬斯派對成員:我們在完全和諧 , 我們想要把它傳播給所有的巴勒斯坦 。
chanting: one united nation .	旁白:一個聯合國 。
fatah , hamas and the popular front !	法塔、哈馬斯和受歡迎的前面 !
news anchor: the clashes over the fence continue .	新聞主持人:柵欄上的撞擊持續 。
reporter: israeli border police were sent to disperse the crowd .	記者:以色列邊境警察被送去散佈群眾 。
they were allowed to use any force necessary .	他們被允許使用任何必要的力量 。
man: these are live bullets .	男子:這些是活子彈 。
it's like fallujah . shooting everywhere .	這就像是羅瓦賈 , 到處拍攝 。
israeli activist: i was sure we were all going to die .	以色列行動主義者:我確信我們都要死 。
but there were others around me who weren't even cowering .	但我身邊還有一些人 , 甚至不在牛仔 。
israeli soldier: a nonviolent protest is not going to stop the [unclear] .	以色列士兵:非暴力抗議不會停止 。
protester: this is a peaceful march .	提議員:這是和平遊行 。
there is no need to use violence .	不需要使用暴力 。
chanting: we can do it ! we can do it !	大聲說:我們能做到 ! 我們能做到 !
julia bacha: when i first heard about the story of budrus , i was surprised that the international media had failed to cover the extraordinary set of events that happened seven years ago , in 2003 .	朱莉亞.巴赫:當我第一次聽到布德魯斯的故事時 , 我很驚訝國際媒體並沒有報導七年前發生的非凡事件 , 那是在2003年 。
what was even more surprising was the fact that budrus was successful .	更令人驚訝的是布德魯斯成功了 。
the residents , after 10 months of peaceful resistance , convinced the israeli government to move the route of the barrier off their lands and to the green line , which is the internationally recognized boundary between israel and the palestinian territories .	居民 , 在十個月的和平抗爭之後 , 說服以色列政府把障礙移到他們的土地和綠線上 , 也就是國際認可以色列和巴勒斯坦領土之間的界線 。
the resistance in budrus has since spread to villages across the west bank and to palestinian neighborhoods in jerusalem .	布德魯斯的抗藥性從西岸散播到村落 , 到耶路撒冷的巴勒斯坦社區 。
yet the media remains mostly silent on these stories .	但媒體仍然沉默在這些故事上 。
this silence carries profound consequences for the likelihood that nonviolence can grow , or even survive , in palestine .	這種沉默對非暴力的可能造成深遠的影響 , 甚至在巴勒斯坦的可能性成長 。
violent resistance and nonviolent resistance share one very important thing in common ; they are both a form of theater seeking an audience to their cause .	暴力抗爭和非暴力抗爭 , 共有一件事非常重要 ; 它們是一場劇場尋找觀眾的原因 。
if violent actors are the only ones constantly getting frontpage covers and attracting international attention to the palestinian issue , it becomes very hard for nonviolent leaders to make the case to their communities that civil disobedience is a viable option in addressing their plight .	如果暴力演員是唯一經常收到的報導 , 吸引巴勒斯坦議題的國際注意力 , 那對非暴力領袖來說 , 公民不服從是有可行的選項 。
the power of attention is probably going to come as no surprise to the parents in the room .	注意力的力量可能是房間裡的父母不會感到驚訝 。
the surest way to make your child throw increasingly louder tantrums is by giving him attention the first time he throws a fit .	要讓你的孩子更大聲地丟棄幻肢的確切方法是首次給他注意他丟了一套套裝置 。
the tantrum will become what childhood psychologists call a functional behavior , since the child has learned that he can get parental attention out of it .	抗癌細胞會變成兒童心理學家稱之為功能性行為 , 因為孩子已經學會了他能從中得到父母的注意力 。
parents can incentivize or disincentivize behavior simply by giving or withdrawing attention to their children .	父母可以獎勵或不獎勵行為 , 只要給予或放棄對孩子的注意 。
but that's true for adults too .	但成年人也是如此 。
in fact , the behavior of entire communities and countries can be influenced , depending on where the international community chooses to focus its attention .	事實上 , 整個社區和國家的行為可能會受到影響 , 取決於國際社會選擇集中注意力的地方 。
i believe that at the core of ending the conflict in the middle east and bringing peace is for us to transform nonviolence into a functional behavior by giving a lot more attention to the nonviolent leaders on the ground today .	我相信 , 在中東結束衝突的核心 , 將和平帶給我們 , 將非暴力行為轉變成功能性行為 , 讓大家更關注現今地面上的非暴力領導者 。
in the course of taking my film to villages in the west bank , in gaza and in east jerusalem , i have seen the impact that even one documentary film can have in influencing the transformation .	在拍攝我的影片到西岸的村落 , 在加薩和東耶路撒冷 , 我看到了一部紀錄片可以影響轉變 。
in a village called wallajeh , which sits very close to jerusalem , the community was facing a very similar plight to budrus .	在一個叫瓦拉賈的村莊 , 非常靠近耶路撒冷的村莊 , 這個社區面臨著非常類似的布德魯斯 。
they were going to be surrounded , lose a lot of their lands and not have freedom of access , either to the west bank or jerusalem .	他們會被圍繞著 , 失去了很多土地 , 沒有自由取得 , 不論是西岸或耶路撒冷 。
they had been using nonviolence for about two years but had grown disenchanted since nobody was paying attention .	他們花了兩年的時間在使用非暴力 , 但從來沒有人注意到這件事情 。
so we organized a screening .	所以我們組織了一個篩檢 。
a week later , they held the most wellattended and disciplined demonstration to date .	一個禮拜後 , 他們舉辦了最完善的示範 。
the organizers say that the villagers , upon seeing the story of budrus documented in a film , felt that there were indeed people following what they were doing , that people cared .	組織者說 , 村民在電影中看到布德魯斯的故事 , 感覺到確實有人追隨他們所做的事 , 人們關心的 。
so they kept on going .	所以他們繼續前進 。
on the israeli side , there is a new peace movement called solidariot , which means solidarity in hebrew .	在以色列的另一面 , 有一種新的和平運動 , 叫做索里達里特 , 意思是希伯來語的團結 。
the leaders of this movement have been using budrus as one of their primary recruiting tools .	這個運動的領導人 , 一直在用布德魯斯作為他們主要的招募工具之一 。
they report that israelis who had never been active before , upon seeing the film , understand the power of nonviolence and start joining their activities .	他們報告說 , 以色列人從來沒有活躍過 , 看電影 , 了解非暴力的力量 , 並開始參與他們的活動 。
the examples of wallajeh and the solidariot movement show that even a smallbudget independent film can play a role in transforming nonviolence into a functional behavior .	瓦哈和索里達州運動的例子顯示 , 即使是小型的獨立電影 , 也可以扮演非暴力行為的角色 。
now imagine the power that big media players could have if they started covering the weekly nonviolent demonstrations happening in villages like bil'in , ni'lin , wallajeh , in jerusalem neighborhoods like sheikh jarrah and silwan the nonviolent leaders would become more visible , valued and effective in their work .	想像一下 , 大型媒體玩家能擁有的力量如果他們開始報導每週的非暴力示威 , 例如bilin、ni''lin、瓦拉賈 , 在耶路撒冷的鄰里 , 像sikhjarrah和silwan , 非暴力領導者在工作中會變得更明顯、更有價值、更有效率 。
i believe that the most important thing is to understand that if we don't pay attention to these efforts , they are invisible , and it's as if they never happened .	我相信最重要的是要了解 , 如果我們不注意這些努力 , 它們是隱形的 , 就好像從未發生過 。
but i have seen first hand that if we do , they will multiply .	但我親眼見到如果我們這麼做 , 他們會乘以乘法 。
if they multiply , their influence will grow in the overall israelipalestinian conflict .	如果他們乘以增加 , 他們的影響會在以色列巴勒斯坦的衝突中成長 。
and theirs is the kind of influence that can finally unblock the situation .	而他們的影響 , 終於可以解開這種情況 。
these leaders have proven that nonviolence works in places like budrus .	這些領袖證明了非暴力在布德魯斯這樣的地方工作 。
let's give them attention so they can prove it works everywhere .	讓我們給他們注意 , 讓他們可以證明它無所不在 。
simon sinek has a simple but powerful model for inspirational leadership all starting with a golden circle and the question " why ? " his examples include apple , martin luther king , and the wright brothers . . .	西蒙•海克有一個簡單且強大的靈感領導模式 , 始於黃金圓圈 , 以及 「 為什麼 ? 」 他的例子包括蘋果、馬丁•路德金、萊特兄弟......
bullseye , business , entrepreneur , leadership , sales , selling , success	bullseye、商業、企業家、領導力、銷售、銷售、成功、成功 。
simon sinek: how great leaders inspire action	西蒙•薩恩克:偉大的領導人有多激勵人心行動 。
how do you explain when things don't go as we assume ?	你要如何解釋當事情不像我們假設的那樣發生 ?
or better , how do you explain when others are able to achieve things that seem to defy all of the assumptions ?	或更好的 , 你要如何解釋當其他人能夠達成似乎違反所有假設時的成果 ?
for example: why is apple so innovative ?	舉例來說:為什麼蘋果這麼創新 ?
year after year , after year , after year , they're more innovative than all their competition .	年復一年 , 年復一年 , 他們比他們的競爭更創新 。
and yet , they're just a computer company .	然而 , 他們只是一家電腦公司 。
they're just like everyone else .	他們就像其他人一樣 。
they have the same access to the same talent , the same agencies , the same consultants , the same media .	他們有相同的才能 , 同一個機構 , 同一個顧問 , 同樣的媒體 。
then why is it that they seem to have something different ?	那麼 , 為什麼他們似乎有不同的東西 ?
why is it that martin luther king led the civil rights movement ?	為什麼馬丁路德王領導民權運動 ?
he wasn't the only man who suffered in a precivil rights america , and he certainly wasn't the only great orator of the day .	他不是唯一在美國受過處方權利的男人 , 而且他肯定不是當天唯一偉大的演員 。
and why is it that the wright brothers were able to figure out controlled , powered man flight when there were certainly other teams who were better qualified , better funded . . .	為何萊特兄弟能夠想出控制權、有電力飛行的男人 , 尤其是其他團隊 , 他們更有資格、更好的資金......
and they didn't achieve powered man flight , and the wright brothers beat them to it .	他們沒有達成驅動力的男人飛行 , 萊特兄弟對此打敗了 。
there's something else at play here .	這裡還有別的東西 。
about three and a half years ago i made a discovery .	大約三年半前 , 我做了一個發現 。
and this discovery profoundly changed my view on how i thought the world worked , and it even profoundly changed the way in which i operate in it .	這項發現深深改變了我對世界如何運作的看法 , 甚至徹底改變了我運作的方式 。
as it turns out , there's a pattern .	結果發現 , 有一種模式 。
as it turns out , all the great and inspiring leaders and organizations in the world whether it's apple or martin luther king or the wright brothers they all think , act and communicate the exact same way .	結果發現 , 世界上所有偉大的領導者和組織 , 無論是蘋果或馬丁•路德•金恩 , 或他們所想的萊特兄弟 , 採取行動和溝通的方式都一樣 。
and it's the complete opposite to everyone else .	完全相反 。
all i did was codify it , and it's probably the world's simplest idea .	我所做的只是將它編碼 , 可能是世界上最簡單的點子 。
i call it the golden circle .	我稱它為黃金圈 。
why ? how ? what ?	為什麼 ? 如何 ? 什麼 ?
this little idea explains why some organizations and some leaders are able to inspire where others aren't .	這個小點子解釋了為什麼有些組織和一些領導者能夠啟發其他人不在哪裡 。
let me define the terms really quickly .	讓我快速定義這個詞 。
every single person , every single organization on the planet knows what they do , 100 percent .	每個人 , 地球上的每個組織都知道他們在做什麼 , 百分之百 。
some know how they do it , whether you call it your differentiated value proposition or your proprietary process or your usp .	有人知道他們是怎麼做到的 , 不管你稱它為你的分化價值提議或是你的先進過程或是你的usp 。
but very , very few people or organizations know why they do what they do .	但很少人或組織知道他們為什麼要做他們要做的事 。
and by " why " i don't mean " to make a profit . "	所謂的 「 為什麼 」 , 我不是說 「 為了賺取利潤 」 。
that's a result . it's always a result .	結果就是這樣 。 結果總是 。
by " why , " i mean: what's your purpose ?	我的意思是:你的目的是什麼 ?
what's your cause ? what's your belief ?	你的原因是什麼 ? 你的信念是什麼 ?
why does your organization exist ?	你的組織為什麼存在 ?
why do you get out of bed in the morning ?	為何你早上起床 ?
and why should anyone care ?	為什麼有人會在乎 ?
well , as a result , the way we think , the way we act , the way we communicate is from the outside in .	因此 , 我們認為我們行為的方式 , 我們溝通的方式來自外界 。
it's obvious . we go from the clearest thing to the fuzziest thing .	很明顯 。 我們從最清晰的東西到最模糊的東西 。
but the inspired leaders and the inspired organizations regardless of their size , regardless of their industry all think , act and communicate from the inside out .	但鼓舞領袖和激勵人心的組織 , 不論他們的大小 , 不論他們的產業都在想 , 行動和溝通 。
let me give you an example .	讓我舉個例子 。
i use apple because they're easy to understand and everybody gets it .	我用蘋果 , 因為他們很容易理解 , 每個人都懂 。
if apple were like everyone else , a marketing message from them might sound like this: " we make great computers .	如果蘋果跟其他人一樣 , 他們的行銷訊息可能聽起來像這樣: 「 我們製造了很棒的電腦 。
they're beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	他們設計得很漂亮 , 很容易使用和使用者友善 。
want to buy one ? " " meh . "	想買一台嗎 ? 「 梅 。 」
and that's how most of us communicate .	這就是我們大多數人溝通的方式 。
that's how most marketing is done , that's how most sales is done and that's how most of us communicate interpersonally .	這就是多數行銷的方法 , 多數銷售的做法 , 這就是我們多數人之間的交流方式 。
we say what we do , we say how we're different or how we're better and we expect some sort of a behavior , a purchase , a vote , something like that .	我們說我們怎麼做 , 我們說我們是如何不同 , 或是我們好好多 , 我們期待某種行為、購買、投票 , 等等 。
here's our new law firm: we have the best lawyers with the biggest clients , we always perform for our clients who do business with us .	這是我們的新法律公司:我們有最好的律師和最大客戶 , 我們總是為我們的客戶做生意 。
here's our new car: it gets great gas mileage , it has leather seats , buy our car .	這是我們的新車:它有很大的氣體里程碑 , 它有皮革座椅 , 買我們的車 。
here's how apple actually communicates .	蘋果是這樣溝通的 。
" everything we do , we believe in challenging the status quo .	「 我們所做的一切 , 我們相信挑戰現狀 。
we believe in thinking differently .	我們用不同的方式相信思考 。
the way we challenge the status quo is by making our products beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	我們挑戰現狀的方式是讓我們的產品美麗設計 , 簡單的使用和使用者友善地使用 。
we just happen to make great computers .	我們剛好製造出很棒的電腦
want to buy one ? "	想買一台嗎 ? 」
totally different right ? you're ready to buy a computer from me .	完全不同了嗎 ? 你準備好要從我身上買一台電腦 。
all i did was reverse the order of the information .	我所做的只是逆轉資訊的順序 。
what it proves to us is that people don't buy what you do ; people buy why you do it .	它向我們證明的是人們不買你做什麼 ; 人們購買你為什麼要做 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼要做 。
this explains why every single person in this room is perfectly comfortable buying a computer from apple .	這解釋了為什麼在這間房間裡的每個人都很舒服從蘋果買一台電腦 。
but we're also perfectly comfortable buying an mp3 player from apple , or a phone from apple , or a dvr from apple .	但我們也很舒服地買蘋果電腦的mp3玩家 , 或蘋果手機 , 或蘋果電腦的dvr 。
but , as i said before , apple's just a computer company .	但 , 如我之前所說的 , 蘋果只是一家電腦公司 。
there's nothing that distinguishes them structurally from any of their competitors .	沒有什麼能區別他們的競爭者的結構 。
their competitors are all equally qualified to make all of these products .	他們的競爭者都同樣有資格來製造這些產品 。
in fact , they tried .	事實上 , 他們嘗試了 。
a few years ago , gateway came out with flat screen tvs .	幾年前 , 蓋茨維出了平面的螢幕電視 。
they're eminently qualified to make flat screen tvs .	他們很有資格來製作平面電視 。
they've been making flat screen monitors for years .	多年來 , 他們一直在製作平面螢幕螢幕 。
dell came out with mp3 players and pdas , and they make great quality products , and they can make perfectly welldesigned products and nobody bought one .	戴爾和帕德斯出櫃 , 他們製作了很棒的品質產品 , 他們可以做出非常好的設計產品 , 沒有人買 。
in fact , talking about it now , we can't even imagine buying an mp3 player from dell .	事實上 , 談到現在 , 我們甚至無法想像從dell買一台mp3播放器 。
why would you buy an mp3 player from a computer company ?	為什麼你要從一家電腦公司買一台mp3播放器 ?
but we do it every day .	但我們每天都這麼做 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼要做 。
the goal is not to do business with everybody who needs what you have .	目標不是要和所有需要你的東西做生意 。
the goal is to do business with people who believe what you believe .	目標是要和那些相信你所相信的人們做生意 。
here's the best part: none of what i'm telling you is my opinion .	最好的部分是:我所說的都不是我的意見 。
it's all grounded in the tenets of biology .	一切都基於生物學的基礎 。
not psychology , biology .	不是心理學、生物學 。
if you look at a crosssection of the human brain , looking from the top down , what you see is the human brain is actually broken into three major components that correlate perfectly with the golden circle .	如果你看一下人類大腦的十字路口 , 從頭向下看 , 你看到的是人類的大腦實際上被分成三個主要元件 , 完全與黃金圈有關聯 。
our newest brain , our homo sapien brain , our neocortex , corresponds with the " what " level .	我們最新的大腦 , 我們的智人腦 , 我們的新皮層 , 會對應 「 什麼 」 的程度 。
the neocortex is responsible for all of our rational and analytical thought and language .	新皮層負責所有理性、分析思維和語言 。
the middle two sections make up our limbic brains , and our limbic brains are responsible for all of our feelings , like trust and loyalty .	中間的兩個區塊構成我們的大腦 , 我們的肢體大腦負責我們所有的感覺 , 比如信任和忠誠 。
it's also responsible for all human behavior , all decisionmaking , and it has no capacity for language .	它也要為所有人類行為負責 , 所有的決策 , 沒有語言的能力 。
in other words , when we communicate from the outside in , yes , people can understand vast amounts of complicated information like features and benefits and facts and figures .	換句話說 , 當我們從外面溝通時 , 是的 , 人們可以了解大量複雜的資訊 , 比如特徵、好處、事實和數字 。
it just doesn't drive behavior .	它並不會驅動行為 。
when we can communicate from the inside out , we're talking directly to the part of the brain that controls behavior , and then we allow people to rationalize it with the tangible things we say and do .	當我們從內部溝通時 , 我們直接和控制行為的大腦溝通 , 接著 , 我們允許人們用我們所說和做的事來合理化 。
this is where gut decisions come from .	這就是腸子決定的來源 。
you know , sometimes you can give somebody all the facts and figures , and they say , " i know what all the facts and details say , but it just doesn't feel right . "	你知道 , 有時候你可以給某人所有的事實和數字 , 他們說: 「 我知道所有事實和細節都說了什麼 , 但感覺不對 。 」
why would we use that verb , it doesn't " feel " right ?	為什麼我們要用那個動詞 , 感覺不對 ?
because the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking doesn't control language .	因為控制決策的部分無法控制語言 。
and the best we can muster up is , " i don't know . it just doesn't feel right . "	我們最好的一點是: 「 我不知道 , 感覺不對 。 」
or sometimes you say you're leading with your heart , or you're leading with your soul .	或者 , 有時你會說你帶著你的心 , 或你帶著你的靈魂去領導 。
well , i hate to break it to you , those aren't other body parts controlling your behavior .	我討厭打破它 , 不是其他身體部位控制你的行為 。
it's all happening here in your limbic brain , the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking and not language .	這一切都發生在你肢體的大腦中 , 控制決策的部分 , 而非語言 。
but if you don't know why you do what you do , and people respond to why you do what you do , then how will you ever get people to vote for you , or buy something from you , or , more importantly , be loyal and want to be a part of what it is that you do .	但如果你不知道為什麼要做你要做的事 , 大家會回應為什麼要做你要做的事 , 那麼你要如何讓人們投票給你 , 或從你身上買東西 , 或是更重要的是忠誠 , 想要成為你所做的事的一部分 。
again , the goal is not just to sell to people who need what you have ; the goal is to sell to people who believe what you believe .	同樣的 , 目標不只是賣給需要你擁有的東西的人 ; 目標是賣給那些相信你所相信的人們 。
the goal is not just to hire people who need a job ; it's to hire people who believe what you believe .	目標不只是要僱用需要工作的人 , 而是僱用那些相信你所相信的人們 。
i always say that , you know , if you hire people just because they can do a job , they'll work for your money , but if you hire people who believe what you believe , they'll work for you with blood and sweat and tears .	我總是說 , 如果你雇用別人 , 只因為他們能做一份工作 , 他們會為你的錢工作 , 但如果你雇用那些相信你所相信的人 , 他們會為你工作 , 用血汗和淚水 。
and nowhere else is there a better example of this than with the wright brothers .	沒有其他比萊特兄弟更好的例子 。
most people don't know about samuel pierpont langley .	大多數人不知道samuelpierpontlangley 。
and back in the early 20th century , the pursuit of powered man flight was like the dot com of the day .	在20世紀早期 , 追求人類飛行的追求就像是日常的地點 。
everybody was trying it .	每個人都在嘗試 。
and samuel pierpont langley had , what we assume , to be the recipe for success .	samuelpierpontlangley認為我們是成功的秘訣 。
i mean , even now , you ask people , " why did your product or why did your company fail ? "	我的意思是 , 即使現在 , 你問人們: 「 為什麼你的產品或為什麼你的公司失敗 ? 」
and people always give you the same permutation of the same three things: undercapitalized , the wrong people , bad market conditions .	人們總是給你相同的三件事:被制定、錯誤的人、不好的市場條件 。
it's always the same three things , so let's explore that .	一直都是一樣的三件事 , 讓我們來探究一下 。
samuel pierpont langley was given 50 , 000 dollars by the war department to figure out this flying machine .	samuelpierpontlangley得到了五萬美金 , 由於戰爭部門提供了這台飛行機器 。
money was no problem .	金錢不是問題 。
he held a seat at harvard and worked at the smithsonian and was extremely wellconnected ; he knew all the big minds of the day .	他在哈佛舉辦了一座西雅圖 , 在史密森尼工作 , 非常有連結 , 他知道當天的所有大頭腦 。
he hired the best minds money could find and the market conditions were fantastic .	他雇用了最好的思想金錢可以找到市場條件很棒 。
the new york times followed him around everywhere , and everyone was rooting for langley .	紐約時報隨後到處追蹤他 , 每個人都根深蒂固 。
then how come we've never heard of samuel pierpont langley ?	為什麼我們從來沒有聽過samuelpierpontlangley ?
a few hundred miles away in dayton ohio , orville and wilbur wright , they had none of what we consider to be the recipe for success .	在俄亥俄州的幾百英里外 , 奧維爾和威爾布萊特 , 他們沒有我們認為成功的秘訣 。
they had no money ; they paid for their dream with the proceeds from their bicycle shop ; not a single person on the wright brothers' team had a college education , not even orville or wilbur ; and the new york times followed them around nowhere .	他們沒有錢 , 他們付錢給他們的夢想 , 拿著自行車店的執行長 ; 萊特兄弟的團隊裡沒有一個人有大學教育 , 甚至不是奧維爾或威爾堡 ; 紐約時報隨他們到處追蹤 。
the difference was , orville and wilbur were driven by a cause , by a purpose , by a belief .	差別在於 , 俄維爾和威爾布爾被一個理由所驅使 , 由一個理由 , 一個理想的信念 。
they believed that if they could figure out this flying machine , it'll change the course of the world .	他們相信如果他們能找出這台飛行機器 , 它會改變世界的軌道 。
samuel pierpont langley was different .	samuelpierpontlangley不同 。
he wanted to be rich , and he wanted to be famous .	他想當有錢人 , 他想要有名 。
he was in pursuit of the result .	他在追求結果 。
he was in pursuit of the riches .	他追求富人 。
and lo and behold , look what happened .	看 , 看看發生了什麼事 。
the people who believed in the wright brothers' dream worked with them with blood and sweat and tears .	相信萊特兄弟的夢想與他們合作 , 用血液、汗水和淚水 。
the others just worked for the paycheck .	其他人只是為了支付而工作 。
and they tell stories of how every time the wright brothers went out , they would have to take five sets of parts , because that's how many times they would crash before they came in for supper .	他們會說故事 , 關於每次萊特兄弟出去 , 他們就得拿五組零件 , 因為他們在購買商品之前會撞到多少次 。
and , eventually , on december 17th , 1903 , the wright brothers took flight , and no one was there to even experience it .	最終 , 在1903年12月17日 , 萊特兄弟搭飛機 , 沒有人會去體驗它 。
we found out about it a few days later .	幾天後 , 我們發現了這件事 。
and further proof that langley was motivated by the wrong thing: the day the wright brothers took flight , he quit .	更進一步的證明 , 萊特兄弟踏上飛機 , 他辭掉了 。
he could have said , " that's an amazing discovery , guys , and i will improve upon your technology , " but he didn't .	他可以說: 「 那是個很棒的發現 , 各位 , 我會改善你的科技 。 」 但他沒有 。
he wasn't first , he didn't get rich , he didn't get famous so he quit .	他不是首先 , 他沒有富有 , 他沒有有名 , 所以他辭掉 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼要做 。
and if you talk about what you believe , you will attract those who believe what you believe .	如果你談到你所相信的 , 你會吸引那些相信你所相信的人們 。
but why is it important to attract those who believe what you believe ?	但為什麼要吸引那些相信你所相信的人們 ?
something called the law of diffusion of innovation , and if you don't know the law , you definitely know the terminology .	所謂的創新法則 , 如果你不知道法律 , 你絕對知道這個條例 。
the first two and a half percent of our population are our innovators .	前2.5%的人口是我們的創新者 。
the next 13 and a half percent of our population are our early adopters .	接下來的13.5%的人是我們早期的採用者 。
the next 34 percent are your early majority , your late majority and your laggards .	接下來的34%是你早期的大多數 , 遲到的多數 , 遲到的階層 。
the only reason these people buy touch tone phones is because you can't buy rotary phones anymore .	這些人只買觸覺電話的唯一原因 , 就是因為你再也買不到輪椅手機了 。
we all sit at various places at various times on this scale , but what the law of diffusion of innovation tells us is that if you want massmarket success or massmarket acceptance of an idea , you cannot have it until you achieve this tipping point between 15 and 18 percent market penetration , and then the system tips .	我們都坐在不同的階段 , 但創新的傳播法則告訴我們 , 如果你想要大眾市場成功或大眾市場接受想法 , 直到你達成了15%到18%的市場侵入之間的轉折點 , 然後系統會短暫 。
and i love asking businesses , " what's your conversion on new business ? "	我喜歡問企業: 「 你對新生意的轉換是什麼 ? 」
and they love to tell you , " oh , it's about 10 percent , " proudly .	他們很愛告訴你: 「 喔 , 大約10% 。 」 很驕傲 。
well , you can trip over 10 percent of the customers .	嗯 , 你可以超過百分之十的客戶 。
we all have about 10 percent who just " get it . "	我們都有百分之十的 「 得到 」 。
that's how we describe them , right ?	這就是我們描述它們的方式 , 對吧 ?
that's like that gut feeling , " oh , they just get it . "	就好像那種直覺: 「 喔 , 他們才剛懂 。 」
the problem is: how do you find the ones that get it before you're doing business with them versus the ones who don't get it ?	問題是:你要如何在你和他們做生意之前找到那些能得到的 , 而不是那些沒有得到的 ?
so it's this here , this little gap that you have to close , as jeffrey moore calls it , " crossing the chasm " because , you see , the early majority will not try something until someone else has tried it first .	所以 , 在這裡 , 這個小小的鴻溝 , 如同傑佛瑞•摩爾稱它為 「 跨越這間鴻溝 」 , 因為 , 你看 , 早期大多數人都不會嘗試 , 直到別人先試過 。
and these guys , the innovators and the early adopters , they're comfortable making those gut decisions .	這些人 , 創新者和早期採用者 , 他們很舒服地做出那些直覺決策 。
they're more comfortable making those intuitive decisions that are driven by what they believe about the world and not just what product is available .	他們更自在地做出那些直覺的決策 , 由他們對世界的信念所驅動 , 而不只是產品所能取得的 。
these are the people who stood in line for six hours to buy an iphone when they first came out , when you could have just walked into the store the next week and bought one off the shelf .	這些人 , 第一次出櫃時 , 站了六個小時 , 買一支iphone , 當你下星期可以走進店裡 , 買了一台貨架 。
these are the people who spent 40 , 000 dollars on flat screen tvs when they first came out , even though the technology was substandard .	這些人 , 第一次出櫃時 , 花了四萬美金在平面電視上 , 儘管科技是被貼上 。
and , by the way , they didn't do it because the technology was so great ; they did it for themselves .	順道一提 , 他們並沒有這麼做 , 因為科技太棒了 , 他們為自己做了 。
it's because they wanted to be first .	因為他們想要成為第一 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it and what you do simply proves what you believe .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼要做 , 而你所做的就是證明你所相信的 。
in fact , people will do the things that prove what they believe .	事實上 , 人們會做那些證明他們所相信的事 。
the reason that person bought the iphone in the first six hours , stood in line for six hours , was because of what they believed about the world , and how they wanted everybody to see them: they were first .	前六個小時買iphone的原因 , 站在線上六個小時 , 是因為他們對世界的信念 , 以及他們想讓每個人都看到的:他們是第一個 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼要做 。
so let me give you a famous example , a famous failure and a famous success of the law of diffusion of innovation .	讓我舉一個有名的例子 , 一個有名的失敗以及一個有名的成功 , 關於創新的散播法則 。
first , the famous failure .	首先 , 著名的失敗 。
it's a commercial example .	這是一個商業的例子 。
as we said before , a second ago , the recipe for success is money and the right people and the right market conditions , right ? you should have success then .	如我們先前所說的 , 成功的秘訣是金錢 , 適當的人和市場條件 , 對吧 ? 你當時應該要成功 。
from the time tivo came out about eight or nine years ago to this current day , they are the single highestquality product on the market , hands down , there is no dispute .	從八、九年前開始 , tivo出現在現今的時代 , 他們是市場上最高品質的產品 , 下降 , 沒有爭議 。
they were extremely wellfunded .	他們非常受歡迎 。
market conditions were fantastic .	市場條件很棒 。
i mean , we use tivo as verb .	我的意思是 , 我們把tivo當作動詞 。
i tivo stuff on my piece of junk time warner dvr all the time .	我常常在垃圾筒裡提取一些東西 , 像是華納dvr 。
but tivo's a commercial failure .	但tivo是個商業失敗 。
they've never made money .	他們從來沒有賺到錢 。
and when they went ipo , their stock was at about 30 or 40 dollars and then plummeted , and it's never traded above 10 .	當他們去ipo時 , 他們的股票大約是30或40美金 , 然後被拔掉 , 從來沒有交易超過10 。
in fact , i don't think it's even traded above six , except for a couple of little spikes .	事實上 , 我不認為它已經超過六次了 , 只不過幾次 。
because you see , when tivo launched their product they told us all what they had .	因為你看 , 當tivo推出他們的產品時 , 他們告訴我們他們所有的產品 。
they said , " we have a product that pauses live tv , skips commercials , rewinds live tv and memorizes your viewing habits without you even asking . "	他們說: 「 我們有一種產品 , 暫停現場電視、滑雪廣告、重製現場電視 , 並記住你看不到的習慣 。 」
and the cynical majority said , " we don't believe you .	絕大多數的憤世嫉俗說: 「 我們不相信你 。
we don't need it . we don't like it .	我們不需要它 。 我們不喜歡它 。
you're scaring us . "	你害怕我們 。 」
what if they had said , " if you're the kind of person who likes to have total control over every aspect of your life , boy , do we have a product for you .	如果他們說: 「 如果你是那種喜歡完全控制你的人生的那種人 , 男孩 , 我們有產品給你 。
it pauses live tv , skips commercials , memorizes your viewing habits , etc . , etc . "	它會暫停現場電視 , 跳過廣告 , 記住你的觀看習慣等等 。 」
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it , and what you do simply serves as the proof of what you believe .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼要做 , 而你所做的就是證明你所相信的 。
now let me give you a successful example of the law of diffusion of innovation .	現在讓我舉一個成功的例子 , 說明創新的擴散法則 。
in the summer of 1963 , 250 , 000 people showed up on the mall in washington to hear dr . king speak .	1963年夏天 , 有25萬人出現在華盛頓的商場上 , 聽見金恩博士演講 。
they sent out no invitations , and there was no website to check the date .	他們沒有邀請 , 也沒有網站來檢查約會 。
how do you do that ?	你怎麼做呢 ?
well , dr . king wasn't the only man in america who was a great orator .	嗯 , 金恩博士不是美國唯一一個偉大的演員 。
he wasn't the only man in america who suffered in a precivil rights america .	他不是美國唯一受過處方權利的男人 。
in fact , some of his ideas were bad .	事實上 , 他的一些想法很糟 。
but he had a gift .	但他有一個禮物 。
he didn't go around telling people what needed to change in america .	他沒有四處走去告訴人們在美國需要改變什麼 。
he went around and told people what he believed .	他四處走來告訴人們他所相信的 。
" i believe , i believe , i believe , " he told people .	「 我相信 , 我相信 , 我相信 , 」 他告訴別人 。
and people who believed what he believed took his cause , and they made it their own , and they told people .	而相信他所相信的人們 , 相信他採取了他的理由 , 他們自己做出來 , 他們告訴人們 。
and some of those people created structures to get the word out to even more people .	有些人創造了結構 , 讓更多人知道這個詞 。
and lo and behold , 250 , 000 people showed up on the right day at the right time to hear him speak .	你看 , 有25萬人在正確的日子上出現 , 聽到他說話 。
how many of them showed up for him ?	有多少人來找他 ?
they showed up for themselves .	他們為自己出現 。
it's what they believed about america that got them to travel in a bus for eight hours to stand in the sun in washington in the middle of august .	他們相信美國能讓他們在車上旅行八個小時 , 站在華盛頓的陽光下 。
it's what they believed , and it wasn't about black versus white: 25 percent of the audience was white .	這是他們所相信的 , 重點不是黑人對白:25%的觀眾是白人 。
dr . king believed that there are two types of laws in this world: those that are made by a higher authority and those that are made by man .	金恩博士相信世上有兩種法律:更高權威的法律和那些由人類所構成的法律 。
and not until all the laws that are made by man are consistent with the laws that are made by the higher authority will we live in a just world .	直到人類所制定的所有法律都與我們在公義世界裡更高權威的法律一致 。
it just so happened that the civil rights movement was the perfect thing to help him bring his cause to life .	剛好 , 民權運動是幫助他帶來他的生命的最佳成因 。
we followed , not for him , but for ourselves .	我們追隨 , 不是為了他 , 而是為了我們自己 。
and , by the way , he gave the " i have a dream " speech , not the " i have a plan " speech .	順道一提 , 他給了 「 我有一個夢想 」 演講 , 而不是 「 我有計畫 」 演講 。
listen to politicians now , with their comprehensive 12point plans .	現在聽聽政治人物 , 用他們全面的12種植物 。
they're not inspiring anybody .	他們沒有鼓舞任何人 。
because there are leaders and there are those who lead .	因為有領導者和領導者 。
leaders hold a position of power or authority , but those who lead inspire us .	領導者持有權力或權威的立場 , 但領導者鼓舞了我們 。
whether they're individuals or organizations , we follow those who lead , not because we have to , but because we want to .	不論是個人或組織 , 我們遵守領導者 , 不是因為我們必須這麼做 , 而是因為我們想要 。
we follow those who lead , not for them , but for ourselves .	我們追蹤那些領導的人 , 不是為了他們 , 而是為了我們自己 。
and it's those who start with " why " that have the ability to inspire those around them or find others who inspire them .	是那些從 「 為什麼 」 開始的人 , 他們有能力去啟發他們身邊的人 , 或找到鼓舞他們的人 。
how do you remember where you parked your car ? how do you know if you're moving in the right direction ? neuroscientist neil burgess studies the neural mechanisms that map the space around us , and how they link to memory and imagination .	你要如何記住你停在哪裡 ? 你要怎麼知道你要往正確的方向移動 ? 神經科學家尼爾負責研究地圖周遭空間的神經機制 , 以及他們如何連結記憶和想像力 。
brain , cognitive science , exploration , neuroscience , science	大腦、認知科學、探索、神經科學、科學、科學、科學 。
neil burgess: how your brain tells you where you are	尼爾堡:你的大腦告訴你你在哪裡 。
when we park in a big parking lot , how do we remember where we parked our car ?	當我們在一個大停車場停車場時 , 我們要如何記住我們停車的地方 ?
here's the problem facing homer .	問題是 , 面對家長的問題 。
and we're going to try to understand what's happening in his brain .	我們會試著去了解他的大腦發生了什麼事 。
so we'll start with the hippocampus , shown in yellow , which is the organ of memory .	我們先從海馬體開始 , 黃色代表記憶的器官 。
if you have damage there , like in alzheimer's , you can't remember things including where you parked your car .	如果你有損傷 , 像阿茲海默症 , 你無法記住 , 包括你停車的地方 。
it's named after latin for " seahorse , " which it resembles .	它是以拉丁文為 「 海馬 」 的名字命名 , 它是相似的 。
and like the rest of the brain , it's made of neurons .	就像大腦的其他部分 , 它是由神經元組成的 。
so the human brain has about a hundred billion neurons in it .	人類的大腦大約有一千億個神經元 。
and the neurons communicate with each other by sending little pulses or spikes of electricity via connections to each other .	神經元互相溝通 , 藉由發送小脈衝或電刺激彼此連結 。
the hippocampus is formed of two sheets of cells , which are very densely interconnected .	海馬體是由兩片細胞組成的 , 密度非常緊密 。
and scientists have begun to understand how spatial memory works by recording from individual neurons in rats or mice while they forage or explore an environment looking for food .	科學家開始了解空間記憶如何運作 , 藉由記錄老鼠或老鼠的個別神經元 , 或是探索尋找食物的環境 。
so we're going to imagine we're recording from a single neuron in the hippocampus of this rat here .	所以 , 我們將想像我們從這隻老鼠的海馬體中紀錄下來 。
and when it fires a little spike of electricity , there's going to be a red dot and a click .	當它發出電量時 , 就會有一個紅點和點擊 。
so what we see is that this neuron knows whenever the rat has gone into one particular place in its environment .	我們看到的是 , 這種神經元知道 , 每當老鼠進入一個特定的地方 。
and it signals to the rest of the brain by sending a little electrical spike .	它會訊號到大腦的其他部位 , 藉由發送小小的電擊 。
so we could show the firing rate of that neuron as a function of the animal's location .	所以 , 我們可以把神經元的發射速度顯示為動物的位置 。
and if we record from lots of different neurons , we'll see that different neurons fire when the animal goes in different parts of its environment , like in this square box shown here .	如果我們從許多不同的神經元記錄下來 , 我們會看到當動物在環境中的不同區域出現不同的神經元 , 比如這個正方形的盒子中 。
so together they form a map for the rest of the brain , telling the brain continually , " where am i now within my environment ? "	所以他們一起為其餘的大腦建立了一張地圖 , 不斷地告訴大腦: 「 我現在在我的環境中是哪裡 ? 」
place cells are also being recorded in humans .	位置細胞也被記錄在人體中 。
so epilepsy patients sometimes need the electrical activity in their brain monitoring .	所以癲癇患者有時需要腦部監控的電活動 。
and some of these patients played a video game where they drive around a small town .	有些病人玩了電玩遊戲 , 他們開車到一個小鎮 。
and place cells in their hippocampi would fire , become active , start sending electrical impulses whenever they drove through a particular location in that town .	把它們的髖骨細胞放進去 , 變成活性 , 開始發送電脈衝 , 每當它們穿過那個小鎮時 。
so how does a place cell know where the rat or person is within its environment ?	那麼 , 一個地方細胞怎麼知道老鼠或人在其環境中的位置 ?
well these two cells here show us that the boundaries of the environment are particularly important .	這兩個細胞告訴我們 , 環境的邊界是特別重要的 。
so the one on the top likes to fire sort of midway between the walls of the box that their rat's in .	所以 , 上面的那個 , 像是在盒子裡的牆壁上開火 ,
and when you expand the box , the firing location expands .	當你擴展盒子時 , 發射位置會擴張 。
the one below likes to fire whenever there's a wall close by to the south .	下面的那一面 , 每當有一面牆靠近南方時都會喜歡火 。
and if you put another wall inside the box , then the cell fires in both place wherever there's a wall to the south as the animal explores around in its box .	如果你把另一面牆放在盒子裡 , 細胞就會在兩個地方發射 , 無論在裡面有一面牆 , 作為動物在其盒子裡探索 。
so this predicts that sensing the distances and directions of boundaries around you extended buildings and so on is particularly important for the hippocampus .	這種預測會感應到你周圍的邊界和方向 , 延伸到大樓之外 , 尤其對海馬體來說是很重要的 。
and indeed , on the inputs to the hippocampus , cells are found which project into the hippocampus , which do respond exactly to detecting boundaries or edges at particular distances and directions from the rat or mouse as it's exploring around .	的確 , 在海馬體的輸入上 , 細胞會發現 , 會進入海馬體中 , 會反應出偵測邊界或邊緣 , 特定位置的特定位置 , 和從老鼠或老鼠探索時的方向 。
so the cell on the left , you can see , it fires whenever the animal gets near to a wall or a boundary to the east , whether it's the edge or the wall of a square box or the circular wall of the circular box or even the drop at the edge of a table , which the animals are running around .	左邊的細胞 , 你可以看到 , 當動物靠近東邊的牆壁或邊界時 , 它會發出火 , 不論是方形的邊緣 , 或是圓形的牆 , 或是圓形的圓形牆 , 或甚至是桌子的邊緣 。
and the cell on the right there fires whenever there's a boundary to the south , whether it's the drop at the edge of the table or a wall or even the gap between two tables that are pulled apart .	右邊的細胞 , 每當南方有邊界 , 不論是桌面或牆壁的邊緣 , 或甚至兩個桌子之間的落差 。
so that's one way in which we think place cells determine where the animal is as it's exploring around .	這就是我們認為位置細胞的一種方式決定動物在周圍探索的位置 。
we can also test where we think objects are , like this goal flag , in simple environments or indeed , where your car would be .	我們也可以檢測我們認為物體的位置 , 像是這個目標旗 , 在簡單的環境中 , 或你的車會在哪裡 。
so we can have people explore an environment and see the location they have to remember .	所以 , 我們可以讓人們探索一個環境 , 看看他們必須記得的位置 。
and then , if we put them back in the environment , generally they're quite good at putting a marker down where they thought that flag or their car was .	然後 , 如果我們把它們放回環境中 , 通常它們很擅長把標記放到他們認為旗子或車子的位置 。
but on some trials , we could change the shape and size of the environment like we did with the place cell .	但在某些試驗中 , 我們可以改變環境的形狀和大小 , 就像我們用的位置細胞一樣 。
in that case , we can see how where they think the flag had been changes as a function of how you change the shape and size of the environment .	在這個例子中 , 我們可以看到旗幟是如何改變你如何改變環境的形狀和尺寸 。
and what you see , for example , if the flag was where that cross was in a small square environment , and then if you ask people where it was , but you've made the environment bigger , where they think the flag had been stretches out in exactly the same way that the place cell firing stretched out .	舉例來說 , 如果國旗在一個小方形的環境中 , 交叉的位置就在一個小方形的環境中 , 如果你問人們它在哪裡 , 但你讓環境變大了 , 他們認為旗幟被用完全相同的方式將細胞發射出來 。
it's as if you remember where the flag was by storing the pattern of firing across all of your place cells at that location , and then you can get back to that location by moving around so that you best match the current pattern of firing of your place cells with that stored pattern .	就好像你還記得旗幟的位置 , 藉由儲存所有位置細胞的模式 , 儲存在你所在位置的位置 , 然後你就可以回到那個位置 , 這樣你就能最好配合你位置細胞的目前模式 , 以儲存的模式來運作 。
that guides you back to the location that you want to remember .	那會引導你回到你想要記得的地點 。
but we also know where we are through movement .	但我們也知道我們在運動中處於何處 。
so if we take some outbound path perhaps we park and we wander off we know because our own movements , which we can integrate over this path roughly what the heading direction is to go back .	所以 , 如果我們採取一些外界的路徑 , 或許我們停了下來 , 我們會知道 , 因為我們的動作 , 我們可以將這個路徑整合起來 , 大約是頭向後走的方向 。
and place cells also get this kind of path integration input from a kind of cell called a grid cell .	位置細胞也得到這種通路綜合輸入 , 來自一種叫做網格細胞的細胞 。
now grid cells are found , again , on the inputs to the hippocampus , and they're a bit like place cells .	網格細胞又被發現在海馬體的輸入上 , 它們有點像地方細胞 。
but now as the rat explores around , each individual cell fires in a whole array of different locations which are laid out across the environment in an amazingly regular triangular grid .	但當老鼠四處探索時 , 每個細胞都在一系列不同的位置上發射 , 在一個非常規則的三角形格子裡 。
and if you record from several grid cells shown here in different colors each one has a gridlike firing pattern across the environment , and each cell's gridlike firing pattern is shifted slightly relative to the other cells .	如果你從幾種格細胞中記錄下來 , 每一種顏色都有類似網格的發射模式 , 每一種細胞的發射模式會稍微改變對方的細胞 。
so the red one fires on this grid and the green one on this one and the blue on on this one .	紅色的 , 在這個格子上發火 , 綠色的 , 藍色的在這個格子上 。
so together , it's as if the rat can put a virtual grid of firing locations across its environment a bit like the latitude and longitude lines that you'd find on a map , but using triangles .	所以 , 整體來說 , 老鼠可以把虛擬的網格放到周圍的環境中 , 有點像是你在地圖上找到的緯度和長距離線 , 但使用三角形 。
and as it moves around , the electrical activity can pass from one of these cells to the next cell to keep track of where it is , so that it can use its own movements to know where it is in its environment .	當它四處移動時 , 電活動可以從其中一個細胞傳遞到下一個細胞 , 一直追蹤它的位置 , 這樣它就可以用它自己的動作來了解它在環境中的位置 。
do people have grid cells ?	人們有網格細胞嗎 ?
well because all of the gridlike firing patterns have the same axes of symmetry , the same orientations of grid , shown in orange here , it means that the net activity of all of the grid cells in a particular part of the brain should change according to whether we're running along these six directions or running along one of the six directions in between .	因為所有的電網發射圖案都有相同的對稱軸 , 這裡的橘色標示著橘色的方向 , 意思是 , 所有電網的電網活動都應該根據我們在這六個方向跑的方向來改變 , 或在兩者之間的六個方向跑 。
so we can put people in an mri scanner and have them do a little video game like the one i showed you and look for this signal .	所以 , 我們可以把人放進核磁共振儀中 , 讓他們做一個小小的電玩遊戲 , 就像我給你們看的一樣 , 去尋找這個訊號 。
and indeed , you do see it in the human entorhinal cortex , which is the same part of the brain that you see grid cells in rats .	的確 , 在人類的牙齒皮質中 , 它也是你在老鼠身上看到的電網細胞的一部分 。
so back to homer .	回到荷馬 。
he's probably remembering where his car was in terms of the distances and directions to extended buildings and boundaries around the location where he parked .	他可能還記得他的車位在距離和方向的位置 , 將建築和界線延伸到他停的位置 。
and that would be represented by the firing of boundarydetecting cells .	這會由邊界偵測細胞的發射來呈現 。
he's also remembering the path he took out of the car park , which would be represented in the firing of grid cells .	他還記得他從汽車公園走出來的道路 , 在發射網格細胞的邊緣 。
now both of these kinds of cells can make the place cells fire .	兩種細胞都可以讓位置細胞發射 。
and he can return to the location where he parked by moving so as to find where it is that best matches the firing pattern of the place cells in his brain currently with the stored pattern where he parked his car .	他可以回到他停下來的位置 , 讓他能移動的位置 , 找到在他大腦中位置細胞的最佳配對模式 , 以儲存的模式 , 讓他停車的車 。
