and that guides him back to that location irrespective of visual cues like whether his car's actually there .	那引導他回到那個視覺暗示的位置 , 像是他的車真的在那裡 。
maybe it's been towed .	也許它已經被告知了 。
but he knows where it was , so he knows to go and get it .	但他知道它在哪裡 , 所以他知道要去哪裡找到它 。
so beyond spatial memory , if we look for this gridlike firing pattern throughout the whole brain , we see it in a whole series of locations which are always active when we do all kinds of autobiographical memory tasks , like remembering the last time you went to a wedding , for example .	所以 , 除了空間記憶之外 , 如果我們在整個大腦中尋找類似網格的發射模式 , 我們會看到一系列的地點 , 當我們做各式各樣的自傳記憶任務時 , 比如記得你上次去婚禮的時候 。
so it may be that the neural mechanisms for representing the space around us are also used for generating visual imagery so that we can recreate the spatial scene , at least , of the events that have happened to us when we want to imagine them .	所以 , 可能是神經機制 , 代表我們周圍的空間 , 也被用來產生視覺影像 , 這樣我們才能重建空間場景 , 至少 , 當我們想要想像它們時 , 發生的事件 。
so if this was happening , your memories could start by place cells activating each other via these dense interconnections and then reactivating boundary cells to create the spatial structure of the scene around your viewpoint .	所以 , 如果這發生了 , 你的記憶可以從細胞開始啟動 , 透過這些密集的交互作用 , 再次啟動邊界細胞 , 來創造你周圍的景象空間結構 。
and grid cells could move this viewpoint through that space .	網格細胞可以透過這個空間移動這個視角 。
another kind of cell , head direction cells , which i didn't mention yet , they fire like a compass according to which way you're facing .	另一種細胞 , 頭部方向細胞 , 我還沒提到 , 它們就像你面臨的指南一樣 。
they could define the viewing direction from which you want to generate an image for your visual imagery , so you can imagine what happened when you were at this wedding , for example .	他們可以定義你想要為你的視覺圖像創造出一張圖像 , 你可以想像當你在婚禮上發生什麼事 。
so this is just one example of a new era really in cognitive neuroscience where we're beginning to understand psychological processes like how you remember or imagine or even think in terms of the actions of the billions of individual neurons that make up our brains .	這只是新時代的一個例子 , 在認知神經科學中 , 我們開始了解心理的過程 , 比如你如何記得、想像 , 甚至以數十億個神經元的行為來思考 。
thank you very much .	謝謝大家 。
imagine a global security driven by collaboration among agencies , government , the private sector and the public . that's not just the distant hope of opensource fans , it's the vision of james stavridis , the supreme commander of nato , who shares vivid moments from recent military history to explain why security of the future should be built with bridges rather than walls .	想像一下 , 全球安全是由組織、政府、私營部門和大眾所驅動的 , 這不僅僅是開放原始碼粉絲的遙遠希望 , 也是納粹的願景 , 納粹指揮官的最高階指揮官 , 他們在近期的軍事歷史中分享vid時刻 , 來解釋未來的安全性 , 而不是牆壁 。
collaboration , global issues , opensource , peace , politics , social media , violence , war	合作、全球議題、開放資源、和平政治、社交媒體、暴力、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭 。
james stavridis: how nato's supreme commander thinks about global security	詹姆斯•史塔里斯:納多的最高指揮官認為全球安全性如何 ?
i'm gonna talk a little bit about opensource security , because we've got to get better at security in this 21st century .	我要談一些開放原始碼安全的議題 , 因為在21世紀 , 我們必須在安全上做得更好 。
let me start by saying , let's look back to the 20th century , and kind of get a sense of how that style of security worked for us .	首先讓我說 , 讓我們回顧二十世紀 , 看看安全的風格是如何影響我們 。
this is verdun , a battlefield in france just north of the nato headquarters in belgium .	這是verdun , 一個法國的戰場 , 位在比利時北部的奈米總部 。
at verdun , in 1916 , over a 300day period , 700 , 000 people were killed , so about 2 , 000 a day .	1916年的verdun , 在1916年 , 超過300天 , 70萬人被殺害 , 一天大約有2 , 000人 。
if you roll it forward 20thcentury security into the second world war , you see the battle of stalingrad , 300 days , 2 million people killed .	如果你將它推向二十世紀的安全轉為第二次世界大戰 , 你會看到史達丁格的戰役 , 300天 , 兩百萬人死亡 。
we go into the cold war , and we continue to try and build walls .	我們進入冷戰 , 我們持續嘗試建造牆壁 。
we go from the trench warfare of the first world war to the maginot line of the second world war , and then we go into the cold war , the iron curtain , the berlin wall .	我們從第一次世界大戰的陷阱 , 到第二次世界大戰的黑暗線 , 接著我們進入冷戰、鐵幕、柏林牆 。
my thesis for us today is , instead of building walls to create security , we need to build bridges .	我今天的論點是 , 與其建立安全牆 , 我們不需要建造橋樑 。
this is a famous bridge in europe .	這是歐洲有名的橋樑 。
it's the bridge over the drina river , the subject of a novel by ivo andrić , and it talks about how , in that very troubled part of europe and the balkans , over time there's been enormous building of walls .	這座橋在大西洋的河邊 , 由ivoandric所組成的小說主題 , 它談到 , 在歐洲和巴爾幹的那一塊非常困擾的部分 , 隨著時間 , 已經有很大的牆壁 。
more recently , in the last decade , we begin to see these communities start , hesitatingly , to come together .	更近期 , 在過去十年 , 我們開始看到這些社區開始猶豫地團結在一起 。
i would argue , again , opensource security is about connecting the international , the interagency , the privatepublic , and lashing it together with strategic communication , largely in social networks .	我認為 , 同樣地 , 開放原始碼安全的重點在於將國際、國際間、私人公共事務 , 將它與戰略通訊結合 , 大多是在社交網路上 。
so let me talk a little bit about why we need to do that , because our global commons is under attack in a variety of ways , and none of the sources of threat to the global commons will be solved by building walls .	讓我稍微談一下為何我們需要這麼做 , 因為我們的全球公有物以各種方式來攻擊 , 沒有任何威脅到全球公有物的來源 , 都會被建立牆壁來解決 。
now , i'm a sailor , obviously .	顯然 , 我是個水手 。
this is a ship , a liner , clipping through the indian ocean .	這是一艘船 , 一艘船 , 穿過印度洋 。
what's wrong with this picture ?	這張照片有什麼問題 ?
it's got concertina wire along the sides of it .	它沿著它的側邊有凝固電線 。
that's to prevent pirates from attacking it .	那就是防止海盜攻擊它 。
piracy is a very active threat today around the world . this is in the indian ocean .	陰謀是現今全世界非常活躍的威脅 。 這是在印度洋 。
piracy is also very active in the strait of malacca .	海盜也在馬拉卡的地鐵上非常活躍 。
it's active in the gulf of guinea .	它在幾內亞灣活躍 。
we see it in the caribbean .	我們在加勒比海看到 。
it's a $10billionayear discontinuity in the global transport system .	它是全球交通系統的十億年的不穩定性 。
last year , at this time , there were 20 vessels , 500 mariners held hostage .	去年 , 去年 , 有20艘船 , 500艘馬丁持有敵人 。
this is an attack on the global commons .	這是針對全球公有物的攻擊 。
we need to think about how to address it .	我們需要思考如何處理它 。
let's shift to a different kind of sea , the cyber sea .	讓我們轉移到另一種海洋 , 網路海 。
here are photographs of two young men .	這裡有兩個年輕男生的照片 。
at the moment , they're incarcerated .	目前 , 他們被監禁了 。
they conducted a credit card fraud that netted them over 10 billion dollars .	他們做了一個信用卡詐欺 , 將他們淨入超過一百億美金 。
this is part of cybercrime which is a $2trillionayear discontinuity in the global economy .	這是網路犯罪的一部分 , 它是全球經濟中2兆美元的連續性 。
two trillion a year .	一年有兩兆 。
that's just under the gdp of great britain .	這只是英國的國內生產總值 。
so this cyber sea , which we know endlessly is the fundamental piece of radical openness , is very much under threat as well .	所以 , 這個網路海 , 我們無止盡地知道是徹底開放的基本一部分 , 都受到威脅 。
another thing i worry about in the global commons is the threat posed by trafficking , by the movement of narcotics , opium , here coming out of afghanistan through europe over to the united states .	在全球公有物中 , 我擔心的另一件事是人口販賣所造成的威脅 , 由毒品、鴉片、從阿富汗來到美國 。
we worry about cocaine coming from the andean ridge north .	我們擔心可卡因從安地斯坦河流來 。
we worry about the movement of illegal weapons and trafficking . above all , perhaps , we worry about human trafficking , and the awful cost of it .	我們擔心非法武器和販運的動作 , 也許最重要的是 , 我們擔心人口販賣 , 以及它的成本 。
trafficking moves largely at sea but in other parts of the global commons .	人口販賣通常在海上移動 , 但在全球公有物的其他部分 。
this is a photograph , and i wish i could tell you that this is a very hightech piece of us navy gear that we're using to stop the trafficking .	這是一張照片 , 我希望我能告訴你們 , 這是我們用來阻止人口販運的高科技裝置 。
the bad news is , this is a semisubmersible run by drug cartels .	壞消息是 , 這是一個半導體可以用毒品軟骨來運作 。
it was built in the jungles of south america .	它是在南美叢林裡建造的 。
we caught it with that lowtech raft — — and it was carrying six tons of cocaine .	我們用那個低科技的強暴抓住它 , 它帶著六噸的可卡因 。
crew of four . sophisticated communications sweep .	四個 , 複雜的溝通 。
this kind of trafficking , in narcotics , in humans , in weapons , god forbid , in weapons of mass destruction , is part of the threat to the global commons .	這種運輸 , 在人體、武器、神禁止、大規模毀滅的武器 , 是全球公有物威脅的一部分 。
and let's pull it together in afghanistan today .	讓我們一起在阿富汗 。
this is a field of poppies in afghanistan .	這是阿富汗的小狗 。
eighty to 90 percent of the world's poppy , opium and heroin , comes out of afghanistan .	世界上百分之八十到九十的流浪、鴉片和海洛因 , 來自阿富汗 。
we also see there , of course , terrorism .	當然 , 我們也看到恐怖主義 。
this is where al qaeda is staged from .	這就是蓋達組織的所在 。
we also see a very strong insurgency embedded there .	我們也看到一個非常強烈的保險制度 。
so this terrorism concern is also part of the global commons , and what we must address .	所以 , 恐怖主義也是全球公有物的一部分 , 我們必須處理的事 。
so here we are , 21st century .	這裡是21世紀 。
we know our 20thcentury tools are not going to work .	我們知道20世紀的工具不會成功 。
what should we do ?	我們該怎麼做 ?
i would argue that we will not deliver security solely from the barrel of a gun .	我會說 , 我們不會只靠槍支來遞送安全 。
we will not deliver security solely from the barrel of a gun .	我們不會直接從槍的桶子上遞送安全 。
we will need the application of military force .	我們需要軍事力量的應用 。
when we do it , we must do it well , and competently .	當我們這麼做時 , 我們必須做得很好 , 並且能做到 。
but my thesis is , opensource security is about international , interagency , privatepublic connection pulled together by this idea of strategic communication on the internet .	但我的論點是 , 開放原始碼安全是關於國際、國際間、私人的連結 , 透過網路上策略溝通的概念 。
let me give you a couple of examples of how this works in a positive way .	讓我舉幾個例子來說明這如何用正面的方式運作 。
this is afghanistan . these are afghan soldiers .	這是阿富汗 。 這些是阿富汗士兵 。
they are all holding books .	他們都拿著書 。
you should say , " that's odd . i thought i read that this demographic , young men and women in their 20s and 30s , is largely illiterate in afghanistan . "	你應該說: 「 那是很奇怪的 。 我想我讀到 , 在二十、三十歲時 , 年輕的男性和女性 , 主要是在阿富汗 。 」
you would be correct .	你會是正確的 。
eightyfive percent cannot read when they enter the security forces of afghanistan .	當他們進入阿富汗的安全力量時 , 85%就無法閱讀 。
why ? because the taliban withheld education during the period of time in which these men and women would have learned to read .	為什麼呢 ? 因為塔利班在時間的期間 , 這些男人和女人會學會閱讀 。
so the question is , so , why are they all standing there holding books ?	所以問題是 , 為什麼他們都站在那裡拿著書 ?
the answer is , we are teaching them to read in literacy courses by nato in partnership with private sector entities , in partnership with development agencies .	答案是 , 我們教導他們讀識字課程 , 由納多和私人機構合作 , 與發展機構合作 。
we've taught well over 200 , 000 afghan security forces to read and write at a basic level .	我們已經教導了超過二十萬個阿富汗安全部隊以基本的角度閱讀和寫字 。
when you can read and write in afghanistan , you will typically put a pen in your pocket .	當你讀和寫在阿富汗 , 你通常會把一支筆放在口袋裡 。
at the ceremonies , when these young men and women graduate , they take that pen with great pride , and put it in their pocket .	在典禮上 , 當這些年輕男女畢業時 , 他們用大驕傲的鉛筆 , 把它放在口袋裡 。
this is bringing together international — there are 50 nations involved in this mission — interagency — these development agencies — and privatepublic , to take on this kind of security .	這將帶來國際性的50個國家與這個任務有關的國際發展機構和私人公共事業 , 採取這種安全 。
now , we are also teaching them combat skills , of course , but i would argue , opensource security means connecting in ways that create longer lasting security effect .	當然 , 我們也在教他們戰鬥技能 , 但我認為 , 開放原始碼安全意味著以更長久的安全效應的方式連結 。
this is a us navy warship .	這是一個美國海軍戰艦 。
it's called the comfort .	它叫做舒適 。
there's a sister ship called the mercy .	有一艘叫mercy的姐妹船 。
they are hospital ships .	他們是醫院船隻 。
this one , the comfort , operates throughout the caribbean and the coast of south america conducting patient treatments .	這個是舒適的 , 在加勒比海和南美洲的海岸進行病人治療 。
on a typical cruise , they'll do 400 , 000 patient treatments .	在典型的情況下 , 他們會做四十萬個病人治療 。
it is crewed not strictly by military but by a combination of humanitarian organizations: operation hope , project smile .	它不是嚴格地被軍隊組合 , 而是由人道主義組織組合: 「 行動希望 」 , 計畫微笑 。
other organizations send volunteers .	其他組織發送志願者 。
interagency physicians come out .	內科醫師出來了 。
they're all part of this .	這些都是其中的一部分 。
to give you one example of the impact this can have , this little boy , eight years old , walked with his mother two days to come to the eye clinic put on by the comfort .	舉個例子 , 這個小男孩 , 八歲 , 帶著他媽兩天走進舒適圈的診所 。
when he was fitted , over his extremely myopic eyes , he suddenly looked up and said , " mama , veo el mundo . "	當他被配合時 , 在他的極端靈光眼中 , 他突然抬頭說: 「 媽媽 , veoelmundo 。 」
" mom , i see the world . "	「 媽 , 我看見世界 。 」
multiply this by 400 , 000 patient treatments , this privatepublic collaboration with security forces , and you begin to see the power of creating security in a very different way .	把這個乘以四十萬個病人治療 , 這種私人合作和安全部隊合作 , 你開始用非常不同的方法來創造安全的力量 。
here you see baseball players .	這裡你可以看到棒球選手 。
can you pick out the two us army soldiers in this photograph ?	你能在照片中挑出兩位美國軍人軍人嗎 ?
they are the two young men on either side of these young boys . this is part of a series of baseball clinics , where we have explored collaboration between major league baseball , the department of state , who sets up the diplomatic piece of this , military baseball players , who are real soldiers with real skills but participate in this mission , and they put on clinics throughout latin america and the caribbean , in honduras , in nicaragua , in all of the central american and caribbean nations where baseball is so popular , and it creates security .	他們是兩位年輕男孩兩方的年輕男孩 。 這是一系列棒球診所的一部分 , 在那裡 , 我們已經探索了主要聯盟棒球、國家部門 , 他們設立了外交棒球員 , 他們是真正的軍事棒球員 , 他們是真正有技能的士兵 , 但參與這個任務 , 他們在拉丁美洲和加勒比亞、加勒比亞、加勒比亞、加勒比亞、加勒比亞、和加勒比 , 在那裡 , 在那裡創造出全美式球 。
it shows role models to young men and women about fitness and about life that i would argue help create security for us .	它展現年輕男女的榜樣 , 關於健身和生活的典範 , 我主張幫助為我們創造安全 。
another aspect of this partnership is in disaster relief .	這種合作關係的另一面是災難的解救 。
this is a us air force helicopter participating after the tsunami in 2004 which killed 250 , 000 people .	這是美國空軍直升機在2004年抵達海嘯之後 , 殺了25萬人 。
in each of these major disasters — the tsunami in 2004 , 250 , 000 dead , the kashmiri earthquake in pakistan , 2005 , 85 , 000 dead , the haitian earthquake , about 300 , 000 dead , more recently the awful earthquaketsunami combination which struck japan and its nuclear industry — in all of these instances , we see partnerships between international actors , interagency , privatepublic working with security forces to respond to this kind of natural disaster .	在每一個重大災難中 , 2004年的海嘯 , 250 , 000人死於巴基斯坦的喀什米里地震 , 2005年 , 8萬5千人死亡 , 海地地地震 , 近期有30萬人死亡 , 日本和其核能產業結合 , 在所有這些情況下 , 我們看到國際演員之間的合作關係 , 國際演員 , 國際關係 , 私人和安全部門合作 , 和安全部隊合作 。
so these are examples of this idea of opensource security .	這些是開放原始碼安全的例子 。
we tie it together , increasingly , by doing things like this .	透過這樣做 , 我們將它結合在一起 。
now , you're looking at this thinking , " ah , admiral , these must be sea lanes of communication , or these might be fiber optic cables . "	現在 , 你看到的這個想法是: 「 啊 , 不公正 , 這些必定是通訊的海平線 , 或這些可能是光纖電纜 。 」
no . this is a graphic of the world according to twitter .	不 , 這是twitter世界的圖像 。
purple are tweets . green are geolocation .	紫色是推特 。 綠色是地理分配 。
white is the synthesis .	白色是合成的 。
it's a perfect evocation of that great population survey , the six largest nations in the world in descending order: china , india , facebook , the united states , twitter and indonesia .	這是個完美的進展 , 關於人口調查 , 世界上六個最大的國家 , 下降順序:中國、印度、臉書、美國、推特和印尼 。
why do we want to get in these nets ?	為什麼我們要拿到這些蚊帳 ?
why do we want to be involved ?	為什麼我們要參與其中 ?
we talked earlier about the arab spring , and the power of all this .	我們先前談到阿拉伯之春 , 以及所有這些力量 。
i'll give you another example , and it's how you move this message .	我再舉另一個例子 , 就是你如何傳遞這個訊息 。
i gave a talk like this in london a while back about this point . i said , as i say to all of you , i'm on facebook . friend me .	我在倫敦演講了一陣子 。 我跟你們說 , 我在臉書上 。 朋友我 。
got a little laugh from the audience .	聽眾有點笑 。
there was an article which was run by ap , on the wire .	有一篇文章是ap , 在電線上運行 。
got picked up in two places in the world: finland and indonesia .	被帶到世界上兩個地方:芬蘭和印尼 。
the headline was: nato admiral needs friends .	標題是:納粹需要朋友 。
and the story was a catalyst , and the next morning i had hundreds of facebook friend requests from indonesians and finns , mostly saying , " admiral , we heard you need a friend , and oh , by the way , what is nato ? "	故事是一個催化劑 , 隔天早上 , 我有數百名facebook朋友 , 來自印尼人和芬蘭 , 主要是說: 「 不論如何 , 我們都聽說你需要一個朋友 , 喔 , 順便一提 , 奈及利亞是什麼 ? 」
yeah , we laugh , but this is how we move the message , and moving that message is how we connect international , interagency , privatepublic , and these social nets to help create security .	沒錯 , 我們笑了 , 但這就是我們如何傳遞訊息 , 傳遞訊息就是我們如何連結國際、國際間、私人企業 , 以及這些社交網路 , 來協助創造安全 。
now , let me hit a somber note .	現在 , 讓我按下一聲點 。
this is a photograph of a brave british soldier .	這是英國士兵的照片 。
he's in the scots guards .	他在蘇格蘭守衛中 。
he's standing the watch in helmand , in southern afghanistan .	他站在阿富汗南部的頭盔上 ,
i put him here to remind us , i would not want anyone to leave the room thinking that we do not need capable , competent militaries who can create real military effect .	我把他放在這裡提醒我們 , 我不會希望任何人離開房間 , 認為我們不需要有能力 , 能創造真正的軍隊效應 。
that is the core of who we are and what we do , and we do it to protect freedom , freedom of speech , all the things we treasure in our societies .	這就是我們所做的事的核心以及我們所做的事 , 來保護自由、言論自由、所有我們在社會中珍惜的東西 。
but , you know , life is not an onandoff switch .	但 , 你知道的 , 人生不是一個開關 。
you don't have to have a military that is either in hard combat or is in the barracks .	你不需要有一支軍隊 , 要麼在戰鬥中 , 要麼是在戰鬥中 。
i would argue life is a rheostat .	我主張生命是一場風暴 。
you have to dial it in , and as i think about how we create security in this 21st century , there will be times when we will apply hard power in true war and crisis , but there will be many instances , as we've talked about today , where our militaries can be part of creating 21stcentury security , international , interagency , privatepublic , connected with competent communication .	你必須在這個21世紀做安全 , 會有時候 , 我們會在真正的戰爭和危機上施加強大的力量 , 但有很多的例子 , 如今 , 我們的軍隊可以是創造21世紀安全、國際安全、跨領域、私人通訊的一部分 。
i would close by saying that we heard earlier today about wikipedia . i use wikipedia all the time to look up facts , and as all of you appreciate , wikipedia is not created by 12 brilliant people locked in a room writing articles .	最後我會說 , 今天我們聽到維基百科 , 我常常用維基百科檢查事實 , 你們都很欣賞 , 維基百科並不是由12名聰明的人在房間寫文章中所創造出來的 。
wikipedia , every day , is tens of thousands of people inputting information , and every day millions of people withdrawing that information .	維基百科 , 每天都有成千上萬的人輸入資訊 , 每天有數百萬人會放棄這些資訊 。
it's a perfect image for the fundamental point that no one of us is as smart as all of us thinking together .	這是個完美的圖像 , 沒有人像我們所有人一樣聰明 。
no one person , no one alliance , no one nation , no one of us is as smart as all of us thinking together .	沒有一個人 , 沒有一個聯盟 , 沒有一個國家 , 我們沒有一個人像我們所有人一樣聰明 。
the vision statement of wikipedia is very simple: a world in which every human being can freely share in the sum of all knowledge .	維基百科的願景很簡單:在這個世界中 , 每個人都可以自由分享在所有知識的總和中 。
my thesis for you is that by combining international , interagency , privatepublic , strategic communication , together , in this 21st century , we can create the sum of all security .	我的論點是 , 透過結合國際、國際間、私人、戰略溝通 , 在21世紀 , 我們能創造出所有安全的總和 。
thank you very much . thank you . thank you .	非常謝謝 。 謝謝 。 謝謝 。
